# Podium Implementation Gap Report

This report records gaps, inconsistencies, and bugs found by reviewing the Podium implementation against the specification in `spec/`. Each spec subsection was reviewed on its own against the Go code, and every finding cites `file:line` evidence. The report represents `main` at commit `e41f44e`.

The original run covered all 82 subsections on branch `feat/layer-visibility-pr` (workflow `wf_e6e03ea1-0e0`). After switching to `main` and pulling to `e41f44e`, the 11 subsections affected by the difference were re-audited against main: 2.2, 4.6, 7.2, 7.3, 9.2, 11, 13.10, 13.11, 13.12, 14.9, and 14.10 (workflows `wf_3a65f359-d54` and `wf_f1d63051-e22`). The remaining subsections cite code that is unchanged between the branch and main. The per-subsection source files are under `tmp/build-gaps/F-{section}.md`. Generated 2026-05-28.

Branch note: `main` at `e41f44e` does not contain the per-layer visibility loading from `.podium/layers.yaml` or the trusted-headers identity provider that exist on `feat/layer-visibility-pr`. The files `pkg/registry/server/layer_visibility.go`, `pkg/registry/server/header_identity.go`, and `pkg/identity/trusted_headers.go` are absent on main. Several findings in the re-audited sections describe that absence as open gaps.

Each finding has an ID of the form `F-{section}.{subsection}.{n}`, a severity in brackets, and a status. Every finding starts at `OPEN`. The description of each finding begins with a kind tag: `(gap)`, `(inconsistency)`, or `(bug)`.

## Totals

- 387 findings across 72 of the 82 reviewed subsections. 10 subsections had no findings.
- By severity: 105 High, 168 Medium, 92 Low, and 22 Info.
- By kind: 216 gap, 126 inconsistency, and 41 bug. Four findings did not carry an inline kind tag.

Severity meanings used by the reviewers:

- **High**: spec-mandated behavior missing or broken in a way that affects correctness, security, data integrity, or auth; bugs causing wrong results, crashes, data loss, or access bypass.
- **Medium**: partial implementation or behavioral deviation with limited blast radius or a workaround; missing validation; wrong edge-case handling.
- **Low**: minor deviation, missing non-critical field, or naming and cosmetic mismatch.
- **Info**: ambiguity, observation, or item to confirm, with no clear defect.

- F-2.2.2 — podium sync has no server-source HTTP path; --watch polls the filesystem instead of subscribing to change events
- F-3.2.1 — search_domains does not run hybrid retrieval over domain projections
- F-3.5.1 — Tenant flag `expose_scope_preview` and `403 scope_preview_disabled` not implemented
- F-4.3.1 — input/output `$ref` object form fails to parse
- F-4.5.1 — DOMAIN.md content is never ingested or read at load_domain time
- F-4.5.2 — load_domain returns no domain description or prose body
- F-4.5.3 — load_domain keywords are never populated
- F-4.5.4 — folded_from annotation is computed in core but dropped on the wire
- F-4.5.5 — unlisted: true is never enforced; subtree is not removed from enumeration

## Detailed findings

## F-0.0 — 0 Quickstart

_Reviewed spec/00-quickstart.md against the implementation._

The quickstart walks an author from a `SKILL.md` + `ARTIFACT.md` pair through ingest, manual reingest, and two MCP tool calls (`load_domain`, `load_artifact`). The artifact-model claims hold: the `ARTIFACT.md` fields `type`, `version`, `when_to_use`, `tags`, and `sensitivity` all exist on `manifest.Artifact` (pkg/manifest/types.go:100-106), `SKILL.md` parses `name`, `description`, and `license` (pkg/manifest/types.go:101-107, pkg/manifest/skill_test.go:31), and a skill is permitted to have an empty `ARTIFACT.md` body (pkg/manifest/parse.go:18-21). The MCP tools `load_domain` and `load_artifact` exist and are wired (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:290-296), and `podium layer reingest <id>` exists (cmd/podium/layer.go:301). Three discrepancies surfaced between the quickstart's illustrated output and the actual wire formats and CLI output.

### - [ ] F-0.0.1 — `podium layer reingest` does not emit the artifact/layer line the quickstart shows [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The quickstart (spec/00-quickstart.md:47-49) shows running `podium layer reingest org-defaults` and getting back:

```
artifact: finance/close-reporting/run-variance-analysis@1.0.0   layer: org-defaults
```

The CLI command POSTs to `/v1/layers/reingest?id=ID` and prints the raw HTTP response body with `fmt.Println(string(out))` (cmd/podium/layer.go:317-322). The server endpoint records the reingest intent and returns `{"queued": "<id>", "queued_at": "<RFC3339>"}` (pkg/registry/server/layers.go:404-407); a code comment states the actual ingest pipeline runs externally and the endpoint only records intent (pkg/registry/server/layers.go:378-382). No code path prints an `artifact: <id>@<version>   layer: <layer>` line; a repo-wide search for that format and for synchronous ingest under the reingest path found nothing (no `artifact: ` / ` layer: ` emitter in cmd/podium or pkg/registry/ingest, and no `reingest`-triggered ingest in pkg/registry/ingest or pkg/registry/filesystem). A reader following the quickstart sees `{"queued":"org-defaults","queued_at":"..."}` rather than a per-artifact confirmation, and the reingest is asynchronous rather than completing before the command returns. Suggested direction: either change the quickstart to show the actual queued/queued_at acknowledgement (and note that ingest is asynchronous), or have the CLI/endpoint surface the ingested artifact and layer once the standalone ingest scheduler that the comment references is wired.

### - [ ] F-0.0.2 — `load_domain` response keys in the quickstart (`domains`, `artifacts`) do not match the wire format (`subdomains`, `notable`) [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The quickstart (spec/00-quickstart.md:54-55) illustrates:

```
load_domain("finance/close-reporting")
→ {domains: [...], artifacts: [{id: "finance/close-reporting/run-variance-analysis", ...}]}
```

The actual `load_domain` response uses `subdomains` for the child-domain list and `notable` for the artifact list (pkg/registry/server/server.go:382-383: `Subdomains []DomainDescriptor json:"subdomains"`, `Notable []ArtifactDescriptor json:"notable"`). This matches the protocol section, which defines `load_domain` as returning the domain's "notable artifacts" and per-subdomain descriptions (spec/05-meta-tools.md:7, 28-30); the key `domains` is the search-response field (pkg/registry/server/server.go:409 `Domains json:"domains,omitempty"`), and `artifacts` does not appear in either response. The MCP bridge proxies `load_domain` through verbatim (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:733-738), so the agent receives `subdomains`/`notable`, not `domains`/`artifacts`. The artifact `id` field the quickstart shows is correct (pkg/registry/core/core.go:396 `ID ... json:"id"`). Suggested direction: change the quickstart's illustrated keys to `{subdomains: [...], notable: [{id: ...}]}` to match §5 and the implementation.

### - [ ] F-0.0.3 — `load_artifact` response in the quickstart uses `manifest:` and a single `materialized_at` string [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The quickstart (spec/00-quickstart.md:57-58) illustrates:

```
load_artifact("finance/close-reporting/run-variance-analysis")
→ {manifest: <SKILL.md body>, materialized_at: "/workspace/.podium/runtime/.../SKILL.md"}
```

The registry response field is `manifest_body`, not `manifest` (pkg/registry/server/server.go:421 `ManifestBody json:"manifest_body"`), and the MCP bridge returns the same key plus `materialized_at` as a list of absolute paths rather than a single string (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:443-450: `"manifest_body": resp.ManifestBody`, `"materialized_at": materialized` where `materialized` is a `[]string` built at main.go:413, 438-440). The protocol section corroborates the plural form, describing "the returned `materialized_at` paths" as absolute (spec/05-meta-tools.md:42). The quickstart's arrow notation is informal, so the impact is limited to a reader who copies the field names; the `manifest` versus `manifest_body` key and the scalar-versus-array `materialized_at` are both wrong relative to the wire format. Suggested direction: update the quickstart to `{manifest_body: <SKILL.md body>, materialized_at: ["/workspace/.podium/runtime/.../SKILL.md"]}`, or add a sentence noting the snippet is illustrative and pointing to §5 for the exact field names.
## F-1.1 — 1.1 What Podium Is

_Reviewed spec/01-overview.md against the implementation._

Section 1.1 is conceptual prose that introduces Podium and enumerates its capabilities. Although it states no wire formats, defaults, or error codes, it makes a set of concrete capability claims. I verified each claim against the code: the artifact types, the extension TypeProvider SPI, the discovery and load meta-tools, the two language SDKs, the `podium sync` one-shot and watcher modes, the `extends:` / `delegates_to:` / `mcpServers:` dependency edges, the most-restrictive-wins and highest-precedence composition rules, per-layer visibility, classification, freeze windows, signing, hash-chained audit, Postgres with pgvector, the HarnessAdapter with a `none` no-op, pluggable identity (OAuth device-code and injected session token), Git and local source ingestion, signed URLs, webhook ingest, and the workspace local overlay. Every concrete claim resolves to working implementation. No findings.

No findings.
## F-1.2 — 1.2 Problem Statement

_Reviewed spec/01-overview.md against the implementation._

Section 1.2 is conceptual framing. It enumerates the problems Podium addresses (capability saturation, discoverability at scale, visibility control, layered composition, governance, type heterogeneity, heterogeneous consumers, and cross-harness portability) and asserts that the implementation handles them together. I extracted every concrete claim from the prose and verified each against code. The artifact type list (skill, agent, context, command, rule, hook, mcp-server) matches pkg/manifest/types.go:19-25 exactly. The cross-type dependency edge field names cited in item 6 (delegates_to, mcpServers, extends) match pkg/manifest/types.go:118,129,139, pkg/dependency/graph.go:14-15, pkg/store/store.go:85, and pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:740-753. Reverse-dependency impact analysis exists at pkg/registry/core/dependents.go and cmd/podium/impact.go. Structured discovery and search exist at pkg/registry/core/rrf.go. Visibility enforcement exists across pkg/layer and pkg/registry/core. The three consumer paths named in the closing paragraph all exist: sdks/podium-py, sdks/podium-ts, cmd/podium-mcp, and the wired `podium sync` subcommand at cmd/podium/main.go:44. The code matches every concrete claim in this subsection.

No findings.
## F-1.3 — 1.3 Design Principles (incl 1.3.1 When Podium Helps)

_Reviewed spec/01-overview.md against the implementation._

Sections 1.3 and 1.3.1 are mostly conceptual prose that defers concrete contracts to later sections (§3 for lazy materialization, §4.6 for visibility and composition, §4.7 for immutability and signing, §4.7.5 for the dependency graph, §6.7 for adapters). Each concrete invariant that 1.3 states is implemented in the code. The artifact type system (`skill`, `agent`, `context`, `command`, `rule`, `hook`, `mcp-server`) is present in pkg/manifest/types.go:19-25 and is extensible through the TypeProvider SPI in pkg/typeprovider/typeprovider.go. Cross-type dependency edges (`extends`, `delegates_to`, `mcpServers`) match in pkg/dependency/graph.go:13-15. Per-layer visibility is evaluated on the request path in pkg/layer/composer.go:50-90. The immutability invariant is enforced in all three metadata stores (pkg/store/memory.go:56-69, pkg/store/sqlite.go:157-205, pkg/store/postgres.go:165-211) with consistent idempotent-on-same-hash and reject-on-different-hash semantics. Signing of higher-sensitivity artifacts is backed by a verification policy in pkg/sign/sign.go:74-92. One defect adjacent to the immutability invariant is recorded below; it concerns error reporting under concurrent ingest in the SQL-backed stores and is principally a §4.7 detail.

### - [x] F-1.3.1 — Concurrent ingest of conflicting bytes can leak a raw constraint error instead of a reported conflict [Low] — CLOSED

(bug) Section 1.3 states the immutability invariant: "Once `(artifact_id, version)` is ingested, it is bit-for-bit immutable in the registry's store regardless of subsequent Git mutations" and the same invariant applies to `local`-source layers. The invariant itself is upheld (no overwrite of existing bytes ever happens). The defect is in how a concurrent violation is reported. The SQL-backed stores implement `PutManifest` as a SELECT-then-INSERT inside a transaction: pkg/store/postgres.go:172-210 and pkg/store/sqlite.go:164-204 first `SELECT content_hash` for the `(tenant_id, artifact_id, version)` key and, when no row is found, fall through to an `INSERT`. The table has a primary key on `(tenant_id, artifact_id, version)` (pkg/store/postgres.go:83, pkg/store/sqlite.go:76). Under concurrent ingest of two different content hashes for the same key, both transactions can pass the SELECT (seeing no row under default isolation), then both attempt the INSERT; one commits and the other fails with a primary-key unique-constraint error. That raw error is returned directly from pkg/store/postgres.go:207-209 and pkg/store/sqlite.go:201-203 without being mapped to `store.ErrImmutableViolation`. The ingest orchestrator at pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:478-488 maps only `ErrImmutableViolation` to a `Conflicts` entry and returns any other error as a hard failure of the entire ingest batch (line 487). The concurrent-conflict test at pkg/registry/ingest/concurrent_test.go:97-160 exercises only `store.NewMemory()`, whose mutex serializes the check-and-insert (pkg/store/memory.go:57-67), so the SQL race path is not covered. The result is that a concurrent immutability violation against Postgres or SQLite can surface as an unmapped 500-class error and abort the batch rather than as the per-artifact conflict the invariant implies. Suggested direction: rewrite the SQL `PutManifest` to use `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (tenant_id, artifact_id, version) DO NOTHING` followed by a read-back comparison of the stored `content_hash`, returning `ErrImmutableViolation` when the stored hash differs, so the conflict path is deterministic under concurrency; alternatively, detect the driver's unique-violation error after the INSERT and map it to `ErrImmutableViolation`. Add a concurrent-conflict store conformance test that runs against the SQLite backend.

Resolution (commit f2dccdb): rewrote `Postgres.PutManifest` and `SQLite.PutManifest` to a single atomic `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (tenant_id, artifact_id, version) DO NOTHING` followed by a read-back of the stored `content_hash`, returning `store.ErrImmutableViolation` when the stored hash differs and a no-op when it matches, so the conflict path is deterministic under concurrency and never leaks a raw constraint error. The shared-cache in-memory SQLite path is serialized to one connection so concurrent writers queue instead of leaking `database table is locked`; file-backed databases keep the pooled WAL + `_busy_timeout` behavior. Added `ConcurrentImmutabilityViolation` to the store conformance suite (Memory, SQLite, and Postgres when `PODIUM_POSTGRES_DSN` is set), a file-backed multi-connection SQLite concurrency test, and an ingest-pipeline integration test over file-backed SQLite. The conformance test fails on the pre-fix SELECT-then-INSERT code (a raw error leaks under the race). The deterministic Postgres MVCC fail-first path is covered by the suite but could not be executed in this environment (no Postgres available); SQLite serializes writers, so the pre-fix code surfaces the leak through shared-cache lock contention rather than a primary-key violation.
## F-1.4 — 1.4 Constraints and Decisions

_Reviewed spec/01-overview.md against the implementation._

This subsection is a table of architectural decisions, most of which are conceptual prose. Each row that carries a concrete contract was traced to the implementing code. Version immutability is enforced bit-for-bit per `(tenant, artifact_id, version)` in every store backend (pkg/store/memory.go:54, pkg/store/sqlite.go:154, pkg/store/postgres.go:162) and in the ingest path (pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:440). The content-addressed cache is keyed by content hash at `~/.podium/cache/` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:779, cmd/podium/cache.go:54) and the workspace overlay lives at `.podium/overlay/` (pkg/overlay/overlay.go:32). The HarnessAdapter roster from row 83 is fully registered (pkg/adapter/adapter.go:100). The store and vector backends (postgres, sqlite, memory; pgvector, sqlitevec, pinecone, qdrant, weaviate) all exist and are pluggable. Ingestion is webhook-driven or triggered by `podium layer reingest` with no registry-side polling. Layer reorder and reingest endpoints exist (pkg/registry/server/layers.go:105). The single `admin` role exists with no per-artifact roles, and the MIT license file is present. One decision is not reflected in code: the per-identity cap on user-defined layers.

### - [x] F-1.4.1 — Cap of 3 user-defined layers per identity is not enforced [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) Row 89 of §1.4 states "Cap of 3 user-defined layers per identity by default" with rationale "Configurable per tenant. Keeps personal-layer growth bounded." The same requirement is restated normatively in §7.3.1 (spec/07-external-integration.md:95: "Default cap: 3 user-defined layers per identity, configurable per tenant") and is listed as a required verification test in spec/11-verification.md:53 ("the user-defined-layer cap is enforced"). The layer registration handler at pkg/registry/server/layers.go:183 (`register`, POST /v1/layers) performs no count of existing user-defined layers owned by the registrant before calling `PutLayerConfig` (pkg/registry/server/layers.go:264). A grep across the repository finds no constant, config field, or check for a user-defined-layer cap: the `store.Quota` struct (pkg/store/store.go:36) carries `StorageBytes`, `SearchQPS`, `MaterializeRate`, and `AuditVolumePerDay`, but no per-identity layer limit, and no enforcement appears in pkg/registry/core/quota.go, pkg/layer, or the CLI. An authenticated caller can register an unbounded number of personal layers. Suggested direction: add a per-tenant configurable limit (default 3) to the tenant quota or layer config, count the caller's existing `UserDefined` layers with matching `Owner` in `register`, and reject with a `429`/quota error envelope (for example `quota.layer_count_exceeded`, mirroring the existing `quota.artifact_count_exceeded` pattern in pkg/registry/ingest) when the projected count would exceed the limit. Note that §7.3.1 is owned by another subsection auditor; this finding records that the row 89 decision is absent from the implementation.

**Resolution (commit `39d402d`):** Canonical fix for this gap; also closes F-7.3.5, F-10.0.1, and F-14.9.1. Added `store.Quota.MaxUserLayers` (zero selects the default of 3 via `server.DefaultMaxUserLayers`, negative disables; persisted by the SQLite and Postgres tenant schemas and covered by a new `storetest.Suite` QuotaRoundTrip case). `LayerEndpoint.register` resolves the effective cap (a `WithMaxUserLayers` override, then the per-tenant quota, then the default) and rejects a user-defined registration that would exceed it with `quota.layer_count_exceeded` at HTTP 429; re-registering an already-owned layer (same id) is an update and is not counted, and admin-defined layers are never capped. serverboot wires `PODIUM_MAX_USER_LAYERS` for the standalone deployment.
## F-1.5 — 1.5 Where Podium Fits

_Reviewed spec/01-overview.md against the implementation._

This subsection positions Podium against adjacent product categories in a comparison table and states the scope of that comparison. It contains conceptual prose rather than concrete API contracts, defaults, endpoints, or invariants. The few concrete claims it makes are the integration points and capabilities named in the "When Podium wins" column: the three consumer paths (language SDKs, MCP server, `podium sync`), the artifact type list (skills, agents, contexts, commands, rules, hooks, MCP server registrations), cross-type dependency edges (`extends:`, `delegates_to:`, `mcpServers:` resolving to `mcp-server` artifacts), per-OIDC-group visibility composed across multiple sources, the published harness-adapter contract for foreign harnesses, and on-prem/standalone deployment. Each of these is implemented and consistent with the spec.

Verification evidence:
- Consumer paths: `cmd/podium` (CLI with `sync`), `cmd/podium-server`, `cmd/podium-mcp`, and `sdks/podium-py` plus `sdks/podium-ts` all exist.
- Artifact types match line 100 exactly: `pkg/manifest/types.go:19-25` defines `skill`, `agent`, `context`, `command`, `rule`, `hook`, and `mcp-server`.
- Cross-type dependency edges named on line 112: `pkg/dependency/graph.go:13-15` defines `EdgeExtends`, `EdgeDelegatesTo`, and `EdgeMCPServer` ("mcpServers"), with a header comment stating edges span types.
- Per-OIDC-group visibility: `pkg/layer/composer.go:14-16` and `:60-71` implement `Public`, `Organization`, and `Groups` filters with group expansion against the caller's JWT groups.
- Published harness-adapter contract for foreign harnesses: `pkg/adapter/adapter.go:38-39` defines the `HarnessAdapter` SPI, with a built-in set including `none` for raw output (`pkg/adapter/none.go`) and the foreign harnesses listed in the table (`pkg/adapter/builtins.go`, `codex.go`, `claudecode.go`).
- On-prem/standalone: `pkg/store/sqlite.go` and local-source layers in `pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:37-65` back the standalone deployment claim.

The forward-looking statement on line 114 about upstream contribution to an MCP-adjacent or AAIF-governed standard is explicitly aspirational ("once the right venue exists; until then, it is specified here") and imposes no implementation requirement. No code contradicts it.

No findings.
## F-1.6 — 1.6 Project Model

_Reviewed spec/01-overview.md against the implementation._

Section 1.6 states project metadata: license, governance, distribution, public registry, multi-vendor neutrality, and standards engagement. Most of these are policy statements without a runtime contract, so the verifiable surface is the set of repository-level files. The license claim holds: `LICENSE` is MIT, and `GOVERNANCE.md:26` and `CONTRIBUTING.md:83` both confirm MIT. `GOVERNANCE.md` exists and describes a single-maintainer governance model, which matches the "Maintainer model" half of the governance claim. The distribution, multi-vendor neutrality, and standards-engagement statements are policy with no code contract and produce no findings. The remaining items show two terminology and reference deviations and one unverifiable hosting claim, detailed below.

### - [ ] F-1.6.1 — Governance process is described as ADR, not "RFC process" [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 1.6 states: "Governance. Maintainer model + RFC process for spec changes; see `GOVERNANCE.md`." `GOVERNANCE.md` describes the decision-making process as Architecture Decision Records, not an RFC process: "Proposals are filed as GitHub Discussions or draft ADRs in `docs/adr/`" (`GOVERNANCE.md:19`), "Decisions are documented in the relevant ADR or issue" (`GOVERNANCE.md:21`). The word "RFC" does not appear in `GOVERNANCE.md`, and the document carries no "spec changes" framing. The spec's "RFC process" wording is also propagated verbatim into the docs site at `docs/getting-started/why-podium.md:130` ("Maintainer model with an RFC process for spec changes"), while the canonical governance page `docs/about/governance.md:27` again uses ADR terminology. The spec and the referenced authority disagree on the process name. Suggested direction: align the terminology. Either rename the process to "RFC" consistently in `GOVERNANCE.md`, `docs/about/governance.md`, and `docs/getting-started/why-podium.md`, or change spec §1.6 (and `why-podium.md:130`) to say "ADR process" to match `GOVERNANCE.md`.

### - [ ] F-1.6.2 — Governance docs reference a non-existent `docs/adr/` directory [Low] — OPEN

(bug) `GOVERNANCE.md:19` links proposals to `docs/adr/` ("draft ADRs in [`docs/adr/`](docs/adr/)"), and `docs/about/governance.md:27` repeats the same path ("draft ADRs in `docs/adr/`"). The directory `docs/adr/` does not exist in the repository (`ls -d docs/adr` returns "No such file or directory"). The link in `GOVERNANCE.md` resolves to a missing location and the prose points contributors to a directory that is absent. This is the location §1.6 directs readers to via "see `GOVERNANCE.md`". Suggested direction: create `docs/adr/` with at least a placeholder index (for example `docs/adr/README.md` describing the ADR format and numbering), or update both `GOVERNANCE.md:19` and `docs/about/governance.md:27` to reference the location where decision records actually live.

### - [ ] F-1.6.3 — Public registry "hosted at the project's public URL" is not verifiable in-repo [Info] — OPEN

(gap) Section 1.6 states: "Public registry. A reference registry with curated example artifacts is hosted at the project's public URL." The repository contains a reference registry as a test fixture under `testdata/registries/reference/` (`testdata/registries/reference/README.md:1`), exercised by `test/conformance/reference_registry_test.go`. No concrete public URL is configured anywhere in the repository; a grep for hosting hostnames (`podium.dev`, `registry.podium`, and similar) returns no deployment configuration, and the parallel claim in `spec/09-extensibility.md:32` and `docs/deployment/extending.md:51` ("A community plugin registry is hosted at the project's public URL") is likewise abstract. This is a forward-looking hosting statement rather than a code contract, so no defect is asserted. Recorded as an observation: the in-repo "reference registry" is a test fixture, and the hosted public registry is external to this repository and cannot be confirmed from the code. No action is required unless §1.6 is intended to assert an in-repo deliverable.
## F-2.1 — 2.1 High-Level Component Map

_Reviewed spec/02-architecture.md against the implementation._

The component map describes the registry as the system of record, three consumers (the Podium MCP server, `podium sync`, and the language SDKs), the meta-tools, the shared identity providers, the load_artifact MCP sequence, and two deployment scenarios for the MCP server binary. The structural claims hold in code: the three binaries exist (cmd/podium, cmd/podium-mcp, cmd/podium-server), the meta-tools `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact` are registered and proxied to the registry (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:260-296), the identity built-ins `oauth-device-code` and `injected-session-token` exist (pkg/identity/identity.go:58, identity.go:86), the registry is backed by Postgres and pgvector (pkg/store/postgres.go, pkg/vector/pgvector.go), the MCP server verifies, adapts, and atomically writes resources and fetches large resources from presigned URLs (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:392-435, large_resources.go:59), and `podium sync` is the only consumer that opens a filesystem-source registry (pkg/sync/sync.go:90). The findings below concern the two deployment-scenario claims for the developer host and one wire-protocol mismatch in the sequence diagram. The canonical contracts for the deployment-scenario details live in §6.3 and §6.4; they are reported here because 2.1 states them as concrete behavior of the MCP server.

### - [ ] F-2.1.1 — MCP server does not implement device-code flow, elicitation, or keychain storage described for the developer host [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 2.1 "Developer's host" deployment scenario (line 83) states: "The MCP server uses an OAuth device-code flow on first use (surfaced via MCP elicitation) to obtain a registry token, stored in the OS keychain." The MCP server binary implements none of this. Its only token sources are the `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN`/`PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_ENV` environment variable and `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:97-106, currentToken at main.go:753-773). When no token is configured, `fetchJSON` omits the Authorization header entirely (main.go:706-708); there is no device-code initiation. A repo-wide search confirms the MCP server contains no elicitation code (`grep -rln "elicit" cmd/podium-mcp` returns nothing) and no device-code or keychain references. The OAuth device-code flow and keychain storage are implemented in pkg/identity (oauth_devicecode.go, keychain.go) and wired only into the `podium login` CLI command (cmd/podium/login.go:53, login.go:77). The implemented model is that a separate `podium login` invocation performs device-code and writes the keychain, after which the MCP server reads a token from env/file. Suggested direction: either wire the device-code flow plus MCP elicitation and keychain read into the MCP server so it matches the scenario, or update 2.1 to describe the actual split where `podium login` obtains and stores the token and the MCP server consumes it from env/file.

### - [ ] F-2.1.2 — Workspace overlay default path `${WORKSPACE}/.podium/overlay/` is not resolved by any consumer [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 2.1 "Developer's host" scenario (line 83) states: "The workspace local overlay reads from `${WORKSPACE}/.podium/overlay/`." The MCP server reads the overlay only from the `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` environment variable (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:107, main.go:168-176); when that variable is empty the overlay layer is disabled. The default-path resolution function `overlay.ResolveWorkspaceOverlay` (pkg/overlay/overlay.go:64-76) implements the documented fallback to `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/`, but a repo-wide search shows it has no callers (`grep -rln "ResolveWorkspaceOverlay" --include=*.go .` returns only the definition file). As a result, the `${WORKSPACE}/.podium/overlay/` default the scenario promises is never applied; the overlay works only when the path is supplied explicitly via `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH`. Suggested direction: call `ResolveWorkspaceOverlay` from the MCP server (passing the workspace directory) so the documented default fallback applies, or update 2.1 to state that the overlay path must be supplied through `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH`.

### - [ ] F-2.1.3 — load_artifact sequence diagram shows `POST /artifacts` but the implementation uses `GET /v1/load_artifact` [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The load_artifact sequence diagram embedded in 2.1 (the SVG at line 52 and its ASCII fallback at lines 54-77) shows the MCP server sending `POST /artifacts` to the registry, and the SVG alt text describes the MCP server as one "which posts to the registry." The SVG source itself contains the literal strings `POST` and `/artifacts` (docs/assets/diagrams/load-artifact-sequence.svg lines 53-54). The implementation uses an HTTP GET against `/v1/load_artifact` with `id` as a query parameter: the MCP server calls `s.fetchJSON("/v1/load_artifact", args)` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:331) and `fetchJSON` builds a GET request (main.go:686-702), and the registry registers the route as `mux.HandleFunc("/v1/load_artifact", s.handleLoadArtifact)` (pkg/registry/server/server.go:328) where the handler reads `r.URL.Query().Get("id")` (server.go:676-677). The method and path in the diagram do not match the wire protocol. Suggested direction: update the SVG, the ASCII fallback, and the alt text to show `GET /v1/load_artifact?id=...` so the sequence diagram matches the implemented request.
## F-2.2 — 2.2 Component Responsibilities

_Reviewed spec/02-architecture.md against the implementation (re-run against main e41f44e)._

This subsection is a responsibilities overview, and most concrete claims hold on main. The Podium Registry machinery (effective-view composition via `pkg/layer/composer.go`, the visibility evaluator `Visible`/`VisibleWith`, manifest indexing, hybrid search, URL signing, the cross-type dependency graph, and change events) is present in `pkg/layer`, `pkg/registry/*`, `pkg/dependency`, and `pkg/objectstore`. The MCP server local state (content-addressed cache, injected-session-token credential, in-memory local overlay, atomic-write materialization) is present in `cmd/podium-mcp`. The IdentityProvider built-ins (`oauth-device-code`, `injected-session-token`) and the full HarnessAdapter roster (`none`, `claude-code`, `claude-desktop`, `claude-cowork`, `cursor`, `codex`, `gemini`, `opencode`, `pi`, `hermes`) match the spec. The shared Go library (`LayerComposer`, parsers, `extends:` resolver, visibility evaluator, harness adapters, `pkg/materialize/atomic.go`, lint rules) is genuinely shared across the registry, the MCP server, and `podium sync`. Three findings remain: the SDKs lack `materialize()`, `podium sync` has no server-source HTTP path, and the registry never wires per-OAuth-identity resolution for either documented identity provider so it does not apply per-layer visibility. All three prior findings carried forward; F-2.2.3 was CORRECTED because its prior citations referenced feature-branch code absent on main (a `trusted-headers` extension, `server.HeaderIdentityResolver`, and serverboot "not yet implemented" log lines), and its severity was raised from Info to Medium. The other two were STILL OPEN with refreshed line numbers. Zero prior findings resolved.

### - [ ] F-2.2.1 — SDKs do not expose materialize() with a harness parameter [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 2.2 (line 101) states "The SDKs accept a harness parameter on `materialize()`." Section 7.6 (spec/07-external-integration.md) gives the concrete contract `artifact.materialize(to="./artifacts/", harness="claude-code")`. Neither SDK implements a `materialize()` method on main. In `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py` the `LoadedArtifact` dataclass (lines 54-62) is a plain dataclass with no methods, and the `Client` (line 65) exposes `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, `load_artifact`, `load_artifacts`, `dependents_of`, `preview_scope`, and `subscribe`, none named `materialize`. In `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts` the `LoadedArtifact` interface (line 21) has no methods and the client (methods at lines 118-227) has no `materialize`. A repository-wide search for `materialize` under `sdks/podium-ts/src/` returns zero matches, and the only `materialize` symbols under `sdks/podium-py/` are unrelated. The sole place a `harness` parameter exists in either SDK is the batch loader: `load_artifacts` forwards `harness` into the `/v1/artifacts:batchLoad` request body (`client.py:173`, `client.py:192-193`), and `loadArtifacts` does the same (`index.ts:166`, `index.ts:177`). That is server-side adaptation, not client-side materialization to disk. Suggested direction: add a `materialize(to, harness=...)` method to the loaded-artifact object (or the client) in both SDKs that writes the canonical or harness-adapted layout to disk, or, if the SDKs are intended to remain pure HTTP clients with no local materialization, update §2.2 line 101 and the §7.6 example to drop the `materialize()` contract.

### - [ ] F-2.2.2 — podium sync has no server-source HTTP path; --watch polls the filesystem instead of subscribing to change events [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 2.2 (line 93) describes `podium sync` as a command that "reads the user's effective view from the registry and writes it to a host-configured layout," with "One-shot or `--watch` mode (subscribes to registry change events)," and line 103 says "`podium sync` in server-source mode are thin HTTP clients that call the registry, then invoke the same module's materialization writer locally." Section 2.1 (line 7) lists `podium sync` among the consumers that "read from the registry over HTTP." On main, only the filesystem-source path exists. In `pkg/sync/sync.go` the `Options` struct (lines 37-48) exposes only `RegistryPath` (the filesystem-source path) with no URL field, and `Run` (line 72) documents that it "does not consult any HTTP service" (line 66) and opens the source with `filesystem.Open(opts.RegistryPath)` (line 90). The CLI in `cmd/podium/main.go` declares `--registry` as "filesystem registry path (required)" (line 189) and errors when it is unset with a message that names a filesystem path (line 212). The `--watch` flag (line 194) routes to `runWatchLoop` (line 246), which calls `sync.Watch` with the filesystem `RegistryPath` (lines 249-252). `sync.Watch` in `pkg/sync/watch.go` requires `opts.Sync.RegistryPath` (line 52) and runs a poll-based watcher (`runWatch`, line 69) that recomputes `watchSignature` over `(path, modtime, size)` tuples of the local registry tree (lines 86, 99, 114-149). It never opens an HTTP connection and never consumes the registry change events (`artifact.published`, `artifact.deprecated`, `layer.config_changed`) from §7.5. The server side of the contract exists: the registry serves `GET /v1/events` (`pkg/registry/server/events.go:112-119`, `handleEvents` at line 119), and the SDKs subscribe to it (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:252`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:228`). Only `podium sync` is missing the server-source path. Suggested direction: add a server (URL) source to `pkg/sync` that reads the effective view over the registry HTTP API, and in `--watch` mode against a URL source subscribe to `/v1/events` to trigger reruns, while keeping the filesystem poller for filesystem-source registries.

### - [ ] F-2.2.3 — Registry never wires per-OAuth-identity resolution for either documented identity provider, so it does not apply per-layer visibility [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 2.2 (line 87) states the registry "Composes the caller's effective view from the configured layer list per OAuth identity, applies per-layer visibility." On main the composer and the visibility evaluator exist (`pkg/layer/composer.go` `Compose` at line 121, `Visible`/`VisibleWith` at lines 50-59), but the production bootstrap never connects a configured identity provider to request-time identity resolution. The server exposes `WithIdentityResolver` to "swap the default anonymous-public resolver for one that maps an HTTP request to an Identity (e.g., decoded JWT)" (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:110-114`), and when no resolver is installed the default treats every caller as `layer.Identity{IsPublic: true}` (`server.go:177-181`). The per-request `identity` helper only forces `IsPublic` when public mode is on, otherwise it returns whatever `resolveID` yields (`server.go:802-808`). A repository-wide search shows `WithIdentityResolver` is called only by tests (`pkg/registry/server/admin_test.go:38`); no production code installs it, and the comment at `pkg/registry/server/admin.go:96` confirms the intent: "Tests bypass via WithIdentityResolver; production wires the JWT-decoded identity." The bootstrap does not wire it: `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go` reads `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` into config (lines 545, 629) and validates only that public mode and an identity provider are mutually exclusive (`server.StartupConfig.Validate`, `pkg/registry/server/config_validate.go:28-34`), but `bootstrapOptions` (serverboot.go:664-675) adds `WithPublicMode` and `WithObjectStore` and never adds `WithIdentityResolver`. The result is that a registry started with `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER=oauth-device-code` or `injected-session-token` (and public mode off) keeps the default anonymous-public resolver, so it does not compose per OAuth identity and does not apply per-layer visibility filtering against the caller, contrary to the responsibility §2.2 line 87 attributes to the registry. The detailed server-side verifier contract belongs to §6.3, so this is the §2.2-level symptom of that gap; on main there is no `trusted-headers` extension, no `server.HeaderIdentityResolver`, and no per-provider "not yet implemented" bootstrap logging (the prior finding cited those because it ran on a feature branch; they are absent here). Suggested direction: in serverboot, when a non-`none` `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` is configured, install a `WithIdentityResolver` that verifies the bearer credential and maps it to `layer.Identity`, tracked under §6.3 server-side verifier work; alternatively, fail startup when an identity provider is configured but no verifier is wired so an operator never silently runs a private registry as anonymous-public.
## F-3.1 — 3.1 The Problem

_Reviewed spec/03-disclosure-surface.md against the implementation._

Section 3.1 is purely motivational prose. It states that tool-call accuracy degrades past roughly 50 to 100 tools in a single system prompt and falls off past roughly 200, and concludes that discovery must be staged for larger catalogs. The subsection defines no fields, flags, defaults, commands, endpoints, invariants, or orderings that the code must implement. The single directive that discovery must be staged is realized by the disclosure layers in §3.2 and following, which fall outside this subsection's scope. A confirmatory grep shows the staged-discovery meta-tools exist in the implementation (cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go, load_artifact, prompts.go, and internal/serverboot/serverboot.go) and that the docs describe discovery as staged (docs/consuming/browsing-the-catalog.md:22), so the conceptual premise is not contradicted by the code. There is no concrete contract in §3.1 to verify against.

No findings.
## F-3.2 — 3.2 Three Disclosure Layers

_Reviewed spec/03-disclosure-surface.md against the implementation._

I checked the §3.2 layer-to-meta-tool mapping and the three layer contracts against the registry core (`pkg/registry/core/core.go`), the HTTP server (`pkg/registry/server/server.go`), the MCP bridge (`cmd/podium-mcp`), the CLI (`cmd/podium/main.go`), and the discovery and hybrid tests. The four meta-tools exist and are registered over MCP and the HTTP API, and the layer mapping in the spec's opening sentence is accurate. Layer 3 (`load_artifact`) is well-implemented: the manifest body is returned inline, large resources are delivered via presigned URLs, and the MCP bridge fetches them lazily with hash verification and retry. Layer 1's `search_domains` and the discovery-config-driven rendering of `load_domain` diverge from the spec, and the Layer 2 hybrid retriever has a defect that suppresses semantic-only matches.

### - [x] F-3.2.1 — search_domains does not run hybrid retrieval over domain projections [High] — CLOSED

(gap) §3.2 Layer 1 states that when the host calls `search_domains(query)`, "Hybrid retrieval (BM25 + embeddings, fused via reciprocal rank) runs over each domain's projection (frontmatter `description` + `keywords` + truncated prose body, per §4.7) and returns ranked domain descriptors." The implementation does none of this. `Registry.SearchDomains` (pkg/registry/core/core.go:646-697) derives the candidate domain set from the unique ancestor paths of visible manifests (lines 664-677) and filters them with a plain case-insensitive substring test against the path string: `if q != "" && !strings.Contains(strings.ToLower(p), q)` (lines 678-685). It sorts the survivors alphabetically (line 686) rather than by any relevance score, and the returned `DomainDescriptor` entries carry only `Path` and `Name` (lines 691-695); `Description` and keywords are never populated because the path-derived domains have no DOMAIN.md projection attached. There is no domain-level embedding anywhere: ingest composes an embedding projection for artifacts only (pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:585 `composeEmbeddingText`), and no equivalent exists for domains. The code comment on `SearchDomains` (core.go:643-645) acknowledges the deferral: "Phase 12 enriches this with §4.5.5 keyword projections; for now, domains are derived from the unique paths of visible manifests." The HTTP and CLI surfaces exist (server.go:537-559, cmd/podium/main.go:626) and the smoke test (pkg/registry/server/extra_handlers_test.go:14-30) only asserts a 200 and a query echo, so the substring behavior is the real behavior. Suggested direction: generate and store a domain projection (description, keywords, truncated body from DOMAIN.md) at ingest, embed it, and run the same BM25-plus-vector RRF path that `SearchArtifacts` uses so `search_domains` returns relevance-ranked descriptors with descriptions.

Resolution: `SearchDomains` (new pkg/registry/core/domain_search.go) now runs the shared BM25 ranker (`bm25Rank`, extracted from `scoreBM25`) over each visible DOMAIN.md's projection (`domain.EmbeddingProjection` = description + keywords + body truncated to 500 tokens), and RRF-fuses with a domain vector index when configured; descriptors carry path/name/description/keywords/score, domains without a DOMAIN.md or under an unlisted ancestor are excluded, and visibility is honored via `mergedDomains`. Domain projections are embedded at ingest (`DomainVectorPut` hook) and by `podium admin reembed` under the reserved `DomainVectorVersion` sentinel. Commit b354da3.

### - [x] F-3.2.2 — load_domain ignores DOMAIN.md imports and registry.yaml discovery config [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §3.2 Layer 1 states that the map rendering "is governed by the discovery rules in §4.5.5, configured at tenant scope in `registry.yaml` and overridable per-subtree via `DOMAIN.md`," that "a domain's children may be augmented or curated by an optional `DOMAIN.md` config that imports artifacts from elsewhere," and that "Multi-membership is allowed: one artifact can show up under more than one domain via imports." The served `load_domain` path realizes none of the DOMAIN.md or registry.yaml inputs. `Registry.LoadDomain` (pkg/registry/core/core.go:239-353) computes the tree purely from manifest `ArtifactID` prefixes via `manifestsUnder` (core.go:358-369); it never loads a DOMAIN.md, never calls `domain.MergeAcrossLayers`, and never applies `Include`/`Exclude` globs, so an artifact can only appear under its own directory path and multi-membership via imports is unreachable. The discovery-config knobs are reachable only through hand-built `LoadDomainOptions` (NotableCount, Featured, FoldBelowArtifacts, FoldPassthroughChains, TargetResponseTokens), but the HTTP handler hardcodes only the caller's `depth` query param and leaves the rest at code defaults: `core.LoadDomainOptions{Depth: atoiOr(q.Get("depth"), 0)}` (server.go:508-509). The `pkg/domain` merge logic (pkg/domain/domain.go:22-74) is never invoked by the registry or serverboot, and the `registry.yaml` discovery block is parsed into `yamlDiscovery` (internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:22, 50-56) but never read or applied anywhere. The net effect is that tenant-scoped discovery configuration and per-subtree DOMAIN.md curation have no effect on served responses. This gap's primary home is §4.5 and §4.5.5, but §3.2 references the behavior directly. Suggested direction: wire DOMAIN.md resolution (merge across layers, apply imports for multi-membership) and the registry.yaml discovery defaults into the `LoadDomain` path so the served map honors the configured rendering rules.

Resolution: already closed by the §4.5 batch (commit 065a613). `LoadDomain` now loads every visible DOMAIN.md via `mergedDomains`/`domain.MergeAcrossLayers`, applies `include:`/`exclude:` imports for multi-membership (`domainpkg.ResolveImports` into the notable candidate pool), and resolves the discovery knobs from registry.yaml and per-domain DOMAIN.md via `resolveKnobs` (F-4.5.8..13). Covered by `TestDomainComposition_IngestToLoadDomain` (imports surface under the importing domain) and `TestLoadDomain_TenantDiscoveryDefaultsApplied`. Verified still in force this batch.

### - [x] F-3.2.3 — hybrid search_artifacts drops vector-only matches [Medium] — CLOSED

(bug) §3.2 Layer 2 states that `search_artifacts` "runs a hybrid retriever (BM25 + embeddings, fused via reciprocal rank) over manifest text." The fusion in `Registry.SearchArtifacts` cannot surface any artifact that the vector ranker finds but BM25 misses, which defeats the purpose of adding embeddings. `scoreBM25` appends a record to its output only when the lexical score is strictly positive: `if score > 0 { out = append(...) }` (pkg/registry/core/core.go:1210-1212), so an artifact with no query-term overlap is absent from `scored`. The fusion step builds the lexical input from that already-filtered list (`lexIDs := scoredIDs(scored)`), fuses it with the vector ranks (`fused := RRFFuse(lexIDs, vecRanks)`), then reorders with `reorderScored(scored, fused)` (core.go:555-557). `RRFFuse` correctly unions both lists (rrf.go:19-47), so a vector-only ID does appear in `fused`, but `reorderScored` rebuilds the result from a map keyed on the BM25 records only and silently drops any fused ID not present there: `for _, id := range fused { if sc, ok := byID[id]; ok { out = append(...) } }` (core.go:620-632). A semantically related artifact that uses different wording than the query is therefore never returned, so the embeddings half can only reorder lexical hits and never contributes a new candidate. The hybrid test exercises only queries that overlap lexically with the descriptions (pkg/registry/core/hybrid_test.go:70-71 uses query "alpha skill" against description "alpha skill"), so the defect is uncaught. Suggested direction: when building the result, materialize descriptors for vector-only IDs by fetching their records from the filtered candidate set rather than dropping them, so `reorderScored` (or its replacement) preserves every entry in `fused`.

Resolution: `reorderScored` now takes the visible candidate set (`latestByID(filtered)`) and materializes a descriptor (score 0, fused rank) for any fused ID the BM25 set lacks, so vector-only matches surface. The same union semantics drive the new `search_domains` fusion. Commit b354da3.
## F-3.3 — 3.3 Three Enabling Concerns

_Reviewed spec/03-disclosure-surface.md against the implementation._

Section 3.3 names three concerns the disclosure surface depends on: visibility filtering, description quality, and learn-from-usage reranking. Visibility filtering is fully implemented in `pkg/registry/core/core.go` and `pkg/layer/composer.go`: every meta-tool call routes through `visibleManifests`, which composes the effective view from the configured layer list via `layer.EffectiveLayersWith` and filters manifests by visible layer, matching the §3.3 description and the §4.6 detail. The other two concerns are largely or entirely absent. The description-quality lint validates only that a skill `description` is non-empty and implements no thin-description or summary-collision check. Learn-from-usage reranking has no implementation at all: there is no search-to-load correlation, no rerank path, no import-candidate suggestion, and no underperforming-description signal. The MCP server advertises a `sessionCorrelation` capability that no code backs.

### - [ ] F-3.3.1 — Learn-from-usage reranking is entirely unimplemented [Medium] — DEFERRED

(gap) Section 3.3 states under "Learn-from-usage reranking" that the registry "observes which artifacts actually get loaded after which queries (correlated within a `session_id`; see §5), and uses that signal to (a) rerank search results, (b) suggest import candidates to domain owners, and (c) flag artifacts whose authored descriptions underperform retrieval expectations." None of these three behaviors exist in the code. A repo-wide search for `rerank`, `learn.from`, `import candidate`, `underperform`, and any usage-signal or analytics surface returns no matches in `pkg/`, `cmd/`, `internal/`, the SDKs, or the web UI. The only `session` machinery in the registry core is the latest-version pin memo for §4.7.6 (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:51-52`, `:735-855`, exercised by `pkg/registry/core/session_test.go`), which records `(session, artifact) -> version` solely to keep `latest` resolution consistent within a session. It does not correlate queries with subsequent loads. The audit event type carries only `Type`, `Caller`, `Target`, and a generic `Context map[string]string` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:90-95`) with no session field, so there is no substrate that retains the search-to-load signal. Search result ordering comes from RRF over BM25 and vector ranks (`pkg/registry/core/rrf.go`) with no usage-based reordering, and `load_domain` notable ordering uses only `featured` plus alphabetical order (`orderNotable` at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:438-460`), even though §5 specifies notable artifacts as "`featured` + learn-from-usage signal." Suggested direction: either implement the search-to-load correlation store and the three downstream consumers, or, if this is deferred, mark it explicitly as future work in the spec so the gap is intentional rather than silent.

Deferral: §3.3 names learn-from-usage reranking as an enabling concern but the spec defines no mechanism — no usage-signal storage schema, no search-to-load correlation algorithm, no rerank weighting, no import-candidate or underperforming-description thresholds, and no API, CLI, or audit surface. The §10 MVP build sequence (phases 0–19) contains no phase for it, and §8 (the natural audit substrate) does not reference it. Implementing would require inventing an unspecified subsystem whose tests could only assert the invented mechanism rather than a spec contract, so "implement to match the spec" is not well-defined here; the spec is read-only and cannot be marked future-work in place. No code changed (tree stays green). The `session_id` substrate this would build on is now threaded end-to-end by F-3.3.3, but the three downstream consumers remain unspecified, so this finding is not directly unblocked.

### - [x] F-3.3.2 — Description-quality lint does not flag thin descriptions or colliding summaries [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) Section 3.3 states under "Description quality" that "The registry lints for thin descriptions and flags clusters of artifacts whose summaries collide." The lint package (`pkg/lint/lint.go`) implements neither check. The only description-related rule, `ruleSkillCompliance`, errors when a skill `SKILL.md` has an empty top-level `description` (`pkg/lint/lint.go:149-151`); it does not evaluate description length, quality, or the "when should I use this?" guidance the spec calls for, and it applies only to skills, not to the universal artifact `description`. No cross-artifact rule compares descriptions or summaries for collision: the registered rule set in `AllRules` (`pkg/lint/lint.go:71-86`) has no collision or duplicate-summary rule, and a repo-wide search for `thin`, `collid`, and description-similarity logic finds nothing in `pkg/lint` or elsewhere. The `cluster`/collision-adjacent code that does exist, `pkg/registry/core/analyze.go`, computes tag-distribution entropy and fold/split candidates for the §4.5.5 domain-reshape report; it operates on tags and subtree counts and has no connection to description text. The same two lint behaviors are restated in §12 ("Ingest-time lint flags thin descriptions and clusters of artifacts with colliding summaries"), so the contract is consistent across the spec and unmet by the code. Suggested direction: add a thin-description lint rule with a documented length or content threshold over the universal `description` field, and add a cross-artifact rule that groups artifacts whose descriptions or summaries are near-identical and emits a warning per cluster.

Resolution: added `lint.thin_description` and `lint.colliding_descriptions` (`pkg/lint/description_rules.go`). The thin rule flags a present-but-inadequate effective description (universal `description`, or SKILL.md `description` for skills) below a documented length/word threshold; the collision rule clusters artifacts whose descriptions match after case/punctuation/whitespace normalization and warns each member, naming its peers. Per §3.3 ("The registry lints…") and §12 ("Ingest-time lint flags…") these run in the registry ingest pipeline over the ingested record set and surface via `ingest.Result.Advisories` (serverboot logs the count); they are advisory (non-gating) and deliberately excluded from the author-facing `podium lint` `AllRules()`. Commit 40d581d.

### - [x] F-3.3.3 — MCP server advertises `sessionCorrelation` capability with no backing behavior [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) Section 3.3 ties learn-from-usage to correlation "within a `session_id`," and the glossary describes the session ID as "used by the registry for `latest`-resolution consistency and learn-from-usage reranking." The MCP server advertises `"sessionCorrelation": true` in its `initialize` capabilities response (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:253`), and an integration test asserts on that advertisement (`test/integration/mcp_test.go:41`). No MCP code generates, accepts, or forwards a `session_id`. The MCP `searchArtifacts` handler forwards the raw `args` map to `/v1/search_artifacts` without originating or threading a session identifier (`cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:12-44`), and no MCP file other than the capability declaration references a session at all (a grep for `session` across `cmd/podium-mcp/*.go` matches only `main.go:253`). The HTTP batch-load endpoint does accept `session_id` (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:21`), but the registry consumes it only for §4.7.6 latest pinning, not for any correlation that the advertised capability would imply. The advertisement therefore overstates what the MCP bridge does. Suggested direction: either thread a host-supplied or bridge-generated `session_id` through the MCP search and load calls and implement the correlation behavior, or drop the `sessionCorrelation` capability flag until the behavior exists, and update the integration-test expectation accordingly.

Resolution: took the first option, because §5 mandates `sessionCorrelation: true` in the `initialize` response, so dropping the flag would violate the spec. The bridge now originates a per-process RFC 4122 v4 `session_id` (`newSessionID` in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`) and threads it through every meta-tool call in `fetchJSON` (a host-supplied `session_id` argument overrides it). The registry's GET `/v1/load_artifact` now reads `session_id` into `LoadArtifactOptions` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go`), so §4.7.6 session-consistent `latest` resolution — previously wired only on batch-load — backs the capability over the MCP path. Verified end-to-end: a bridge process pins `latest` across a mid-session ingest while a fresh process sees the new latest. Commit 40d581d.
## F-3.4 — 3.4 Discovery Flow

_Reviewed spec/03-disclosure-surface.md against the implementation._

Section 3.4 is a narrative subsection that synthesizes the disclosure contracts defined in §3.2 and §6.6. Its concrete, verifiable claims are the discovery sequence (an empty session calls `load_domain()` or `search_domains(query)`, drills with `load_domain("<sub>")` or jumps to `search_artifacts(query, scope="<domain>")`, then calls `load_artifact`), the per-step return semantics, and the invariant that only `load_artifact` writes to the host filesystem. I verified the four meta-tools are wired in the MCP bridge (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:289-300), backed by HTTP endpoints (pkg/registry/server/server.go:325-328) and core functions (pkg/registry/core/core.go LoadDomain, SearchDomains, SearchArtifacts, LoadArtifact). LoadDomain returns the top-level map for an empty path and drills into a subdomain otherwise (core.go:239-353, confirmed by discovery_test.go); SearchArtifacts and SearchDomains return descriptors only with the `scope` filter honored at a path-segment boundary (core.go:526, 1085-1096); LoadArtifact returns the manifest body and materializes via the §6.6 pipeline (main.go:435). I traced every filesystem-write site in the MCP bridge and confirmed that `proxyGet` (load_domain, search_domains), `searchArtifacts`, and the prompts handlers never write the working set; only `loadArtifact` and `loadArtifactFromOverlay` call `materialize.Write`. The implementation matches the §3.4 flow. No gaps, inconsistencies, or bugs are attributable to this subsection.

No findings.
## F-3.5 — 3.5 Scope Preview (Pre-Session)

_Reviewed spec/03-disclosure-surface.md against the implementation._

I verified the scope preview surface end to end: the core aggregator (`pkg/registry/core/dependents.go`), the HTTP endpoint (`pkg/registry/server/server.go`), the Python and TypeScript SDK methods, and the claimed consumer paths (MCP server, `podium sync`, `podium status`). The core endpoint exists and returns the four spec-named fields with matching wire names, and the OAuth identity drives layer composition through the shared `s.identity(r)` path. The tenant gate `expose_scope_preview` and the `403 scope_preview_disabled` response are absent (the implementing code documents this itself), the aggregate counts double-count artifact versions, the `layers` array has no stable ordering, and several mandated consumer paths do not expose the preview.

### - [x] F-3.5.1 — Tenant flag `expose_scope_preview` and `403 scope_preview_disabled` not implemented [High] — CLOSED

(gap) Spec §3.5 states the endpoint is gated by tenant config `expose_scope_preview` (default `true`) and that "When `false`, the endpoint returns `403 scope_preview_disabled`." The implementation has no such gate. `PreviewScope` in `pkg/registry/core/dependents.go:62` always computes and returns the preview, and its own doc comment at lines 59-61 states "this implementation ships the always-on path. Adding the 403 surface is one Tenant config check away." The handler `handleScopePreview` at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:662` performs no gating. A repo-wide search for `expose_scope_preview`, `ExposeScopePreview`, and `scope_preview_disabled` returns only that single doc-comment reference, and the `store.Tenant` struct at `pkg/store/store.go:29` has no corresponding field. Because aggregate counts can hint at the existence of restricted content (the rationale the spec gives for the gate), the missing flag is a disclosure-control gap. Add an `ExposeScopePreview` field to the tenant config (defaulting to true), wire it through `internal/serverboot`, and have `handleScopePreview` return `403` with error code `scope_preview_disabled` when it is false.

**Resolution (fdf8587):** Added `store.Tenant.ExposeScopePreview *bool` (tri-state, nil = default true) plus `Tenant.ScopePreviewEnabled()`, persisted across the memory, SQLite, and Postgres backends (new nullable `expose_scope_preview` column, `sql.NullBool` round trip, storetest `ScopePreviewFlagRoundTrip` conformance). `core.PreviewScope` checks the gate first and returns the new `ErrScopePreviewDisabled` sentinel; `handleScopePreview` maps it to `403 scope_preview_disabled`. `internal/serverboot` resolves the flag from `PODIUM_EXPOSE_SCOPE_PREVIEW` and registry.yaml's `tenant.expose_scope_preview` (env wins) and seeds it on the default tenant.

### - [ ] F-3.5.2 — `podium status` does not surface scope preview data [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Spec §3.5 states "The `podium status` CLI surfaces the same data for human inspection." `cmd/podium/status.go` prints registry URL, harness, cache settings, identity provider, session token, tenant, reachability, and registry mode (lines 31-69), but never calls `/v1/scope/preview` and never prints `artifact_count`, `by_type`, or `by_sensitivity`. A search of `cmd/podium/status.go` for `preview`, `scope`, `by_type`, `by_sensitivity`, and `artifact_count` finds nothing. Add a section to `podium status` that fetches `GET /v1/scope/preview` for the configured registry and prints the aggregate counts.

### - [ ] F-3.5.3 — MCP server does not expose the scope preview [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Spec §3.5 states "The MCP server, SDK, and `podium sync` all expose this preview." A search across `cmd/podium-mcp/` for `preview`, `Preview`, `scope/preview`, `preview_scope`, and `PreviewScope` returns no matches, so the MCP bridge offers no preview affordance (tool, prompt, or resource). Note the same paragraph also says agents do not call the preview during a session, so the MCP exposure is a transparency affordance for the operator or reviewer rather than an agent-facing tool. Either add an MCP-side exposure of the preview (for example an out-of-session tool or resource that calls `/v1/scope/preview`) or reconcile the spec text if the MCP exposure is intentionally deferred.

### - [ ] F-3.5.4 — `podium sync` does not expose the scope preview [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Spec §3.5 names `podium sync` among the consumer paths that "all expose this preview." A search across `pkg/sync/` and the `cmd/podium/sync*.go` sources for `preview`, `Preview`, `scope/preview`, and `PreviewScope` returns no matches. Add a preview affordance to the sync path (for example a `podium sync --preview` flag or a preview line in sync output) that calls `GET /v1/scope/preview`, or reconcile the spec if this exposure is intentionally deferred.

### - [x] F-3.5.5 — Aggregate counts count artifact-versions instead of distinct artifacts [Medium] — CLOSED

(bug) Spec §3.5 presents `artifact_count` and the `by_type` / `by_sensitivity` breakdowns as counts of artifacts (the example shows `artifact_count: 1234` with per-type and per-sensitivity sums that add to it). `PreviewScope` at `pkg/registry/core/dependents.go:67-77` sets `ArtifactCount` to `len(visible)` and increments `ByType[m.Type]` and `BySensitivity[m.Sensitivity]` once per record returned by `visibleManifests`. `visibleManifests` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:1051`) calls `store.ListManifests`, which returns one record per `(artifact_id, version)` pair: the memory store keys manifests by `mkey(tenantID, artifactID, version)` (`pkg/store/memory.go:31,60`) and lists every record (lines 83-98). An artifact with multiple ingested versions is therefore counted once per version, inflating all three figures. The search path already establishes the correct convention by deduplicating on `m.ArtifactID` with a `seen` map (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:596-602`). Deduplicate the preview by artifact ID before counting (for example collapse to the latest version per artifact id, then tally).

**Resolution (fdf8587):** `PreviewScope` now collapses visible records to one per artifact ID via `latestPerArtifact` before counting. Each artifact's type and sensitivity come from the version §4.7.6 `latest` resolves to (most recently ingested non-deprecated, reusing `version.ResolveLatest`), so a multi-version artifact counts once and the breakdowns reflect the latest version.

### - [x] F-3.5.6 — `layers` array has non-deterministic order and omits empty visible layers [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) Spec §3.5 shows `layers` as an ordered composition (`["admin-finance", "alice-personal", "workspace-overlay"]`) and states the preview is "a read-only projection of that composition"; §4.6 defines the effective view as an ordered list in precedence order (lowest first). `PreviewScope` builds `Layers` by collecting `m.Layer` into a Go map `layerSet` and then ranging over the map (`pkg/registry/core/dependents.go:72-80`), so the resulting slice order is non-deterministic across calls. The same code derives the layer set only from layers that contain at least one visible manifest, so a layer the caller can see but that is currently empty never appears in `layers`, which diverges from "the composition of every layer the caller's identity is entitled to see." Derive `Layers` from `layer.EffectiveLayersWith(r.layers, id, r.resolveGroup)` (already used by `visibleManifests` at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:1059`) so the array reflects every visible layer in precedence order.

**Resolution (fdf8587):** When layers are configured, `Layers` is now built from `layer.EffectiveLayersWith(r.layers, id, r.resolveGroup)` in precedence order (lowest first), so the order is deterministic and a visible-but-empty layer is included. The bare-core / filesystem-source fallback (no layer config) derives the distinct layers from the visible records and sorts them for a stable response.

### - [ ] F-3.5.7 — Python SDK `preview_scope` accepts and sends constraint params the spec and server do not define [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Spec §3.5 shows `preview_scope()` taking no arguments, and the server handler reads no query parameters (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:662-669`). The Python SDK method at `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:225-240` accepts `scope`, `type`, and `tags` and forwards them as query params to `/v1/scope/preview`, where the server silently ignores them, so callers can pass filters that have no effect. The TypeScript SDK `previewScope()` at `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:220` correctly takes no arguments. The Python docstring also cites "spec §6.4" while the contract for this surface is §3.5. Remove the unused parameters from the Python `preview_scope` (or implement matching server-side filtering and update the spec), and correct the docstring reference.

### - [x] F-3.5.8 — `by_sensitivity` can contain an empty-string bucket for unset sensitivity [Low] — CLOSED

(bug) Spec §3.5 illustrates `by_sensitivity` with the keys `low`, `medium`, and `high`. The `sensitivity` frontmatter field is optional (`yaml:"sensitivity,omitempty"` at `pkg/manifest/types.go:106`), ingest stores it verbatim as `string(rec.Artifact.Sensitivity)` without defaulting (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:708`), and `parse.go` never sets a default. `PreviewScope` increments `BySensitivity[m.Sensitivity]` unconditionally (`pkg/registry/core/dependents.go:75`), so an artifact that omits `sensitivity` produces a `by_sensitivity[""]` bucket rather than falling into one of the documented buckets. Normalize an empty sensitivity to a defined bucket (the spec leaves the default unstated, so `low` is the natural floor) before counting, or omit empty-key buckets, so the response keys match the documented set.

**Resolution (fdf8587):** `PreviewScope` now tallies `by_sensitivity` through `sensitivityBucket`, which maps an empty (unset) sensitivity to the `low` floor. The response no longer carries an empty-string bucket; an artifact that omits `sensitivity` counts under `low`.

### - [x] F-3.5.9 — Scope preview handler does not reject non-GET methods [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) Spec §3.5 defines the endpoint as `GET /v1/scope/preview`. Sibling GET handlers in the same file reject other methods with `405` (for example `handleDomainAnalyze` at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:648-652`). `handleScopePreview` at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:662-669` performs no method check, so a POST, PUT, or DELETE to the path is served identically to a GET. Add a method guard that returns `405` for non-GET requests, matching the other read endpoints.

**Resolution (fdf8587):** `handleScopePreview` now rejects any non-GET method with `405 registry.invalid_argument`, matching the sibling `handleDomainAnalyze` guard.
## F-4.1 — 4.1 Artifacts Are Packages of Arbitrary Files (first-class + extension types)

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md against the implementation._

I verified the concrete contracts in §4.1: the first-class type identifiers (skill, agent, context, command, rule, hook), the built-in extension type (mcp-server), the extensibility of the type system through the TypeProvider SPI, the manifest-size lint (~20K-token cap and the SKILL.md 5K-token / 500-line guidance), and the three size thresholds (256 KB inline cutoff, 1 MB per-file soft warning, 10 MB per-package soft error). The type constants, the size constants, the bundled-resource size lint, and the inline-cutoff path all match the spec values. Two areas diverge: the TypeProvider SPI is not wired into the ingest or lint pipeline, so registered extension types are not treated uniformly, and the manifest-size lint counts whole manifest files for skills rather than the SKILL.md body that §4.1 specifies. The `mcp-server` type is classified internally as first-class even though §4.1 lists it under built-in extension types.

### - [x] F-4.1.1 — Extension TypeProvider registry is not consulted during lint or ingest [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.1 (lines 37, 39) states the type system is extensible: "deployments register additional types with their own lint rules. Podium treats every type uniformly for discovery, search, and load." The `TypeProvider` SPI exists in `pkg/typeprovider/typeprovider.go`, and `typeprovider.Default` pre-registers every first-class type plus `mcp-server` (typeprovider.go:60-74). However, nothing outside the `typeprovider` package and its tests imports or calls it: a repo-wide search for `typeprovider` outside `pkg/typeprovider/` and `*_test.go` returns no matches, and the ingest path (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:355`) runs only `req.Linter.Lint(...)` with `lint.AllRules()`. The lint rule that judges types, `ruleRequiredFields.Check` (pkg/lint/lint.go:121-124), checks only `manifest.IsFirstClassType(a.Type)` and emits a `lint.unknown_type` warning for any type that is not first-class, regardless of whether an extension `TypeProvider` is registered for it. Consequences: a deployment that registers a `dataset` provider through the SPI still receives a spurious `lint.unknown_type` warning at ingest, and the provider's `Validate` method is never invoked, so extension-type lint rules never run. The SPI is effectively dead code with respect to the ingest pipeline. Suggested direction: have `ruleRequiredFields` (or a dedicated rule) consult `typeprovider.Default.Get(a.Type)`, suppress the unknown-type warning when a provider is registered, and dispatch to the provider's `Validate` so extension-type lint rules participate in ingest.

Resolution (3f23977): `ruleRequiredFields` now consults the TypeProvider registry through `typeprovider.Registry.Require`, so a type registered with any provider (first-class, built-in extension, or deployment-registered extension) no longer triggers `lint.unknown_type`. A new `ruleTypeProviderValidate` rule dispatches each artifact to its provider's `Validate` and surfaces the resulting diagnostics, so extension-type lint rules run at ingest. Both rules default to `typeprovider.Default` and accept an injected registry for tests.

### - [x] F-4.1.2 — Manifest-size 20K-token error counts the whole ARTIFACT.md and SKILL.md files for skills instead of the SKILL.md body [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §4.1 (line 41) states: "A reasonable cap is ~20K tokens of manifest content. ... For skills, the cap applies to the `SKILL.md` body." The implementation in `pkg/lint/size_rules.go:107` computes `manifestTokens := approxTokenCount(rec.ArtifactBytes) + approxTokenCount(rec.SkillBytes)` and raises the 20K-token error on that sum for every type, including skills. `ArtifactBytes` and `SkillBytes` are the full raw file contents, including YAML frontmatter, per `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:22-23` and the assignment at walk.go:150 and walk.go:168. For a skill, this counts the entire ARTIFACT.md file plus the entire SKILL.md file (frontmatter and body), rather than the SKILL.md body alone. The 5K-token and 500-line skill warnings at size_rules.go:119-120 use `approxTokenCount(rec.SkillBytes)` and `countLines(rec.SkillBytes)`, which likewise measure the whole SKILL.md file rather than its parsed body. The deviation is conservative (the error fires marginally earlier than the spec prescribes) and frontmatter is small relative to 20K tokens, so the blast radius is small. Suggested direction: for `type: skill`, measure `rec.Skill.Body` (the parsed prose body, already available on the record) for both the 20K-token error and the 5K-token / 500-line warnings, matching the wording in §4.1 and §4.3.4.

Resolution (3f23977): `ruleManifestSize` now measures the parsed SKILL.md body (`rec.Skill.Body`) for the 20K-token cap and the 5K-token / 500-line soft warnings on skills, and the ARTIFACT.md content for every other type, per §4.1. The frontmatter and the ARTIFACT.md file no longer count toward a skill's cap.

### - [x] F-4.1.3 — `mcp-server` is classified as a first-class type rather than a built-in extension type [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §4.1 groups types into "First-class types" (lines 13-22: skill, agent, context, command, rule, hook) and "Built-in extension types" (lines 24-28: mcp-server). The implementation treats `mcp-server` as first-class: `manifest.IsFirstClassType` returns `true` for `TypeMCPServer` (pkg/manifest/parse.go:143-150), its doc comment says "one of the seven first-class types" (parse.go:141-142), and the test `TestIsFirstClassType_AllSevenAreRecognized` asserts all seven (including `mcp-server`) are first-class (pkg/manifest/artifact_test.go:159-168). The package comment in pkg/typeprovider/typeprovider.go:1-5 similarly lists `mcp-server` among "each first-class artifact type." Behaviorally the only effect of `IsFirstClassType` is suppressing the `lint.unknown_type` warning, and `mcp-server` should not warn, so the runtime impact is negligible. The mismatch is in classification and naming: the spec deliberately separates first-class types (full conformance commitment) from built-in extension types (no conformance commitment beyond the type owner's, per line 26). Suggested direction: either rename the predicate to reflect "first-class or built-in extension" and update the comments and test names, or split `mcp-server` into a separate built-in-extension predicate so the code's vocabulary matches §4.1.

Resolution (3f23977): `manifest.IsFirstClassType` now returns true only for skill, agent, context, command, rule, and hook. A new `manifest.IsBuiltinExtensionType` reports mcp-server, and `manifest.FirstClassTypes` / `manifest.BuiltinExtensionTypes` expose the §4.1 taxonomy that seeds the default TypeProvider registry. mcp-server stays recognized at lint time through that registry, so it produces no unknown-type warning. Comments and tests in `pkg/manifest` and `pkg/typeprovider` were updated to match.

### - [x] F-4.1.4 — `ErrUnknownType` is declared but never used [Info] — CLOSED

(gap) `pkg/manifest/parse.go:29-31` declares `ErrUnknownType = errors.New("manifest: unknown artifact type")` with a comment tying it to §4.1 ("a type field not registered with any TypeProvider (first-class or extension)"). A repo-wide search shows the sentinel is referenced only at its declaration; no code returns or checks it. §4.1 treats extension types as valid when registered, so parse-time acceptance of arbitrary type strings is correct, but the unused sentinel signals an intended validation path (reject a type that is neither first-class nor registered with a TypeProvider) that is not implemented. This is the parse-side counterpart of F-4.1.1. Suggested direction: either wire `ErrUnknownType` into a validation step that consults the TypeProvider registry, or remove the unused sentinel if the lint-warning path in F-4.1.1 is the intended behavior.

Resolution (3f23977): Wired the sentinel into a validation path rather than removing it. `typeprovider.Registry.Require` returns an error wrapping `manifest.ErrUnknownType` for a type with no registered provider, and `ruleRequiredFields` emits `lint.unknown_type` when `errors.Is(err, manifest.ErrUnknownType)`. Parse-time acceptance of arbitrary type strings is unchanged, because §4.1 treats extension types as valid when registered.
## F-4.2 — 4.2 Registry Layout on Disk

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md against the implementation._
