I checked the §4.2 contract that the canonical artifact ID is the directory path under the registry root, that references use that ID with an optional `@<semver>` or `@sha256:<hash>` suffix, that the hierarchy nests to arbitrary depth without changing the ID, and that each layer maps its directory hierarchy (optionally rooted at a subpath) to the domain hierarchy. The two artifact-walk implementations are `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go` (filesystem-source registry) and `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go` (server ingest from a Git or local snapshot). Both compute the canonical ID from the directory path with forward-slash separators, the Git source applies the `root:` subpath before walking, and arbitrary nesting depth is handled by relative-path computation. Folding preserves canonical IDs (rendering only). The two walkers diverge on a root-level `ARTIFACT.md`, no validation constrains the characters in a canonical-ID segment, and resource capture does not stop at a nested artifact boundary.

### - [x] F-4.2.1 — Server ingest assigns an empty canonical ID to a root-level ARTIFACT.md [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §4.2 states the canonical artifact ID "is the directory path under the registry root (e.g., `finance/ap/pay-invoice`)" and the layout model treats leaves as artifact packages, so an artifact has a non-empty directory path. The two walk implementations disagree on what happens when an `ARTIFACT.md` sits directly at the layer (or subpath) root. The filesystem-source registry rejects it: `canonicalID` returns an error when `filepath.Rel` yields `"."` ("artifact must live in a subdirectory of the layer") at `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:206-215`. The server ingest path silently accepts it: in `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go`, `loadOne` computes the ID with `dirToCanonical(dirOf(artifactPath))`, and for a top-level path such as `ARTIFACT.md`, `dirOf` returns `"."` (`ingest.go:830-835`) and `dirToCanonical(".")` returns `""` (`ingest.go:844-849`). The artifact is then ingested with `ArtifactID == ""`. No downstream guard rejects an empty artifact ID: the lint rules in `pkg/lint/lint.go` and the store paths do not check for it, and for a non-skill type (for example `type: context`) the skill name-versus-directory check at `lint.go:153-157` never runs. The result is a stored artifact whose canonical ID is `""`, which cannot be addressed by any reference and which collides with any other top-level manifest mapping to the same empty ID. The Git source descends into `cfg.Root` before walking (`pkg/layer/source/git.go:73-78`), so a layer rooted at a subpath that itself contains `ARTIFACT.md` at the subpath root hits this case. Suggested direction: have the ingest walker reject a root-level `ARTIFACT.md` with the same error the filesystem registry uses, or validate that `rec.ID` is non-empty before storing, so both ingest paths share the §4.2 invariant.

**Resolution (e192684):** Added `filesystem.ValidateCanonicalID`, called from both walk paths. The server ingest walk (`loadOne`) now rejects a root-level `ARTIFACT.md` (empty canonical ID) with the same invariant the filesystem registry enforces, so no artifact is stored with an unaddressable `""` ID. Covered by `TestLoadOne_RootLevelRejected`, `TestIngest_RootLevelArtifactRejected`, `TestWalk_RootLevelArtifactRejected`, and the e2e/integration `lint`/`sync` rejection tests.

### - [x] F-4.2.2 — Canonical-ID segments are unvalidated and the reference `@`-split direction is inconsistent [Low] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.2 defines the reference grammar as the canonical ID "optionally suffixed with `@<semver>` or `@sha256:<hash>`." The implementation derives the canonical ID directly from directory names (`pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:206-215`, `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:844-849`) without validating the characters in a path segment, so a directory name may contain `@`. The reference-splitting helpers then disagree on which `@` separates the ID from the suffix: `splitRef` in ingest (`ingest.go:823-828`) and `SplitArtifactRef` in the layer composer (`pkg/layer/composer.go:224-229`) use `strings.Index` (first `@`), `stripPin` likewise uses `strings.Index` (`ingest.go:766-771`), while `splitParentRef` in core uses `strings.LastIndex` (last `@`) at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:978-983`. For a well-formed ID with no `@` in any segment, every helper agrees, so this does not affect valid input. With an `@` inside a directory name, ingest would split the ID at the wrong position and store a malformed `ExtendsPin`, and core would later split it differently, so the parent reference would not round-trip. Suggested direction: validate canonical-ID segments at ingest (reject `@`, and decide on the rest of the segment grammar relative to §4.3.4 name constraints), and converge the reference-split helpers on a single direction so the ID-plus-suffix grammar is parsed identically everywhere.

**Resolution (e192684):** `filesystem.ValidateCanonicalID` rejects any path segment containing `@` at both walk paths, and `core.splitParentRef` now splits on the first `@` (`strings.Index`) like `ingest.splitRef`/`stripPin` and `composer.SplitArtifactRef`, so every reference-split helper parses `<id>@<suffix>` identically. Segment validation is limited to `@` rejection: §4.2 does not otherwise constrain segment characters and the spec's own layout uses domain directories such as `_shared`, so applying the §4.3.4 `name` grammar to every segment would reject valid input. Covered by `TestValidateCanonicalID`, `TestSplitParentRef` (multi-`@` case), `TestLoadOne_AtSegmentRejected`, `TestIngest_AtSegmentRejected`, and `TestWalk_AtSegmentRejected`.

### - [x] F-4.2.3 — Resource capture does not stop at a nested artifact boundary [Low] — CLOSED

(bug) §4.2 models the hierarchy as domain directories with artifact packages as the leaves, and §4.4 defines a bundled resource as "every file under the artifact's root other than `ARTIFACT.md` (and, for skills, `SKILL.md`)." Both resource-capture passes walk the artifact directory recursively and skip only the package's own top-level `ARTIFACT.md`/`SKILL.md`: `captureResources` at `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:177-202` skips the exact paths `filepath.Join(dir, "ARTIFACT.md")` and `filepath.Join(dir, "SKILL.md")` only, and the ingest resource walk at `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:667-685` skips only base names `ARTIFACT.md`/`SKILL.md` at any depth. Neither walker stops descending when it crosses into a subdirectory that is itself an artifact (no `fs.SkipDir` after an `ARTIFACT.md` is discovered in `walkLayer`). If an artifact directory contains a nested artifact, the nested artifact is discovered as its own record by the layer walk and, simultaneously, its files (including its `ARTIFACT.md`, since the ingest skip matches by base name but its own `SKILL.md` would also be captured by the filesystem pass when the outer type is not skill) are captured as bundled resources of the parent. No lint rule forbids nested artifacts. The effect is duplicated content and a parent package that carries another artifact's bytes. Suggested direction: detect a nested `ARTIFACT.md` during resource capture and either skip that subtree (treating the nested directory as a separate package boundary) or reject nesting at lint time, consistent with the leaf-package model in §4.2.

**Resolution (e192684):** Both resource-capture walks now return `SkipDir` when they cross into a subdirectory that carries its own `ARTIFACT.md`, treating it as a separate leaf package (§4.2). A nested artifact's files, including its `ARTIFACT.md`/`SKILL.md`, are no longer captured as the parent's bundled resources; the nested artifact remains its own record keyed by its own canonical ID. Covered by `TestWalk_NestedArtifactNotCapturedAsResource`, `TestLoadOne_NestedArtifactNotCaptured`, and `TestIngest_NestedArtifactsIngestedSeparately`.
## F-4.3 — 4.3 Artifact Manifest Schema (universal/caller-interpreted/type-specific/external resources, 4.3.4 SKILL.md, 4.3.5 hook events)

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md against the implementation._

I checked the §4.3 universal, caller-interpreted, type-specific, and external-resource fields against `pkg/manifest/types.go` and `parse.go`, the §4.3.4 SKILL.md compliance lint against `pkg/lint`, the §4.3.5 canonical hook events against `pkg/lint` and `pkg/adapter`, and the persistence path through `pkg/registry/ingest` and `pkg/store`. The frontmatter parser and the size/skill/hook/hint lint rules largely follow the schema, but several typed fields either fail to parse the documented YAML form, are parsed and then dropped, or are accepted without the validation the spec mandates. The most serious item is that the documented `input`/`output` `$ref` form fails to parse at all. Several §4.3.4 and §4.3.5 lint checks named in the spec are absent.

### - [x] F-4.3.1 — input/output `$ref` object form fails to parse [High] — CLOSED

(bug) §4.3 type-specific fields document `input: { $ref: ./schemas/input.json }` and `output: { $ref: ./schemas/output.json }` for `type: agent` (lines 195-196), and §4.1's non-skill package layout example ships an agent with `schemas/input.json` and `schemas/output.json`. In `pkg/manifest/types.go:127-128` the fields are typed as `Input string` and `Output string`. Decoding the documented YAML map into a `string` field fails: `ParseArtifact` returns `ErrInvalidYAML` ("cannot unmarshal !!map into string") for any manifest that uses the spec's `{ $ref: ... }` syntax, so the artifact is rejected outright at parse time before lint runs. There is no custom `UnmarshalYAML` and no alternate parse path. Suggested direction: type `Input`/`Output` as a struct (for example `*SchemaRef{ Ref string yaml:"$ref" }`) or `map[string]any`/`yaml.Node` so the documented form decodes, and update any consumer accordingly.

**Resolution (7ceb07c):** `Input`/`Output` are now `*SchemaRef` with a custom `UnmarshalYAML` (`pkg/manifest/parse.go`) that decodes both the `{ $ref: ./schemas/x.json }` mapping and a bare scalar path; a sequence value is rejected with `ErrInvalidYAML`. No production code read the old string fields. Covered by `TestParseArtifact_InputOutputRefObjectForm/ScalarForm/InvalidKind`.

### - [x] F-4.3.2 — `hook_event` is not validated against the canonical taxonomy [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.3.5 states `hook_event` "is constrained to a canonical event name from the table below" (line 304) and enumerates the canonical events (lines 308-329). The canonical list appears only in the spec-coverage tool `tools/matrix/matrices.go:147-156` and in `pkg/adapter/hook_events_test.go:11`; no production code validates the field. `pkg/manifest/types.go:134` stores `HookEvent` as a free-form string, and the only hook lint rule, `ruleHookConsistency` in `pkg/lint/lint.go:200-233`, emits an informational note when the event is one of the two generic events and otherwise says nothing. A `type: hook` artifact with an unknown or misspelled `hook_event` (for example `hook_event: on_stop`) passes ingest. Suggested direction: define the canonical event set in `pkg/manifest` and add a lint rule that errors when a `type: hook` artifact declares a `hook_event` outside the set.

**Resolution (7ceb07c):** `pkg/manifest/hook_events.go` defines the §4.3.5 taxonomy (`CanonicalHookEvents`, `IsCanonicalHookEvent`). New `ruleHookEventCanonical` (`pkg/lint/lint.go`) errors with `lint.unknown_hook_event` when a `type: hook` declares an off-taxonomy event (`on_stop`, native PascalCase, etc.); the empty case and non-hook types are left alone. Covered by `TestLint_HookEventUnknownErrors/CanonicalAccepted/IgnoredForNonHook` and `TestCanonicalHookEvents`. The one fixture that used the native `PreToolUse` (`docs_concepts`) was corrected to a canonical event.

### - [x] F-4.3.3 — `search_visibility: direct-only` is parsed but never persisted or enforced [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.3 universal fields define `search_visibility: indexed | direct-only` with default `indexed` (line 150), and §4.5.3 (line 477) requires that artifacts "Appear in `search_artifacts` results normally (subject to per-artifact `search_visibility:`)", which means `direct-only` excludes an artifact from search results. `pkg/manifest/types.go:108` parses the field, but `store.ManifestRecord` (`pkg/store/store.go:46-78`) has no `SearchVisibility` field, and `manifestRecordFor` (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:700-716`) does not copy it, so the value never reaches the store. `SearchArtifacts` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:502`) filters by `Deprecated` (line 535) but not by `search_visibility`; a repo-wide search finds no use of `SearchVisibilityDirectOnly` outside the type declaration. A `direct-only` artifact is returned in search results identically to an `indexed` one. The raw frontmatter is preserved on the record, so a host could read the field after the fact, but the registry-side search filtering the spec describes does not happen. Suggested direction: persist `search_visibility` on `ManifestRecord` and have `SearchArtifacts` exclude `direct-only` artifacts by default.

**Resolution (7ceb07c):** `store.ManifestRecord` gains a `SearchVisibility` field with a backing `search_visibility` column on the Memory, SQLite, and Postgres backends; `manifestRecordFor` copies it at ingest, and `SearchArtifacts` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go`) excludes `direct-only` records while leaving them reachable via `load_artifact`. Covered by the new `storetest` `SearchVisibilityRoundTrip` case, `TestSearchArtifacts_DirectOnlyExcluded`, and the now-unskipped e2e `TestArtifactTypes_SearchVisibilityDirectOnly`, `TestFrontmatter_DirectOnlyHiddenFromSearch`, `TestHooks_DirectOnlyHiddenFromSearch`.

### - [x] F-4.3.4 — `target_harnesses` is parsed but never honored [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.3 type-specific fields define `target_harnesses: [...]` as the way to "opt out of cross-harness materialization for this artifact" (lines 239-240), and §4.3.5 line 333 plus §6.7.1 reference it as the mechanism that excludes an unsupported harness so ingest is not rejected at a ✗ intersection. `pkg/manifest/types.go:140` parses `TargetHarnesses`, but a repo-wide search finds no consumer of the field in `pkg/materialize`, `pkg/sync`, `cmd/podium-mcp`, `pkg/adapter`, or `pkg/lint`. Materialization therefore targets every configured harness regardless of `target_harnesses`, and lint cannot use it to suppress an unsupported-harness rejection (which is itself not implemented; see F-4.3.7-adjacent note in F-4.3.2). Suggested direction: filter adapter targets by `target_harnesses` during materialization and consult it in the capability-matrix lint rule when that rule is added.

**Resolution (7ceb07c):** `manifest.TargetsHarness` (empty list targets every harness, non-empty restricts to the named adapters) now gates materialization. `podium sync` skips an excluded artifact and records it in `Result.Skipped`; the `podium-mcp` materialize paths suppress the on-disk write (manifest content still returns). Covered by `TestTargetsHarness`, `TestRun_TargetHarnessesFiltersAdapter`, and `TestPodiumMCP_TargetHarnessesSuppressesMaterialize`. The capability-matrix lint consult remains with the unimplemented matrix lint (F-6.7.x).

### - [x] F-4.3.5 — SKILL.md body size lint counts frontmatter as body [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §4.1 (line 41) and §4.3.4 (line 290) state the body size guidance applies to "the `SKILL.md` body": warn above 5K tokens and 500 lines. `ruleManifestSize` in `pkg/lint/size_rules.go:118-140` computes `approxTokenCount(rec.SkillBytes)` and `countLines(rec.SkillBytes)`, where `rec.SkillBytes` is the entire SKILL.md file including its YAML frontmatter (`pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:168` assigns the full `os.ReadFile` result). The parsed body is available as `rec.Skill.Body` but is not used. The frontmatter (name, description, license, compatibility, metadata, allowed-tools) is counted against the body budget, so the token and line counts are inflated relative to the spec definition. The existing tests mask this because they place body text directly into `SkillBytes` with no frontmatter (`pkg/lint/size_rules_test.go:66-106`). Suggested direction: count tokens and lines over `rec.Skill.Body` (or over `bodyAfterFrontmatter(rec.SkillBytes)`) rather than over the whole file.

**Resolution (ba0eaae):** Already fixed by the F-4.1.2 batch. `ruleManifestSize` (`pkg/lint/size_rules.go`) measures `rec.Skill.Body` for the skill 20K cap and the 5K-token / 500-line soft warnings, so frontmatter no longer counts. Guarded by `TestRuleManifestSize_SkillCapMeasuresBodyNotFiles` and `TestRuleManifestSize_SkillSoftCapMeasuresBodyNotFrontmatter`.

### - [x] F-4.3.6 — Several §4.3.4 skill-artifact ingest lint checks are missing [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.3.4 (lines 292-300) lists the skill-artifact ingest lint checks. Three are not implemented anywhere (`pkg/lint`, `pkg/manifest`, `pkg/registry/ingest` all searched):

- "SKILL.md does not contain Podium-only fields (`type`, `version`, `when_to_use`, `tags`, etc.); if present, error" (line 297). `ParseSkill` (`pkg/manifest/parse.go:72-83`) uses `yaml.Unmarshal` without `KnownFields(true)`, so any Podium-only key in SKILL.md is silently dropped rather than flagged, and no lint rule inspects for it.
- "`ARTIFACT.md` does not contain `name`, `description`, or `license` fields (warning); if present, the values must match `SKILL.md` exactly (error on mismatch)" (line 298). `ruleSkillCompliance` (`pkg/lint/lint.go:132-160`) only checks SKILL.md `name`/`description`; it never warns on a present `Artifact.Name`/`Description`/`License` for a skill and never compares them against SKILL.md.
- "The `skills-ref validate` reference check from the agentskills.io project passes against `SKILL.md` (warning on failure; lint suppression flag available)" (line 300). No `skills-ref` integration or suppression flag exists in the repo.

The implemented checks (both files present, name matches directory, description non-empty, name syntax, ARTIFACT.md body empty-or-single-comment) are present. Suggested direction: add a strict-decode or key-scan rule for Podium-only fields in SKILL.md, a presence/mismatch rule for `name`/`description`/`license` in a skill's ARTIFACT.md, and wire the `skills-ref validate` check with a suppression flag.

**Resolution (b6914d0):** Added three §4.3.4 lint rules in `pkg/lint/skill_rules.go`: `ruleSkillPodiumOnlyFields` errors on a Podium-only key in SKILL.md (scanning raw frontmatter via the new `manifest.TopLevelFrontmatterKeys`, since `ParseSkill` drops unknown keys); `ruleSkillArtifactFields` warns on `name`/`description`/`license` in a skill's ARTIFACT.md and errors on a value mismatch with SKILL.md; `ruleSkillRefValidate` stands in for the agentskills.io `skills-ref validate` check by warning when the SKILL.md description exceeds 1024 chars or compatibility exceeds 500, honoring a per-artifact `lint_suppress` flag (new `Artifact.LintSuppress`). `manifestRecordFor` now indexes a skill's description from SKILL.md so the spec-conformant omit-from-ARTIFACT.md form stays searchable. Covered by `pkg/lint/skill_rules_test.go`, `test/integration/skill_lint_test.go`, and e2e tests in `docs_first_skill_test.go`.

### - [x] F-4.3.7 — Type-specific required fields are not validated [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.3 documents required fields per type that ingest does not enforce. The `rule_mode` table (lines 216-221) marks `rule_globs` as required when `rule_mode: glob` and `rule_description` as required when `rule_mode: auto`; the `type: hook` schema (lines 226-231) shows `hook_event` and `hook_action` as the defining fields. No lint rule in `AllRules()` (`pkg/lint/lint.go:71-86`) checks any of these: a repo-wide search finds no validation that `rule_mode: glob` carries `rule_globs`, that `rule_mode: auto` carries `rule_description`, or that a `type: hook` artifact carries `hook_event` and `hook_action`. A `type: rule` with `rule_mode: glob` and no `rule_globs`, or a `type: hook` with no `hook_action`, passes ingest. Suggested direction: add a per-type required-field lint rule covering the rule-mode conditional requirements and the hook event/action requirements.

**Resolution (b6914d0):** Added `ruleTypeRequiredFields` in `pkg/lint/required_fields.go`, which errors when `rule_mode: glob` omits `rule_globs`, `rule_mode: auto` omits `rule_description`, or a `type: hook` omits `hook_event` or `hook_action`. The companion `ruleRuleModeHygiene` adds the `docs/authoring/rule-modes.md` "Lint behavior" warnings (an ignored companion field, and `rule_mode` on a non-rule). This unskips the six e2e tests that cited the finding (`docs_rule_modes_test.go` T-D-rule-modes-10..14 and `docs_hooks_test.go` T-D-hooks-44). Covered by `pkg/lint/required_fields_test.go` and `test/integration/skill_lint_test.go`.

### - [x] F-4.3.8 — Hook generic/subtype lint differs from the spec in severity and trigger [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §4.3.5 line 331 states "Authors should not declare both a generic hook and the corresponding subtype hook for the same artifact; lint warns when this happens." `ruleHookConsistency` (`pkg/lint/lint.go:212-233`) emits `SeverityInfo` (the spec says warn) and triggers on any artifact whose single `hook_event` is a generic event (`pre_tool_use`/`post_tool_use`), rather than on the spec's condition of a generic and a subtype declared together. Because `hook_event` is a single scalar, one ARTIFACT.md cannot declare both a generic and a subtype, so the spec's literal condition is not reachable per artifact and the code substitutes a different check at a lower severity. Suggested direction: clarify in the spec whether multiple hook events per artifact are intended; if a single event remains the model, align the rule's message and reconcile the severity (warning vs info) with the spec text.

**Resolution (b6914d0):** Kept the single-scalar `hook_event` model (matching §4.3.5) and rewrote `ruleHookConsistency` (`pkg/lint/lint.go`). It now emits `SeverityWarning` (was `SeverityInfo`) and fires only when a generic hook and a corresponding subtype hook are both present in the linted set, naming the overlapping subtype. A lone generic hook is clean, matching §4.3.5 ("Authors choose the level of specificity that matches the action's intent"). Since the literal "same artifact" condition is unreachable under a scalar, the rule applies the check across the artifact set. Covered by `TestLint_HookLoneGenericClean` / `TestLint_HookGenericAndSubtypeWarns`; the e2e assertions that pinned the old lone-generic info behavior (`docs_hooks`, `docs_frontmatter`, `docs_artifact_types`) were updated.

### - [x] F-4.3.9 — `compatibility` is not derived for skills at materialization [Low] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.3.4 line 271 states that when `compatibility` is not authored in SKILL.md, "the Podium adapter derives it from `runtime_requirements` and `sandbox_profile` at materialization time for harnesses that consume only the agentskills.io subset." A repo-wide search finds no derivation of `compatibility` in `pkg/adapter` or `pkg/materialize`; `Skill.Compatibility` (`pkg/manifest/types.go:197`) is only parsed and passed through. Harnesses that consume only the agentskills.io subset receive no derived compatibility string when the author omits it. Suggested direction: derive a `compatibility` string from `runtime_requirements` and `sandbox_profile` in the adapter for skill outputs when the field is absent.

**Resolution (b6914d0):** `pkg/adapter/compatibility.go` adds `deriveSkillCompatibility`, which parses the SKILL.md and ARTIFACT.md, and when `compatibility` is absent renders a human-readable string from `runtime_requirements` and `sandbox_profile` (capped at 500 chars) and injects it as the first SKILL.md frontmatter line. The claude-code adapter, the built-in that materializes SKILL.md without ARTIFACT.md (the agentskills.io subset), applies it; verbatim adapters such as `none` are unaffected. Covered by `pkg/adapter/compatibility_test.go`, `test/integration/skill_lint_test.go` (`TestPodiumSync_DerivesSkillCompatibility`), and e2e `TestFirstSkill_ClaudeCodeDerivesCompatibility`.
## F-4.4 — 4.4 Bundled Resources (4.4.1 Execution Model Contract, 4.4.2 Content Provenance)

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md against the implementation._

I verified the §4.4 intro contracts (implicit resource discovery, no `resources:` frontmatter list, content-addressed storage, atomic `.tmp`+rename materialization, prose-reference resolution as an ingest error) and the §4.4.1 / §4.4.2 contracts (`runtime_requirements` rejection with `materialize.runtime_unavailable`, `sandbox_profile` host-refusal gate, and provenance-marker rewriting to trust regions). The directory-implicit resource discovery (`pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go`), the atomic write (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go`), the bundled-file existence lint (`pkg/lint/body_rules.go`), and the sandbox-profile refusal gate (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`) all match the spec. Three areas diverge: the `materialize.runtime_unavailable` check is implemented but never wired into the materialize path; the prose-reference URL HEAD validation is disabled in every production ingest path; and provenance rewriting is applied only to skill bodies. Two smaller observations concern dead-code type handling and the unshipped seccomp baseline.

### - [x] F-4.4.1 — `materialize.runtime_unavailable` check is implemented but never invoked [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.4.1 (spec line 370) states: "Hosts that cannot satisfy a requirement reject the artifact at load time with `materialize.runtime_unavailable`." The reference host is the Podium MCP server. The implementation provides `CheckRuntimeRequirements` and `HostCapabilities` in `pkg/materialize/atomic.go:34-78`, and the function returns the correct error wrapping `ErrRuntimeUnavailable = errors.New("materialize.runtime_unavailable")` (atomic.go:28). It is unit-tested in `pkg/materialize/runtime_test.go`. However, the materialization flow in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go` (`deliverLoadArtifact`, lines 383-451, and `loadArtifactFromOverlay`, lines 466-511) enforces the signature policy and the sandbox policy but never calls `CheckRuntimeRequirements`. A repo-wide search confirms `CheckRuntimeRequirements` and `HostCapabilities` have no callers outside the materialize package's own tests, and the MCP config (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:99-118`) has no host-capability inputs (no `PODIUM_HOST_PYTHON`, `PODIUM_HOST_NODE`, or host-packages env var) to populate `HostCapabilities`. The mandated load-time rejection therefore never fires in the reference host. Suggested direction: parse `runtime_requirements` from the resolved manifest in `deliverLoadArtifact`, populate `HostCapabilities` from new host-capability config, call `CheckRuntimeRequirements`, and return `errorResult("materialize.runtime_unavailable: ...")` on failure, mirroring the existing sandbox gate.

**Resolution (82e8416):** `podium-mcp` gained host-capability config (`PODIUM_HOST_PYTHON`/`_NODE`/`_PACKAGES`, plus `PODIUM_ENFORCE_RUNTIME_REQUIREMENTS` and `PODIUM_IGNORE_RUNTIME_REQUIREMENTS`); `deliverLoadArtifact` now parses `runtime_requirements`, calls `CheckRuntimeRequirements`, and refuses with `materialize.runtime_unavailable`. The gate activates once the host advertises a capability (the spec mandates fail-closed only for `sandbox_profile`, not runtime), so unconfigured hosts still surface requirements without refusing. Unit `runtime_policy_test.go` + e2e bundled-16/17, hooks-10, handling-14 unskipped.

### - [x] F-4.4.2 — Prose-reference URL HEAD validation is disabled in every production ingest path [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.4 (spec lines 349-355) requires the ingest-time linter to validate that prose references resolve to bundled files (existence check), URLs (HTTP HEAD returns 200/3xx), or other artifacts, and states "Drift between manifest text and bundled files is an ingest error." The rule `ruleProseReferenceResolution` in `pkg/lint/body_rules.go:89-211` implements the bundled-file existence check (error severity, lines 169-174) and the URL HEAD check accepting status `>= 200 && < 400` (lines 177-211). The URL check is gated on a non-nil `HTTPClient`: when nil, `checkURL` returns immediately and the reference is not validated (lines 91-92, 178-180). The constructor `NewProseReferenceRule(client)` exists to inject a client, but `AllRules()` registers the rule as `ruleProseReferenceResolution{}` with a nil client (`pkg/lint/lint.go:82`). Every ingest path builds the linter as `&lint.Linter{}` with empty `Rules`, which falls back to `AllRules()`: `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:315-316` (default), `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:182-186`, `pkg/registry/server/server.go:212-216`, and the CLI lint command `cmd/podium/main.go:469`. None supplies a custom linter or HTTP client. URL prose references are therefore never validated in any deployment, contradicting the §4.4 requirement; the bundled-file existence check does run and does block ingest at error severity. Suggested direction: wire a configured `*http.Client` into the linter for non-offline ingests (with an explicit offline opt-out) so the URL HEAD check runs, or document the URL check as out of scope and adjust the spec.

**Resolution (82e8416):** `lint.Linter` gained an `HTTPClient` field; `Lint()` now builds the rule set via `AllRulesWithClient(l.HTTPClient)`, and `NewIngestLinter(offline)` + `DefaultHTTPClient()` were added. `serverboot`, `server.NewFromFilesystem`, and `podium lint` wire a client by default with an explicit offline opt-out (`PODIUM_INGEST_OFFLINE` / `--offline`); the core `ingest.Ingest` nil-fallback stays offline for library/test hermeticity. Integration `prose_url_lint_test.go` (live + offline) and e2e CLI URL-check tests added.

### - [x] F-4.4.3 — Provenance markers are rewritten only for skill bodies, not for other types [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.4.2 (spec lines 385-399) describes provenance for "Prose in artifact manifests" generally and states "Adapters propagate provenance markers to harnesses that support trust regions (e.g., Claude's `<untrusted-data>` convention)." It calls differential trust "the primary defense against prompt injection from manifests that aggregate external content." The Claude Code adapter applies `rewriteProvenanceForClaude` only on the skill path: `pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:40` rewrites `src.SkillBytes` for `type: skill`. The `rule` case (lines 46-49), the `agent` case (lines 51-54), and the `default` case covering `context`, `command`, `hook`, and `mcp-server` (lines 64-67) all write `src.ArtifactBytes` verbatim with no provenance rewrite. For non-skill types the MCP server passes the full ARTIFACT.md (frontmatter plus prose body, since `manifestRecordFor` stores the whole file in `Frontmatter` at `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:714`) as `ArtifactBytes` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:425`), so any `<!-- begin imported source="..." -->` block in a `context` or `agent` body survives into the materialized Claude Code file as a raw HTML comment rather than an `<untrusted-data>` region. `context` artifacts are described in §4.1 as reference material and "large knowledge bases," which is exactly the content most likely to aggregate imported external text, so the prompt-injection defense is absent for the type that most needs it. The provenance tests (`pkg/adapter/provenance_test.go`) exercise only the skill body. Suggested direction: apply `rewriteProvenanceForClaude` to the body portion of `src.ArtifactBytes` in the `agent`, `rule`, and `default` branches of the Claude Code adapter, and add coverage for non-skill provenance.

**Resolution (82e8416):** the claude-code adapter now applies `rewriteProvenanceForClaude` to `src.ArtifactBytes` in the `agent`, `rule`, and `default` (`context`, `command`, `hook`, `mcp-server`) branches, not just skills. The rewrite only matches imported provenance blocks, so passing the full ARTIFACT.md is a no-op when none are present. Table-driven `provenance_test.go` coverage for non-skill types + an e2e claude-code non-skill sync added.

### - [x] F-4.4.4 — `CheckRuntimeRequirements` system_packages type assertion fails for parsed manifests [Low] — CLOSED

(bug) `CheckRuntimeRequirements` in `pkg/materialize/atomic.go:70` asserts `req["system_packages"].([]string)`. The manifest stores runtime requirements as a typed struct (`RuntimeRequirements.SystemPackages []string` in `pkg/manifest/types.go:170`), but the function takes `map[string]any`. A caller that bridges the typed struct to the map by a generic YAML or JSON round-trip produces `[]any` for `system_packages`, and the `[]string` assertion silently fails, skipping the package check entirely (no error, requirement treated as satisfied). The unit test passes a literal `[]string` (`pkg/materialize/runtime_test.go:36`), which is why the gap is invisible in tests. This is currently latent because the function has no production caller (see F-4.4.1), but it would manifest the moment the check is wired in via a YAML/JSON-derived map. Suggested direction: accept both `[]string` and `[]any` (coerce each element to string), or change the signature to take the typed `*manifest.RuntimeRequirements` so the package list is statically typed.

**Resolution (82e8416):** `CheckRuntimeRequirements` now coerces `system_packages` from `[]string` **and** `[]any` (each element stringified) via a `systemPackages` helper, so a YAML/JSON round-tripped map no longer silently skips the package check. The `map[string]any` signature is kept (the e2e/first-agent tests exercise it directly); the MCP server builds the map from the typed `*manifest.RuntimeRequirements`. Unit test `TestCheckRuntimeRequirements_SystemPackagesAnySlice` added (fails on the old `[]string`-only assertion).

### - [x] F-4.4.5 — No seccomp baseline profile ships with Podium [Low] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.4.1 (spec line 379) describes `seccomp-strict` as "Strict syscall allowlist (per a baseline profile shipped with Podium)." A repo-wide search for `seccomp`, "baseline profile", and a syscall allowlist finds no such profile in any package, asset, or config; the only `syscall` references are signal handling in `cmd/podium/main.go`. The surrounding prose frames sandbox enforcement as the host's responsibility ("Hosts with sandbox capability honor the profile"), and Podium's enforced behavior is the refusal gate in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:592-620`, which is implemented correctly. The parenthetical claim that Podium ships a baseline seccomp profile is therefore unmet. Suggested direction: either ship a baseline seccomp profile referenced by the adapter or materialization layer, or soften the spec parenthetical to describe the baseline as host-supplied.

**Resolution (82e8416):** Podium now ships `pkg/materialize/seccomp-strict.json`, an OCI/Docker seccomp document with a strict default-ERRNO syscall allowlist, embedded via `go:embed`. New `SeccompStrictProfile`/`SandboxBaselineProfile`/`WriteSandboxProfile` expose and deliver it; `podium-mcp` writes the baseline under `<root>/.podium/seccomp-strict.json` when a host honors `sandbox_profile: seccomp-strict`. Unit `seccomp_test.go` (validates strict allowlist, copy semantics, atomic write) + e2e delivery test added.
## F-4.5 — 4.5 Domain Organization (4.5.1 DOMAIN.md, 4.5.2 Imports/Globs, 4.5.3 Unlisted Folders, 4.5.4 Across Layers, 4.5.5 Discovery Rendering)

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md against the implementation._

I checked the DOMAIN.md parse/merge/render code in `pkg/domain` and `pkg/manifest`, the `LoadDomain` discovery renderer in `pkg/registry/core/core.go`, the HTTP wire surface in `pkg/registry/server/server.go`, the filesystem ingest walk in `pkg/registry/filesystem`, the store interface in `pkg/store`, and the import lint rules in `pkg/lint/domain_imports.go`. The notable-list ordering, featured surfacing, default knobs, pass-through chain folding, sparse-subdomain folding, and the depth-cap rendering note are implemented and tested in core. The DOMAIN.md content model is not wired into the read path: the store has no domain record, the ingest walk discards `DOMAIN.md`, and `LoadDomain` synthesizes the response purely from artifact manifest records. As a result the description slots, keywords, include/exclude imports, unlisted suppression, per-domain discovery overrides, cross-layer DOMAIN.md merge, multi-level subtree depth, and the wire `folded_from` annotation are missing or unreachable.

### - [x] F-4.5.1 — DOMAIN.md content is never ingested or read at load_domain time [High] — CLOSED

**Resolution (546bdf0):** ingest now walks DOMAIN.md and persists a `store.DomainRecord` per (tenant, layer, path) (new `PutDomain`/`ListDomains` across Memory/SQLite/Postgres); `LoadDomain` loads the visible records and merges per-path candidates across layers via `domain.MergeAcrossLayers`, then applies description, keywords, imports, unlisted, and discovery overrides.

(gap) §4.5.1 defines `DOMAIN.md` as the file that configures domain composition (description, prose body, `unlisted`, `include`/`exclude`, per-domain `discovery:` overrides) and states that without one a folder is a regular navigable domain. §4.5 says a domain's members include "anything brought in by an explicit import." The filesystem walk that feeds ingest explicitly skips DOMAIN.md: `pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:98` ("DOMAIN.md files are ignored at this stage; phase 8 adds domain composition") and the walk only records files named `ARTIFACT.md` (`walk.go:112`). The metadata store has no domain record type at all (`pkg/store/store.go:131-155` interface exposes only manifest, dependency, admin-grant, and layer-config methods; `ManifestRecord` at `store.go:46-78` has no domain fields). `LoadDomain` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:239-353`) builds its entire response from `r.visibleManifests` and never consults any DOMAIN.md. `pkg/domain/domain.go` (`MergeAcrossLayers`, `DefaultRender`, `SortDescriptors`) has zero non-test callers, and `manifest.ParseDomain` is called only by the linter (`pkg/lint/domain_imports.go:107`), never by the registry or ingest. The effect is that none of the DOMAIN.md-driven behavior in §4.5 reaches a live `load_domain` response. Suggested direction: persist parsed DOMAIN.md per (tenant, layer, domain-path) at ingest, then have `LoadDomain` load and merge the relevant DOMAIN.md candidates and apply description, keywords, imports, unlisted, and discovery overrides.

### - [x] F-4.5.2 — load_domain returns no domain description or prose body [High] — CLOSED

**Resolution (546bdf0):** the requested domain's `Description` resolves to the prose body, then the frontmatter `description`, then the synthesized basename fallback (`domain.FallbackDescription`); each child or sibling `DomainDescriptor.Description` carries the frontmatter `description` or fallback, never the body.

(gap) §4.5.5 "Description rendering" requires that the requested domain's description resolve to the prose body if present, else the frontmatter `description`, else a synthesized fallback (directory basename, title-cased and de-slugged), and that each child or sibling carry its frontmatter `description` (or fallback). §4.5.1 likewise states the frontmatter `description:` is used wherever the domain appears as a child or sibling. In `LoadDomain` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:262-353`), `res.Description` is never assigned and the `DomainDescriptor` entries appended at `core.go:304-307` set only `Path` and `Name`, leaving `Description` empty. There is no basename title-casing or de-slugging fallback anywhere in the function. The wire response (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:514-523`) therefore always returns an empty `description` for both the requested domain and every subdomain. Suggested direction: once DOMAIN.md is ingested (F-4.5.1), populate the requested domain's `Description` from body-or-frontmatter-or-fallback and each subdomain's `Description` from its frontmatter-or-fallback, applying the body only to the requested path.

### - [x] F-4.5.3 — load_domain keywords are never populated [High] — CLOSED

**Resolution (546bdf0):** `LoadDomain` surfaces the merged DOMAIN.md `discovery.keywords` for the requested domain and emits an explicit empty list at the root per §4.5.5.

(gap) §4.5.5 lists `keywords` as "Returned verbatim in `load_domain` output for this domain," and §4.5.1 shows `discovery.keywords` in DOMAIN.md frontmatter. The result struct carries the field (`LoadDomainResult.Keywords`, `pkg/registry/core/core.go:172`) and the server serializes it (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:381,517`), but `LoadDomain` never assigns `res.Keywords`, so it is always nil. §4.5.5 "Root domain" requires `keywords` to be `[]` at root; the field is `omitempty` on the wire (`server.go:381`) and is left nil, so it is omitted rather than emitted as `[]`. Suggested direction: surface the merged DOMAIN.md `discovery.keywords` for the requested domain and emit an explicit empty list at the root.

### - [x] F-4.5.4 — folded_from annotation is computed in core but dropped on the wire [High] — CLOSED

**Resolution (546bdf0):** the server `ArtifactDescriptor` gained `folded_from string \`json:"folded_from,omitempty"\``, and `descriptorOf` copies it from the core descriptor, so a folded artifact's navigation hint reaches the caller.

(inconsistency) §4.5.5 "Folding mechanics" requires that a folded subdomain's artifacts "surface in the parent's leaf list with a `folded_from: <subpath>` annotation so the agent can navigate further." Core computes this correctly: `ArtifactDescriptor.FoldedFrom` is set in `LoadDomain` at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:292-295`. The HTTP `ArtifactDescriptor` type has no `folded_from` field (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:394-402`), and the conversion helper `descriptorOf` (`server.go:834-842`) copies only ID, Type, Version, Description, Tags, and Score, discarding `FoldedFrom`. The notable list in the `load_domain` response is built through that helper (`server.go:525-526`), so a folded artifact reaches the caller indistinguishable from a direct child and the navigation hint the spec promises is lost. Suggested direction: add `FoldedFrom string \`json:"folded_from,omitempty"\`` to the server `ArtifactDescriptor` and copy it in `descriptorOf`.

### - [x] F-4.5.5 — unlisted: true is never enforced; subtree is not removed from enumeration [High] — CLOSED

**Resolution (546bdf0):** `LoadDomain` drops any domain whose merged DOMAIN.md (or an ancestor) sets `unlisted: true` from `Subdomains` enumeration (`unlistedAt`), and returns `ErrDomainNotFound` when the requested path resolves only under an unlisted folder; artifacts inside stay reachable via `load_artifact`, `search_artifacts`, and imports.

(gap) §4.5.3 requires that `unlisted: true` in a folder's DOMAIN.md "removes that folder and its entire subtree from `load_domain` enumeration" while artifacts inside remain reachable via `load_artifact`, appear in `search_artifacts`, and can be imported. §4.5.5 "Unknown paths" further requires that a path existing only under `unlisted: true` return `domain.not_found` so unlisted folders are indistinguishable from typos. Because DOMAIN.md is never ingested (F-4.5.1), the `Unlisted` flag (`manifest.Domain.Unlisted`, `pkg/manifest/types.go:207`) is parsed only by the linter and never reaches `LoadDomain`. The renderer enumerates every visible manifest under the path with no unlisted suppression (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:267-308`), so an unlisted subtree is fully enumerable through `load_domain`, and `load_domain(<unlisted-path>)` returns a normal result rather than `domain.not_found`. This is a confidentiality gap: unlisted folders intended to be undetectable through enumeration probing are exposed. Suggested direction: during enumeration, drop any domain whose merged DOMAIN.md has `unlisted: true` (and its subtree) from `Subdomains`, and return `ErrDomainNotFound` when the requested path resolves only under an unlisted ancestor.

### - [x] F-4.5.6 — include/exclude imports are not resolved at load_domain time [High] — CLOSED

**Resolution (546bdf0):** `LoadDomain` expands the merged `include:` globs over the visible catalog and subtracts `exclude:` (`domain.ResolveImports`), merging the imported artifacts into the notable candidate pool under their canonical IDs. Imports are dynamic (resolved per call, no re-ingest).

(gap) §4.5.2 specifies that `include:`/`exclude:` globs resolve at `load_domain` time over the effective view, that `exclude:` is applied after `include:`, and that imports are dynamic (a new artifact under an included glob is picked up without re-ingest). §4.5.5 "Visibility-aware counts," "Candidate pool," and "Notable selection" all state that a domain's artifact set is "canonical children plus those brought in by `DOMAIN.md include:` (after `exclude:`)." `LoadDomain` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:267-272`) only considers manifests whose canonical ID is under the requested path prefix (`manifestsUnder`, `directArtifactsOf`); it never reads `include`/`exclude` and never pulls in artifacts from other prefixes. The glob matcher and import-pattern resolution exist (`pkg/lint/domain_imports.go:128-261`, mirrored from `pkg/sync/scope.go`) but run only as ingest-time lint warnings. Consequently imported artifacts never appear in `load_domain` output, folding/budget counts ignore imports, and `exclude:` has no runtime effect. Suggested direction: in `LoadDomain`, after loading the merged DOMAIN.md for the path, expand `include:` globs against the visible catalog, subtract `exclude:`, and merge the resulting artifacts into the candidate pool used for the notable list and the recursive counts.

### - [x] F-4.5.7 — load_domain renders a single level only; depth and max_depth ceiling do not expand a subtree [High] — CLOSED

**Resolution (546bdf0):** `DomainDescriptor` (core and wire) now carries a nested `Subdomains` tree; `renderSubtree` recurses up to the resolved depth. The effective render depth defaults to the resolved `max_depth` ceiling (merged DOMAIN.md `discovery.max_depth`, else 3); a caller `depth` overrides it and is capped at the ceiling with the cap surfaced in the rendering note.

(gap) §4.2 and §4.5.5 specify that `load_domain` returns a rendered subtree bounded by `max_depth` (default 3) and that a caller `depth` "counts levels in the rendered (post-fold) tree," with `load_domain("finance", depth=2)` returning "a two-level subtree of subdomains, each rendered with their short `description` only." §4.5.5 "Caller overrides" gives a worked example where depth reaches a deep descendant through a pass-through chain. The implementation renders only the immediate children of the requested path (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:286-308` iterates `childNames` and appends one `DomainDescriptor` per immediate child; subdomains carry no nested children and no depth recursion exists). `opts.Depth` is used solely to emit the "capped" note (`core.go:341-346`) and never to expand or limit the rendered tree, and `maxDepth` is a fixed constant (`core.go:252`) that bounds nothing structurally. The response type has no nested-subtree representation (`LoadDomainResult.Subdomains` is a flat `[]DomainDescriptor`, `core.go:173`). So any `depth > 1` request returns the same single level, and the `max_depth` ceiling is inert except for the note. Suggested direction: render subdomains recursively up to the resolved depth ceiling, attaching a nested children representation per `DomainDescriptor`, and honor the post-fold depth-counting semantics.

### - [x] F-4.5.8 — DOMAIN.md cross-layer merge (§4.5.4) is implemented but never invoked [Medium] — CLOSED

**Resolution (7b2dafe):** the unreachable-merge defect was closed by F-4.5.1 (`mergedDomains` now calls `domain.MergeAcrossLayers` over the per-layer DOMAIN.md candidates inside `LoadDomain`). For the empty-description edge, the non-empty-last-layer-wins rule is the correct §4.5.4 reading: YAML cannot distinguish an omitted `description:` from `description: ""`, and treating empty as "clear" would erase a lower layer's description whenever a higher layer only adds `include:` patterns. Documented in `MergeAcrossLayers`; regression-guarded by `TestLoadDomain_CrossLayerDescriptionNotClearedByOmission`.

(gap) §4.5.4 specifies the cross-layer merge rules for DOMAIN.md: `description`/body last-layer-wins, `include`/`exclude` additive, `unlisted` most-restrictive, `discovery.*` most-restrictive (lowest for `max_depth`/`notable_count`/`target_response_tokens`, highest for `fold_below_artifacts`, `true` over `false` for `fold_passthrough_chains`), and `featured`/`deprioritize`/`keywords` append-unique. `pkg/domain/domain.go:22-74` (`MergeAcrossLayers`, `mergeDiscovery`) implements these rules and is unit-tested (`pkg/domain/domain_test.go`). However the function has no non-test caller (verified by grep across the repo), because DOMAIN.md never reaches the registry runtime (F-4.5.1). The merge logic is therefore unreachable from `load_domain`. One additional detail: §4.5.4 mandates last-layer-wins for `description`, but `MergeAcrossLayers` only overwrites `out.Description` when the candidate's value is non-empty (`domain.go:33-35`), so a higher-precedence layer that intentionally clears the description to empty cannot override a lower layer's non-empty value. Suggested direction: invoke `MergeAcrossLayers` over the per-layer DOMAIN.md candidates inside `LoadDomain` once DOMAIN.md ingestion exists, and reconsider whether an explicitly empty higher-layer `description` should win.

### - [x] F-4.5.9 — deprioritize and notable signal/source tagging are not implemented [Medium] — CLOSED

**Resolution (7b2dafe):** `deprioritize` is honored by `orderNotable` (ranked last, excluded when the notable cap leaves no room; already wired via F-4.5.1's `resolveKnobs`). Added a `Source` discriminator to the core and wire `ArtifactDescriptor`: `orderNotable` tags featured entries `"featured"` and the rest `"signal"` per §4.5.5 notable-selection (featured wins on dedup). The §3.3 learn-from-usage signal source is not yet wired, so the `"signal"` slot is currently filled by domain enumeration ranking. Covered by `TestLoadDomain_NotableSourceTagging`, `TestLoadDomain_RootNotableSourceSignalOnly`, and e2e `TestDomains_NotableSourceTag`.

(gap) §4.5.5 "Knobs" defines `deprioritize` (children matching are ranked last and excluded from the notable list unless space permits) and "Notable selection" requires the notable list to be the union of `featured:` entries and learn-from-usage reranked artifacts, with a deduplicated artifact "tagged `source: \"featured\"`." `LoadDomain` honors `featured` ordering and the `notable_count` cap (`orderNotable`, `pkg/registry/core/core.go:442-467`; cap at `core.go:315-317`), but it never reads `deprioritize` (the field exists at `manifest.DomainDiscovery.Deprioritize`, `pkg/manifest/types.go:226`, but is not consulted in the renderer) and there is no `source` discriminator on `ArtifactDescriptor` (`core.go:187-199`) to mark featured-vs-signal entries. The signal/learn-from-usage source is also absent; only the featured source contributes, which makes the spec's deduplication-and-cap rules effectively no-ops beyond truncation. The `deprioritize` gap is reachable as soon as DOMAIN.md is wired. Suggested direction: apply `deprioritize` glob matching to push matching children to the end of the notable candidate pool and exclude them unless budget permits, and add a `source` field to the descriptor when a signal source is introduced.

### - [x] F-4.5.10 — rendering note omits the depth-reduction case for the response budget [Medium] — CLOSED

**Resolution (7b2dafe):** with multi-level rendering present (F-4.5.7), the §4.5.5 budget pass now tightens the rendered subtree depth (coarse) before the notable list (fine). `estimateResponseTokens` recurses into nested subdomains so depth reduction measurably shrinks the estimate; `renderedDepth`/`truncateToDepth` drop the deepest levels. The note emits "Subtree depth reduced from X to Y to fit the response budget.", the notable-only form, and the combined "Notable list reduced from A to B; subtree depth reduced from X to Y ..." form. Covered by `TestLoadDomain_BudgetReducesDepthNote`, `TestLoadDomain_BudgetReducesDepthAndNotableNote`, and e2e `TestDomains_BudgetReducesSubtreeDepthNote`.

(inconsistency) §4.5.5 "Rendering note" lists two budget-driven note forms: "Notable list reduced from X to Y to fit the response budget." and "Subtree depth reduced from X to Y to fit the response budget." (and a combined form). The renderer only tightens the notable count to meet `target_response_tokens` and only ever emits the notable-list note (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:322-340`); it never reduces subtree depth for the budget and never produces the "Subtree depth reduced ..." sentence. This follows from the single-level renderer (F-4.5.7), since there is no multi-level subtree to tighten. The depth-cap note ("Requested depth N capped at the configured ceiling of M.") is implemented and tested (`core.go:341-346`, `discovery_test.go:101-113`). Suggested direction: once multi-level rendering exists (F-4.5.7), tighten depth before or alongside notable count under the budget and emit the corresponding note variant.

### - [x] F-4.5.11 — per-domain discovery overrides and allow_per_domain_overrides are not applied [Medium] — CLOSED

**Resolution (7b2dafe):** `resolveKnobs` now layers the discovery knobs in §4.5.5 precedence order: package defaults (max_depth 3, notable_count 10, target_response_tokens 4000, the §4.5.5 default) → §13.12 tenant `registry.yaml` discovery block (`core.DiscoveryDefaults`, wired via `Registry.WithDiscoveryDefaults`) → per-domain merged DOMAIN.md `discovery:` block (gated by `allow_per_domain_overrides`) → caller options. serverboot parses the `discovery:` block (including `allow_per_domain_overrides`, tri-state `fold_passthrough_chains`) and applies it; the §4.5.5 lint warning (`lint.domain_discovery_override_disabled`) flags DOMAIN.md `discovery:` blocks when overrides are disabled. Covered by `TestLoadDomain_TenantDiscoveryDefaultsApplied`, `TestLoadDomain_AllowPerDomainOverridesGate`, `TestRuleDomainDiscoveryOverrideDisallowed`, `TestApplyYAML_DiscoveryBlock`, and integration `TestDomainComposition_AllowPerDomainOverridesGate`.

(gap) §4.5.5 "Where they're configured" states that a `discovery:` block in DOMAIN.md frontmatter overrides the tenant defaults for that subtree (subject to cross-layer merge), and that a tenant-level `discovery.allow_per_domain_overrides: false` disables per-domain overrides registry-wide with a lint warning. `LoadDomain` resolves `notableCount`, `foldPassthrough`, `maxDepth`, `TargetResponseTokens`, and `FoldBelowArtifacts` only from caller-supplied `LoadDomainOptions` or hardcoded defaults (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:252-260`, plus the option fields at `core.go:202-224`); it never reads a DOMAIN.md `discovery:` block for the requested subtree (a consequence of F-4.5.1). There is no `allow_per_domain_overrides` handling anywhere (grep finds no such identifier in the codebase). The tenant-scope `discovery:` block in `registry.yaml` (§13.12) is also not consulted by `LoadDomain`; the defaults are the package constants `DefaultMaxDepth`/`DefaultNotableCount` and literals. Suggested direction: resolve the effective discovery knobs as caller-override over merged-DOMAIN.md-override over tenant `registry.yaml` over package defaults, gated by `allow_per_domain_overrides`.

### - [x] F-4.5.12 — analyze fold/split thresholds are hardcoded and not configurable [Low] — CLOSED

**Resolution (7b2dafe):** no spec-driven change is required — §4.5.5 names the sparsity/pass-through/split/fold heuristics but does not quantify them, and the §13.12 `discovery:` block tunes `load_domain` rendering, not the analyze report. Exposing analyze thresholds as tenant config would introduce configuration the spec does not define, so the heuristics stay fixed. Corrected the misleading `AnalyzeDomain` comment that promised a future "registry-wide discovery config can override them later".

(inconsistency) §4.5.5 "Layout analysis" describes `podium domain analyze [<path>]` as a quality report covering sparsity, pass-through chains, and split (high artifact count + tag-cluster entropy) or fold (low artifact count) candidates; the command is implemented in core (`pkg/registry/core/analyze.go:56-106`) and wired in the CLI (`cmd/podium/main.go:542-571`, endpoint `/v1/domain/analyze`), and it computes sparsity, pass-through chain length, and tag entropy as required. The fold threshold (`recursive_count <= 1`) and split thresholds (`recursive_count >= 20` and tag entropy `>= 0.7`) are hardcoded (`analyze.go:89-103`). The code comment at `analyze.go:54-55` says "the registry-wide `discovery:` config can override them later," and the spec attributes the heuristics to §4.5.5, but the section does not actually specify these numeric thresholds, so this is a minor observation rather than a contract violation. Suggested direction: keep the heuristics or expose them via the tenant `discovery:` config if operators need to tune them; no spec-driven change is required.

### - [x] F-4.5.13 — passthrough chain folding may collapse past a domain that has imported members [Low] — CLOSED

**Resolution (7b2dafe):** with imports resolved at load time (F-4.5.6), `collapsePassthroughChain` now stops at a curated domain (`curatedDomainPaths`: a DOMAIN.md description, body, keywords, or resolved `include:` members), and the `fold_below_artifacts` recursive count (`subtreeMemberCount`) unions canonical descendants with members imported by any DOMAIN.md in the subtree. A domain whose members arrive only through `include:` is no longer collapsed or folded away. Covered by `TestLoadDomain_ImportedMembersPreventPassthroughCollapse`, `TestLoadDomain_ImportedMembersCountTowardFold`, integration `TestDomainComposition_ImportedMembersPreserveDomain`, and e2e `TestDomains_ImportedMembersPreventCollapse`.

(bug) §4.5.5 folds a pass-through chain only at "single-child intermediate domains," meaning a domain with members should not be folded away. `collapsePassthroughChain` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:403-418`) decides a level is a pass-through purely from canonical children: it stops only when `directArtifactsOf` is non-empty or the immediate-child group count is not exactly 1. Because imports are not resolved at load time (F-4.5.6), a domain whose only members arrive through `DOMAIN.md include:` looks empty to this function and would be collapsed away, dropping it from the rendered tree even though it has a curated member set and likely a description and keywords. The same blind spot applies to the `fold_below_artifacts` recursive count (`core.go:288-289`), which counts only canonical descendants. This becomes observable once imports are wired (F-4.5.6); flagged Low because it is latent today. Suggested direction: include imported members in the per-level membership test used by both `collapsePassthroughChain` and the recursive fold count, and do not treat a domain with a DOMAIN.md description/keywords as a bare pass-through.
## F-4.6 — 4.6 Layers and Visibility

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md against the implementation (re-run against main e41f44e)._

I re-verified the layer model, the visibility evaluator, the source-type infrastructure, the `extends:` merge semantics, the field-semantics table, the cross-layer collision rule, the layer-management endpoint, and the new standalone layer bootstrap (`bootstrapLayerPath`) plus the new yaml/env keys and tests. The actual checked-out tree is plain `main` at e41f44e: commit `1e67daa` (serverboot ingest from `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH`) and the `--layer-path` flag are present, but commits `d95c7bf`, `e2c9c59`, and `b74041c` (per-layer `visibility:` loading from `.podium/layers.yaml` and trusted-headers identity) are not ancestors of HEAD, so `pkg/registry/server/layer_visibility.go` does not exist in this tree. None of the prior findings were resolved by the merge. All eight remain open with refreshed citations; one (F-4.6.8) is restated because the per-layer-visibility loading its prior text referenced is absent here, and the bootstrap instead hardcodes `Public:true`. The merge added one new finding: the standalone bootstrap marks every layer `Public:true` unconditionally, including when an identity provider is configured.

### - [x] F-4.6.1 — `extends:` merge ignores most of the field-semantics table and never reaches the served frontmatter [High] — CLOSED

(gap) The field-semantics table (spec lines 686-703) mandates per-field merge for `description`, `name`, `release_notes`, `tags`, `when_to_use`, `sensitivity`, `mcpServers`, `requiresApproval`, `runtime_requirements`, `sandbox_profile`, `delegates_to`, `external_resources`, `license`, and `search_visibility`, with list-append, deep-merge-by-name, most-restrictive, and child-wins rules respectively. The implementation merges only three table fields. `mergeChain` (pkg/registry/core/core.go:904-938) folds `Description` (child wins, line 910-912), `Tags` (append-unique, line 916), and `Sensitivity` (most-restrictive, line 917) at the `store.ManifestRecord` level, then takes the child's `Frontmatter` and `Body` byte blobs wholesale (core.go:929-934). Every other table field (`name`, `release_notes`, `when_to_use`, `mcpServers`, `requiresApproval`, `runtime_requirements`, `sandbox_profile`, `delegates_to`, `external_resources`, `license`, `search_visibility`) lives only inside the raw `Frontmatter` bytes because `store.ManifestRecord` does not carry them as structured fields, so none of them are merged. The consumer reads the merged manifest through `LoadArtifactResult.Frontmatter`, which `resultFromRecord` sets to `rec.Frontmatter` (core.go:1005) — the unmerged child blob. `LoadArtifact` calls `assembleResult`, which builds the result from the merged record (core.go:870-871), but the merged record's `Frontmatter` is still the child blob from line 932-934. The HTTP response returns it verbatim (`Frontmatter: string(res.Frontmatter)`, pkg/registry/server/server.go:684). The merged `Tags` and `Description` record fields are therefore lost for any consumer that parses the frontmatter, and the parent's `when_to_use`, `mcpServers`, `requiresApproval`, `runtime_requirements`, `delegates_to`, and `external_resources` are never inherited. `TestExtends_LoadMergesFields` and `TestExtends_HiddenParent` (pkg/registry/core/extends_test.go:80-176) only assert the child's description, version, body, and the presence of the child's own frontmatter content (line 158-160), so the missing merges are not caught. Suggested direction: parse the child and parent frontmatter into `manifest.Artifact`, apply the full table per-field, and re-serialize the merged frontmatter (or surface the merged structured fields) before returning from `assembleResult`.

**Resolution (commit `4cd19b4`):** Added `manifest.MergeExtends` (full §4.6 table: scalar child-wins, list append/append-unique, most-restrictive sensitivity/sandbox/search_visibility, deep-merge mcpServers/runtime_requirements, child-overrides-if-set for unlisted fields) and `manifest.SerializeArtifact`. `core.mergeChain` now parses each record's frontmatter, folds the chain via `MergeExtends`, surfaces the merged scalar fields onto the record, and re-serializes the merged frontmatter (with `extends:` stripped for §4.6 hidden-parent privacy) so every consumer of the served frontmatter sees the merge.

### - [x] F-4.6.2 — `extends:` does not enforce that child and parent share the same `type:` [High] — CLOSED

(gap) The spec (line 703) states: "The child's `type:` must match the parent's; ingest rejects an `extends:` chain that crosses types." `resolveExtendsPin` (pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:779-821) resolves and pins the parent version but never compares the parent's `Type` against the child's. At read time `mergeChain` does the opposite of rejecting: `if c.Type != "" { out.Type = c.Type }` (pkg/registry/core/core.go:913-915) overwrites with the child's type, masking any mismatch. A `type: skill` artifact can extend a `type: context` parent and ingest succeeds. Suggested direction: in `resolveExtendsPin` (or the ingest record assembly), load the resolved parent record and reject with `ingest.invalid_artifact` when `parent.Type != child.Type`.

**Resolution (commit `4cd19b4`):** `resolveExtendsPin` now returns the resolved parent's `Type` alongside the pin; the ingest loop rejects with `ingest.invalid_artifact` when it differs from the child's type. `mergeChain` no longer masks a mismatch because ingest never stores a cross-type chain.

### - [x] F-4.6.3 — Cross-layer collision rejection does not honor the `extends:` exception [High] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) The spec (lines 675-682) states a collision on the same canonical ID across layers "is rejected at ingest **unless** the higher-precedence artifact declares `extends: <lower-precedence-id>`," and "Silent shadowing is never permitted." The filesystem walk's collision check (pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:54-70) rejects every duplicate canonical ID unconditionally when `CollisionPolicyError`/`Default` is in effect, with no inspection of whether the higher-precedence record declares `extends:`. The two intended behaviors collapse into one: a legitimate same-ID extends-overlay is rejected exactly like an illegal silent shadow. `TestWalk_CollisionWithoutExtendsFails` (pkg/registry/filesystem/walk_test.go) only covers the without-extends case; no test exercises the allowed extends-collision path. Separately, the server-store ingest path (pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go) performs no cross-layer collision detection at all; `PutManifest` keys records by `(tenant, artifact_id, version)` with the layer excluded, so two layers contributing the same canonical ID at different versions without `extends:` are both stored and silently shadowed at read time, which the spec forbids. This is now reachable through the new standalone bootstrap: `bootstrapLayerPath` ingests each layer via `ingest.Ingest` (internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:168-175) in a loop with no cross-layer ID check. Suggested direction: in `Walk`, allow the collision when the higher-precedence record's `Artifact.Extends` resolves to the colliding ID; add cross-layer same-ID detection to the server-store ingest path.

**Resolution (commit `4cd19b4`):** `filesystem.Walk` permits a same-ID collision when the higher-precedence record declares `extends:` resolving to the colliding ID (`declaresExtendsTo`). The server-store ingest path indexes manifests from other layers and rejects a same-ID record with `ingest.collision` unless an `extends:` overlay links the two (so the standalone bootstrap no longer silently shadows). `resolveExtendsPin` distinguishes a same-ID cross-layer overlay (a legal parent in a lower layer) from a true self-cycle. `podium lint` switched to `CollisionPolicyDefault` so collisions surface while legitimate overlays pass.

### - [x] F-4.6.4 — User-defined layer visibility can be widened beyond `users: [<registrant>]` [High] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) The spec (line 616) states user-defined layers "have implicit visibility `users: [<registrant>]`; the field is set automatically and cannot be widened." The register handler accepts caller-supplied `public`, `organization`, `groups`, and `users` verbatim for a user-defined layer and persists them (pkg/registry/server/layers.go:208-229). The implicit-users branch only fills `Users` when none were supplied and `Owner` is non-empty (layers.go:227-229); it never clears `Public`, `Organization`, or `Groups`. A request with `user_defined: true, owner: alice, public: true` produces a stored layer that is both user-defined and `Public: true`, visible to everyone. The CLI exposes this combination (cmd/podium/layer.go register flags). The `update` handler compounds the issue: it only ever adds visibility (`if patch.Public { cfg.Public = true }`, layers.go:163-174), so a user-defined layer can be widened and never narrowed through it. Additionally, `Owner` is read from the request body (layers.go:160-162, 217) rather than derived from the authenticated identity, so a caller can register a "user-defined" layer owned by an arbitrary subject. No validation anywhere rejects or strips widened visibility on `UserDefined` layers. Suggested direction: when `UserDefined` is true, force `Public=false`, `Organization=false`, `Groups=nil`, `Users=[authenticatedSub]` and ignore caller-supplied visibility; derive `Owner` from the request identity.

**Resolution (commit `4cd19b4`):** `register` forces a user-defined layer to `Public=false`/`Organization=false`/`Groups=nil`/`Users=[owner]` and derives `Owner` from the authenticated identity (new `LayerEndpoint.WithIdentityResolver`), ignoring caller-supplied visibility and a spoofed owner. `update` skips the visibility/owner patch fields for a user-defined layer and gates admin auth on admin-defined layers only, so a user-defined layer's implicit `users:[owner]` can never be widened.

### - [x] F-4.6.5 — Layer-management endpoint runs without admin authorization in the wired server [High] — CLOSED

(bug) The spec (lines 584, 618) reserves admin-defined layer add/remove/reorder and visibility edits for tenant admins; §4.7.2 governs the `admin` role. `LayerEndpoint` defaults `authAdmin` to a no-op (`func(*http.Request) error { return nil }`, pkg/registry/server/layers.go:55) and exposes `WithAdminAuth` to install a real check (layers.go:60-63). `WithAdminAuth` is never called for the layer endpoint in non-test code; serverboot constructs the endpoint with only `WithDefaultVisibility` (internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:323-324) and mounts it at `/v1/layers` and `/v1/layers/` (serverboot.go:343-344). Every admin-gated operation — registering an admin-defined layer (layers.go:201-206), `update` (which gates solely on `authAdmin`, layers.go:137-140), `unregister` (layers.go:309-314), and `reorder` (layers.go:358-363) — passes the admin check trivially in the running server. Any caller that can reach the API can create, mutate, widen, or delete admin-defined layers and their per-layer visibility. The grep across the repo confirms only `RuntimeKeyEndpoint.WithAdminAuth` (runtime_endpoint.go:37) has a production caller; `LayerEndpoint.WithAdminAuth` has none. Suggested direction: wire `LayerEndpoint.WithAdminAuth` to a check backed by `core.Registry.AdminAuthorize` (pkg/registry/core/admin.go:21) in serverboot.

**Resolution (commit `4cd19b4`):** serverboot now wires `LayerEndpoint.WithAdminAuth` to `core.Registry.AdminAuthorize`. The check is bypassed only when no identity provider is configured (the §13.10/§13.11 standalone, where the local operator is the de facto admin, mirroring the §4.6 visibility bypass); with an identity provider set, an unauthenticated caller is denied `auth.forbidden`, closing the unauthenticated admin-defined-layer mutation surface.

### - [x] F-4.6.6 — Direct `users:` visibility match compares only the OIDC subject, not the email [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) The visibility table (spec line 614) defines `users: [<user-id>, ...]` as "Listed user identifiers (OIDC subject)," and the config example (line 670) lists `users: [alice@acme.com]`, an email-style identifier. The direct evaluator matches a user only against `id.Sub`: `for _, u := range v.Users { if u == id.Sub { return true } }` (pkg/layer/composer.go:84-88). The group-resolver path, by contrast, matches against both `id.Sub` and `id.Email` (composer.go:76-82), and `TestVisibleWith_ResolverMatchesEmail` (pkg/layer/scim_visibility_test.go:62) documents that IdPs may carry the human identifier in `Email` while `Sub` is opaque (e.g., `auth0|abc123`). A caller whose `Sub` is opaque and whose `Email` is `alice@acme.com` is therefore denied a layer that lists `users: [alice@acme.com]`, even though the spec's own example uses that form. Suggested direction: in the direct `users:` loop, match `u == id.Sub || u == id.Email`, consistent with the group-resolver path.

**Resolution (commit `1da3ddc`):** `pkg/layer.VisibleWith`'s direct `users:` loop now matches `u == id.Sub || (id.Email != "" && u == id.Email)`, mirroring the group-resolver path, so a caller whose OIDC subject is opaque (`auth0|abc123`) but whose email matches a `users: [alice@acme.com]` entry sees the layer.

### - [x] F-4.6.7 — Search descriptors do not apply the `extends:` sensitivity merge, under-reporting child sensitivity [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) The field-semantics table (spec line 693) requires `sensitivity` to merge most-restrictive across an `extends:` chain. `SearchArtifacts` builds each result descriptor directly from the raw stored child record via `descriptorOf(sc.rec)` (pkg/registry/core/core.go:571) and never resolves the extends chain, so a child whose parent is `high` but whose own frontmatter declares `low` is surfaced in search results as `low`. `LoadArtifact` resolves the chain and reports `high` (core.go:870-871, 917), so the same artifact carries two different sensitivity values across the two read surfaces. Because `sensitivity` is informational metadata used for display and filtering (§4.7.4), the blast radius is limited, but discovery understates the effective sensitivity. Suggested direction: resolve `ExtendsPin` (or precompute the merged sensitivity at ingest) when building search descriptors so search and load agree.

**Resolution (commit `1da3ddc`):** Added a `Sensitivity` field to the core and wire `ArtifactDescriptor` (§4.7.4 names sensitivity as a `search_artifacts` response field, which was previously absent from the search surface entirely), and `SearchArtifacts` populates it via a new `mergedSensitivity` helper that folds the `extends:` chain most-restrictively, so the search and `load_artifact` surfaces report the same value. The e2e `TestExtends_SearchSensitivityMostRestrictive` (T-D-extends-48) is unskipped.

### - [x] F-4.6.8 — Admin-defined layer list with `source:` and `visibility:` blocks is not loaded from registry config [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) The §4.6 config schema (spec lines 628-671) is a per-tenant `layers:` list where each entry carries `id`, a `source:` block (`git:` with `repo`/`ref`/`root`, or `local:` with `path`), and a `visibility:` block (`public`, `organization`, `groups`, `users`). The serverboot YAML config parses no such list: `yamlConfig.Layers` is `yamlLayerCfg{ DefaultVisibility string; Path string }` (internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:58-64), two scalars and no per-layer `source:`/`visibility:` entries. The grep across the current tree confirms no `.podium/layers.yaml` per-layer visibility loader exists (the `layer_visibility.go` referenced by the prior finding is from commits `d95c7bf`/`e2c9c59`, which are not ancestors of e41f44e). Standalone boot derives layers from the filesystem walk of `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` and hardcodes `Public:true` for every layer with no visibility input: `bootstrapLayerPath` sets `LayerConfig{... Public:true}` and `layer.Layer{Visibility: layer.Visibility{Public:true}}` (internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:182-198), and `NewFromFilesystem` does the same (pkg/registry/server/server.go:227-231). The git-source and config-declared layer path is reachable only by registering layers at runtime through `/v1/layers` (which itself lacks admin authorization, see F-4.6.5); the declarative `registry.yaml` `layers:` block in the spec is not ingested at boot. Suggested direction: parse the full `layers:` list (id, source.git/source.local, visibility) from registry config and seed `store.LayerConfig` rows at startup, or document that the declarative layer list is supplied exclusively through the layer-management API.

**Resolution (commit `1da3ddc`):** `registry.yaml`'s `layers:` key now parses the §4.6 per-tenant list (`id`, `source.git`/`source.local`, `visibility`); the prior `layers.path`/`layers.default_visibility` scalars moved to top-level `layer_path:`/`default_layer_visibility:` keys to free the `layers:` key for the list (these scalars were implementation inventions with no spec-defined YAML shape). `bootstrapDeclaredLayers` seeds a `store.LayerConfig` per entry at startup, ingests `local` sources so their artifacts are immediately searchable, and seeds `git` sources as config rows for the §7.3.1 reingest/webhook path (a boot-time clone is unbounded network I/O that must not block startup, per the anti-hang rule). Declared layers compose before any `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` layers.

### - [x] F-4.6.9 — Standalone bootstrap forces `Public:true` on every layer regardless of deployment auth mode [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) The §4.6 visibility model governs every admin-defined layer through its config visibility, and read-side enforcement runs on every call (spec lines 605-618). The public-mode and filesystem-registry bypasses (lines 620-622) are the only sanctioned ways to short-circuit the evaluator to `true`. The new standalone bootstrap defeats this for any layer it ingests: `bootstrapLayerPath` runs unconditionally whenever `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` is set (internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:233), with no gate on `identityProvider` or `publicMode`, and assigns `Public:true` to both the persisted `LayerConfig` (serverboot.go:182-190) and the in-memory `layer.Layer` fed to `core.New` (serverboot.go:194-198). The deployment-wide `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY` (which defaults to `private` per spec line 464 and is wired into the register handler at layers.go:235-245) has no effect on bootstrap layers. The spec ties the public default to the §13.10 standalone, no-identity-provider deployment (lines 175, 466), but the code applies it even when `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` is configured, so an authenticated server that bootstraps from a filesystem path exposes every bootstrap layer to all callers, including unauthenticated ones, contradicting the §4.6 model. These layers carry `UserDefined:false` (admin-defined class) and cannot be narrowed later through `update`, which only widens (see F-4.6.4). Suggested direction: when an identity provider is configured and public mode is off, apply `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY` (or refuse the unconditional public default) to bootstrap layers rather than hardcoding `Public:true`, and reserve the public default for the no-IdP standalone path the spec describes.

**Resolution (commit `1da3ddc`):** `bootstrapLayerPath` and the declared-layer bootstrap stamp visibility via `defaultBootstrapVisibility`: `public` only for a no-identity-provider standalone or public mode (§13.10/§13.11, where the evaluator short-circuits to `true` anyway and spec line 466 specifies the public default), otherwise the configured `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY` (default `private`). An authenticated deployment that bootstraps from a filesystem path no longer marks every bootstrap layer `Public:true`. `NewFromFilesystem` keeps `Public:true` because the §13.11 filesystem-source registry has no identity provider by definition (spec line 455) and the visibility evaluator short-circuits there.
## F-4.7 — 4.7 Registry as a Service (4.7.1 Tenancy/Residency, 4.7.2 Access Control, 4.7.3 Reverse Dep Index, 4.7.4 Classification/Lifecycle, 4.7.5 Audit, 4.7.6 Version Resolution, 4.7.7 Vuln Tracking out-of-scope, 4.7.8 Quotas, 4.7.9 Signing)

_Reviewed spec/04-artifact-model.md against the implementation._
