I verified the version immutability invariant, embedding generation, dual-write semantics for external vector backends, tenancy, access control, the reverse dependency index, classification and lifecycle, version resolution and session consistency, audit, quotas, and signing against pkg/version, pkg/dependency, pkg/sign, pkg/vector, pkg/embedding, pkg/registry/core, pkg/registry/ingest, pkg/registry/server, pkg/store, internal/serverboot, and the relevant CLI commands. The immutability invariant, freeze windows with break-glass, the `delegates_to`/`extends` reverse-dependency edges, deprecation lifecycle, signing providers, materialize-time signature verification, force-push tolerance with `layer.history_rewritten`, and storage/search-QPS/materialize-rate quotas are implemented and match the spec. Several concrete contracts diverge from the spec: the embedding text projection contradicts the documented field set, the transactional outbox for external vector backends is absent, `latest` resolution uses highest-semver rather than most-recently-ingested, the `mcpServers` reverse-dependency edge does not resolve via `server_identifier`, the audit-volume quota is unenforced, and several model-versioning and ranking behaviours are missing.

### - [x] F-4.7.1 — Embedding text projection embeds the prose body and omits `when_to_use` [High] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) The §4.7 "Embedding generation" subsection defines the artifact embedding projection as built from frontmatter only — `name`, `description`, `when_to_use` (joined with newlines), and `tags` (joined) — and states explicitly: "The prose body is **not** embedded (the `SKILL.md` body for skills, the `ARTIFACT.md` body for other types). The body is noisy for retrieval and risks busting embedding-model context limits at the long-tail end." The implementation does the opposite. `composeEmbeddingText` in pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:589-603 builds the projection from `mr.ArtifactID`, `mr.Description`, `mr.Tags`, and the **first 1024 bytes of `mr.Body`** (the prose body). The identical core-side copy at pkg/registry/core/reembed.go:114-128 does the same. Three divergences: (1) the prose body is embedded despite the spec forbidding it; (2) `when_to_use` is never included; (3) `mr.ArtifactID` substitutes for `name`. The root cause is that `store.ManifestRecord` (pkg/store/store.go:46-78) carries no `Name` and no `WhenToUse` field — `WhenToUse` exists on the manifest type (pkg/manifest/types.go:104) but is dropped at `manifestRecordFor` (pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:694-718), so the projection cannot include it even if the code wanted to. Suggested direction: persist `Name` and `WhenToUse` on `ManifestRecord`, then rewrite both `composeEmbeddingText` functions to emit `name` + `description` + `strings.Join(whenToUse, "\n")` + `strings.Join(tags, " ")` and drop the body prefix entirely.

**Resolution:** Added `Name` and `WhenToUse` to `store.ManifestRecord` and populated them in `manifestRecordFor` (name and description sourced from `SKILL.md` for skills). Rewrote both `composeEmbeddingText` copies (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go` and `pkg/registry/core/reembed.go`) to emit `name` + `description` + `when_to_use` (newline-joined) + `tags` (space-joined), skipping empty parts via `joinNonEmpty` and dropping the prose body entirely. Unit tests in `pkg/registry/ingest/projection_internal_test.go` assert the field order and that neither the body nor the artifact id appears.

### - [ ] F-4.7.2 — Transactional outbox for external vector backends is not implemented [High] — DEFERRED

(gap) The §4.7 "Dual-write semantics for external vector backends" subsection mandates that when `RegistrySearchProvider` is configured to a backend outside the metadata store (any managed service or a separate pgvector instance), the registry coordinates writes through a transactional outbox: at ingest the manifest commit and a `vector_pending` row land in the same `RegistryStore` transaction; a background worker drains the outbox with exponential-backoff retry; "Ingest itself never blocks on the external service"; and a `vector.outbox_lagging` event fires when outbox depth or oldest-row age exceeds a threshold. No outbox exists in the code. A repository-wide search for `outbox`, `vector_pending`, and `outbox_lagging` finds matches only in spec/, deploy/runbook.md, deploy/grafana-dashboard.json (which references a `podium_vector_outbox_depth` metric), and docs/deployment/vector-backends.md. Ingest writes to the vector backend synchronously inline at pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:570-583 (`embedAndStore` calls `req.VectorPut(...)` directly), and a backend failure is recorded as an `EmbeddingFailure` (pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:549-557) with no retry beyond a manual `podium admin reembed`. Managed backends are fully wired and selectable (pkg/vector/pinecone.go, weaviate.go, qdrant.go; internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:435-443, 552-557; `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND`), so this configuration is reachable. The result is that ingest blocks on the external vector service and there is no transactional outbox, no drain worker, and no `vector.outbox_lagging` event. Suggested direction: add a `vector_pending` table written in the same transaction as `PutManifest`, a background drainer that retries with backoff and marks rows complete, and a depth/age gauge plus `vector.outbox_lagging` event; route managed-backend writes through the outbox while keeping the collocated pgvector/sqlite-vec single-transaction fast path.

**Deferred:** This is a new subsystem: a `vector_pending` outbox table added to all three `RegistryStore` backends, a background drain worker with exponential backoff, a Prometheus depth/age gauge, and a `vector.outbox_lagging` event. It is out of proportion to this batch and not safely completable green with fail-first tests in one session. No code was changed for this finding, so the tree stays green; tracked for a dedicated change.

### - [x] F-4.7.3 — `latest` resolves to highest semver, not most recently ingested [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §4.7.6 defines `load_artifact(<id>)` resolution: "`latest` = 'the most recently ingested non-deprecated version visible under the caller's effective view, at resolution time.'" The implementation resolves `latest` to the highest semver among visible non-deprecated versions, ignoring ingest time. In pkg/registry/core/core.go:824 the `PinLatest` path calls `version.Resolve(pin, resolveVersions)`, and `version.Resolve` (pkg/version/version.go:107-125) sorts candidates descending by semver and returns the first that matches; for `PinLatest`, `matches` returns `true` for every candidate (pkg/version/version.go:129-130), so the highest semver wins. `IngestedAt` is recorded on `ManifestRecord` (pkg/store/store.go:64) but is never consulted in resolution, and `ListManifests` orders by `(artifact_id, version)` lexically (pkg/store/memory.go:92-97, pkg/store/sqlite.go:232, pkg/store/postgres.go:238). The two definitions agree for monotonic version bumps but diverge when an older line gets a release ingested after a newer one (a backport): the spec would resolve to the backport (most recently ingested), the code resolves to the higher semver. The tests encode the highest-semver behaviour (pkg/version/version_test.go:70 asserts `latest` -> `2.1.3`; pkg/registry/core/core_test.go:249 expects `2.1.0`), so the divergence is currently masked by test data where highest semver is also newest. Suggested direction: for `PinLatest`, select by maximum `IngestedAt` among non-deprecated visible candidates (breaking ties by semver), rather than delegating to `version.Resolve`.

**Resolution:** Added `version.Candidate` (version + `IngestedAt`) and `version.ResolveLatest`, which selects the greatest `IngestedAt` with ties broken by the higher semver. The `LoadArtifact` `PinLatest` path in `pkg/registry/core/core.go` now builds candidates from the non-deprecated visible records and calls `ResolveLatest` (falling back to all versions when every candidate is deprecated); range, exact, and hash pins still use semver-ordered `version.Resolve`. Fail-first unit tests in `pkg/version/version_test.go` cover the backport case (a lower-semver line ingested last wins) and the ingest-time tie-break.

### - [x] F-4.7.4 — `mcpServers` reverse-dependency edge keys on the local name, not `server_identifier` [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §4.7.3 lists the indexed edges and specifies the MCP edge as "`mcpServers:` references that resolve to `mcp-server`-type artifacts via `server_identifier`." The implementation does not resolve via `server_identifier`. `edgesFor` in pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:750-754 builds the edge as `{From: id, To: srv.Name, Kind: "mcpServers"}`, where `srv.Name` is the consumer-side `mcpServers[].name` label (pkg/manifest/types.go:151-155, e.g. `finance-warehouse`). The canonical `server_identifier` (e.g. `npx:@company/finance-warehouse-mcp`) lives on the `mcp-server`-type target artifact (pkg/manifest/types.go:136) and is referenced nowhere in resolution logic (the only repository hit outside the type definition is that field declaration). Because `MCPServerRef` carries only `name`, `transport`, `command`, and `args` and no identifier, the edge target never matches the `mcp-server` artifact's canonical ID or its `server_identifier`, so the reverse index does not connect consumers to the `mcp-server` artifact they depend on. Suggested direction: derive a server identifier from the consumer's `mcpServers` entry (for example `transport:command` or `command:args[0]`), match it against ingested `mcp-server` artifacts' `server_identifier`, and set the edge `To` to the resolved `mcp-server` artifact ID; emit no edge (or a warning) when no `mcp-server` artifact resolves.

### - [ ] F-4.7.5 — Audit-volume quota is stored but never enforced [Medium] — DEFERRED

(gap) §4.7.8 lists the per-org admin-configurable limits as storage (bytes), search QPS, materialization rate, and audit volume, and states quota exhaustion returns structured errors (`quota.storage_exceeded`, etc.). Storage, search QPS, and materialize rate are enforced (pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:389-401 for storage; pkg/registry/server/rate_limit.go and server.go:538-563, 673 for search QPS and materialize rate). Audit volume is not. `AuditVolumePerDay` is persisted on the `Quota` struct (pkg/store/store.go:40) and round-tripped through SQLite and Postgres (audit_volume_quota column), but no code consults it: a repository search for `AuditVolumePerDay`, `quota.audit_volume_exceeded`, and `AllowAudit` finds no enforcement path. The comment at pkg/registry/server/rate_limit.go:11-12 claims audit volume is "enforced elsewhere (ingest, audit retention scheduler)," but internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go and pkg/audit/retention.go implement time-based retention (deleting records by age), which is a distinct mechanism from rejecting audit writes beyond a daily budget. There is no `quota.audit_volume_exceeded` error code. Suggested direction: add a per-tenant audit-volume counter checked before audit writes (or a daily rolling window) and return a `quota.audit_volume_exceeded` structured error when the configured `AuditVolumePerDay` is exceeded, or update the spec if audit volume is intentionally retention-only.

### - [ ] F-4.7.6 — Per-artifact `(model_id, dimensions)` recording and mixed-dimension query restriction are absent [Medium] — DEFERRED

(gap) The §4.7 "Model versioning and re-embedding" paragraph states: "The vector store records `(model_id, dimensions)` per artifact. When the configured embedding model changes ... the registry triggers a background re-embed via `podium admin reembed`. During re-embedding, the vector store may transiently contain mixed dimensions; query-time the registry restricts results to vectors matching the currently-configured model and emits `embedding.reembed_in_progress` events for progress monitoring. Once re-embedding completes, stale-dimension rows are purged." None of these per-row model-versioning behaviours exist. The vector `Put` SPI signature carries only `(tenantID, artifactID, version, embedding)` (pkg/vector/vector.go:65), and the pgvector schema stores only `(tenant_id, artifact_id, version, embedding)` with a single global dimension configured per backend (pkg/vector/pgvector.go:90-105, 27-31); there is no `model_id` column. `Query` filters only by tenant and orders by distance (pkg/vector/pgvector.go:111-141) with no model-version restriction. No `embedding.reembed_in_progress` event is emitted (the string appears only in docs/deployment/vector-backends.md) and no stale-dimension purge runs after re-embed (pkg/registry/core/reembed.go has no purge step). With a single global dimension, a model switch requires a full `podium admin reembed --all` and tolerates no transient mixed-dimension state. Suggested direction: add `model_id` (and dimensions) to the vector row and `Put`/`Query` SPI, restrict `Query` to the currently-configured model during re-embed, emit `embedding.reembed_in_progress`, and purge stale-model rows on completion.

**Deferred:** Threading `model_id`/`dimensions` through the `vector.Provider` `Put`/`Query` SPI touches all six backends (memory, pgvector, sqlite, pinecone, weaviate, qdrant) and every call site, plus query-time model restriction, `embedding.reembed_in_progress` emission, and the stale-row purge in `reembed.go`. This SPI-wide refactor cannot land green with fail-first tests alongside the other fixes in this batch. No code was changed for this finding, so the tree stays green; tracked for a dedicated change.

### - [ ] F-4.7.7 — Reverse-index search-ranking signal and cascading review are not implemented [Medium] — DEFERRED

(gap) §4.7.3 states the reverse dependency index drives three behaviours: impact analysis, cascading review ("When a high-sensitivity dependency changes, flag downstream artifacts for re-review"), and search ranking signals ("Frequently-depended-on artifacts surface higher"). Impact analysis is implemented (pkg/registry/core/dependents.go:22-47 `DependentsOf`, surfaced via `podium impact` at cmd/podium/impact.go). The other two are absent. Search ranking fuses only BM25 and vector cosine ranks via RRF (pkg/registry/core/core.go:500-558, pkg/registry/core/rrf.go) with no dependency-count term; a search for dependency-frequency ranking signals finds nothing. Cascading review is absent entirely: a repository search for `cascad`, `re-review`, and "flag downstream" finds no implementation. Suggested direction: feed the reverse-dependency in-degree into the RRF fusion as a ranking signal, and add a cascading-review trigger that flags downstream artifacts when a high-sensitivity dependency is re-ingested (or document these as deferred if not yet in scope for this milestone).

**Deferred:** The cascading-review half has no spec-defined mechanism. §4.7.3 names the behaviour ("flag downstream artifacts for re-review") but defines no event, audit type, or persistent artifact state for the flag, and the two relevant taxonomies are closed enumerations that exclude it: §7.3.2 outbound webhooks (`artifact.published`, `artifact.deprecated`, `domain.published`, `layer.ingested`, `layer.history_rewritten`) and the §8.1 audit table (no review/cascade event). Implementing it would require inventing a wire surface the spec does not define, which conflicts with the spec being the source of truth. The search-ranking-signal half is implementable (reverse-dependency in-degree fused into RRF) but needs a new store SPI to enumerate edges/in-degrees and a rework of the fusion path; it cannot close this finding on its own because §4.7.3 requires both behaviours. The finding's own suggested direction sanctions deferral. No code was changed, so the tree stays green; tracked for a dedicated change once the cascading-review mechanism is specified.

### - [x] F-4.7.8 — `podium admin reembed --since <timestamp>` flag is missing [Low] — CLOSED

(gap) The §4.7 "Model versioning and re-embedding" paragraph names the re-embed trigger as "`podium admin reembed` (`--all` or `--since <timestamp>`)." The CLI supports `--artifact`/`--version` (single artifact) and `--only-missing`, and the no-flag default re-embeds everything (covering `--all` semantically), but there is no `--since <timestamp>` flag for incremental re-embedding of artifacts ingested after a cutoff (cmd/podium/admin.go:160-194; the server endpoint at /v1/admin/reembed reads only `artifact`, `version`, and `only_missing`). Suggested direction: add a `--since` flag plumbed to a store-side filter on `IngestedAt` so operators can re-embed only recently-ingested artifacts after a model change, matching the spec's named surface.

**Resolution (3ba32dd):** Added `ReembedOptions{OnlyIfMissing, Since}`; `Reembed` drops manifests with `IngestedAt` before `Since` (inclusive boundary). `podium admin reembed --since <RFC3339>` validates the timestamp locally then sends it as the `since` query param; the `/v1/admin/reembed` handler parses RFC3339 and rejects a malformed value with `registry.invalid_argument`.

### - [x] F-4.7.9 — `podium sign` / `podium verify` take `--content-hash`/`--signature` flags instead of an artifact argument [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §4.7.9 documents the verification CLI as "`podium verify <artifact>` for ad-hoc verification. `podium sign <artifact>` for explicit signing outside the ingest flow." Both forms take a positional `<artifact>` (an artifact ID or path). The implementation instead requires `--content-hash sha256:...` for `sign` and `--content-hash` plus `--signature` for `verify` (cmd/podium/sign.go:16-72), operating on a raw content hash rather than resolving an artifact and computing its canonical hash. A user following the spec would run `podium verify finance/ap/pay-invoice` and get a usage error. Suggested direction: accept a positional `<artifact>` that resolves the artifact, derives its canonical content hash (and reads the stored signature for `verify`), and keep the `--content-hash` form as an explicit lower-level option.

**Resolution (3ba32dd):** `podium sign <artifact>` and `podium verify <artifact>` now resolve the artifact via `/v1/load_artifact`, deriving its canonical content hash (and, for `verify`, the stored signature envelope). The lower-level `--content-hash` (sign) and `--content-hash`+`--signature` (verify) forms are retained and are mutually exclusive with the positional. An unsigned artifact reports the missing envelope rather than passing. The registry URL comes from `--registry`/`PODIUM_REGISTRY`, matching the documented `podium verify finance/ap/pay-invoice` form.

### - [x] F-4.7.10 — reembed `--only-missing` presence probe yields false negatives for catalogs over 100 artifacts [Low] — CLOSED

(bug) `Reembed(ctx, onlyIfMissing=true)` decides whether an artifact already has a stored vector by querying the backend with an arbitrary probe vector `[1, 0, 0, ...]` at `topK=100` and checking whether the artifact appears among the 100 nearest neighbours (pkg/registry/core/reembed.go:52-64). For a tenant with more than 100 artifacts, an existing vector that is not among the 100 closest to that arbitrary probe is reported as missing, so the artifact is re-embedded even though a vector already exists. The effect is wasted embedding calls and vector writes rather than incorrect data (re-embedding is an idempotent per-row upsert per pkg/vector/vector.go:61-65), so the impact is performance and cost, not correctness of results. The probe comment ("We cheat a bit") acknowledges the shortcut. Suggested direction: add a vector SPI method to test for the presence of a specific `(tenant, id, version)` row (or have `Query` return all matches scoped to an artifact), and use that instead of a top-K nearest-neighbour probe.

**Resolution (3ba32dd):** The presence check now issues one exhaustive query with `topK = len(manifests)` and builds a `(id@version)` present-set. The store keys at most one vector per manifest record, so retrieving `len(manifests)` nearest returns every stored vector for the tenant regardless of catalogue size, eliminating the false negatives past 100. This also collapses the per-artifact probe into a single query. A vector-SPI presence method was considered but rejected as disproportionate for a Low finding (it would touch all six backends, three of which are live-test-only).

### - [x] F-4.7.11 — Per-call audit records omit resolved layer composition and result size [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §4.7.5 states every `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact` call "is logged with caller identity, visibility outcome, requested artifact (or query), timestamp, resolved layer composition, and result size." The emitted `AuditEvent` carries only `Type`, `Caller`, `Target`, and `Context` (pkg/registry/core/core.go:90-95), and the call sites populate caller, target, and a small context map (query/scope/type/version) but no resolved layer composition and no result size (pkg/registry/core/core.go:240-243, 503-506, 647-650, 746-751). A search of pkg/audit and internal/serverboot for `ResultSize`, `LayerComposition`, and `resolved_layers` finds no enrichment downstream. Visibility outcome is partially captured via the separate `visibility.denied` event (pkg/registry/core/core.go:767-773), and the timestamp is presumably added by the sink. §4.7.5 defers the full contract to §8 ("Detail in §8"), so this overlaps another subsection; recorded here because the resolved-layer-composition and result-size fields are named concretely in §4.7.5 and are absent from the registry-emitted events. Suggested direction: extend `AuditEvent` (or the emitter) to record the resolved layer IDs composing the caller's effective view and the result count for each read call.

**Resolution (3ba32dd):** `core.AuditEvent` and `audit.Event` gained `ResolvedLayers []string` (the caller's effective view in §4.6 precedence order) and `ResultSize int`. The four read methods now emit via a deferred event so the size is captured on the success path while the event still fires on early/error returns: search counts returned results, load_domain counts rendered subdomains plus notable entries, load_artifact records 1 for a resolved artifact. The serverboot audit emitter maps both fields into the FileSink, and they persist to the JSON-Lines log and participate in the tamper-evident hash chain.

### - [x] F-4.7.12 — Stale `podium vuln explain` reference in the dependency package [Info] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §4.7.7 places vulnerability tracking out of scope: the registry "emits no `vulnerability.detected` events" and performs no scanning. No `podium vuln` command exists in the code, which is correct. However, the doc comment on `ImpactSet` in pkg/dependency/graph.go:60-61 states the function is "Used by `podium vuln explain` and the admin impact-analysis CLI (§4.7.5)." The referenced `podium vuln explain` command does not exist and would contradict §4.7.7 if it did. This is a documentation-only artifact with no behavioural effect. Suggested direction: drop the `podium vuln explain` reference from the comment and cite only the impact-analysis surface (`podium impact`).

**Resolution (3ba32dd):** The `ImpactSet` comment now cites the §4.7.3 impact-analysis surface (`podium impact`) and notes that vulnerability tracking is out of scope per §4.7.7, removing the nonexistent `podium vuln explain` reference. Comment-only change with no behavioural effect, so no test accompanies it.
## F-5.0 — 5.0 Why Tools, Not Resources

_Reviewed spec/05-meta-tools.md against the implementation._

This subsection states the rationale for exposing the meta-tools as MCP tools and makes one concrete additional contract: artifact bodies are also exposed as MCP resources as a read-only mirror of `load_artifact`, while the meta-tools remain the canonical interface. The meta-tools themselves are registered correctly as MCP tools in the bridge (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:257` `tools/list` and `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:266` `tools/call`, dispatching `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact`). The MCP resources mirror described in the subsection is absent from the entire repository. A secondary inconsistency exists between this subsection and the section preamble over whether the `resources` capability is declared at all.

### - [ ] F-5.0.1 — MCP resources mirror of load_artifact is not implemented [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Spec §5.0 (spec/05-meta-tools.md:22) states: "Artifact bodies are also exposed as MCP resources for hosts that prefer that pattern (read-only mirror of `load_artifact`); the canonical interface remains the meta-tools." This describes a second consumer interface in which a host can read an artifact body through MCP's resource protocol (`resources/list` and `resources/read`) as a read-only mirror.

The MCP bridge implements only the tools and prompts protocols. The JSON-RPC dispatcher in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:231-277` handles `initialize`, `tools/list`, `tools/call`, `prompts/list`, and `prompts/get`; every other method, including `resources/list` and `resources/read`, falls through to the default branch at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:273-274` and returns `-32601 method not found`. The `initialize` capability advertisement at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:248-256` declares `tools`, `prompts`, and `sessionCorrelation`, but not `resources`, so a host would never attempt the resource protocol. A repository-wide search for `resources/list`, `resources/read`, `ReadResource`, `ListResources`, and a `resources` capability returns no handler in the MCP bridge, the registry server (`cmd/podium-server`, `pkg/registry/server`), the internal packages, or the SDKs (`sdks/podium-py`, `sdks/podium-ts`); the only "resources" occurrences refer to bundled artifact resources (blobs materialized to disk via `fetchLargeResources` in `cmd/podium-mcp/large_resources.go` and the content cache in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:799-823`), which are a different concept. The tools-list test (`cmd/podium-mcp/main_helpers_test.go:249-270`) covers the four meta-tools and no resource entry, and there is no test exercising any `resources/*` method.

Suggested direction: implement the read-only resource mirror in the bridge by advertising a `resources` capability in the `initialize` response and adding `resources/list` plus `resources/read` handlers that return artifact bodies sourced from the same `/v1/load_artifact` path (without the materialization side effects, since the mirror is read-only). If the mirror is deliberately deferred, reconcile §5.0 with the implementation by marking the resources mirror as planned rather than present.

### - [ ] F-5.0.2 — Section preamble and §5.0 disagree on whether the resources capability is declared [Info] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The §5 preamble at spec/05-meta-tools.md:14 fixes the `initialize` capability set to `{tools: true, prompts: <conditional on prompt artifacts>, sessionCorrelation: true}`, which omits any `resources` capability. Section §5.0 at spec/05-meta-tools.md:22 states that artifact bodies are exposed as MCP resources, which an MCP host can only discover when the server advertises a `resources` capability in `initialize`. These two statements are in tension: a resources mirror that is never advertised in the capability set is undiscoverable through the standard MCP handshake.

The implementation follows the preamble: `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:248-256` advertises exactly `tools`, `prompts`, and `sessionCorrelation`, with no `resources` entry. So the code matches spec line 14 and contradicts spec line 22.

Suggested direction: decide whether the resources mirror is part of the contract. If it is, add `resources` to the capability list in spec/05-meta-tools.md:14 and advertise it in `initialize`. If it is not, remove or qualify the claim at spec/05-meta-tools.md:22 so the two passages agree.
## F-5.1 — 5.1 Meta-Tool Descriptions and Prompting Guidance

_Reviewed spec/05-meta-tools.md against the implementation._

This subsection defines the canonical tool descriptions that the MCP server exposes to the LLM and an example system-prompt fragment. The only implementing surface is the MCP bridge's `tools/list` handler in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`. The four meta-tool names match the spec, and the routing in `callTool` covers all four. The descriptions returned to clients are truncated to the first sentence of each canonical string, the `tools/list` entries declare no `inputSchema`, and the example system-prompt fragment is not surfaced by any code path. Tests assert only that the four tool names are present and do not pin descriptions or parameter schemas.

### - [ ] F-5.1.1 — `tools/list` descriptions are truncated to the first sentence [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §5.1 states the strings under each tool heading "are the canonical tool descriptions exposed to the LLM via MCP" and that hosts "SHOULD use them verbatim unless customizing for a specific runtime." The canonical strings are multi-sentence and carry the prompting guidance the LLM needs (for example `load_domain`: "Browse the artifact catalog hierarchically. Call with no path to see top-level domains. Call with a path ... Optional `depth` arg ... To use an artifact you find here, call `load_artifact`."). The MCP bridge instead returns only the first sentence of each: `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:260-263` sets `load_domain` to "Browse the artifact catalog hierarchically.", `search_domains` to "Search the catalog for relevant domains.", `search_artifacts` to "Search or browse the artifact catalog.", and `load_artifact` to "Load a specific artifact by ID." The remaining guidance (when to use each tool, the `depth`/`note`/`materialized_at`/`total_matched` behavior, and the cross-references between tools) is dropped, so the LLM never receives the navigation guidance the spec intends. Suggested direction: store the full canonical strings from §5.1 as constants and emit them verbatim as the `description` for each tool in the `tools/list` result.

### - [ ] F-5.1.2 — `tools/list` entries omit `inputSchema` for every meta-tool [High] — OPEN

(bug) The MCP `tools/list` handler at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:257-265` returns tool objects with only `name` and `description`. It declares no `inputSchema`. The MCP protocol version negotiated by this server is `2024-11-05` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:47`), and under that protocol each tool in `tools/list` carries an `inputSchema` JSON Schema object describing its parameters. Without it, a compliant client and the LLM have no machine-readable parameter information for any meta-tool, even though the parameters are concrete and documented in §5.1 and §5 (for example `load_domain` accepts `depth` and `session_id`; `search_domains` accepts `scope`, `top_k`, and `session_id`; `search_artifacts` accepts `query`, `type`, `tags`, `scope`, `top_k`, and `session_id`; `load_artifact` accepts `id`, `version`, `session_id`, and `harness`). The call-time code already reads these arguments (for example `cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:31-35` reads `query`, `type`, `scope`, `tags`, and `top_k`), so the parameters exist but are never advertised. The result is that the tools are effectively undiscoverable in their parameters: the model must guess argument names, and strict MCP clients may reject tool entries that lack `inputSchema`. Suggested direction: add an `inputSchema` for each meta-tool that declares the documented parameters and required fields, matching the arguments parsed in `callTool` and the per-tool handlers.

### - [ ] F-5.1.3 — Example system-prompt fragment is not provided by any code surface [Low] — OPEN

(gap) §5.1 includes an "Example system-prompt fragment" giving the canonical orientation text for hosts ("You have access to a catalog of authored skills and agents through the Podium meta-tools: ... Sessions start empty. Use search_domains when you don't know the right neighborhood; ..."). A repository-wide search finds this fragment only in `spec/05-meta-tools.md`; it is absent from `cmd/podium-mcp`, the CLI under `cmd/podium`, the SDKs under `sdks/`, and `docs/`. The spec presents it as an example rather than a mandated output, so the severity is low, but no command or constant lets a host obtain the canonical fragment programmatically. Suggested direction: if hosts are expected to consume this fragment, expose it as a constant or via a small CLI helper (for example a `podium`-level command or an MCP server-info field); otherwise confirm the fragment is illustrative only and requires no code surface.
## F-5.2 — 5.2 Prompt Projection

_Reviewed spec/05-meta-tools.md against the implementation._

The subsection describes two behaviors. A `type: command` artifact loaded with `expose_as_mcp_prompt: true` in frontmatter is also exposed through MCP's `prompts/get` for harnesses with slash-menu support, with the wire field keeping the MCP name `expose_as_mcp_prompt`. The `mcpServers:` declarations in a loaded artifact's manifest are stored by Podium and exposed through `load_artifact` for the host's runtime to wire up. The implementation lives in `cmd/podium-mcp/prompts.go` (handlers for `prompts/list` and `prompts/get`), with the manifest fields in `pkg/manifest/types.go`. The wire field names, the opt-in default, the `type: command` runtime guard, and the `mcpServers` exposure through `load_artifact` all match the spec. Two deviations affect completeness at scale and capability advertisement, and one observation concerns argument handling.

### - [ ] F-5.2.1 — prompts/list silently truncates opt-ins beyond 50 command artifacts [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 5.2 states that a `type: command` artifact with `expose_as_mcp_prompt: true` "is also exposed via MCP's `prompts/get`," and the implementing code's own comment frames the promise as "every `type: command` artifact in the caller's view that opted in ... becomes one entry" (`cmd/podium-mcp/prompts.go:12-14`). `collectPromptDescriptors` enumerates command artifacts by calling `/v1/search_artifacts` with `{"type": "command", "top_k": 50}` and no `query` (`cmd/podium-mcp/prompts.go:97-100`). The registry rejects `top_k > 50` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:508-509`) and offers no offset or pagination parameter, so at most 50 command artifacts are returned. With an empty query, BM25 returns matched records ordered alphabetically by ID (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:542-543`), so a deployment with more than 50 command artifacts receives only the first 50 by ID. Opted-in commands whose IDs sort after the 50th are dropped from `prompts/list` and never appear in a slash menu. The decoder also ignores the `total_matched` field the registry returns (`cmd/podium-mcp/prompts.go:104-112`), so the truncation is silent. `prompts/get` still resolves a dropped command by name because it loads the artifact directly (`cmd/podium-mcp/prompts.go:51`), but a user cannot discover it through enumeration. Suggested direction: paginate the command enumeration (request successive pages until the count reported by `total_matched` is exhausted) or add a registry-side filter that returns only command artifacts with `expose_as_mcp_prompt: true` without the `top_k` ceiling, so the projected prompt list is complete regardless of catalog size.

### - [ ] F-5.2.2 — initialize advertises the prompts capability unconditionally [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The MCP server declares its capabilities in the `initialize` response as `{tools: true, prompts: <conditional on prompt artifacts with expose_as_mcp_prompt: true>, sessionCorrelation: true}` (spec line 14, the contract for the prompt projection mechanism described in 5.2). The implementation hardcodes `"prompts": map[string]any{}` in the `initialize` handler (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:252`), which advertises the capability as present regardless of whether any opted-in command artifact exists. The helper written to express the conditional, `promptsCapabilityActive`, always returns `true` and is never called by the `initialize` handler; it is referenced only from a test (`cmd/podium-mcp/prompts.go:136-142`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main_helpers_test.go:140-141`). The helper's own comment concedes it matches the spec wording "loosely." The practical effect is small because clients can call `prompts/list` and receive an empty list, but the advertised capability does not reflect the presence of prompt artifacts as the spec specifies. Suggested direction: either compute the capability from the presence of at least one opted-in command artifact (calling the existing helper after the helper is made to perform a real check) or amend the spec to state that the capability is advertised whenever the MCP server is configured.

### - [ ] F-5.2.3 — prompts/get accepts MCP arguments but performs no substitution [Info] — OPEN

(gap) Section 5.2 surfaces command artifacts through MCP's `prompts/get` for "harnesses with slash-menu support," and section 4.3 describes `type: command` artifacts as "parameterized prompt templates a human invokes (typically as a slash command)" (`spec/04-artifact-model.md:20`). The `prompts/get` handler decodes an `arguments` map from the request (`cmd/podium-mcp/prompts.go:42-44`) but never reads it; it returns the raw manifest body verbatim as the user-message text (`cmd/podium-mcp/prompts.go:78-89`). MCP `prompts/get` semantics expect the server to interpolate declared arguments into the returned messages, and `prompts/list` entries normally declare an `arguments` schema, which the descriptor here omits (`cmd/podium-mcp/prompts.go:19-22`). Section 5.2 defines `expose_as_mcp_prompt` only as a boolean and does not mandate an argument schema or substitution, so this is not a contract violation. Recorded as an observation: a parameterized command projected through `prompts/get` cannot receive parameters from the slash menu, which limits the usefulness of the projection for templates that expect arguments. Suggested direction: confirm whether argument projection is intended; if so, define an argument convention for command artifacts and have `prompts/list` declare the arguments and `prompts/get` interpolate the supplied values.
## F-6.1 — 6.1 The Bridge

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md against the implementation._

Section 6.1 describes the MCP server as a thin in-process bridge that exposes the meta-tools over MCP and forwards calls to the registry, holds no per-session server-side state, limits local state to a content-addressed disk cache, OS-keychain credentials in `oauth-device-code` mode, an in-memory local-overlay index, and the materialized working set, shares no state across processes, ships as a single Go binary configured via env vars, command-line flags, or a config file, and requires a server-source registry because it speaks HTTP and does not work against a filesystem-source registry. The implementation in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go` matches the stateless and single-binary claims: the `mcpServer` struct carries only configuration, an HTTP client, the disk caches, the adapter registry, and an overlay slice loaded once at startup, with no per-session mutable state. The server forwards `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact` to `/v1/...` registry endpoints. The verified gaps concern the server-source requirement, the absence of the keychain-backed identity path in the bridge, and the configuration surface. The second and third findings overlap with §6.2 and §6.3 and are scoped narrowly here to the claims §6.1 itself makes.

### - [ ] F-6.1.1 — MCP server does not reject a filesystem-source registry [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 6.1 states "**Requires a server-source registry.** The MCP server speaks HTTP and does not work against a filesystem-source registry (§13.11)." Section 7.5.2 defines the dispatch rule: a `defaults.registry` (or `PODIUM_REGISTRY`) value with an `http://` or `https://` prefix routes to a server, and any other value is a filesystem path; "`podium sync` is the only consumer that works against a filesystem registry. The MCP server and the SDKs require a server source" (spec/07-consumer-paths.md:261-262). The implementation never validates the registry source. `loadConfig` only checks that `PODIUM_REGISTRY` is non-empty (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:119-121`) and `fetchJSON` concatenates the value with the request path and issues an HTTP request via `url.Parse(s.cfg.registry + path)` followed by `http.NewRequest("GET", ...)` and `s.http.Do(req)` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:687-715`). A whole-repo sweep found no scheme check on the registry value in the bridge code path; `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go` is the only non-test file in the binary that reads and uses `PODIUM_REGISTRY`. As a result, a filesystem path such as `/srv/registry` or a `file://` URL passes startup, and the bridge fails only on the first tool call with an opaque Go HTTP-client error (for example `unsupported protocol scheme ""` or `unsupported protocol scheme "file"`) rather than refusing to start with a clear message. This contradicts the §6.1 requirement and breaks the §6.9 precedent that comparable misconfigurations (unknown `PODIUM_HARNESS`, version mismatch) refuse to start with a helpful CLI message. Suggested direction: in `loadConfig`, after the non-empty check, reject any `PODIUM_REGISTRY` value that does not begin with `http://` or `https://` with a structured startup error in the §6.10 namespace (for example `config.filesystem_registry_unsupported`) that names the offending value and states that the MCP server requires a server-source registry.

### - [ ] F-6.1.2 — Bridge never realizes the keychain-credential local-state form [Info] — OPEN

(gap) Section 6.1 enumerates "OS-keychain-stored credentials (in `oauth-device-code` mode)" as one of the permitted forms of the bridge's local state, and §6.2 lists `oauth-device-code` as the default `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER`. The shared library implements this provider with keychain storage (`pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go`, `pkg/identity/keychain.go`), but the bridge does not wire it. `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go` does not import `pkg/identity`, `loadConfig` does not read `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER`, and the only credential path implemented is the injected session token read from `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN` or `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` in `currentToken` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:753-772`). Consequently the keychain-credential local-state category that §6.1 lists is never populated by the bridge. The substantive contract for the default identity provider and for surfacing the device-code verification URL via MCP elicitation belongs to §6.2 and §6.3, and the detailed gap is best tracked there; this finding records only that the §6.1 enumeration overstates what the bridge currently exhibits. Suggested direction: confirm with the §6.2 and §6.3 reviews whether the bridge is expected to wire the existing `oauth-device-code` provider, and reconcile §6.1's local-state enumeration with the implemented authentication path.

### - [ ] F-6.1.3 — Bridge binary accepts only env vars, not flags or a config file [Low] — OPEN

(gap) Section 6.1 states "A single Go binary serves every deployment context. The host configures it via env vars, command-line flags, or a config file." The `podium-mcp` binary reads configuration exclusively from environment variables: `loadConfig` calls `os.Getenv`/`envDefault` for every parameter (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:93-135`), and there is no flag parsing or config-file loading in the binary (no `flag` package usage, no `os.Args` inspection, no YAML/TOML/JSON config reader in `cmd/podium-mcp/`). The package doc comment acknowledges this by noting that flags are "also supported by the launcher" (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:10`), implying a wrapper rather than the binary itself. The detailed configuration contract, including the statement that "`--flag` and config-file equivalents are accepted," lives in the §6.2 table header (spec/06-mcp-server.md:13), so the depth of this gap belongs to the §6.2 review; this finding records only that the §6.1 claim is not satisfied by the binary alone. Suggested direction: either add flag and config-file parsing to the binary, or reconcile §6.1 and §6.2 prose so the configuration surface the binary implements matches what the spec promises.
## F-6.2 — 6.2 Configuration

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md against the implementation._

The subsection defines the MCP server configuration parameters, their env-var names, descriptions, and defaults, and states that flag and config-file equivalents are accepted. The primary implementation is `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go` (`config` struct and `loadConfig`). The defaults that are wired match the spec for `PODIUM_HARNESS` (`none`), `PODIUM_CACHE_DIR` (`~/.podium/cache/`), `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE` (`always-revalidate`), `PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES` (`medium-and-above`), and the registry-side `PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS` (3600). Several parameters are not honored by the MCP server: `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` is never read, `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` is read but unused, the `sync.yaml` fallback for `PODIUM_REGISTRY` is absent, and the per-call destination alternative for `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT` is not implemented. One parsing defect causes the signature-verification control to fail open on an unrecognized `PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES` value.

### - [ ] F-6.2.1 — PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES is not validated and fails open on an unknown value [High] — OPEN

(bug) §6.2 lists `PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES` with default `medium-and-above` and the value set `never` / `medium-and-above` / `always` (per §6.5/§4.7.9 the recognized values). `loadConfig` reads it as `verifyPolicy: sign.VerificationPolicy(envDefault("PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES", string(sign.PolicyMediumAndAbove)))` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:112` without validating the result against the known policy constants. `loadConfig` validates `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE` and rejects unknown values (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:128-133`) but applies no equivalent check to the verification policy. Downstream, `needsVerification` in `pkg/sign/sign.go:87-98` switches on the policy and returns `false` in its `default` branch, so any unrecognized policy string disables signature enforcement entirely. The effect is that a typo such as `PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES=medium-and-aboe` or `mediumandabove` silently turns off signature verification on materialization rather than failing to start. This is a fail-open defect on a security control. Suggested direction: validate the parsed policy in `loadConfig` against `sign.PolicyNever`, `sign.PolicyMediumAndAbove`, and `sign.PolicyAlways`, returning a startup error for any other value, mirroring the `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE` switch; optionally make `needsVerification` fail closed (return `true`) for unknown policies as defense in depth.

### - [ ] F-6.2.2 — MCP server does not fall back to sync.yaml defaults.registry for PODIUM_REGISTRY [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §6.2 documents the `PODIUM_REGISTRY` default as "(read from `sync.yaml`'s `defaults.registry` per §7.5.2 if unset; required if neither is set)". The MCP server reads only the env var and errors immediately when it is empty: `registry: os.Getenv("PODIUM_REGISTRY")` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:99` and `if c.registry == "" { return nil, fmt.Errorf("PODIUM_REGISTRY is required") }` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:119-121`. The MCP server does not import `pkg/sync` and never calls `sync.ReadConfig` / `sync.ResolveRegistryPath`. The CLI implements this fallback (`cmd/podium/main.go:204-209`), and the resolution helper exists (`pkg/sync/config.go:64-82`, `pkg/sync/config.go:96-112`), so the capability is present in the module but not wired into the MCP binary. This also breaks the §6.11 "Standalone (no env override)" recipe, which states the MCP server resolves the registry from an auto-bootstrapped `~/.podium/sync.yaml` and the env var can be omitted. Suggested direction: when `PODIUM_REGISTRY` is unset, read `defaults.registry` from the applicable `sync.yaml` (workspace and home-global per §7.5.2) and resolve it with `sync.ResolveRegistryPath` before erroring; keep the "required if neither is set" error as the final fallback.

### - [ ] F-6.2.3 — PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER is never read; default oauth-device-code not honored [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §6.2 lists `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` with default `oauth-device-code`. The MCP server's `config` struct and `loadConfig` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:68-135`) contain no `identityProvider` field and never read `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER`; a repository search finds the env var only in `internal/serverboot` (the registry server) and never in `cmd/podium-mcp`. The MCP server unconditionally uses the injected-session-token path: `currentToken()` reads `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` / `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN` and attaches the result as a bearer token (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:706-707`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:749-773`). It never selects a provider and never reads OS-keychain-cached tokens, even though the `oauth-device-code` provider and keychain support exist in `pkg/identity` (`pkg/identity/identity.go:86-87`, `pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go`, `pkg/identity/keychain.go`). The documented default identity provider is therefore not implemented in the MCP server, and the `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` parameter is silently ignored. Suggested direction: read `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` (default `oauth-device-code`), dispatch to the corresponding `pkg/identity` provider for attaching identity to registry calls, and reject unrecognized provider values at startup.

### - [ ] F-6.2.4 — PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK is read but never used; no local audit, no default sentinel [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §6.2 specifies `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` as the local audit destination, with default "(unset → registry audit only)" and the behavior "When set without a value (or set to `default`), uses `~/.podium/audit.log`". The MCP server reads the var into `cfg.auditSink` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:108`) but never consumes it: a search across `cmd/podium-mcp` finds no reference to `auditSink` beyond the struct field and its assignment, no handling of the `default` sentinel, and no local audit emission. The supporting infrastructure exists and already implements the spec default path: `audit.NewFileSink("")` defaults to `~/.podium/audit.log` (`pkg/audit/file.go:26-37`), and the CLI admin commands use it (`cmd/podium/admin.go:213`). The MCP server does not wire `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` to a `FileSink` or any sink, so local auditing on the MCP side is absent. Suggested direction: when `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` is set (treating an empty value or `default` as `~/.podium/audit.log`), construct an audit sink via `pkg/audit` and emit local audit events for MCP operations; leave registry-only auditing when the var is unset.

### - [ ] F-6.2.5 — PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT has no per-call destination equivalent [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §6.2 documents the `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT` default as "(host specifies per call)", and §6.6 line 126 states the destination "comes from the host, either via `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT` or per-call in the `load_artifact` arguments". The MCP server materializes only when the env var is set: `if s.cfg.materializeRoot != ""` guards all write sites (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:414`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:486`), and `materialize.Write(s.cfg.materializeRoot, out)` is always called with the env-var value (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:435`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:505`). The per-call delivery options carry only the harness override (`deliverOpts` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:374-376`), and the `load_artifact` tool entry advertises no input schema with a destination property (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:263`). No `path`, `destination`, or `root` argument is read from the `load_artifact` arguments. When `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT` is unset and the host passes a destination per call, the materialize block is skipped and `materialized_at` is empty, so nothing is written to disk. The harness is overridable per call but the destination root is not, which contradicts the documented contract. Suggested direction: read a per-call destination argument from the `load_artifact` arguments, prefer it over `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT` when present, and materialize whenever either source supplies a path.

### - [ ] F-6.2.6 — Flag and config-file configuration forms are not accepted by the binary [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §6.2 line 13 states "env-var form shown; `--flag` and config-file equivalents are accepted". The MCP server reads configuration exclusively from environment variables: `loadConfig` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:93-135`) calls only `os.Getenv` / `envDefault`, and a search of `cmd/podium-mcp` finds no flag parsing (`flag.FlagSet`, `flag.String`) and no config-file reader. No CLI launcher in `cmd/podium` spawns `podium-mcp` with flag-to-env translation. The §6.11 host recipes configure the server only through the `env` block, so the env-var path is the working integration; the binary does not accept the `--flag` or config-file forms the spec text claims. Suggested direction: either add flag and config-file parsing to the MCP binary, or soften the §6.2 text to state that hosts supply configuration as environment variables (the §6.11 recipes already reflect this).

### - [ ] F-6.2.7 — PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS is listed as MCP config but consumed only by the registry [Info] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §6.2 presents its parameter table as MCP server configuration (§6 is the MCP server) and lists `PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS` with default 3600. The MCP server does not read this var; it is consumed only by the registry server bootstrap (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:595-602`, with the default at `pkg/objectstore/objectstore.go:42-44`). This placement is consistent with the architecture, because presigned URLs are generated registry-side and the MCP server only consumes URLs it receives, so the MCP binary has nothing to apply the TTL to. The default value matches the spec, and the var is honored system-wide. No defect; flag only as a documentation placement observation so a reader does not expect the MCP binary to read `PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS`. Suggested direction: note in §6.2 (or §6.5/§6.6) that `PODIUM_PRESIGN_TTL_SECONDS` is a registry-side parameter.

### - [ ] F-6.2.8 — PODIUM_CACHE_DIR silently disables the cache when the home directory is unresolvable [Low] — OPEN

(bug) §6.2 specifies the `PODIUM_CACHE_DIR` default as `~/.podium/cache/`. When the var is unset, `loadConfig` resolves the home directory and falls back to it only on success: `if c.cacheDir == "" { home, err := os.UserHomeDir(); if err == nil { c.cacheDir = filepath.Join(home, ".podium", "cache") } }` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:122-127`). When `os.UserHomeDir()` returns an error, `cacheDir` stays empty, the error is swallowed, and `newContentCache("")` returns a disabled cache (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:786-790`). The documented default cache directory is therefore not applied in environments where the home directory cannot be determined, and the cache is silently disabled instead. The blast radius is limited to unusual environments, and the degradation is graceful, but it diverges from the documented default without any warning. Suggested direction: surface a warning when the cache is disabled because the home directory could not be resolved, or fail startup so the operator can set `PODIUM_CACHE_DIR` explicitly (the spec notes ephemeral-home contexts should point it at a volume).
## F-6.3 — 6.3 Identity Providers (6.3.1 Claim Derivation, 6.3.2 injected-session-token Runtime Trust, 6.3.2.1 Token Rotation Contract)

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md against the implementation._

I checked the two built-in identity providers (`oauth-device-code`, `injected-session-token`), claim derivation (SCIM push, the `IdpGroupMapping` adapter, OAuth scope narrowing), the runtime trust model (registry-side JWT verification and `auth.untrusted_runtime`), and the token rotation contract. The client-side and unit-level building blocks are present and well-tested: `pkg/identity/runtime.go` implements a correct `JWTVerifier` (enforces `iss`, `aud`, `sub`, `act`, `exp`, registered key, and algorithm), the device-code flow in `pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go` follows RFC 8628, SCIM 2.0 push exists in `pkg/scim`, and the MCP server reads the injected token fresh on every call. The principal gaps are at the wiring layer. The registry never verifies the injected JWT on a real request and falls back to an anonymous-public identity that bypasses visibility filtering. The MCP server does not implement the default `oauth-device-code` provider. The `IdpGroupMapping` adapter and the fine-grained OAuth scope narrowing described in §6.3.1 are absent.

### - [x] F-6.3.1 — Registry never verifies the injected session token on a real request [High] — CLOSED

(gap) Spec §6.3.2 requires that for `injected-session-token` "The registry verifies the signature on every call" against the runtime-specific signing key registered at onboarding. The verifier exists in `pkg/identity/runtime.go:94` (`RuntimeKeyRegistry.JWTVerifier`) and is exercised by unit tests, but it is never called from any production request path. A repo-wide search for non-test callers of `JWTVerifier` and `InjectedSessionToken{...}` returns none. The server-boot wiring at `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:288-289` explicitly logs, for both `oauth-device-code` and `injected-session-token`, "server-side verifier wiring not yet implemented; falling back to anonymous-public resolver." With no resolver installed, `pkg/registry/server/server.go:176-181` defaults `resolveID` to `func(*http.Request) layer.Identity { return layer.Identity{IsPublic: true} }`. Per `pkg/layer/composer.go:48-60` and `pkg/registry/core/core.go:989,1056`, `IsPublic` short-circuits the visibility evaluator so every layer is visible. The result: when an operator selects `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER=injected-session-token`, the registry does not verify the bearer token and treats the caller as anonymous-public with full visibility, defeating the trust model the section specifies. Suggested direction: wire an identity resolver in serverboot for `injected-session-token` that extracts the bearer token from the `Authorization` header, calls `RuntimeKeyRegistry.JWTVerifier(audience, nil)` with the registered keys (the same `runtimeKeys` store created at `serverboot.go:321`), and maps the verified claims into `layer.Identity`; reject with `auth.untrusted_runtime` when verification fails.

**Resolution (commit 92675d4):** Added `server.WithIdentityVerifier` plus a `withIdentityVerification` middleware (`pkg/registry/server/identity_verify.go`) that verifies the bearer token on every meta-tool route (health/SCIM/objects exempt) and carries the verified `layer.Identity` to handlers via context. `serverboot.injectedTokenVerifier` wires it from the same `runtimeKeys` store the admin endpoint writes, mapping verified claims (groups, scopes) to the identity; only `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER=injected-session-token` installs it, so standalone/public/oauth-device-code stay anonymous.

### - [x] F-6.3.2 — `auth.untrusted_runtime` rejection is never produced by the registry at request time [High] — CLOSED

(gap) Spec §6.3.2 states "Without a registered signing key, the registry rejects with `auth.untrusted_runtime`," and §6.9 lists the same behavior for the "Untrusted runtime (`injected-session-token`)" failure mode. The error sentinel and code exist (`pkg/identity/identity.go:18` maps `ErrUntrustedRuntime` to `auth.untrusted_runtime`), the admin registration endpoint and CLI exist (`pkg/registry/server/runtime_endpoint.go`, `cmd/podium/admin_runtime.go`), and `runtime_endpoint.go:18-19` comments that "The registry passed in here is the same one the JWT verifier consults at request time." No verifier consults it at request time, so an unregistered or unsigned token is never rejected with `auth.untrusted_runtime` on a real call; it is silently accepted as anonymous-public (see F-6.3.1). The runtime-key registration half of the contract is implemented while the enforcement half is not, which means registering or omitting a signing key has no observable effect on request authorization. Suggested direction: as part of the resolver wiring in F-6.3.1, surface `ErrUntrustedRuntime` from verification as the structured `auth.untrusted_runtime` envelope (with `details.runtime_iss`) per §6.10, and add a server-level test that an unregistered issuer is rejected.

**Resolution (commit 92675d4):** `JWTVerifier` now returns a typed `*identity.UntrustedRuntimeError` carrying the issuer; `writeIdentityError` maps it to a 401 `auth.untrusted_runtime` envelope with `details.runtime_iss` (and `auth.token_expired` for expiry). Verified server, integration, and e2e tests (`TestDocHTTPAPI_51`, `TestExtending_11`) that an unregistered issuer and a missing token are both rejected.

### - [x] F-6.3.3 — MCP server does not implement the default `oauth-device-code` provider or MCP elicitation [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) Spec §6.2 sets `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` default to `oauth-device-code`, and §6.3 states that for that provider the "MCP server uses MCP elicitation; the host displays the URL and code in the agent UI." The MCP server does not read `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` at all (no match in `cmd/podium-mcp/`), and it contains no reference to `oauth-device-code`, the device-code flow, or elicitation. Its only authentication path is the injected-session-token flow: `currentToken()` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:753-773` reads `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN` / `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` and `fetchJSON` attaches it as `Authorization: Bearer` at `main.go:706-708`. The device-code machinery exists in `pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go` but is wired only into the CLI (`cmd/podium/login.go`), not the MCP server. Under the default configuration the MCP server therefore sends no credentials and performs no interactive authentication. Suggested direction: have the MCP server honor `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER`, and for `oauth-device-code` drive `DeviceCodeFlow` with tokens cached in the keychain (reusing `pkg/identity/keychain.go`), surfacing the verification URL and code via MCP elicitation as the section describes.

**Resolution (commit 92675d4):** The MCP server reads `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` (default `oauth-device-code`). `cmd/podium-mcp/identity.go` adds a provider-aware `bearerToken`: injected-session-token reads the env/file token; oauth-device-code loads a keychain-cached token (`KeychainStore`, keyed by registry URL) and, when an IdP authorization endpoint is configured and no token is cached, drives `DeviceCodeFlow`, surfaces the URL+code via an `elicitation/create` server→client message, polls (bounded), and caches the token. With no IdP configured it falls back to any injected token, so existing anonymous bridges are unaffected.

### - [x] F-6.3.4 — `IdpGroupMapping` adapter (registry-side OIDC group-claim mapping) is absent [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) Spec §6.3.1 states "For IdPs without SCIM, the `IdpGroupMapping` adapter reads OIDC group claims from the token and maps them to group names per a registry-side configuration." No such adapter or registry-side mapping configuration exists. A repo-wide search for `IdpGroupMapping`, group-name mapping, and group aliasing returns nothing in non-test code, and neither `internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go` nor `pkg/registry/server/config_validate.go` defines a group-mapping table. What exists is direct pass-through matching: `pkg/identity/runtime.go:164-170` copies the raw `groups` claim values into `Identity.Groups`, and `pkg/registry/core/core.go:60-63` falls back to "JWT-claim group matching only" when the SCIM resolver is nil. Direct matching covers IdPs whose group-claim values already equal the layer `groups:` names, but it does not implement the configurable mapping the spec describes (for example translating an Okta group OID to a friendly name). Suggested direction: either add a registry-side `IdpGroupMapping` configuration that rewrites token group claims to layer group names before visibility evaluation, or amend §6.3.1 to document the pass-through matching behavior as the supported non-SCIM path.

**Resolution (commit 92675d4):** Added `identity.IdpGroupMapping` (`pkg/identity/group_mapping.go`): a registry-side table (claim value → layer group name) configured via `PODIUM_IDP_GROUP_MAPPING` ("oktaOID=finance,..."). `injectedTokenVerifier` applies it to the verified token's group claims before the identity reaches visibility evaluation; unmapped values pass through unchanged so direct-match deployments keep working. Surfaced in `podium config show` as `idp_group_mapping`.

### - [x] F-6.3.5 — Fine-grained OAuth scope narrowing is not implemented [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) Spec §6.3.1 specifies "Fine-grained narrowing via OAuth scope claims (e.g., `podium:read:finance/*`, `podium:load:finance/ap/pay-invoice@1.x`); narrow scopes intersect with the caller's layer visibility, and the smaller surface wins." No code reads `podium:read:`, `podium:load:`, or `podium:write:` scope claims, and there is no intersection logic between a scope surface and layer visibility anywhere in the repo. The only "scope" constructs found are unrelated: OAuth request scopes in `cmd/podium/login.go:34` (`openid profile email groups`) and the sync-side `ScopeFilter` in `pkg/sync/scope.go`. The JWT verifier in `pkg/identity/runtime.go` does not extract a `scope`/`scp` claim, so a token carrying a narrowed scope is treated as if it granted the caller's full layer visibility. Suggested direction: parse the scope claim in the verifier, carry it on `Identity`, and intersect it with the visibility result so the smaller surface wins, as the section requires; add tests covering the wildcard and pinned-version scope forms.

**Resolution (commit 92675d4):** The verifier parses the `scope` (RFC 6749) and `scp` claims onto `Identity.Scopes`. New `pkg/layer/scope.go` parses `podium:<action>:<resource>[@version]` grants (wildcard subtree, version-pin matching). `core.visibleManifests` intersects read/load grants with layer visibility (read implied by load) and `LoadArtifact` gates each resolution through a load-scope check that mirrors visibility-denial (no leak). When no `podium:*` scope is present, no narrowing applies.

### - [x] F-6.3.6 — Token rotation contract implements per-call re-read but omits SIGHUP and fsnotify file watching [Low] — CLOSED

(gap) Spec §6.3.2.1 lists three rotation mechanisms: env-var change observed at the next call, SIGHUP forced re-read, and `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` watched via fsnotify and re-read on change. The MCP server implements the first by reading fresh on every call in `currentToken()` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:753-773`, covered by `cmd/podium-mcp/token_rotation_test.go`). It installs no signal handler and no fsnotify watcher: the `serve` loop at `main.go:214-229` is a plain stdio scanner, there is no `os/signal` or `fsnotify` import in `cmd/podium-mcp/`, and the only SIGHUP reference is the comment at `main.go:764`. Because `currentToken()` re-reads the env var and re-reads the file on every request, the overriding obligation stated in the same section, "the MCP server's only obligation is to read fresh on every call," is satisfied, so the observable token used is always current and the missing mechanisms do not change request behavior. The two bulleted mechanisms are nonetheless described in the contract and not present. Suggested direction: either add the SIGHUP handler and the fsnotify file watcher to match the contract, or revise §6.3.2.1 to describe SIGHUP and fsnotify as optional given the per-call fresh read.

**Resolution (commit 92675d4):** Added `cmd/podium-mcp/token_watch.go`: `serve` starts a watcher that re-reads the token on a SIGHUP (cross-platform via `hangup_unix.go`/`hangup_windows.go`) and on a detected change of `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE`. The per-call fresh read in `currentToken()` remains the authoritative path; the watcher honors the contract's two named mechanisms and logs each rotation. A polling stat-watch substitutes for fsnotify, which is not an available dependency in this build environment; the observable behavior ("watched and re-read on change") matches the contract.

### - [x] F-6.3.7 — `act` claim is checked for presence only, not validated against the runtime [Info] — CLOSED

(observation) Spec §6.3.2 lists `act` as a required claim and describes it as "actor (the runtime itself)." The verifier enforces presence at `pkg/identity/runtime.go:146-148` but does not validate that `act` identifies the runtime (for example, that it equals the `iss` or the registered runtime identifier). The spec text does not state an explicit equality requirement, so this is not clearly a defect, but the parenthetical "the runtime itself" implies the actor should be the verified runtime. If the intent is that `act` must reflect the runtime, the verifier should compare it against the issuer or the registered runtime identity; otherwise the section could clarify that only the presence of `act` is required.

**Resolution (commit 92675d4):** The verifier now validates that `act` identifies the runtime, comparing it against `iss` (the registered runtime identifier). Both the bare-string form (`act: "<runtime>"`) and the RFC 8693 nested form (`act: {"sub": "<runtime>"}`) are accepted; a mismatched actor is rejected with `auth.untrusted_runtime`. The existing test fixtures already set `act == iss`, confirming this is the intended convention.
## F-6.4 — 6.4 Workspace Local Overlay (6.4.1 Local Search Index)

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md against the implementation._

The §6.4 overlay machinery is split across pkg/overlay/overlay.go (the `LocalOverlayProvider` filesystem walker plus a path-resolution helper), cmd/podium-mcp/main.go (load at startup and the load_artifact overlay-precedence path), cmd/podium-mcp/local_search.go (§6.4.1 BM25 over overlay records), and cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go (registry plus local fan-out with RRF fusion). The overlay precedence at load time, the BM25 local index, the RRF fan-out, the format compatibility, and the trust boundary for signatures are implemented and tested. Three §6.4 contracts are not honored by the MCP server: the fsnotify watch and re-index on change, the MCP roots/list path fallback, and the "warn once" behavior on a missing overlay path. The fused `total_matched` field is computed with arithmetic that conflates two different counts.

### - [ ] F-6.4.1 — MCP server does not watch the overlay path via fsnotify or re-index on change [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §6.4 states: "The MCP server watches the resolved path via fsnotify and re-indexes on change." The MCP server loads the overlay exactly once, at process construction in `newServer`, into `srv.overlay` and reuses that slice for the bridge lifetime (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:166-177, with the comment "load now and reuse for the bridge lifetime"). There is no fsnotify watcher and no re-index path: a repo-wide search for `fsnotify` returns no non-test occurrences in any package, and `go.mod`/`go.sum` carry no fsnotify dependency. A search of cmd/podium-mcp for `Watch`, `NewWatcher`, `reindex`, `go func`, or `Ticker` returns nothing. Both `searchArtifacts` (search_artifacts.go:36) and the load_artifact overlay path (main.go:184-191) read the stale `s.overlay` slice captured at startup. A developer who adds, edits, or removes an overlay artifact while the MCP server is running sees no change until the host restarts the subprocess. This breaks the in-progress-iteration workflow §6.4 describes as the overlay's primary use. Suggested direction: add an fsnotify watcher on the resolved overlay path that re-runs `overlay.Filesystem{Path: ...}.Resolve` and atomically swaps `s.overlay` (guarded by a mutex or atomic pointer, since reads happen on the request goroutine), or document a deliberate deviation if watching is intentionally deferred.

### - [ ] F-6.4.2 — MCP roots/list fallback for overlay path resolution is not implemented [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §6.4 path resolution step 2 requires: "The MCP server falls back to MCP roots when available: the `roots/list` response identifies the workspace, and the overlay defaults to `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` if that directory exists." The MCP server resolves the overlay solely from the `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` env var (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:107 reads it into `cfg.overlayPath`, and main.go:168-169 uses that value directly). When `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` is unset, `cfg.overlayPath` is empty and the overlay is disabled, skipping straight to step 4 without ever consulting MCP roots. The helper `overlay.ResolveWorkspaceOverlay` exists (pkg/overlay/overlay.go:64-76) but is never called by the MCP server (the only callers are pkg/sync/sync.go and the overlay package's own tests), and even that helper implements only the env-var and an explicit-`workspace`-argument fallback; it has no MCP roots/list integration. A repo-wide search for `roots/list` or `RootsList` returns no implementation, and the MCP `initialize` handler (main.go:234-256) does not advertise or request the roots capability. Consequently a host that identifies the workspace through MCP roots, as the §6.11 Claude Code recipe contemplates, gets no overlay unless it also sets the env var. Suggested direction: issue a `roots/list` request (or read roots from the client capabilities exchanged at `initialize`), derive `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/`, and feed it through `ResolveWorkspaceOverlay` so the documented precedence (env var, then MCP roots, then disabled) holds.

### - [ ] F-6.4.3 — Missing overlay path does not warn once; the error is silently swallowed [Low] — OPEN

(gap) The §6.9 failure-mode table, governing the §6.4 overlay, specifies for "Workspace overlay path missing": "Skip the workspace local overlay; warn once." The MCP server skips the overlay correctly but emits no warning. In `newServer`, when `overlay.Filesystem{...}.Resolve` returns any error (including `ErrNoOverlay` for a path that does not exist), the code silently leaves `srv.overlay` nil: "Errors other than ErrNoOverlay are silently ignored" (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:169-176). A search of cmd/podium-mcp and pkg/overlay for `warn` finds only the unrelated sandbox-override warning. A developer who sets `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` to a path that does not exist, or whose overlay directory was removed, gets no diagnostic and may not realize their drafts are invisible. Suggested direction: when a configured `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` resolves to `ErrNoOverlay` (path absent) or any other error, emit a single warning to stderr identifying the path, while still starting without the overlay.

### - [ ] F-6.4.4 — Fused `total_matched` double-counts overlay hits and mixes pre-truncation counts [Low] — OPEN

(bug) §6.4.1 describes fusing the registry and local-index result lists via reciprocal rank fusion before returning. In the fan-out path, the MCP server reports `"total_matched": registry.TotalMatched + len(local)` (cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:42). Two problems. First, an artifact present in both streams (a draft on the overlay that the registry also returns) is counted once inside `registry.TotalMatched` and again in `len(local)`, so the reported total exceeds the deduplicated result count; `rrfFuse` correctly merges such an item into a single descriptor (search_artifacts.go:91-104), which makes `total_matched` inconsistent with `len(results)` whenever streams overlap. Second, `registry.TotalMatched` is the registry's count of all matching records before `top_k` truncation (pkg/registry/core/core.go:544 sets `totalMatched := len(scored)` ahead of the `top_k` slice at core.go:566-568), whereas `len(local)` is the already-`topK`-capped local hit count (local_search.go:83-85). Adding a pre-truncation registry total to a post-truncation local count yields a number whose meaning is undefined. The existing test only exercises non-overlapping streams with results below `top_k` (search_artifacts_test.go:46-69), so the double-count and the truncation mismatch are not caught. Suggested direction: define `total_matched` precisely for the fused response (for example the count of distinct artifacts that matched across both streams) and compute it from the deduplicated fusion set rather than by summing two differently-scoped counts.
## F-6.5 — 6.5 Cache

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md against the implementation._

I checked the §6.5 cache contract against the MCP bridge cache code (`cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go`, the `contentCache` type and `loadArtifact` path in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`) and the CLI prune command (`cmd/podium/cache.go`), plus their tests. The two cache layers exist: a resolution index keyed by `(id, version)` and a content-addressed content cache. The three cache modes are accepted and validated, and `always-revalidate` is the default. Several concrete claims in §6.5 are not implemented: the 30-second resolution-cache TTL, HEAD revalidation in `always-revalidate` mode, and the BoltDB-or-SQLite index DB. The resolution index maps to a content hash rather than the semver the spec states, and `podium cache prune` can delete the resolution index because it treats every subdirectory of the cache root as a content bucket.

### - [ ] F-6.5.1 — Resolution-cache 30s TTL not implemented [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §6.5 specifies the resolution cache "Maps `(id, "latest")` to `semver`. TTL 30s by default." The implementation stores resolution entries with no timestamp and no expiry. `resolutionCache` (cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go:18-22) holds only `map[string]string` (key to content hash); `Put` (lines 78-89) and `Get` (lines 93-101) never record or check an age. A repo-wide search for any TTL or freshness tracking in the cache path (`30 * time.Second`, `cacheTTL`, `fetchedAt`, etc.) returns nothing in `cmd/podium-mcp`. Consequently, in `offline-first` mode a cached `(id, "latest")` resolution is served indefinitely regardless of age, and the spec's bound on `latest` staleness does not exist. Suggested direction: persist a fetch timestamp per entry and treat entries older than a configurable TTL (default 30s) as misses for `latest` resolutions, falling through to a registry call (or HEAD revalidation per F-6.5.2).

### - [ ] F-6.5.2 — always-revalidate performs a full fetch every call instead of HEAD revalidation [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §6.5 states the resolution cache is "Revalidated via HEAD on hit when `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE=always-revalidate`," and that `always-revalidate` (default) means "HEAD-revalidate the resolution cache on every call." The implementation does not issue an HTTP HEAD anywhere in the MCP cache path. In `loadArtifact` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:317-369), `always-revalidate` skips the cache entirely and calls `fetchJSON("/v1/load_artifact", args)` (line 331), which issues a full `GET` that downloads the entire manifest and resources (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:702). The resolution cache and content cache are consulted only as a degraded-network fallback after the fetch fails (lines 337-348), never to short-circuit an unchanged artifact via a HEAD-validated content hash. Freshness is preserved because every call fetches in full, but the HEAD revalidation contract and the content-cache reuse it implies are absent. Suggested direction: in `always-revalidate`, when a resolution and content bucket exist, issue a HEAD (or conditional request) to confirm the resolved content hash is unchanged and serve the cached content on a match, falling back to a full fetch on change or HEAD failure.

### - [ ] F-6.5.3 — `podium cache prune` can delete the resolution index `.resolutions` [Medium] — OPEN
