(bug) The resolution cache is stored at `${PODIUM_CACHE_DIR}/.resolutions/index.json` (cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go:29, 40). `podium cache prune` enumerates every entry directly under the cache root and removes any directory whose newest file mtime is older than the cutoff, with no exclusion for the `.resolutions` directory or for dot-prefixed names (cmd/podium/cache.go:62-95; the only filter is `if !e.IsDir() { continue }` at lines 74-77). If no new resolutions have been written within the prune window (default 30 days), `index.json`'s mtime falls before the cutoff and `os.RemoveAll(bucket)` (line 90) deletes the entire resolution index. Losing the index breaks `offline-only` and `offline-first` resolution of `(id, version)` to content hashes even though the content buckets may still be present. Suggested direction: skip `.resolutions` (and any non-content-bucket entries) during prune, for example by ignoring dot-prefixed directories or only pruning directories that contain a `frontmatter` file.

### - [ ] F-6.5.4 — Resolution cache stores content_hash, not the resolved semver [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §6.5 says the resolution cache "Maps `(id, "latest")` to `semver`." The implementation maps `(id, version)` to the content hash instead: `r.entries[resolutionKey(id, version)] = contentHash` (cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go:78-88), and the value flows straight into `loadArtifactFromCache` as a content hash (main.go:321-323, resolution_cache.go:106-107). The code does additionally memoize a `(id, resolvedVersion) -> contentHash` entry on a `latest` fetch (main.go:363-367), but the `(id, "latest")` entry's value is a content hash rather than the resolved semver the spec describes, so the resolved version for `latest` is not recoverable from the cache as the spec states. Suggested direction: either record the resolved semver for the `latest` key (and derive the content hash via the version entry) to match the spec, or update §6.5 to describe the `(id, version) -> content_hash` mapping the code actually uses.

### - [ ] F-6.5.5 — Index DB is a JSON file and directory tree, not BoltDB or SQLite [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §6.5 states "Index DB: BoltDB or SQLite." The MCP cache uses neither. The resolution index is a human-readable JSON file read and written with `encoding/json` and `os.ReadFile`/`os.Rename` (cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go:36-64), and the content cache is a plain directory tree of per-hash buckets with `frontmatter`, `body`, and `resources/` files (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:799-823). No BoltDB or SQLite dependency is used by the MCP cache; the only `go-sqlite3` dependency in `go.mod` serves the registry metadata store. The functional contract is met, but the stated index-DB technology does not match. Suggested direction: reconcile the spec with the JSON-plus-directory implementation, or migrate the index to one of the named stores if the spec requirement is intended literally.

### - [ ] F-6.5.6 — Prune "last access" uses mtime; reads do not refresh it [Low] — OPEN

(bug) `podium cache prune` documents removal of buckets "older than N days since their last access" (cmd/podium/cache.go:13-18, and the `--days` flag help at line 42). The eviction decision uses the newest file modification time via `bucketAccessTime`, which reads `ModTime()` only (cmd/podium/cache.go:104-121). Content buckets are written once by `contentCache.put` and only read afterward; `loadArtifactFromCache` reads them with `os.ReadFile` (cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go:108-129), which does not update mtime, and the code never touches access time. A bucket that is read frequently but never rewritten is therefore pruned once its write time crosses the cutoff, contradicting the stated "last access" semantics. Because content is immutable and re-fetchable, the impact is an extra registry fetch rather than data loss. Suggested direction: either touch the bucket mtime on cache hit so reads count as access, or change the help text to describe mtime-based (write-age) eviction.

### - [ ] F-6.5.7 — Content bucket directory name is `sha256-<hex>`, spec shows `<sha256>` [Info] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §6.5 describes the disk cache as `${PODIUM_CACHE_DIR}/<sha256>/`. The implementation stores each content bucket under a sanitized name where the `sha256:` prefix's colon becomes a hyphen, producing `sha256-<hex>` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:803, 837-848; confirmed by the test fixtures `sha256-old`/`sha256-young` in cmd/podium/cache_test.go:15-16). This is a cosmetic divergence in the documented path layout; the sanitization is deliberate to keep the colon out of filesystem names. Suggested direction: note the sanitized bucket-name convention in §6.5, for example `${PODIUM_CACHE_DIR}/sha256-<hex>/`.
## F-6.6 — 6.6 Materialization

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md against the implementation._

I checked the five-step materialization pipeline that §6.6 mandates (Fetch, Verify, Adapt, Hook, Write) against the MCP server path in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go` (`loadArtifact`, `deliverLoadArtifact`, `loadArtifactFromOverlay`), the fetch path in `cmd/podium-mcp/large_resources.go`, and the write path in `pkg/materialize/atomic.go` and `pkg/materialize/hook.go`. The Fetch step with retry/backoff, the signature-verification portion of Verify, the Adapt step, and per-file atomic Write are implemented. The hook step (step 4) is implemented as a library function but never wired into the MCP server, the content-hash portion of Verify is only applied to large resources and not to the inline manifest bytes, the per-call destination argument is absent, the large-resource fetch omits the session token that the filesystem backend requires, the tree-level atomicity guarantee is not met on a mid-batch write failure, and the symlink protection the sandbox comment claims is not implemented.

### - [ ] F-6.6.1 — Hook step (step 4) is never executed in the MCP server [High] — OPEN

(gap) §6.6 step 4 ("Hook") requires that "Configured `MaterializationHook` plugins (§9.1) run in declared order over the adapter's output, with read+rewrite access to per-file bytes plus the manifest for context," and §6.6 states "The hook step (4) runs whether or not an adapter is configured." The hook chain runner exists in `pkg/materialize/hook.go:14` (`Materialize(destination, files, hooks)`) and the SPI exists in `pkg/hook/hook.go`, but neither is ever called from production code. The MCP server's materialization sites call `materialize.Write` directly, bypassing the hook chain: `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:435` (`deliverLoadArtifact`) and `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:505` (`loadArtifactFromOverlay`). A repo-wide search shows `materialize.Materialize` and `hook.Run` are referenced only from tests; `pkg/sync/sync.go:151` also uses `materialize.Write`. The MCP `main.go:7` doc comment claims the bridge "runs the configured HarnessAdapter and MaterializationHook chain," but no hook chain is built or invoked. Suggested direction: load configured hooks at boot, adapt them to `materialize.HookFunc` (or call `hook.Run` over the adapter output with the parsed manifest), and replace the two `materialize.Write` calls with `materialize.Materialize(dest, out, hooks)` so step 4 runs after Adapt and before Write on both the live-fetch and overlay paths.

### - [ ] F-6.6.2 — Inline manifest content-hash is never verified against content_hash [High] — OPEN

(gap) §6.6 step 2 ("Verify") requires "Signature verification (per `PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES`) and content-hash match." §4.6 defines `content_hash` as "the SHA-256 of the canonicalized manifest + bundled resources," and §13.11 states the consumer "verifies `sha256(bytes) == content_hash` after fetch." The MCP server verifies the signature against the `content_hash` string in `enforceSignaturePolicy` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:565`, delegating to `sign.EnforceVerification`), and it verifies the content hash of large resources in `cmd/podium-mcp/large_resources.go:38-44`. It never recomputes a hash over the returned `Frontmatter`, `ManifestBody`, and inline `Resources` and compares it to `resp.ContentHash`. The signature provider only checks that the signature matches the `content_hash` string (for example `sign.Noop.Verify` at `pkg/sign/sign.go:66`), so nothing binds the delivered manifest bytes to that hash. A registry response (or a man-in-the-middle on a non-TLS hop) that carries a consistent `(content_hash, signature)` pair but tampered `manifest_body`, `frontmatter`, or inline resource bytes would pass verification and be materialized onto the host filesystem. For artifacts below the verification threshold (sensitivity under `medium` with the default `medium-and-above` policy) no signature is checked at all, so the inline content-hash match is the only integrity gate the spec defines and it is absent. The canonicalization needed to verify locally already exists at `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:722` (`contentHashOf`) over `version.ContentHash`. Suggested direction: recompute the canonical hash over the inline bytes in the same order the registry uses and fail with `materialize.content_hash_mismatch` (or reuse the large-resource error) before materializing when it does not equal `resp.ContentHash`.

### - [ ] F-6.6.3 — Large-resource fetch omits the session token required by the filesystem backend [High] — OPEN

(bug) §6.6 step 1 ("Fetch") downloads each resource, and §13.11 specifies the auth model: for the filesystem backend, "URLs point at the registry's authenticated `/objects/{content_hash}` route ... the consumer sends the same session token it used for `load_artifact`." The MCP fetch issues a bare unauthenticated request: `cmd/podium-mcp/large_resources.go:59` calls `http.Get(link.URL)` with no `Authorization` header and no `X-Podium-Tenant` header, unlike the authenticated registry path `fetchJSON` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:706-714`) which sets both. Against a filesystem-backend registry the `/objects/{content_hash}` route would reject the request, the code would observe a 401 or 403, retry the same URL until it exhausts attempts, and fail the whole `load_artifact` call with `materialize.fetch_failed` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:402-404`). The result is that no artifact with a large (over the 256 KB inline cutoff) bundled resource can be materialized on the filesystem backend, which is a documented deployment mode. Suggested direction: route the large-resource fetch through an authenticated request that reuses `s.currentToken()` for the `Authorization: Bearer` header and forwards `X-Podium-Tenant` when `tenantID` is set, matching `fetchJSON`. The S3 backend URLs are self-signed and ignore the extra header, so adding it is safe for both backends.

### - [ ] F-6.6.4 — Write is per-file atomic but not all-or-nothing across the tree on a mid-batch failure [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §6.6 step 5 ("Write") requires the server to write "atomically to a host-configured destination path (`.tmp` + rename), ensuring the destination either contains a complete copy or nothing," and §6.9 ("Materialization destination unwritable") requires "Fail the `load_artifact` call with a structured error; nothing partial is left on disk." `materialize.Write` validates every path before writing so a bad path fails the batch with no writes (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:183-191`), but it then writes files one at a time in a loop (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:197-205`), each via `<path>.tmp` + rename (`writeAtomic`, lines 229-242). If file i fails (for example the destination fills or a directory is unwritable mid-batch), files 0..i-1 are already renamed into place, so the destination holds a partial copy. The atomicity guarantee holds per file and for path-validation failures, but not at the tree level under an I/O failure. The test `TestWrite_RejectionLeavesNoPartialState` (`pkg/materialize/atomic_test.go:87`) only covers the path-validation case, and its comment "the whole batch is atomic at the directory level" overstates the guarantee. Suggested direction: stage all files under a temporary directory and rename the directory into place once every file is written, or write all `.tmp` files first and rename them only after every write succeeds (rolling back the staged `.tmp` files on any failure) so a mid-batch failure leaves the destination unchanged.

### - [ ] F-6.6.5 — Per-call destination argument on load_artifact is not supported [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §6.6 states "The destination path comes from the host, either via `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT` or per-call in the `load_artifact` arguments." The MCP server reads the destination only from `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:104`, used at `main.go:414` and `main.go:486`). The `load_artifact` argument parsing handles a per-call `harness` override (`harnessFromArgs`, `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:455`) but no per-call destination; `argsIDAndVersion` (`cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go:146`) reads only `id` and `version`, and a repo-wide search finds no argument such as `materialize_root`, `destination`, or `root` consumed by the load path. A host that wants to direct one call's output to a different path than the process-wide default cannot do so. Suggested direction: read an optional per-call destination argument in `loadArtifact`, pass it through `deliverOpts` (and the overlay path), validate it the same way the configured root is validated, and fall back to `PODIUM_MATERIALIZE_ROOT` when the argument is absent.

### - [ ] F-6.6.6 — Retry on 403/expired reuses the same URL instead of fetching a fresh URL set [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §6.6 step 1 requires that "On 403/expired during fetch, retries with a fresh URL set (max 3 attempts, exponential backoff)." The implementation retries the same presigned URL rather than re-requesting a fresh set: `cmd/podium-mcp/large_resources.go:58-84` loops up to three times calling `http.Get(link.URL)` on the identical URL with exponential backoff, and the function's own comment (`large_resources.go:19-25`) acknowledges "there's no separate 'fresh URL' call out to the registry." Retrying the same URL helps ride through a transient 403 blip, but for a genuinely expired presigned URL (the case the spec calls out) every retry returns the same 403 and the call fails after exhausting attempts. Suggested direction: on a 403, re-issue `/v1/load_artifact` to obtain a freshly presigned `large_resources` URL set and retry the fetch against the new URL, keeping the max-3-attempts and exponential-backoff bounds.

### - [ ] F-6.6.7 — Sandbox path check does not resolve symlinks despite the comment claiming it does [Medium] — OPEN

(bug) §6.6 step 5 and the §6.7 sandbox contract require "no writes outside the materialization destination," and the `materialize.Write` doc comment states that paths escaping the destination "via "..", an absolute path, or a symlink) cause the call to fail with `ErrOutOfDestination` before any file is written" (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:171`). The path check `resolveSandboxedPath` (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:212-225`) is purely lexical: it rejects empty and absolute paths and uses `filepath.Join` plus a `filepath.Clean` prefix comparison, with no `os.Lstat` or `filepath.EvalSymlinks`. A search confirms no symlink resolution anywhere in the package. If the destination root or an intermediate directory under it is a symlink (for example a pre-existing `sub -> /etc` inside the destination), `writeAtomic`'s `os.MkdirAll` and `os.WriteFile` follow it, so a write to `sub/passwd` lands outside the destination even though the lexical check passes. Current built-in adapters return only file bytes and cannot create symlinks, which limits the blast radius, but the comment overstates the protection and the contract is not enforced against symlinked components. Suggested direction: resolve the destination and each target's parent with `filepath.EvalSymlinks` (or `os.Lstat` each path component) and confirm the resolved path is still contained within the resolved destination root before writing, or correct the comment to state that symlink containment is not checked.

### - [ ] F-6.6.8 — MCP response struct ignores the resources_base64 wire flag [Low] — OPEN

(gap) The registry's `/v1/load_artifact` response carries `resources_base64` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:426`, `ResourcesB64`), documented as the signal that inline resources are base64-encoded. The MCP server's mirror struct `loadArtifactResponse` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:537-549`) has no corresponding field, so the flag is dropped during decode and `cmd/podium-mcp/large_resources.go` and the materialization path treat every inline resource string as raw content. The current registry never sets `ResourcesB64` to true or base64-encodes resources (a search finds no encoder), so this is presently dormant rather than a live corruption. If a future registry build encodes binary resources and sets the flag, the MCP would write the base64 text to disk instead of the decoded bytes, and the large-resource content-hash check would then fail because the bytes no longer match. Suggested direction: add a `resources_base64` field to `loadArtifactResponse` and base64-decode the inline resource values when it is set, before the content-hash check and materialization.
## F-6.7 — 6.7 Harness Adapters (6.7.1 The Author's Burden)

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md against the implementation._

I reviewed §6.7.1 (lines 185-212), which describes two mitigations for the author's burden (a documented core feature set, and a per-(field, harness) capability matrix backed by ingest-time lint), the `target_harnesses:` opt-out, the capability-matrix table values, and the `hook_event` row semantics. The adapter SPI and built-in adapters live in pkg/adapter; lint lives in pkg/lint; ingest wiring is in pkg/registry/ingest. The capability matrix and `target_harnesses` opt-out are documented in spec and docs and are referenced as a hard requirement by §4.3 and §4.3.5, but the enforcement machinery is absent from the code. The `target_harnesses` field is parsed but consumed nowhere, and several spec-✗ capability cells are accepted silently. The only "capability matrix" artifact in the tree is a test-coverage scaffolding tool in tools/matrix, not a production data structure or lint rule.

### - [x] F-6.7.1 — Ingest-time capability-mismatch lint is absent [High] — CLOSED

(gap) §6.7.1 mitigation 2 requires a "Per-(field, harness) compatibility table maintained alongside the adapters" and states "Ingest-time lint surfaces capability mismatches: 'field `X` is used but adapter `cursor` cannot translate it.'" §4.3.5 (spec/04-artifact-model.md:333) and §4.3 reinforce this: "lint rejects ingest at the unsupported (✗) intersection unless `target_harnesses:` excludes the unsupported harness." The lint rule set `AllRules()` (pkg/lint/lint.go:71-86) contains no rule that consults any capability matrix and no rule that inspects harness compatibility. A whole-repo search finds no capability-matrix data structure in production code (only tools/matrix/matrices.go, which is a spec-coverage scaffolder, not a runtime table) and no diagnostic message of the form "is used but adapter ... cannot translate it." As a result, ingest accepts artifacts that use fields the target adapter marks ✗ (for example `rule_mode: glob` on `claude-desktop`, or `hook_event` on `claude-desktop`) with neither the mandated lint error for ✗ cells nor the mandated lint warning for ⚠ cells. Suggested direction: add a lint rule (for example `lint.harness_capability`) backed by a maintained per-(field/mode, harness) table, emit Error for ✗ cells and Warning for ⚠ cells, scope the harness set to the artifact's `target_harnesses` when present, and register it in `AllRules()`.

**Resolution (af8ffc1):** New `pkg/adapter/capability.go` encodes the §6.7.1 matrix as production data (`Cell`, `Evaluate`, `UsedCapabilities`). New `lint.harness_capability` (`pkg/lint/harness_capability.go`, registered in `AllRules()`) checks every used field against each harness in `target_harnesses`: a ✗ cell is an ingest error ("field `X` is used but adapter `Y` cannot translate it"), a ⚠ cell is a warning. An artifact without `target_harnesses` declares no harness set and draws no capability diagnostic, matching the doc-derived conformance suite (T-D-artifact-types-37/38, T-D-first-agent-2, which lint `delegates_to` / `rule_mode: auto` artifacts clean). Covered by `pkg/adapter/capability_test.go` and `pkg/lint/harness_capability_test.go`.

### - [x] F-6.7.2 — `target_harnesses:` opt-out is parsed but has no behavioral effect [High] — CLOSED

(gap) §6.7.1 states "Authors who must use a non-portable feature can declare `target_harnesses:` in frontmatter to opt out of cross-harness materialization for that artifact," and the legend ties the ✗ cell to "`target_harnesses:` opt-out required." §4.3.5 (spec/04-artifact-model.md:333) makes the field the explicit escape hatch from ingest rejection. The field is declared at pkg/manifest/types.go:140 (`TargetHarnesses []string`), but a repo-wide search shows it is read nowhere: no lint rule, no ingest path (pkg/registry/ingest), and no adapter or materialize code references `TargetHarnesses`. Consequently the opt-out is inert: it neither suppresses any capability lint (which itself does not exist per F-6.7.1) nor restricts which harness adapters materialize the artifact. Suggested direction: have the capability lint from F-6.7.1 treat `target_harnesses` as the allowed harness set when present, and have the consumer-side materialization path (MCP server and `podium sync`) refuse or skip adapters not listed in `target_harnesses` so the opt-out actually narrows cross-harness materialization.

**Resolution (af8ffc1):** `target_harnesses` now narrows both surfaces. The consumer-side materialization skip (`podium sync` and the MCP `load_artifact` paths consulting `manifest.TargetsHarness`) landed in 7ceb07c; this batch adds the lint scoping from F-6.7.1, so the field is the harness set the capability lint checks against. The two e2e tests previously skipped on this finding are unskipped and pass: `TestFrontmatter_TargetHarnessesExcludesSkips` (T-D-frontmatter-38) and `TestHandlingResponses_TargetHarnessMismatch` (T-D-handling-responses-4).

### - [x] F-6.7.3 — ✗ capability cells produce silent fallback output instead of failing or warning [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) The §6.7.1 capability matrix legend defines ✗ as "not supported (lint error or `target_harnesses:` opt-out required)" and ⚠ as "supported via fallback (lint warning)." Because no capability lint exists (F-6.7.1), the only remaining enforcement point is the adapter itself, and the built-in adapters silently emit pass-through output for every field regardless of the cell value. For example, `ClaudeDesktop.Adapt` (pkg/adapter/builtins.go:27-29) calls `placeUnder`, which copies `ARTIFACT.md` verbatim (pkg/adapter/builtins.go:156-178), so a `rule_mode: glob` rule (✗ for claude-desktop per spec line 207) or a `hook_event` artifact (✗ for claude-desktop per spec line 210) is written without error and without any warning. The adapter-level tests confirm this is the intended current behavior: they assert only that output is non-empty and that the sentinel survives (pkg/adapter/capability_matrix_test.go:152-159, pkg/adapter/rule_mode_test.go:16-37), not that ✗ cells fail. This diverges from the spec, which requires ✗ cells to be rejected (at lint, or at `load_artifact` per §6.9 "Adapter cannot translate an artifact"). Suggested direction: pair the lint rule from F-6.7.1 with a materialization-time guard so an adapter that cannot translate a field for the selected harness returns the structured `load_artifact` error named in §6.9 rather than emitting an unannotated verbatim copy.

**Resolution (af8ffc1):** `deliverLoadArtifact` and the overlay `load_artifact` path now call `adapter.TranslationError(harness, artifact)` before adapting. A field whose §6.7.1 cell is ✗ for the selected harness fails the call with `materialize.untranslatable` (the §6.9 "Adapter cannot translate an artifact" mode), naming the field and suggesting `harness: none`, and writes nothing to disk. `harness: none` and custom adapters carry no per-field contract and never fail. Covered by `TestPodiumMCP_UntranslatableFieldFailsMaterialize` (real binary, glob rule under claude-desktop) and `pkg/adapter/capability_test.go`.

### - [x] F-6.7.4 — Cursor `rule_mode` is not translated to native `alwaysApply` / `globs` / `description` [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) The §6.7.1 capability matrix marks `cursor` as ✓ (supported natively) for `rule_mode: always`, `rule_mode: glob`, `rule_mode: auto`, and `rule_mode: explicit` (spec lines 206-209), and §6.7 line 159 specifies that the cursor adapter writes `.cursor/rules/<name>.mdc` "with `alwaysApply` / `globs` / `description` per `rule_mode`." The cursor adapter writes the `.mdc` path correctly (pkg/adapter/builtins.go:54-64) but `cursorRuleBody` (pkg/adapter/builtins.go:70-77) emits only a `---` block containing a generated-by comment followed by the raw `ARTIFACT.md` bytes. It does not derive `alwaysApply`, `globs`, or `description` from `rule_mode`, `rule_globs`, or `rule_description`, despite the function's own doc comment claiming it does (pkg/adapter/builtins.go:66-69). The artifact's own `rule_mode:` frontmatter is carried through verbatim, so Cursor receives Podium's canonical field names rather than Cursor-native keys, which is the opposite of the "native" translation the ✓ cells assert. The generated header also self-identifies as the "claude-cursor adapter," which is a stray label. Suggested direction: map `rule_mode: always` to `alwaysApply: true`, `rule_mode: glob` to `globs:` from `rule_globs`, `rule_mode: auto` to `description:` from `rule_description`, and `rule_mode: explicit` to neither, then emit those keys in the `.mdc` frontmatter so the ✓ cells hold.

**Resolution (af8ffc1):** `cursorRuleBody` (`pkg/adapter/builtins.go`) now parses the artifact and emits the Cursor-native frontmatter key per `rule_mode` (`always` → `alwaysApply: true`, `glob` → `globs:` from `rule_globs`, `auto` → `description:` from `rule_description`, `explicit` → no auto-apply key), followed by the rule prose. The canonical field names no longer leak into the `.mdc`, and the stray "claude-cursor adapter" label is removed. A parse quirk falls back to wrapping the canonical bytes so the `.mdc` is never empty. Covered by `pkg/adapter/cursor_test.go`.

### - [x] F-6.7.5 — No machine-checkable "core feature set" definition [Low] — CLOSED

(gap) §6.7.1 mitigation 1 describes a "core feature set": "A documented subset of canonical fields and patterns that all built-in adapters support." Prose descriptions exist in docs (docs/getting-started/concepts.md:210, docs/consuming/configure-your-harness.md:486, docs/authoring/rule-modes.md), but there is no enumerated definition in code that an author or a lint rule could check an artifact against, and no surface that reports whether an artifact stays within the core feature set. The capability-matrix tests in pkg/adapter only assert per-field pass-through for selected ✓ cells; they do not define the core set as the intersection of supported fields across all adapters. This is primarily a documentation and tooling deliverable rather than a runtime defect, so the severity is low, but the core feature set is the basis on which the capability lint (F-6.7.1) decides which fields are universally portable. Suggested direction: encode the core feature set as a data structure (the set of (field, value) cells that are ✓ across every built-in adapter) and reuse it both to drive the F-6.7.1 lint and to back a documented reference that stays in sync with the adapter table.

**Resolution (af8ffc1):** `adapter.CoreFeatureSet()` and `adapter.InCoreFeatureSet()` (`pkg/adapter/capability.go`) compute the §6.7.1 mitigation-1 core feature set as the cells that are ✓ across every first-class harness (`description`, `mcpServers`, `expose_as_mcp_prompt`), derived from the same `capabilityMatrix` the F-6.7.1 lint reads, so the two cannot drift. Covered by `TestCapability_CoreFeatureSet`.
## F-6.8 — 6.8 Process Model

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md against the implementation._

Section 6.8 is brief and describes the MCP server as a stdio subprocess whose host owns the lifecycle (spawn, signal handling, and shutdown), with one subprocess per workspace for developer hosts and one subprocess per session for managed agent runtimes. The stdio model is implemented in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`: `main` wires `os.Stdin` and `os.Stdout` into `serve` (main.go:62), and `serve` reads line-delimited JSON-RPC and exits the loop when stdin reaches EOF (main.go:214-229), which matches the host closing the pipe to shut the process down. The binary contains no signal handlers, which is consistent with the spec delegating signal handling and shutdown to the host. The per-process server struct holds only local state and shares nothing across processes, matching the per-workspace and per-session process model. The findings below concern defects in the serve loop that implements this process model rather than missing spec behavior.

### - [ ] F-6.8.1 — Serve loop replies to JSON-RPC notifications during the host-owned lifecycle [Medium] — OPEN

(bug) Section 6.8 states that the host is responsible for the MCP server lifecycle. The MCP lifecycle handshake the host drives requires the host to send a `notifications/initialized` notification after `initialize`, and the host may also send other notifications such as `notifications/cancelled` and `notifications/roots/list_changed`. JSON-RPC 2.0 notifications carry no `id` and must not receive a response. The serve loop unmarshals every inbound line into an `rpcRequest` and unconditionally encodes a response for every successfully parsed request (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:218-226`). A notification has `req.ID == nil` and a method name that does not match any case in `handle`, so it falls through to the `default` branch and produces an error frame `{"jsonrpc":"2.0","error":{"code":-32601,"message":"method not found: notifications/initialized"}}` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:273-274`), which `serve` then writes back to the host. Emitting a response, and in particular a `-32601` error, in reply to a notification violates JSON-RPC 2.0, and a spurious error frame in the middle of the initialize handshake can be treated as a protocol error by strict hosts. Suggested direction: detect notifications in the serve loop (a request whose `id` field is absent) and skip both `handle` and `enc.Encode` for them, or have `handle` signal "no response" for methods that begin with `notifications/` so the loop suppresses the write.

### - [ ] F-6.8.2 — Oversized inbound JSON-RPC frame terminates the subprocess [Low] — OPEN

(bug) The §6.8 process model is a long-lived stdio subprocess that the host keeps open for the workspace or session. The serve loop builds a `bufio.Scanner` with a fixed 1 MiB maximum token size (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:215-216`). When a single inbound line exceeds 1 MiB, `scanner.Scan()` returns false and `scanner.Err()` returns `bufio.ErrTooLong`, which `serve` returns (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:228`); `main` then prints the error and calls `os.Exit(1)` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:62-65`). One oversized request frame tears down the entire subprocess and every subsequent request on the same stdio session, rather than failing only the offending request. A `tools/call` for `load_artifact` whose arguments include large inline data can plausibly cross this limit. Suggested direction: when the scanner hits `ErrTooLong`, return a structured per-request error to the host and continue serving instead of exiting, or read frames with an unbounded reader (for example `bufio.Reader.ReadString('\n')` with a documented cap that produces an error response rather than a process exit).

### - [ ] F-6.8.3 — Host-owned signal handling is correctly absent [Info] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 6.8 states that the host is responsible for signal handling and shutdown. The MCP server registers no signal handlers anywhere in `cmd/podium-mcp` (no `os/signal` import or `signal.Notify` usage), and it relies on stdin EOF to end the serve loop (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:218-228`). This matches the spec's delegation of signals and shutdown to the host and is recorded here only to confirm the behavior was verified; no change is required. Note that §6.3.2.1 separately requires the server to treat SIGHUP as a forced token re-read, which is outside this subsection's scope and is reviewed under F-6.3.
## F-6.9 — 6.9 Failure Modes

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md against the implementation._

This subsection is a table mapping fourteen failure conditions to required behaviors. The registry-side rows (visibility denial, untrusted runtime, quota exhausted, registry unavailable) are surfaced correctly at the registry layer: `pkg/registry/core/core.go:763` emits `visibility.denied` and returns `ErrNotFound` without leaking the layer, and `pkg/registry/server` maps store outages, quota, and untrusted-runtime to structured envelopes with `retryable`/`suggested_action` (server.go:459). The defects concentrate in the MCP bridge (`cmd/podium-mcp`): the degraded-network fallback is wired only to `load_artifact` rather than the browse and search tools the row names, reachable HTTP rejections are relabeled as a network error, the unknown-harness startup refusal is missing, the runtime-requirement check is defined but never called, and the `oauth-device-code` reauth-via-elicitation behavior is absent because the bridge implements only `injected-session-token`.

### - [ ] F-6.9.1 — Offline fallback wired to load_artifact instead of load_domain / search_domains / search_artifacts [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The "Registry offline" row requires "Serve from cache; return explicit 'offline' status on fresh `load_domain` / `search_domains` / `search_artifacts`." In the implementation the offline serve-from-cache path exists only for `load_artifact` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:331`-`349`, which sets `status: offline` and `served_from_cache: true` at lines 342-343). The three tools the row names take a different path: `load_domain` and `search_domains` go through `proxyGet` (`main.go:291`-`293`, `main.go:733`-`739`), and `search_artifacts` has its own handler (`search_artifacts.go:12`-`16`). All three call `errorResult(err.Error())` on a fetch failure regardless of `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE`; none serves from a cache or returns a `status: offline` field. There is also no response cache for domain or search results to serve from (the content and resolution caches are keyed by content hash and `(id, version)` for `load_artifact`). As a result the row's named behavior is unimplemented for browse and search, and in `offline-first` mode these tools surface an error rather than serving silently per the cross-referenced degraded-network contract. Suggested direction: add a cached descriptor path for `load_domain` / `search_domains` / `search_artifacts` (or document in the spec that the offline status applies to `load_artifact`), and make the browse and search handlers honor the cache mode the way `load_artifact` does.

### - [ ] F-6.9.2 — Unknown PODIUM_HARNESS does not refuse to start [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The "Unknown `PODIUM_HARNESS` value" row requires "Refuse to start; CLI lists the available adapter values." The bridge reads `PODIUM_HARNESS` with a default of `none` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:100`) but never validates it against the adapter registry at startup. `loadConfig` (`main.go:93`-`135`) and `newServer` (`main.go:154`-`178`) perform no harness check, and `main` (`main.go:51`-`66`) exits only on config or server-construction errors. The unknown-harness condition is detected lazily, on the first `load_artifact` materialization, when `s.adapters.Get(harnessID)` fails (`main.go:419`-`421` and `main.go:491`-`493`), at which point it returns `config.unknown_harness` per call. The registry of valid IDs and a listing helper exist (`pkg/adapter/adapter.go:74`-`96`, where `Get` already includes `(have: ...)`), but the bridge never calls them during startup. Suggested direction: in `loadConfig` or `newServer`, call `adapter.DefaultRegistry().Get(cfg.harness)` (or validate against `IDs()`) and return a fatal error listing the available adapters so the process exits before serving.

### - [ ] F-6.9.3 — Runtime requirement check defined but never invoked on the materialize path [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The "Runtime requirement unsatisfiable" row requires "Fail with `materialize.runtime_unavailable`; lists the unsatisfied requirement." `pkg/materialize/atomic.go:47` implements `CheckRuntimeRequirements`, which returns `ErrRuntimeUnavailable` (`atomic.go:28`) wrapping the unmet requirement, and it has unit coverage in `pkg/materialize/runtime_test.go`. However, no caller invokes it from the bridge: a repository search for `CheckRuntimeRequirements` and `HostCapabilities` finds only the definition and its own tests. The bridge's materialization path `deliverLoadArtifact` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:383`-`451`) runs signature and sandbox enforcement and then materializes, but never checks the artifact's `runtime_requirements` against host capabilities. The bridge also has no configuration for host capabilities (no Python/Node/system-package env vars in `config`). Consequently `materialize.runtime_unavailable` is never produced in practice and an artifact materializes even when the host cannot satisfy its declared runtime. Suggested direction: thread a `HostCapabilities` value into the config, parse `runtime_requirements` from the manifest frontmatter, and call `CheckRuntimeRequirements` in `deliverLoadArtifact` before writing, returning the wrapped error as the structured `materialize.runtime_unavailable` envelope.

### - [ ] F-6.9.4 — Reachable HTTP rejection relabeled as network.registry_unreachable in load_artifact [High] — OPEN

(bug) `fetchJSON` returns a non-nil error for any HTTP status >= 400 (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:724`-`726`), so a reachable-but-rejected response (for example 403 visibility denial, 409 quota exhausted, 401 token expired, or 403 untrusted runtime) is delivered to `loadArtifact` as an error. In the default `always-revalidate` mode with no cache entry, `loadArtifact` unconditionally wraps that error as `network.registry_unreachable` (`main.go:337`-`348`). This conflates a registry that answered and refused with a registry that could not be reached: the registry's structured envelope and its actual code (`auth.untrusted_runtime`, `auth.token_expired`, `quota.storage_exceeded`, or the visibility-denied not-found) are discarded and replaced with a code whose envelope is marked retryable. The `auth.token_expired` row, the quota row, and the visibility-denial row are therefore mis-surfaced for `load_artifact` whenever the artifact is not already cached. Suggested direction: distinguish transport failures from HTTP error responses (for example return a typed transport error from `fetchJSON`, or inspect `resp.StatusCode`), only fall back to cache and emit `network.registry_unreachable` on a genuine transport failure, and pass through the registry's structured error body otherwise.

### - [ ] F-6.9.5 — oauth-device-code token-expiry reauth via MCP elicitation not implemented in the bridge [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The "Auth token expired (`oauth-device-code`)" row requires "Trigger refresh; if interactive refresh required, surface in tool response with reauth instructions via MCP elicitation." `oauth-device-code` is the default identity provider for the MCP server per §6.3, and §6.3 line 37 states the MCP server surfaces the verification URL via MCP elicitation. The bridge implements only `injected-session-token`: `currentToken` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:753`-`773`) reads a bearer token from `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN`/`PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` and attaches it (`main.go:706`-`708`), and `cmd/podium-mcp` does not import `pkg/identity` at all. The device-code flow and the `ErrDeviceCodeRequired` signal exist (`pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:31`, `pkg/identity/identity.go:90`) but are wired only into the CLI. There is no MCP `elicitation` capability or any elicitation request emitted by the bridge (a repository search for `elicit` outside `pkg/identity` finds none in non-test code). Consequently the entire `oauth-device-code` failure-mode behavior is absent from the MCP server. Suggested direction: wire the `pkg/identity` device-code provider into the bridge, advertise the elicitation capability in `initialize`, attempt a transparent refresh on token expiry, and emit an MCP elicitation carrying the verification URL and code when interactive reauth is required.

### - [ ] F-6.9.6 — Missing workspace overlay path is skipped without the required one-time warning [Low] — OPEN

(gap) The "Workspace overlay path missing" row requires "Skip the workspace local overlay; warn once." `newServer` loads the overlay when `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` is set and silently drops any error (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:168`-`176`: it assigns records only `if err == nil` and the comment states errors are "silently ignored"). A configured path that does not exist resolves to `overlay.ErrNoOverlay` (`pkg/overlay/overlay.go:44`-`47`), which the bridge discards with no stderr message. The "skip" half is implemented; the "warn once" half is not, so an operator who misconfigures the overlay path gets no signal that the layer was disabled. Suggested direction: emit a single stderr warning when a non-empty `overlayPath` resolves to `ErrNoOverlay` (or any load error), guarding against repetition since the overlay is loaded once per process.

### - [ ] F-6.9.7 — MCP version negotiation echoes a fixed version instead of negotiating down [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The "MCP protocol version mismatch" row requires "Negotiate down to host's max supported MCP version; if no compatible version, fail with `mcp.unsupported_version`." The `initialize` handler rejects a requested `protocolVersion` older than `supportedSince` with `mcp.unsupported_version` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:241`-`246`), which satisfies the no-compatible-version half. For a host whose requested version is within range it always returns the server's own constant `protocolVersion = "2024-11-05"` (`main.go:248`-`249`) rather than negotiating down to the host's value, and `TestHandle_InitializeAcceptsCurrentProtocol` asserts the server echoes its own version. With a single live protocol version in the supported window the practical impact is small, but the echoed-version behavior does not implement the "negotiate down" wording. The string comparison `initParams.ProtocolVersion < supportedSince` (`main.go:241`) also relies on lexical ordering of the date strings, which holds for the `YYYY-MM-DD` format but is fragile if the version scheme changes. Suggested direction: return `min(host requested, server max)` for a compatible request, or update the spec wording if echoing the server version is the intended contract.

### - [ ] F-6.9.8 — Adapter-cannot-translate failure mode has no triggering path or harness: none suggestion [Low] — OPEN

(gap) The "Adapter cannot translate an artifact" row requires "Fail with structured error naming the missing translation; suggest `harness: none` for raw output." No built-in adapter returns a translation-failure error: every `Adapt` in `pkg/adapter/builtins.go` and the per-harness files returns `nil` for the error and always produces output (for example `Cursor.Adapt` at `builtins.go:54`, `placeUnder` at `builtins.go:156`). The only adapter-related structured error the bridge can emit is `config.unknown_harness` for an unregistered ID (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:419`-`421`), which is a different condition. There is no code path that detects an artifact a known adapter cannot translate, no error that names the missing translation, and no message suggesting `harness: none`. Suggested direction: define an adapter capability or per-type translation contract so an adapter can report an untranslatable artifact, and have the bridge surface that as a structured error suggesting `harness: none`.

### - [ ] F-6.9.9 — "Nothing partial is left on disk" holds per file but not across a multi-file write [Low] — OPEN

(bug) The "Materialization destination unwritable" row requires "Fail the `load_artifact` call with a structured error; nothing partial is left on disk." `materialize.Write` validates every output path before writing and then writes each file atomically via temp-file-plus-rename (`pkg/materialize/atomic.go:173`-`207`, `writeAtomic` at `atomic.go:229`-`242`). Path validation makes path-escape rejection atomic, and per-file rename prevents a half-written file. A mid-batch IO failure for a multi-file artifact is not atomic, however: if file two of three fails (for example the destination fills or permissions change after the first rename), file one is already committed and remains on disk, so a partial tree is left. The common destination-unwritable cases (the directory cannot be created, or the first file fails) leave nothing partial, so the blast radius is narrow. Suggested direction: stage all files into a temporary directory and promote them as a unit, or remove already-written files on a mid-batch failure, so a failed multi-file materialization leaves nothing behind.

### - [ ] F-6.9.10 — Binary version mismatch refuse-to-start is host-side only; confirm bridge obligation [Info] — OPEN

(gap) The "Binary version mismatch with host caller" row reads "Refuse to start; host's CLI prompts an update." The bridge advertises its version in the `initialize` result (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:255`, `serverInfo.version` from `buildinfo.Version`) but has no logic that refuses to start on a version mismatch, and no version is exchanged at process spawn. The row assigns the prompt to the host's CLI, so the refuse-to-start step may be intended as host-side behavior with the binary only advertising its version. No defect is asserted here; this notes the ambiguity so the intended ownership of the refuse-to-start step can be confirmed.
## F-6.10 — 6.10 Error Model

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md against the implementation._

Section 6.10 defines a structured error envelope with the fields `code`, `message`, `details`, `retryable`, and `suggested_action`, namespaced codes across `auth.*`, `config.*`, `ingest.*`, `materialize.*`, `quota.*`, `mcp.*`, `network.*`, `registry.*`, and `domain.*`, and a requirement that errors are mapped to MCP error payloads per the MCP spec. The registry server implements the envelope as `ErrorResponse` in `pkg/registry/server/server.go` and maps core errors via `errorEnvelopeFor` in `pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go`. All nine namespaces appear in non-test source. Two envelope fields from the spec example are absent from the registry envelope, and the MCP bridge collapses every error into a flat string under a single `error` key, so the structured envelope does not survive to MCP clients.

### - [x] F-6.10.1 — Registry error envelope omits the `details` field [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) Section 6.10 defines the envelope with a `details` object, shown in the example as `"details": { "runtime_iss": "managed-runtime-x" }`. The registry's `ErrorResponse` type in `pkg/registry/server/server.go:455-461` declares only `Code`, `Message`, `Retryable`, and `SuggestedAction`; there is no `Details` field. A repository-wide search finds no `details` JSON key and no `Details` struct field anywhere in `pkg/registry/server` or `cmd/podium-mcp`, so no code path can populate it. Clients that the spec leads to expect machine-readable context (for example `runtime_iss` for `auth.untrusted_runtime`) receive only the free-text `message`. Add a `Details map[string]any \`json:"details,omitempty"\`` field to `ErrorResponse` and populate it for the codes whose spec examples carry structured context.

**Resolution (77ad29e):** Added a `Details map[string]any` field to `ErrorResponse` and a `writeErrorDetails` helper. The `quota.layer_count_exceeded` 429 now carries `{"limit","current"}` in `details`, and the MCP bridge decodes and forwards the registry's `details` object (for example `runtime_iss` for `auth.untrusted_runtime`) to clients.

### - [x] F-6.10.2 — MCP bridge flattens the structured envelope to `{"error": "<string>"}` [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) Section 6.10 requires errors to use the structured envelope with namespaced `code` and to be mapped to MCP error payloads. The MCP bridge returns errors through `errorResult` in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:775`, which produces `map[string]any{"error": msg}`, a single free-text string with no `code`, `details`, `retryable`, or `suggested_action`. On a registry HTTP error, `fetchJSON` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:724-725` collapses the registry's JSON envelope into `fmt.Errorf("HTTP %d: %s", resp.StatusCode, body)`, so the `code`, `retryable`, and `suggested_action` fields the registry set in `errorEnvelopeFor` (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:103-113`) are embedded in a string and never reach the MCP client as discrete fields. Bridge-originated errors prefix a code into the message text (for example `"materialize.signature_invalid: "` at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:392` and `"network.registry_unreachable: "` at line 348), but the code is not a separate field and downstream consumers must parse the string to recover it. Decode the registry envelope in `fetchJSON` on `StatusCode >= 400` and return the structured fields, and have `errorResult` emit the full envelope (`code`, `message`, `details`, `retryable`, `suggested_action`) rather than a single string.

**Resolution (77ad29e):** `fetchJSON` decodes the registry envelope on HTTP status >= 400 into a structured `registryError`, and `errorResult`/`errorResultFrom` emit the full envelope (`code`, `message`, `details`, `retryable`, `suggested_action`) in the MCP tool result. The human-readable `error` summary string is retained for host display.

### - [x] F-6.10.3 — `suggested_action` is never populated by any code path [Low] — CLOSED

(gap) The envelope in §6.10 includes `suggested_action`, and the example sets a concrete value (`"Register the runtime's signing key via 'podium admin runtime register'."`). The `SuggestedAction` field exists on `ErrorResponse` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:460`), but a repository-wide search for `SuggestedAction:` in non-test source returns no assignments, so the field is emitted empty and dropped by `omitempty` on every response. `errorEnvelopeFor` (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:103-113`), `writeCoreError` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:821-832`), `writeError` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:853-855`), and `writeQuotaError` (`pkg/registry/server/rate_limit.go:122-124`) all leave it unset. Clients never receive the remediation hint the spec advertises. Populate `SuggestedAction` for the codes that have a clear operator remediation (for example `auth.untrusted_runtime`, `quota.storage_exceeded`, `config.unknown_harness`), matching the spec example.

**Resolution (77ad29e):** A central `errorCodeRegistry`, applied by `enrichEnvelope` in `writeError` and `errorEnvelopeFor`, populates `suggested_action` for the emitted codes (`registry.unavailable`, the quota codes) and for the spec's canonical `auth.untrusted_runtime`, which uses the verbatim spec hint. The MCP bridge supplies hints for its own codes (`network.registry_unreachable`, `config.unknown_harness`, `materialize.signature_invalid`).

### - [x] F-6.10.4 — `retryable` is set only for `registry.unavailable` [Low] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) The envelope carries a boolean `retryable`. The only place `Retryable: true` is assigned in non-test source is `errorEnvelopeFor` for `core.ErrUnavailable` (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:108`). The `writeError` path used by `writeCoreError`, `writeQuotaError`, and all direct handler callers constructs `ErrorResponse{Code: code, Message: msg}` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:853-855`) and never sets `Retryable`, so quota errors (`quota.search_qps_exceeded` at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:539` and `563`, returned with HTTP 429 by `writeQuotaError`) and the default-branch `registry.unavailable` from `writeCoreError` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:830`) are reported with `retryable: false`. The §6.9 failure table and the §13/§7 quota semantics treat rate-limit and transient-unavailable conditions as retry-after cases, so the flat `false` understates retryability for HTTP 429 and for the 500 `registry.unavailable` branch. Set `Retryable: true` for the quota rate-limit codes and the `writeCoreError` default `registry.unavailable` branch, or route those through `errorEnvelopeFor` so the retryable bit is assigned consistently.

**Resolution (77ad29e):** `enrichEnvelope` marks `registry.unavailable` and the quota rate codes (`quota.search_qps_exceeded`, `quota.materialize_rate_exceeded`) retryable across every emission path, including the `writeCoreError` default branch (via `writeError`) and the batch-load `errorEnvelopeFor`. Hard caps such as `quota.layer_count_exceeded` remain non-retryable.
## F-6.11 — 6.11 Host Configuration Recipes

_Reviewed spec/06-mcp-server.md against the implementation._

This subsection documents per-host MCP config snippets for Claude Desktop, Claude Code, Cursor, OpenCode, Pi, and Hermes, plus a standalone recipe that omits the registry env var. I verified the binary name (`podium-mcp`), the env-var contract (`PODIUM_REGISTRY`, `PODIUM_HARNESS`, `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH`), every `PODIUM_HARNESS` value used in a recipe (`claude-desktop`, `claude-code`, `cursor`, `opencode`, `pi`, `hermes`, and `none`), and the standalone registry-from-`sync.yaml` claim. All harness identifiers in the recipes are registered adapters in `pkg/adapter` (`adapter.DefaultRegistry`, cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:164), and the `none` adapter writes the canonical layout as the spec promises. The docs-site recipes in docs/consuming/configure-your-harness.md match the spec recipes and the registered adapter set. The one substantive defect is that the standalone recipe does not work for the MCP server: the server has no `sync.yaml` fallback for the registry and errors when `PODIUM_REGISTRY` is unset.

### - [ ] F-6.11.1 — Standalone recipe fails: MCP server has no sync.yaml registry fallback [High] — OPEN

(gap) §6.11 line 357 ("Standalone (no env override)") states that when `podium serve` has auto-bootstrapped `~/.podium/sync.yaml` with `defaults.registry: http://127.0.0.1:8080`, or `podium init --global --standalone` has written it explicitly, "the MCP server resolves the registry from there and the env var can be omitted." The §6.2 default table corroborates this: the `PODIUM_REGISTRY` default is "(read from `sync.yaml`'s `defaults.registry` per §7.5.2 if unset; required if neither is set)." §7.5.2 line 261 lists the MCP server among the consumers that work against a URL registry, and §13.10 line 223 names "Clients (CLI, MCP server, SDK)" as reading the client registry value from `sync.yaml`'s `defaults.registry`.

The MCP server does not implement this. `loadConfig()` reads `os.Getenv("PODIUM_REGISTRY")` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:99) and immediately returns `fmt.Errorf("PODIUM_REGISTRY is required")` when the value is empty (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:119-121). There is no read of `~/.podium/sync.yaml` or `<workspace>/.podium/sync.yaml` anywhere in `cmd/podium-mcp`; the package does not import `pkg/sync`, and `os.UserHomeDir()` is used only to default the cache directory (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:122-127). The `podium-mcp` binary is spawned directly by the host (the recipes use `"command": "podium-mcp"`) with no `podium mcp` launcher subcommand that could inject the registry, so the resolution must live inside `cmd/podium-mcp` and currently does not. As a result, a host that follows the standalone recipe and omits `PODIUM_REGISTRY` gets exit code 2 with "PODIUM_REGISTRY is required" instead of a server that resolves `http://127.0.0.1:8080` from the bootstrapped `sync.yaml`.

The CLI does perform this fallback: cmd/podium/main.go:204-209 reads `sync.ReadConfig(ws)` and applies `sync.ResolveRegistryPath` when `--registry` and `PODIUM_REGISTRY` are unset. The `pkg/sync` helpers already exist (`ReadConfig`, `Defaults.Registry`, `ResolveRegistryPath` in pkg/sync/config.go:31-32, 64, 99). Suggested direction: in `loadConfig()`, when `PODIUM_REGISTRY` is empty, resolve the registry from `sync.yaml` before erroring, consulting at minimum the user-global `~/.podium/sync.yaml` scope that the standalone recipe relies on (the §7.5.2 precedence list also includes `<workspace>/.podium/sync.local.yaml` and `<workspace>/.podium/sync.yaml`). Only error when the value is unset across all scopes, and surface `config.no_registry` per §6.10/§13.11.2 rather than a bare "required" message.

### - [ ] F-6.11.2 — Package doc comment claims flag support the binary does not provide [Info] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The `cmd/podium-mcp` package doc comment states "Configuration (env vars; flags also supported by the launcher)" (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:10). `main()` calls `loadConfig()`, which reads only `os.Getenv` values and parses no command-line flags (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:51-66, 93-135). The §6.11 recipes are env-var-only and explicitly "reuse the same env-var contract from §6.2" (§6.11 line 258), so this does not break any recipe in this subsection; the flag claim is a documentation-comment artifact and the broader "`--flag` equivalents are accepted" statement belongs to §6.2. Suggested direction: either remove the "flags also supported by the launcher" clause from the doc comment, or implement flag parsing if the §6.2 contract is intended to hold for this binary. Recorded as Info because no §6.11 recipe depends on flags.
## F-7.1 — 7.1 The Registry: Podium Server or Local Filesystem (latency SLOs)

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md against the implementation._

Section 7.1 makes a small number of concrete claims: the registry is reachable as a Podium server over HTTP/JSON or as a local filesystem directory; the Podium CLI reads the filesystem directly via `podium sync`; the dispatch between the two is governed by `defaults.registry` in the merged `sync.yaml` such that a URL routes to a server and a filesystem path routes to the filesystem; both modes apply layer composition; the MCP server, the SDKs, and identity-based visibility filtering require a server source; and a set of latency SLO targets applies to the server source. The server applies layer composition and visibility filtering in `pkg/registry/core/core.go`, the filesystem source applies composition through `pkg/registry/filesystem` and `pkg/sync`, and the MCP and SDK consumers reach a server over HTTP, so most claims hold. Two issues surfaced: the URL-to-server dispatch principle is not honored by the `podium sync` consumer named in this section, and no latency instrumentation exists to observe the stated SLO targets.

### - [ ] F-7.1.1 — `podium sync` does not route a URL `defaults.registry` to a Podium server [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 7.1 line 10 states the dispatch principle: "The dispatch between them is governed by the value of `defaults.registry` in the merged `sync.yaml` (§7.5.2): a URL routes to a Podium server, a filesystem path routes to local filesystem." Line 8 names `podium sync` as the consumer that reads the filesystem source directly. The helper `sync.ResolveRegistryPath` (`pkg/sync/config.go:68`) is documented to pass URLs through unchanged "so the caller can distinguish filesystem from server source by inspecting the scheme," and `TestResolveRegistryPath_URLPassesThrough` (`pkg/sync/config_resolve_test.go:33`) asserts that behavior. No caller performs the dispatch for sync. `syncCmd` (`cmd/podium/main.go:204-225`) resolves `defaults.registry` and passes the value straight into `sync.Options.RegistryPath`, and `sync.Run` (`pkg/sync/sync.go:90`) calls `filesystem.Open(opts.RegistryPath)` unconditionally with no scheme check. `filesystem.Open` (`pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:107-118`) runs `filepath.Abs` then `os.Stat` on the value. A server URL therefore never reaches an HTTP client; the `pkg/sync` package contains no HTTP client at all. Reproduced directly: `ResolveRegistryPath("/ws", "https://podium.acme.com")` returns `https://podium.acme.com`, and `filesystem.Open` on that value returns `filesystem: registry path does not exist: <cwd>/https:/podium.acme.com` because `filepath.Abs` collapses the URL into a relative path under the working directory. The CLI then prints `sync failed: <that error>`. This contradicts the dispatch principle in 7.1 (and the detailed dispatch in §7.5.2, which states the MCP server and SDKs require a server source while implying sync also accepts one). The MCP and SDK paths handle server sources through their own HTTP clients, so the principle is satisfied for those consumers; only the `podium sync` consumer named in 7.1 is affected. Suggested direction: in `syncCmd` (or `sync.Run`), branch on the registry scheme using the existing `http://`/`https://` detection, and either route to a server-backed sync path or, until that path exists, fail with the canonical error rather than a mangled filesystem path. The `--registry` flag help and the error string at `cmd/podium/main.go:188` and `:211` currently claim the flag is a filesystem path only, which compounds the mismatch with the documented dispatch.

### - [ ] F-7.1.2 — No instrumentation exists to observe the section 7.1 latency SLO targets [Info] — OPEN

(gap) The "Latency budgets (SLO targets, server source)" sub-subsection (lines 14-22) lists p99 targets for `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact`, and directs that "Server deployments that miss these should investigate." A repository-wide search finds no latency instrumentation: no metrics endpoint, no histograms or percentile tracking, no per-request duration timing or access logging in `pkg/registry/server/server.go` or `internal/serverboot`, and no metrics or telemetry dependency in `go.mod` (no Prometheus, OpenTelemetry, or expvar). Without any timing surface, an operator has no way to determine whether the stated SLOs are met, which makes the "should investigate" directive unactionable. The section frames these as monitoring targets rather than a behavioral contract the server must implement, so this is recorded as an observation rather than a defect. Suggested direction: if observability against these targets is intended, add per-handler request-duration recording (latency histogram or at minimum structured access logs with elapsed time) keyed by operation name so deployments can compare against the budgets.
## F-7.2 — 7.2 Control Plane / Data Plane Split

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md against the implementation (re-run against main e41f44e)._

Section 7.2 defines two surfaces: a control plane (HTTP API) that returns metadata under the caller's OAuth identity with visibility filtering, and a data plane (object storage) that holds bundled resources. The concrete contracts are the 256 KB inline cutoff, returning resources below the cutoff inline, returning presigned URLs for resources above the cutoff, and never streaming large bytes through the control plane. The inline/large split logic, the cutoff constant, the presigned-URL response field, the S3 and filesystem object-store backends, and the data-plane visibility re-check exist and are unit-tested in `pkg/objectstore` and `pkg/registry/server`. They are wired only through the `server.NewFromFilesystem` constructor, which has no non-test caller. Neither shipping binary reaches that code, so the data-plane split is non-functional at runtime. All five prior findings remain open on main. None resolved against main. F-7.2.1 is corrected: the prior run cited a doc comment in `pkg/registry/server/layer_visibility.go` (a feature-branch file that is absent on main) and cited a `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` ingest block at stale line numbers; the standalone ingest now lives in `bootstrapLayerPath` and likewise omits bundled-resource capture. The other four findings are refreshed to current line numbers.

### - [x] F-7.2.1 — Bundled resources are never delivered by the running server; the data-plane split is unreachable in both binaries [High] — CLOSED

(gap) Section 7.2 requires `load_artifact` to return bundled resources: inline when below the 256 KB cutoff, and as presigned URLs into object storage when above it ("Below the inline cutoff, resources are returned inline"; "`load_artifact` returns presigned URLs that the Podium MCP server fetches directly from object storage", spec lines 30-32). The inline/large split is implemented only in `server.NewFromFilesystem` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:191-256`), which populates `s.resources` (inline) and calls `uploadLargeResources` to fill `s.largeResources` (presigned). Both production entrypoints (`cmd/podium-server/main.go:19` and `cmd/podium serve` at `cmd/podium/serve.go:49`) call `serverboot.Run`, which constructs the server with `server.New(registry, bootOpts...)` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:317`). `server.New` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:171-184`) never sets `s.resources` or `s.largeResources`, and `bootstrapOptions` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:664-675`) wires only public mode and the object store, with webhooks, mode, SCIM, and the quota limiter appended afterward in `Run` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:299-316`); none of these populate bundled resources. The `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` / `--layer-path` standalone bootstrap runs through `bootstrapLayerPath` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:156-203`), which ingests metadata into the store and persists a `store.LayerConfig` per layer but never captures bundled resources; its own comment says it "Mirrors server.NewFromFilesystem for the pieces needed for search and load_artifact" (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:227`), and the resource-capture pieces are not among them. A repo-wide search confirms `NewFromFilesystem` has no non-test caller: the only references are doc comments in `server.go` (lines 36, 186), the mirroring comment in `serverboot.go:227`, the test harness `internal/testharness/registryharness/registryharness.go:35`, and `pkg/registry/server/large_resources_test.go`. The result is that a server started by `podium serve` or `podium-server` returns the manifest body and frontmatter from `handleLoadArtifact` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:660-715`) but returns no inline `resources` and no `large_resources`, because both maps are empty. The §7.2 data-plane split therefore does not function in either shipping binary. Suggested direction: in `serverboot.Run`, after `bootstrapLayerPath`, populate `s.resources` and run the large-resource upload against the configured object store (reuse `uploadLargeResources` and the strip logic from `NewFromFilesystem`), or refactor `NewFromFilesystem`'s resource-wiring into a shared helper that `serverboot.Run` also calls.

**Resolution (9ccda56):** `serverboot.Run` now opens the object store before ingest and threads a `ResourcePut` seam into `bootstrapLayerPath` and `bootstrapDeclaredLayers`, so bundled resources persist as artifacts ingest; `handleLoadArtifact` serves them from the per-request core load result rather than a construction-time cache, so both shipping binaries deliver the §7.2 inline/large split. The construction-time `s.resources`/`s.largeResources` caches and the dead `resourceFunc`/`WithResources`/`uploadLargeResources` path are removed. Verified end-to-end through the real `podium serve` binary (e2e T-D-bundled-resources-7/8/38/39/51, browsing-27, handling-responses-23, hooks-35, all unskipped).

### - [x] F-7.2.2 — Ingest hashes bundled resource bytes and then discards them; nothing persists resources for later retrieval [High] — CLOSED

(bug) Section 7.2 states the registry "holds bundled resources" in the data plane and serves them via `load_artifact`. The production ingest path reads each bundled resource into `rec.Resources` (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:666-689`) and folds the bytes into the content hash (`contentHashOf`, `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:719-734`), but `manifestRecordFor` (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:692-717`) persists only `Frontmatter` and `Body` into `store.ManifestRecord`. The `store.ManifestRecord` type (`pkg/store/store.go`) has no resources field, and the ingest package contains no reference to `objectstore` at all, so resources are never uploaded to the configured object store either. The resource bytes are read, hashed, and discarded. `core.LoadArtifactResult` declares a `Resources` field (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:711`), but `resultFromRecord` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:998-1012`) never assigns it, so `core.LoadArtifact` always returns `Resources == nil`. Even if F-7.2.1 were fixed for the `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` standalone bootstrap, artifacts ingested through the normal ingest pipeline (the webhook and reingest paths described in §7.3.1) would still have no retrievable resources. Suggested direction: persist bundled resources at ingest by uploading every resource to the object store keyed by its content hash (small ones can also stay inline in the store, or be re-read on load), and have `core.LoadArtifact` populate `LoadArtifactResult.Resources` and a large-resource reference list from that persisted state so the HTTP layer can serve them.

**Resolution (9ccda56):** `manifestRecordFor` now builds a `store.ResourceRef` per bundled file (path, content hash, size, content type) and ingest persists it on `ManifestRecord.Resources`. Small resources keep their bytes inline on the record; large ones upload to the object store via the new `ResourcePut` seam (keyed by content hash, §4.4 dedup) and drop their inline copy. The SQLite and Postgres backends gained a `resources` JSON column (covered by the `ResourcesRoundTrip` conformance case), and `core.LoadArtifact` returns the refs via `resultFromRecord`/`mergeChain`.

### - [x] F-7.2.3 — `handleLoadArtifact` ignores `core.LoadArtifactResult.Resources`; resource delivery depends entirely on a server-construction-time cache [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) Section 7.2 frames resource delivery as a property of `load_artifact`. In the implementation, `handleLoadArtifact` builds its inline `resources` map exclusively from `s.resources` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:692-697`) and never reads `res.Resources` returned by `core.LoadArtifact` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:671-673`). The `core.LoadArtifactResult.Resources` field (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:711`) is the natural place for the core load path to return per-request resources, yet the HTTP layer bypasses it in favor of a map snapshotted once at construction time. The batch path `loadOneForBatch` (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:76-100`) also omits resources entirely, so `/v1/artifacts:batchLoad` returns no resources at all. There is a `ResourceFunc` SPI (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:98`) with a `WithResources` option (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:117-120`) intended to supply bundled bytes on demand, but `s.resourceFunc` is only ever assigned (the `WithResources` setter and `NewFromFilesystem` at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:236`) and never invoked; a repo-wide search finds no `s.resourceFunc(` call site, so this hook is dead. The combination couples resource delivery to the construction path rather than to the load operation, and it is the mechanism by which F-7.2.1 silently drops resources for `server.New`-constructed servers. Suggested direction: have `handleLoadArtifact` and `loadOneForBatch` prefer `res.Resources` (populated by core per F-7.2.2) for the inline set and derive `large_resources` from a core-provided reference list, reducing the load path to a single source of truth; either wire `resourceFunc` into the handler or remove the dead option.

**Resolution (9ccda56):** `handleLoadArtifact` and `loadOneForBatch` now build their resource sets from `res.Resources` (the core load result) via a shared `attachResources` helper that splits at `objectstore.InlineCutoff`. The construction-time `s.resources`/`s.largeResources` maps and the dead `ResourceFunc`/`WithResources` option are deleted. The batch endpoint returns the §7.6.2 presigned `resources` array (new `BatchResource` type) instead of nothing.

### - [x] F-7.2.4 — The `/objects/{key}` data-plane route buffers each resource fully in memory [Low] — CLOSED

(bug) Section 7.2 describes the data plane as the surface for bundled resources up to the documented sizes (§7.1 references resources up to 10 MB at spec line 20). The filesystem-backed data-plane route reads the entire object into a `[]byte` via `objectstore.Filesystem.Get` (`os.ReadFile`, `pkg/objectstore/filesystem.go:87-96`) and writes it in a single `w.Write(body)` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:755-773`); the S3 backend's `Get` likewise does `io.ReadAll` over the object (`pkg/objectstore/s3.go:76-85`). For the filesystem standalone deployment (§13.10), `/objects/{key}` is the actual fetch path for every large resource, so each concurrent fetch buffers the full resource (potentially multiple megabytes) in server memory. HEAD requests still call `Get` and read the whole body before discarding it; only the final write is skipped for HEAD (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:755-773`). The `Provider.Get` signature (`pkg/objectstore/objectstore.go:57-58`) returns `[]byte`, which forces full buffering. This is a robustness and memory-pressure concern rather than a spec violation. Suggested direction: add a streaming read to the `Provider` SPI (for example an `io.ReadCloser`-returning method) and stream bytes to the response writer; short-circuit HEAD so it reports size without reading the body.

**Resolution (9ccda56):** The `objectstore.Provider` SPI gained `GetStream` (returns an `io.ReadCloser` plus `ObjectInfo`) and `Stat` (size/content type without a read), implemented for the Memory, Filesystem, and S3 backends. `handleObjectsRoute` streams the body via `io.Copy` on GET and answers HEAD from `Stat` (size in `Content-Length`, no body read). Visibility is re-checked per fetch via the new `core.ResolveResourceOwner` (by content hash) instead of the removed construction-time `largeResources` map.

### - [x] F-7.2.5 — Large-resource link field is named `url`, while the §7.6.2 batch example uses `presigned_url` [Info] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) Section 7.2 describes the data-plane reference generically as a presigned URL and does not pin a wire field name. The `load_artifact` response models each large-resource reference as `LargeResourceLink` with JSON field `url` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:437-442`). The §7.6.2 batch-load example in the same spec file shows large resources under `resources` with a `presigned_url` field (spec lines 562-564). The two consumer paths therefore use different field names for the same concept. This is outside the strict text of §7.2 (which names no field), and the batch endpoint currently returns no resources at all (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:76-100`, per F-7.2.3), so this is recorded as an observation for the §4.4 and §7.6.2 owners to reconcile rather than a §7.2 defect. Suggested direction: settle on one field name for presigned resource references across `load_artifact` and the batch endpoint, and align the spec examples with the chosen name.

**Resolution (9ccda56):** Standardized on `presigned_url`, the only field name the spec pins (§7.6.2 batch example). `LargeResourceLink` (load_artifact), the new `BatchResource` (batch), and the MCP bridge's `largeResourceLink` all use it; the `url` JSON tag is gone. The spec is read-only and already uses `presigned_url`, so no spec change was needed; the `docs_http_api` e2e tests were updated to the conformant name.
## F-7.3 — 7.3 Host Integration (7.3.1 Authoring and Ingestion, 7.3.2 Outbound Webhooks)

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md against the implementation (re-run against main e41f44e)._

I re-checked the authoring and ingestion flow (the new `podium artifact scaffold` command, ingest triggers, ingest cases, the layer CLI, user-defined layer rules, the startup layer bootstrap, and ingest error codes) and the outbound webhook surface (event set, payload schema, retries, secrets, and CRUD). The merge added a filesystem-only `podium artifact scaffold` that produces lint-clean ARTIFACT.md/SKILL.md files for every §4.3 first-class type; it matches the §7.3.1 sentence and has no findings. The merge also added the standalone layer bootstrap (`PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` / `--layer-path`), which ingests a filesystem registry at startup and persists a `local`-source `LayerConfig` per resolved layer, so `GET /v1/layers`, `DELETE /v1/layers`, and `POST /v1/layers/reingest` now resolve the bootstrap layers. The bootstrap resolves the addressability premise behind one prior finding but runs the plain `ingest.Ingest` with no event publisher, no audit emitter, and no force-push handling. None of the ten prior findings were fully resolved by the merge; one (F-7.3.4) is partially addressed and restated below. All ten remain open with refreshed citations.

### - [ ] F-7.3.1 — Outbound webhook payload omits required `trace_id` and `actor` fields [High] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.3.2 defines the outbound webhook body schema as `{event, trace_id, timestamp, actor, data}` (spec lines 111-119). The delivery worker marshals only `{event, timestamp, data}` (`pkg/webhook/webhook.go:120-124`); `trace_id` and `actor` never appear in the POST body. The server-side publish path that feeds the worker cannot supply them either: `Server.PublishEvent` discards its `ctx` argument (`pkg/registry/server/events.go:174-191`, with the trailing line `_ = fmt.Sprintf("%v", ctx) // ctx reserved for future trace_id propagation`) and never sets an actor, and the ingest emission seam `EventEmitter func(eventType string, data map[string]any)` (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:244`) has no parameter for either field. The internal `/v1/events` stream type `registryEvent` declares `TraceID` and `Actor` fields (`pkg/registry/server/events.go:50-56`) but `PublishEvent` populates only `Event`, `Timestamp`, and `Data` (`pkg/registry/server/events.go:185-189`), and the outbound worker uses a separate marshal path that omits both regardless. No test asserts these keys. Receivers that key on `trace_id` for correlation or `actor` for attribution get neither. Suggested direction: thread a trace identifier and actor descriptor through `EventEmitter`/`PublishEvent` and include both keys in the worker's marshaled body (emit `actor` even as an empty object so the schema stays stable).

### - [ ] F-7.3.2 — Inbound Git-provider webhook endpoint does not exist [High] — OPEN

(gap) §7.3.1 specifies the built-in `git` source trigger: the Git provider fires a webhook to the registry, "The registry validates the webhook signature, fetches the new commit, ingests" (spec line 62), and `podium layer register` "returns the webhook URL and HMAC secret to register on the source repo" (spec line 93). The register handler advertises `WebhookURL = "/v1/layers/" + cfg.ID + "/webhook"` and returns the generated `WebhookSecret` (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:269-273`), but no HTTP route serves that path. The layer mux registers only `/v1/layers`, `/v1/layers/reorder`, `/v1/layers/reingest`, and `/v1/layers/update` (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:90-108`), and `serverboot` mounts that handler at `/v1/layers/` without a per-layer webhook route (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:343-344`).
