The `/v1/webhooks` and `/v1/webhooks/` routes that do exist are the outbound-receiver CRUD endpoints (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:328-329`), unrelated to inbound delivery. A Git provider POSTing to the advertised URL receives a 404. The inbound signature verifier in `pkg/layer/webhook/webhook.go` (GitHub, GitLab, and Bitbucket `Verify`, mapping failures to `ingest.webhook_invalid`) is fully implemented and tested but has no production importer (a repo-wide search for imports of `pkg/layer/webhook` returns only the package's own files), so the webhook-trigger ingest path has no end-to-end wiring and `ingest.webhook_invalid` is never surfaced over HTTP. Suggested direction: add a `/v1/layers/{id}/webhook` handler that looks up the layer's `WebhookSecret`, verifies the signature via the appropriate `pkg/layer/webhook` provider, and drives the ingest pipeline (see F-7.3.4) on success.

### - [ ] F-7.3.3 — `domain.published` outbound event is never emitted [High] — OPEN

(gap) §7.3.2 lists `domain.published` as an outbound webhook event: "a `DOMAIN.md` was added or changed" (spec lines 105). The only references to this event in the codebase are the audit-event constant `EventDomainPublished = "domain.published"` (`pkg/audit/audit.go:36`) and the retention configuration that lists it (`internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go:73`). Nothing publishes it: the ingest pipeline emits `artifact.published` and `artifact.deprecated` (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:496-509`), and the orchestrator emits `layer.ingested` and `layer.history_rewritten` (`pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:104-149`), but there is no `PublishEvent("domain.published", ...)` call anywhere, and the DOMAIN.md merge path (`pkg/domain`) does not emit change events. Downstream receivers subscribed to `domain.published` never receive a delivery when a `DOMAIN.md` is added or changed. Suggested direction: detect `DOMAIN.md` additions and changes during ingest and call `PublishEvent("domain.published", ...)` with the domain path and layer.

### - [ ] F-7.3.4 — Manual reingest endpoint records intent but never runs the ingest pipeline [High] — OPEN

(gap) §7.3.1 defines manual reingest as a trigger that "forces a fresh snapshot regardless of the trigger model" (spec line 65) and the ingest cases table requires that reingest hash and store new content, reject same-version content conflicts as `ingest.immutable_violation`, reject lint failures, and honor freeze windows (spec lines 73-79). The `reingest` handler returns `{queued, queued_at}` without invoking any ingest logic; its comment still states "The actual ingest pipeline runs externally; this endpoint records the intent... the pipeline integration lands when the standalone server's ingest scheduler ships" (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:378-407`). The pipeline driver `SourceIngestWithOptions` requires a `source.Provider` (`pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:74-80`), and `pkg/layer/source` has no production importer (a repo-wide search returns only the package and its tests), so no source provider is wired in `serverboot`, and there is no ingest scheduler or poller in `internal/serverboot/`. The merge changed the addressability premise of this finding: `bootstrapLayerPath` now persists a `local`-source `LayerConfig` per bootstrapped layer (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:182-193`), so `GetLayerConfig` resolves the layer and the reingest handler reaches its stub success path instead of 404. The §13.12 spec text and the serverboot comment claim the bootstrap layers are addressable by `POST /v1/layers/reingest`, which is now true, but the endpoint still performs no ingest. This is sharper for `local` layers: §7.3.1 line 56 names `podium layer reingest <id>` as the sole re-ingest trigger after an author edits a `local` layer in place, and that trigger is a no-op, so an edited bootstrap `local` layer can never be re-snapshotted. Suggested direction: have the reingest handler resolve the layer's source provider and run `SourceIngestWithOptions` (with the wired linter, signer, embedder, audit emitter, and `PublishEvent`), returning the result summary.

### - [x] F-7.3.5 — User-defined layer cap (default 3 per identity) is not enforced [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) §7.3.1 states "Default cap: 3 user-defined layers per identity, configurable per tenant" and the Errors paragraph lists "quota exhaustion (`quota.*`, including the user-defined-layer cap)" (spec lines 95, 97). The register handler creates user-defined layers with no per-identity count check (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:201-274`); it only computes an ordering value (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:247-252`). The ingest pipeline enforces a storage quota and an artifact-count quota (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:389-419`), but no code counts user-defined layers per owner or returns a `quota.*` error when the cap is exceeded. A repo-wide search finds no per-identity layer cap. An authenticated user can register an unbounded number of user-defined layers. Suggested direction: before persisting a user-defined layer in `register`, count existing `LayerConfig` rows with the same `Owner` and reject with a `quota.*` error code once the configured cap (default 3) is reached.

**Resolution (commit `39d402d`):** Closed by the canonical fix F-1.4.1. `LayerEndpoint.register` now counts the registrant's existing user-defined `LayerConfig` rows by `Owner` and returns `quota.layer_count_exceeded` at HTTP 429 once the configured cap (default 3, per-tenant `store.Quota.MaxUserLayers` / `PODIUM_MAX_USER_LAYERS`) is reached.

### - [ ] F-7.3.6 — `last_ingested_at` is not exposed per layer [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §7.3.1 states "`last_ingested_at` is exposed per layer for staleness monitoring" (spec line 67). The store `LayerConfig` carries `LastIngestedRef` (the commit SHA of the last successful ingest), `ForcePushPolicy`, and `CreatedAt`, but no `LastIngestedAt` timestamp (`pkg/store/store.go:99-127`). The layer list endpoint returns `LayerConfig` rows directly (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:278-285`), so the listed layers expose `last_ingested_ref` but never a `last_ingested_at` timestamp. The new bootstrap path sets neither (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:182-190` populates `CreatedAt` only), and the orchestrator updates `LastIngestedRef` without a companion timestamp (`pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:157`). A repo-wide search finds no `last_ingested_at` field or `LastIngestedAt` Go identifier. Operators cannot read the last-ingest time for staleness monitoring as the spec promises. Suggested direction: add a `LastIngestedAt time.Time` field to `LayerConfig`, set it when an ingest cycle completes (alongside the existing `LastIngestedRef` update), and serialize it as `last_ingested_at` in the layer list response.

### - [ ] F-7.3.7 — `force_push_policy` cannot be set through the layer API, CLI, or config [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §7.3.1 says force-push handling is "Tolerant by default" and "Strict mode is configurable per layer (`force_push_policy: strict` rejects)" (spec line 78). The store persists `ForcePushPolicy` (`pkg/store/store.go:121-125`; columns at `pkg/store/sqlite.go:113` and `pkg/store/postgres.go:120`) and the orchestrator reads it to choose strict versus tolerant behavior (`pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:94-118`). No interface lets an operator set it: `LayerRegisterRequest` has no `force_push_policy` field (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:65-79`), the `update` handler does not copy one (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:120-180`), the `register` handler never assigns it (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:208-223`), the new bootstrap path leaves it unset (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:182-190`), the `podium layer register` and `podium layer update` CLIs expose no corresponding flag (`cmd/podium/layer.go`), and no YAML layer-config key sets it. The field is therefore always the empty string (tolerant), and the spec-promised per-layer strict policy is unreachable. Suggested direction: add a `force_push_policy` field to the register and update request bodies (and a CLI flag), validate it against `{"", "tolerant", "strict"}`, and persist it into `LayerConfig`.

### - [ ] F-7.3.8 — Concurrent webhook deliveries race on the persisted failure counter [Medium] — OPEN

(bug) `Server.PublishEvent` launches a fresh goroutine that calls `Worker.Deliver` for every event (`pkg/registry/server/events.go:178-184`). `Deliver` reads the full receiver list via `Store.List`, and for each matching receiver mutates a local copy's `FailureCount`/`LastDelivery`/`LastFailure`/`Disabled` and writes it back with `Store.Put` (`pkg/webhook/webhook.go:128-152`). When two events fire close together, two `Deliver` calls run concurrently against the same tenant; each loads the same starting `FailureCount` and writes back its own result, so one update is lost (read-modify-write without a per-receiver lock or atomic increment in the store). The auto-disable threshold (32 consecutive failures, spec §7.3.2 and `pkg/webhook/webhook.go:112-115`) can therefore be reached late, or a success from one delivery can clobber a concurrent failure's increment. The per-event goroutines are also unbounded and use `context.Background()` (`pkg/registry/server/events.go:182`), so a slow or hung receiver leaves goroutines and in-flight HTTP requests outstanding with no cap. Suggested direction: serialize per-receiver state updates (a store-side atomic counter increment, or a single delivery worker draining a queue) so concurrent events do not lose failure-count updates, and bound the number of concurrent delivery goroutines.

### - [ ] F-7.3.9 — `podium layer reingest` CLI lacks `--break-glass` and `--justification` [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The §7.3.1 layer CLI lists `podium layer reingest <id> [--break-glass --justification <text>]` (spec line 89), and the freeze-window ingest case is bypassable only "unless `--break-glass` passed via the manual reingest path" (spec line 77). The `layerReingest` command defines no `--break-glass` or `--justification` flag and POSTs a nil body to `/v1/layers/reingest?id=ID` (`cmd/podium/layer.go:301-324`); the reingest handler reads no request body (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:383-407`). The break-glass machinery exists in the ingest pipeline (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:67-90` and `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:323-343`, requiring a justification and two distinct approvers, emitting a `freeze.break_glass` audit event), but it is unreachable from the manual reingest CLI path the spec names. An operator cannot break a freeze window through `podium layer reingest`. This gap is compounded by F-7.3.4 (the endpoint does not run the pipeline at all). Suggested direction: add `--break-glass` and `--justification` flags to `layerReingest`, send them in the reingest request body, and have the handler pass the break-glass grant into the ingest pipeline.

### - [ ] F-7.3.10 — `artifact.deprecated` fires on first publish of a deprecated manifest, not only on a flip [Info] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.3.2 describes `artifact.deprecated` as "a manifest update flipped `deprecated: true`" (spec line 104), which reads as a transition from not-deprecated to deprecated. The ingest pipeline emits `artifact.deprecated` whenever a newly accepted manifest has `deprecated: true`, including the first ingest of a `(artifact_id, version)` that is born deprecated (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:503-509`). Because `(artifact_id, version)` is immutable, a within-version flip is impossible, so any deprecation is necessarily a new version; emitting on first publish of a deprecated version is a defensible reading. This is recorded as an observation rather than a defect: confirm the intended semantics and align the spec wording or the emission condition if a strict transition (prior non-deprecated version of the same `artifact_id` existed) is desired.
## F-7.4 — 7.4 Degraded Network

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md against the implementation._

The degraded-network contract in §7.4 defines three `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE` behaviors when the registry is unreachable, an offline result envelope (`{status: "offline", served_from_cache: true}`), the structured error `network.registry_unreachable`, and a statement that `podium sync` and the SDKs apply the same cache modes. The MCP server implements the full contract for `load_artifact` only (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:317-351, resolution_cache.go). The discovery meta-tools (`load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`) ignore the cache mode entirely and surface raw transport errors. `offline-only` does not prevent registry contact for those meta-tools. `podium sync` (pkg/sync, cmd/podium) and both SDKs implement no cache-mode handling at all. The findings below are ordered from highest to lowest severity.

### - [ ] F-7.4.1 — Degraded-network fallback implemented only for load_artifact [High] — OPEN

(gap) §7.4 states "When the registry is unreachable, the MCP server falls back to its content cache" and that fresh calls in `always-revalidate` "return `{status: "offline", served_from_cache: true}` alongside cached results; if no cache, structured error `network.registry_unreachable`." The text scopes this to the MCP server generally, covering every meta-tool that contacts the registry. The implementation only wires this for `load_artifact` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:331-351). The other meta-tools dispatch through `proxyGet` (`load_domain`, `search_domains` at main.go:290-293) and `searchArtifacts` (main.go:294-295), both of which call `fetchJSON` and on error return `errorResult(err.Error())` (main.go:736 for proxyGet, search_artifacts.go:13-16). That path emits the raw transport error string (for example "connect: connection refused") with no `status: "offline"` field and no `network.registry_unreachable` code. A host that wants to detect offline state for a search or domain lookup, as the spec describes, receives no structured signal. Suggested direction: route `load_domain`, `search_domains`, and `search_artifacts` through the same degraded-network handling so an unreachable registry yields `network.registry_unreachable` (and, where a cache can serve, the offline envelope), or narrow §7.4 to state explicitly that only `load_artifact` participates in cache fallback.

### - [ ] F-7.4.2 — offline-only still contacts the registry for search and domain calls [High] — OPEN

(gap) §7.4 defines `offline-only` as "never contact the registry; structured error if cache miss." The cache-mode short-circuit that enforces this exists only inside `load_artifact` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:320, 326-328). The dispatch for `load_domain`, `search_domains`, and `search_artifacts` (main.go:289-301) performs no cache-mode check, so each calls `fetchJSON` and reaches out to the registry regardless of `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE`. In `offline-only` mode a `search_artifacts` or `load_domain` call therefore opens a network connection, directly contradicting "never contact the registry." There is no search-result or domain cache in the MCP server, so these operations have nothing local to serve, but the spec still forbids the network call. Suggested direction: in `offline-only` mode, gate the discovery meta-tools before `fetchJSON` and return a structured error (the offline-miss code) instead of attempting a request.

### - [ ] F-7.4.3 — podium sync and the SDKs do not apply cache modes [High] — OPEN

(gap) §7.4 ends with "`podium sync` and the SDKs apply the same cache modes." Neither does. In `pkg/sync`, `Run` only opens a filesystem-source registry via `filesystem.Open(opts.RegistryPath)` (pkg/sync/sync.go:90) and has no `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE`, content cache, or registry-unreachable fallback anywhere in the package. The CLI wrapper `syncCmd` (cmd/podium/main.go:177-240) reads no cache-mode flag or env var; the only reference to `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE` in the CLI is a display line in `cmd/podium/status.go:34`. The Python SDK's `Client.from_env` reads `PODIUM_REGISTRY`, `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER`, and `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` but not `PODIUM_CACHE_MODE` (sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:85-92), and a search of sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py and sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts for cache, offline, unreachable, or revalidate returns no matches. The cache-mode contract is consequently MCP-server-only. Suggested direction: either implement cache-mode handling (resolution cache, content cache, and the offline fallback) in `pkg/sync` and the SDK HTTP clients, or remove the sentence from §7.4 and document that cache modes apply to the MCP server alone.

### - [ ] F-7.4.4 — offline-first returns a raw error on cache-miss plus unreachable registry [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.4 describes `offline-first` as "no error; serve cached results silently." The implementation serves silently on a cache hit (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:320-325), but on a cache miss it falls through to `fetchJSON` (main.go:331); when the registry is then unreachable, the `always-revalidate` branch at main.go:337 is skipped and control reaches `return errorResult(err.Error())` at main.go:350. The caller therefore receives an error in `offline-first` mode, contradicting "no error." The error is also the raw transport string rather than a structured code. §6.5 describes `offline-first` as "use cached resolution and content if present; only call the registry on miss," which permits a registry call on miss and is in mild tension with §7.4's absolute "no error." The two sections should be reconciled. Suggested direction: decide the intended `offline-first` behavior on a cache miss with the registry down (silent empty result, or a structured `network.registry_unreachable`) and align both the code and §7.4 to it.

### - [ ] F-7.4.5 — offline-only cache-miss uses an undeclared error namespace (cache.offline_miss) [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.4 says `offline-only` returns a "structured error if cache miss" without naming a code. The implementation returns `errOfflineCacheMiss`, whose message is `cache.offline_miss: artifact not in offline cache` (cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go:142), and the comment maps it to "the §6.10 namespace." The §6.10 namespace list is `auth.*, config.*, ingest.*, materialize.*, quota.*, mcp.*, network.*, registry.*, domain.*` (spec/06-mcp-server.md:254) and does not include `cache.*`. The code's offline-miss therefore lives in a namespace the error model does not define. Suggested direction: either add `cache.*` to the §6.10 namespace list or move this code into an existing namespace (for example `network.offline_cache_miss`), and apply the same code consistently to the discovery meta-tools once F-7.4.2 is addressed.

### - [ ] F-7.4.6 — Integration test asserts a substring that the search path never emits [Low] — OPEN

(bug) `TestPodiumMCP_NetworkRegistryUnreachable` (test/integration/mcp_protocol_test.go:88-110) calls `search_artifacts` against a closed port and its comment claims "the MCP bridge surfaces network.registry_unreachable in the tool-call result." The assertion only checks that stdout contains one of `connect`, `refused`, or `reachable` (lines 105-108). The `search_artifacts` path returns the raw transport error (search_artifacts.go:13-16), which contains "connect"/"refused" but never the `network.registry_unreachable` code, because that code is only added in the `load_artifact` always-revalidate branch (main.go:348). The test passes on the raw error and gives false confidence that the §7.4 structured-error contract holds for search. Suggested direction: once F-7.4.1 routes search through the degraded-network handler, tighten the assertion to require the literal `network.registry_unreachable`; until then, correct the comment so it does not claim coverage the test does not provide.
## F-7.5 — 7.5 podium sync (7.5.1 Scope Filters, 7.5.2 sync.yaml, 7.5.3 sync.lock, 7.5.4 Watch/Toggle, 7.5.5 override, 7.5.6 save-as, 7.5.7 profile edit)

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md against the implementation._

The implementation in pkg/sync and cmd/podium covers a filesystem-source materialization core (walk, adapter, atomic lock write, stale-file cleanup, poll-based watch) plus standalone helpers for override toggles, save-as, and profile edit. Several spec-mandated parts of §7.5 are absent or diverge: scope filtering (`--include`/`--exclude`/`--type`) is implemented as a `ScopeFilter` type with unit tests but never wired into `sync.Run` or the CLI; profiles, `--config` multi-target, `--check`, multi-scope `sync.yaml` resolution (user-global / project-local), precedence, and the profile-collision warning do not exist on the sync path; server-source (URL) sync is not implemented; override and watch do not touch the target directory or apply toggles; the lock file's `profile`/`scope`/`last_synced_by` fields are not populated as specified; and the harness adapter is never resolved from `PODIUM_HARNESS` or the `sync.yaml` `harness` field, so a sync that omits `--harness` writes the canonical layout rather than the configured harness-native layout. Findings below.

### - [ ] F-7.5.1 — Scope filters (`--include`/`--exclude`/`--type`) never applied during sync [High] — OPEN

(gap) §7.5.1 defines three filters that narrow the materialized set, with `--include`/`--exclude` repeatable globs matched against canonical IDs and `--type` a comma-separated type list, and §7.5 shows `podium sync ... --include ... --exclude ...` and `podium sync --type skill,agent`. The package contains a complete `ScopeFilter` with `Apply` (pkg/sync/scope.go:27) and passing unit tests (pkg/sync/scope_test.go), but nothing calls it: a repo-wide search shows `ScopeFilter`/`.Apply` referenced only in scope.go and its test. `sync.Run` (pkg/sync/sync.go:72) walks the registry and adapts every record with no filtering, and `Options` (pkg/sync/sync.go:37) has no Include/Exclude/Types fields. The CLI `syncCmd` (cmd/podium/main.go:186) defines only `--registry`, `--target`, `--harness`, `--dry-run`, `--json`, `--watch`, `--overlay`; there are no `--include`, `--exclude`, or `--type` flags. Result: every documented scope-narrowing invocation silently materializes the full effective view. Suggested direction: add `Include/Exclude/Types` to `Options`, apply `ScopeFilter.Apply` to the walked records inside `Run` before adapting, and register the three flags (with `--type` comma-split) in `syncCmd`.

### - [ ] F-7.5.2 — `--profile`, `sync.yaml` profiles, and `--config` multi-target unimplemented on the sync path [High] — OPEN

(gap) §7.5 and §7.5.2 require `podium sync --profile <name>` (load a named scope from `profiles:`), `podium sync --config <path>` (iterate `targets:` and run one sync per entry), and resolution where a profile's fields merge on top of `defaults:` with CLI flags overriding. The `SyncConfig`/`Profile`/`TargetEntry` types exist (pkg/sync/config.go:24-57), but `sync.Run` never reads `sync.yaml` for scope or profile selection; the CLI only reads `defaults.registry` as a fallback when `--registry` is unset (cmd/podium/main.go:204-209) and defines no `--profile` or `--config` flag. There is no code that selects a profile, merges it onto defaults, or iterates `targets:`. Suggested direction: implement profile resolution (lookup under `profiles:`, merge onto `defaults:`, apply resulting include/exclude/type as the scope) and a multi-target loop for `--config`, each target writing its own lock per §7.5.2.

### - [ ] F-7.5.3 — Multi-scope `sync.yaml` resolution, precedence, env vars, and collision warning absent [High] — OPEN

(gap) §7.5.2 specifies reading `sync.yaml` from up to three scopes (user-global `~/.podium/sync.yaml`, project-shared `<ws>/.podium/sync.yaml`, project-local `<ws>/.podium/sync.local.yaml`), workspace discovery by walking up from CWD to find `.podium/` (mirroring how git finds `.git`), per-key precedence (CLI flags > `PODIUM_*` env > project-local > project-shared > user-global > defaults), additive profile merge with whole-profile overwrite on collision, and a stderr warning when invoking a colliding profile. The implementation reads only the single workspace file via `ReadConfig` (pkg/sync/config.go:99), which opens `<workspace>/.podium/sync.yaml` and nothing else. There is no walk-up discovery, no `sync.local.yaml` read, no merge across scopes, no `PODIUM_*` precedence for sync, and no collision detection or warning. Suggested direction: implement a resolver that discovers the workspace by walking up, loads all three scope files, merges per-key by the documented precedence (including env), and reports profile-name collisions.

### - [ ] F-7.5.4 — Server-source (URL) sync not implemented [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §7.5 states `podium sync` "works against either kind of registry source: a server (URL) or a local filesystem (path)" and that against a server source it "uses the same identity providers as the MCP server, the same content cache, and the same harness adapters"; §7.5.2 lists `podium sync` among the consumers that work when `defaults.registry` is a URL. `sync.Run` only calls `filesystem.Open(opts.RegistryPath)` (pkg/sync/sync.go:90) and has no HTTP client path; `hasURLScheme` exists (pkg/sync/config.go:87) but is used only by `ResolveRegistryPath` to pass URLs through unchanged. The CLI passes the URL string straight into `Run`, where `filesystem.Open` will fail on a URL, and the CLI error text hardcodes "--registry is required (filesystem path)" (cmd/podium/main.go:211). Result: a configured URL registry cannot be synced. Suggested direction: branch in `Run` (or the CLI) on `hasURLScheme` and drive an HTTP-source delivery path (identity, cache, batch load, adapter) for URL registries, or explicitly document and enforce filesystem-only with a clear error if URL sync is deferred.

### - [ ] F-7.5.5 — `podium sync override` does not materialize or delete files [High] — OPEN

(bug/gap) §7.5.5 requires batch override to act on the target directory: `--add <id>` "fetches and writes the artifact through the active harness adapter, just like a full sync would," and `--remove <id>` "deletes the artifact's materialized files from the target." `Override` (pkg/sync/override.go:47) only mutates the lock file's `toggles.add`/`toggles.remove` and writes the lock; it never opens the registry, runs an adapter, writes artifact files, or removes any files (a search of override.go finds no `materialize`, `Adapt`, `filesystem.Open`, or `os.Remove`). The CLI `syncOverrideCmd` (cmd/podium/main.go:282) likewise only prints the resulting toggle lists. Result: `podium sync override --add X` records a toggle but the artifact is never written to disk, and `--remove X` never deletes anything. Suggested direction: in `Override`, resolve and adapt the added IDs into the target (respecting visibility) and delete the materialized paths for removed IDs (using the lock's recorded `materialized_path`), updating the artifacts list accordingly.

### - [ ] F-7.5.6 — Watch mode does not apply toggles or re-resolve a profile [High] — OPEN

(bug/gap) §7.5.4 requires watch mode to materialize `profile + toggles from the lock file` on startup, and on every change event to "re-resolve the profile, apply toggles on top, and update the lock file," with toggles persisting across events and restarts; §7.5.5 states toggles "survive watcher events." The watcher (`runWatch`, pkg/sync/watch.go:69) simply re-invokes `sync.Run`, and `Run` never reads `toggles` from the lock (it builds a fresh `LockFile` at pkg/sync/sync.go:164 with no toggle handling) and never resolves a profile. A search of watch.go finds no `Toggle`/`profile`/`scope` references. Result: watch ignores any prior `toggles.add`/`toggles.remove`, and because each rerun writes a fresh lock, toggles recorded by `override` are dropped on the next watch event rather than reapplied. Suggested direction: have the watch path load the lock's toggles and active profile, materialize `profile + toggles`, and rewrite the lock preserving toggles on every event.

### - [ ] F-7.5.7 — `last_synced_by` written as `podium-sync`, not the documented `full | watch | override` [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.5.3 defines the lock field `last_synced_by: full # full | watch | override`. `sync.Run` writes the literal `"podium-sync"` (pkg/sync/sync.go:168) for every invocation, including watch reruns (watch calls the same `Run`). None of the three documented enum values is ever produced by the code path that actually writes the lock (only the lock_test fixture uses `"full"`). Result: consumers that key on the documented enum will not match. Suggested direction: write `full` for a manual one-shot sync, `watch` for watcher-driven reruns, and `override` for override-driven lock writes.

### - [ ] F-7.5.8 — `sync.Run` never populates the lock's `profile` and `scope`, breaking save-as and the active-profile default [High] — OPEN

(bug) §7.5.3 says the lock's `profile:` is the active profile that "`override`, `save-as`, and `profile edit` use as the default when no `--profile` flag is given," and the schema includes `scope: {include, exclude, type}` describing the resolved scope. `sync.Run` constructs the new lock with only `Target`, `Harness`, `LastSyncedAt`, `LastSyncedBy`, and the artifacts list (pkg/sync/sync.go:164-178); it leaves `Profile` empty and `Scope` empty. `SaveAs` reads `lock.Scope.Include/Exclude/Type` verbatim to build the profile (pkg/sync/override.go:176-178), so after a normal sync `save-as` always emits an empty include/exclude/type block (the override_test only passes because it hand-writes a lock with a populated `Scope`). The active-profile default for override/save-as/profile-edit can never resolve from the lock because `Profile` is never set. Suggested direction: once scope/profile resolution exists (F-7.5.1, F-7.5.2), have `Run` persist the resolved `Profile` and `Scope` into the lock so downstream commands and `save-as` see the real materialized scope.

### - [ ] F-7.5.9 — `--dry-run --json` envelope fields do not match the spec [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.5 specifies the `--json` dry-run envelope as `{profile, target, harness, scope, artifacts: [{id, version, type, layer}, ...]}`. `printJSON` (cmd/podium/main.go:825) emits `{adapter, target, artifacts: [{id, layer, files}]}`: it omits `profile`, `harness`, and `scope`; names the harness field `adapter`; and the per-artifact objects omit `version` and `type` while adding a non-spec `files` array. Result: a `jq` consumer following the documented schema (for example reading `.harness` or `.artifacts[].version`) gets nothing. Suggested direction: rename `adapter` to `harness`, add `profile` and `scope` (the resolved scope) and per-artifact `version` and `type`, and reconcile or document the extra `files` field.

### - [ ] F-7.5.10 — `podium sync --check` validation subcommand/flag missing [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §7.5.2 specifies `podium sync --check` to "validate the merged config against the schema and report unresolved profile references, malformed globs, target collisions, and profile-name collisions across scopes (warning, not error)." No `--check` flag is defined in `syncCmd` (cmd/podium/main.go:186) and there is no validation routine in pkg/sync that reports unresolved profile references, malformed globs, or target collisions. Suggested direction: add a `--check` flag that loads the merged config, validates profile references and globs, detects `targets:` id collisions and cross-scope profile-name collisions, and reports collisions as warnings.

### - [ ] F-7.5.11 — `podium profile edit` uses a `--profile` flag instead of the documented positional name, and never preserves comments/formatting [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.5.7 documents `podium profile edit finance-team --add-include "..."` (positional profile name) and `podium profile edit` with no name as an error, and states the command edits `sync.yaml` "preserving formatting and comments around the edited keys (round-trip via a comment-preserving YAML parser)." The implementation requires a `--profile` flag (cmd/podium/main.go:372,383); the documented positional form `podium profile edit finance-team` leaves `--profile` empty and exits 2. `ProfileEdit` rewrites the whole file with `WriteConfig` → `yaml.Marshal` (pkg/sync/config.go:121), which strips comments and reorders/normalizes formatting rather than round-tripping; the `SyncConfig` doc comment claims unknown fields and comments are preserved (pkg/sync/config.go:20-23), but a plain `yaml.v3` Marshal does not preserve either. Suggested direction: accept the profile name positionally (erroring with a name-required message when absent, matching the spec), and use a comment-preserving round-trip (for example `yaml.Node`) so existing comments and formatting survive the edit.

### - [ ] F-7.5.12 — `podium sync --profile`, the override TUI, and the profile-edit TUI are not provided [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §7.5 lists `podium sync --profile finance-team`; §7.5.5 specifies a no-flag TUI mode for `podium sync override` that renders the effective view as an expandable checklist; §7.5.7 specifies a no-flag/positional TUI for `podium profile edit`. The CLI provides no `--profile` flag on `sync` (cmd/podium/main.go:186), and both `syncOverrideCmd` (cmd/podium/main.go:282) and `profileCmd` (cmd/podium/main.go:355) implement only the batch flag paths with no interactive checklist; running `podium sync override` with no flags writes no toggles and just prints empty lists, and `podium profile edit` with no `--profile` exits 2. Suggested direction: add the `sync --profile` flag (see F-7.5.2) and implement (or explicitly defer with a clear message) the override and profile-edit TUI checklists described in §7.5.5 and §7.5.7.

### - [ ] F-7.5.13 — `podium sync` ignores `PODIUM_HARNESS` and the `sync.yaml` harness, always defaulting the adapter to `none` [High] — OPEN

(gap) §7.5.2 defines `harness` as a `sync.yaml` field (`defaults.harness`, line 230; per-target `harness` at lines 250 and 254) and resolves it per key in precedence order (lines 214-221: CLI flags, then `PODIUM_*` env vars, then project-local, then project-shared, then user-global, then built-in defaults), with the user-global scope holding the typical `harness` default (line 206) and §7.5.2 stating that a project pins `harness` by placing it in the project-shared file (line 210). The `podium sync` CLI honors only the `--harness` flag and the built-in default. `syncCmd` declares `harness := fs.String("harness", "none", ...)` (cmd/podium/main.go:191) and reads `sync.yaml` only for `cfg.Defaults.Registry` (cmd/podium/main.go:205-209); it never reads `cfg.Defaults.Harness` (declared at pkg/sync/config.go:33, with per-profile and per-target `Harness` at config.go:45 and config.go:51) and never consults `PODIUM_HARNESS`. A whole-file search of cmd/podium/main.go shows `os.Getenv` used only for `PODIUM_REGISTRY` (lines 490, 556, 582, 608, 657); `PODIUM_HARNESS` is read by `podium status` (cmd/podium/status.go:32) and by the separate MCP binary (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:100), never on the sync path. The resolved `AdapterID` therefore stays `"none"` for any invocation that omits `--harness`, so `sync.Run` selects the `None` adapter (pkg/sync/sync.go:85, pkg/adapter/none.go:20) and writes the canonical layout `<artifact-id>/ARTIFACT.md` and `<artifact-id>/SKILL.md` instead of the Claude Code layout `.claude/skills/<name>/SKILL.md` that `ClaudeCode.Adapt` produces (pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:34-44). A developer who selects Claude Code through the documented `PODIUM_HARNESS=claude-code` env var or a `defaults.harness: claude-code` entry in `sync.yaml` receives the canonical files with no error, while `podium status` reports `harness: claude-code` (cmd/podium/status.go:32) for the same environment the sync materializes as `none`. The harness documentation states the env-var path applies to sync: "The harness still needs `PODIUM_HARNESS` set (or `--harness <name>` on the sync command)" (docs/consuming/configure-your-harness.md:482). Suggested direction: change the `--harness` flag default to empty so an unset flag falls through, then resolve the adapter ID in the §7.5.2 precedence order (`--harness` when set, then `PODIUM_HARNESS`, then `cfg.Defaults.Harness` and the selected profile's or target's `Harness`, then `none`) before constructing `sync.Options`, mirroring the existing `defaults.registry` fallback at cmd/podium/main.go:205-209.
## F-7.6 — 7.6 Language SDKs (7.6.1 Read CLI, 7.6.2 Bulk Fetch)

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md against the implementation._

I checked the SDK surface (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts`), the read CLI subcommands (`cmd/podium/main.go`: `search`, `domain show`, `domain search`, `artifact show`), the bulk-fetch endpoint (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go`), and the backing handlers in `pkg/registry/server/server.go` and `pkg/registry/core/core.go`. The bulk-fetch wire format, the 50-ID cap, partial-failure handling, and `version_pins` are implemented and tested. Several documented surface elements are missing or diverge: the Python SDK reads the wrong field for `dependents_of` and the wrong query parameter for `subscribe`; the batch endpoint returns no resources or presigned URLs; the read CLI omits the `--tags`, `--version`, and `--session-id` flags and emits raw JSON instead of the documented human-readable rendering for domain and artifact output; `session_id` is absent from `search_artifacts` everywhere; the SDKs expose no `materialize` method; and the `visibility.denied` error code documented for batch load is never emitted on the wire.

### - [ ] F-7.6.1 — Python SDK `dependents_of` reads the wrong response field and decodes the wrong shape [High] — OPEN

(bug) The spec §7.6 lists `deps = client.dependents_of("finance/ap/pay-invoice@1.2")` as part of the SDK surface. The server's `/v1/dependents` handler returns `{"edges": [{"from", "to", "kind"}]}` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:600-606`). The Python SDK reads `body.get("dependents", [])` (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:213` and `:222`) and decodes each entry as an `ArtifactDescriptor` with `id`/`type`/`version`. Against the real server the `dependents` key is absent, so `dependents_of` always returns an empty list; even if the key matched, the edge fields (`from`, `to`, `kind`) do not map onto `ArtifactDescriptor`. The unit test `test_dependents_of_decodes_envelope` (`sdks/podium-py/tests/test_client.py:131-142`) masks the defect by stubbing `{"dependents": [...]}`, a response the server never produces. The TypeScript SDK reads `body.edges` and types them as `DependencyEdge` (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:211-216`), which matches the server. Suggested direction: change the Python SDK to read `body.get("edges", [])` and return edge objects (a `from`/`to`/`kind` dataclass) consistent with the TypeScript SDK and the server, and update the test fixture to the server's actual envelope.

### - [ ] F-7.6.2 — Bulk-load envelopes omit resources and presigned URLs [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The spec §7.6.2 wire format shows each batch envelope carrying `resources: [{path, presigned_url, content_hash}]` (lines 562-564) and states that "large bundled resources travel via presigned URLs (§4.4) so the response body stays small; the SDK fetches resources concurrently after the response" (line 580). The example also calls `result.materialize(to="./artifacts/")` (line 547). The `loadOneForBatch` implementation populates only manifest metadata and never sets resources (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:88-99`); the `BatchLoadEnvelope` struct has a `Resources map[string]string` field but no presigned-URL field at all (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:36`). By contrast the single `/v1/load_artifact` handler returns inline `resources` and `large_resources` presigned links (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:703-720`). A consumer cannot materialize anything from a batch response because no resource bytes or links are returned. Suggested direction: have `loadOneForBatch` populate inline resources and presigned `large_resources` the same way `handleLoadArtifact` does, and add the presigned-URL representation the spec example shows.

### - [ ] F-7.6.3 — `search_artifacts` does not accept `session_id` in the SDKs or the server [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The spec §7.6 documents the "Full filter surface: type, tags, scope, top_k, session_id" for `search_artifacts` and shows `client.search_artifacts("variance analysis", ..., session_id=session_id)` (lines 439-447). The Python `search_artifacts` accepts only `type`, `scope`, `tags`, `top_k` (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:118-126`); the TypeScript `searchArtifacts` accepts only `type`, `scope`, `tags`, `topK` (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:134-149`); the server handler reads only `query`, `type`, `scope`, `tags`, `top_k` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:566-577`); and `core.SearchArtifactsOptions` has no `SessionID` field (`pkg/registry/core/core.go`). The `session_id` filter argument is unimplemented end to end. Suggested direction: thread `session_id` through `SearchArtifactsOptions`, the `/v1/search_artifacts` handler, and both SDK signatures, or remove `session_id` from the §7.6 surface description if search is not session-scoped.

### - [ ] F-7.6.4 — Read CLI `podium search` is missing the `--tags` flag [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The spec §7.6.1 command table states that `podium search <query>` exposes flags "`--type`, `--tags`, `--scope`, `--top-k` mirror the SDK args" (line 481). The `searchCmd` implementation defines `--type`, `--scope`, `--top-k`, and `--json`, but no `--tags` (`cmd/podium/main.go:486-515`). The server already filters on a `tags` query parameter (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:567-570`), so a CLI user has no way to reach tag filtering despite the documented flag. Suggested direction: add a repeatable or comma-separated `--tags` flag to `searchCmd` and forward it as the `tags` query parameter.

### - [ ] F-7.6.5 — Read CLI `podium artifact show` is missing `--version` and `--session-id` [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The spec §7.6.1 command table for `podium artifact show <id>` states "Flags: `--version`, `--session-id`" (line 484). The `artifactShow` implementation defines only `--registry` and forwards a single `id` parameter (`cmd/podium/main.go:650-670`); neither `--version` nor `--session-id` is defined or sent. The server's `/v1/load_artifact` honors `version` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:683`) but does not read `session_id` at all (see F-7.6.6), so even adding the CLI flag would not produce session-consistent resolution on the single-load path. Suggested direction: add `--version` and `--session-id` flags to `artifactShow`; add `session_id` reading to the single `/v1/load_artifact` handler so the flag has an effect.

### - [ ] F-7.6.6 — Single `/v1/load_artifact` ignores `session_id` while batch load honors it [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The spec §7.6.1 documents `--session-id` for `podium artifact show` (which maps to `Client.load_artifact`), and §7.6.2 says batch load "honors the same `latest`-resolution semantics as load_artifact" (line 541), implying single load is session-aware. The core layer supports session-pinned latest resolution via `LoadArtifactOptions.SessionID` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:735-738`, `:816-829`), and the batch endpoint passes it through (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:79`). The single `handleLoadArtifact` constructs `LoadArtifactOptions` with only `Version` and never reads or forwards `session_id` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:682-684`). As a result, the single-load path cannot freeze `latest` per session, so single and batch load diverge on session consistency. Suggested direction: read `session_id` from the query in `handleLoadArtifact` and pass it as `LoadArtifactOptions.SessionID`, matching the batch path. The SDK `load_artifact` methods also need a `session_id` argument to exercise this.

### - [ ] F-7.6.7 — Batch load never emits the `visibility.denied` error code documented in §7.6.2 [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The spec §7.6.2 shows a per-item error envelope `"error": { "code": "visibility.denied", ... }` (line 568) and states "Items the caller cannot see come back as `status: "error"` with `visibility.denied`" (line 577). The core layer maps a visibility-filtered artifact to `ErrNotFound` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:762-774`), emitting `visibility.denied` only as an internal audit-event type. `errorEnvelopeFor` translates `ErrNotFound` to `registry.not_found` and has no `visibility.denied` case (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:103-113`), so both a missing artifact and a hidden artifact return `registry.not_found`. The `visibility.denied` string is never written as a wire error code anywhere in the codebase (confirmed by grep). The batch test even comments that hidden items return `visibility.denied` while asserting only `registry.not_found` (`pkg/registry/server/batch_load_test.go:76-108`). The §7.6.2 text is internally inconsistent here, because it also requires "no leak about whether the artifact exists in some hidden layer," which `registry.not_found` satisfies and `visibility.denied` would violate. Suggested direction: reconcile §7.6.2 with the non-leak behavior the code implements (drop the `visibility.denied` wire code from the batch example and prose), or, if a distinct code is intended, define how it avoids the existence leak the same section forbids.

### - [ ] F-7.6.8 — Python SDK `subscribe` sends `types` while the server reads `type` [Medium] — OPEN

(bug) The spec §7.6 shows `client.subscribe(["artifact.published", "artifact.deprecated"])` for streaming change events. The server's `/v1/events` handler reads repeated `type` query parameters (`r.URL.Query()["type"]`, `pkg/registry/server/events.go:136`). The TypeScript SDK appends one `type` parameter per event (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:229-231`), which matches. The Python SDK sends a single comma-joined `types` parameter (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:249-254`), which the server never reads, so the server applies no filter and streams every event type instead of the requested subset. The Python signature is also keyword-only (`subscribe(*, types=...)`) whereas the spec example passes a positional list, so the documented call form does not type-check. Suggested direction: change the Python SDK to append repeated `type` parameters matching the server and the TypeScript SDK, and accept the event-type list positionally to match the §7.6 example.

### - [ ] F-7.6.9 — SDKs expose no `materialize` method [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The spec §7.6 SDK surface shows `artifact.materialize(to="./artifacts/", harness="claude-code")` (line 461) and the §7.6.2 example shows `result.materialize(to="./artifacts/")` (line 547). The Python `LoadedArtifact` dataclass has no `materialize` method (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:53-62`), the bulk result is a plain `list[dict]` with no method, and the TypeScript `LoadedArtifact`/`BatchLoadEnvelope` are interfaces with no behavior (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:21-52`). A grep for `materialize` in both SDK trees returns nothing. Consumers cannot write artifacts to disk through the SDK as the spec example shows; they would have to reimplement the harness adapter themselves. Suggested direction: add a `materialize(to, harness)` method to the loaded-artifact and batch-result types in both SDKs that writes manifest plus resources through the harness adapter, or amend §7.6 to drop the `materialize` examples and direct consumers to `podium sync`.

### - [ ] F-7.6.10 — Read CLI default output for `domain show`, `domain search`, and `artifact show` is raw JSON, not the documented human-readable rendering [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The spec §7.6.1 "Output formats" states the default is "human-readable rendering": "domain trees are nested bullets; manifests are printed as the markdown body with frontmatter at the top" (line 488), with `--json` reserved for the structured envelope. `domainShow` prints the raw JSON body in both the `--json` and the default branch (`cmd/podium/main.go:595-601`). `domainSearch` has no `--json` flag at all and always prints the raw JSON body (`cmd/podium/main.go:604-628`), even though the spec documents a `domain search ... --json` schema (lines 498-503). `artifactShow` has no `--json` flag and always prints the raw JSON body (`cmd/podium/main.go:666-668`), so its default output is the structured envelope rather than the markdown body with frontmatter the spec specifies. Only `podium search` renders a human-readable table (`printSearchHuman`, `cmd/podium/main.go:801-822`). Suggested direction: add human-readable renderers for the domain and artifact commands (nested bullets for domains, frontmatter-plus-body for artifacts) and gate raw JSON behind a `--json` flag on each, including a `--json` flag for `domain search`.

### - [ ] F-7.6.11 — `podium search --json` and `domain show --json` envelopes diverge from the documented §7.6.1 schemas [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The spec §7.6.1 documents the read CLI `--json` schemas and states "output drift between them is treated as a bug" (line 520). The `podium search ... --json` schema shows result items as `{id, type, version, score, frontmatter}` (lines 493-496), but the read CLI forwards the server's `ArtifactDescriptor`, which carries `description` and `tags` and no `frontmatter` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:395-402`, `:834-843`). The `podium domain show <path> --json` schema shows notable items as `{id, type, summary, source: "featured|signal", folded_from}` (lines 508-512), but the server's `/v1/load_domain` renders notable items via the same `ArtifactDescriptor` (`description`, no `summary`, no `source`, no `folded_from`) at `pkg/registry/server/server.go:526`. Because the CLI prints the server body verbatim, the emitted JSON does not match the documented schema. Suggested direction: align the search descriptor and the domain notable-item descriptor with the §7.6.1 schemas (add `frontmatter` to search results; add `summary`, `source`, and `folded_from` to notable items), or correct the §7.6.1 schemas to the implemented field names. This overlaps the §4.5 domain surface and should be coordinated.

### - [ ] F-7.6.12 — MCP server does not use the batch-load endpoint for prefetch cache warm-up [Low] — OPEN

(gap) The spec §7.6.2 states "The MCP server uses this endpoint internally for cache warm-up when configured to prefetch" (line 582). A grep across `cmd/podium-mcp/` for `batchLoad`, `prefetch`, and `warm` returns nothing, and the only callers of `/v1/artifacts:batchLoad` are the two SDKs and the endpoint tests. No prefetch or warm-up wiring exists in the MCP bridge. Suggested direction: wire an optional prefetch path in the MCP server that calls `/v1/artifacts:batchLoad` for cache warm-up, or remove the claim from §7.6.2 since it describes behavior that is not present.

### - [ ] F-7.6.13 — SDKs and read CLI send no identity, contradicting the "same identity ... server-side" guarantee [Low] — OPEN

(gap) The spec §7.6 states "Identity providers, the cache, visibility filtering, layer composition, and audit are all the same as in the MCP path" and §7.6.1 states the read CLI "uses the same identity, cache, layer composition, and visibility filtering server-side" (line 477). The Python and TypeScript clients store an `identity_provider`/`identityProvider` value but never mint or attach a token; their requests send only `Content-Type` and no `Authorization` header (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:197-200`, `:266-276`; `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:185-189`, `:258-279`). The read CLI uses a bare `http.Get` with no auth header (`cmd/podium/main.go:771-798`). The Python `DeviceCodeRequired` docstring notes OAuth is deferred (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:23-28`). The clients therefore reach the registry as the unauthenticated/default identity, so the documented per-identity visibility filtering does not take effect through these transports. This is a known staged limitation; reported here because the §7.6 text presents identity as functional. Suggested direction: attach the resolved OAuth token (per §6.3) to SDK and read-CLI requests once the device-code flow lands, and adjust §7.6 wording until then.
## F-7.7 — 7.7 Onboarding: podium init, config show, login

_Reviewed spec/07-external-integration.md against the implementation._

I checked the three onboarding commands the subsection defines: `podium init` (cmd/podium/main.go:672-769), `podium config show` (cmd/podium/config.go and the server config in internal/serverboot/serverboot.go), and `podium login` / `podium logout` (cmd/podium/login.go), plus the supporting `sync.yaml` machinery in pkg/sync/config.go and the OAuth device-code flow in pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go and pkg/identity/keychain.go. The `init` command implements the scope flags, the `--standalone` shortcut, the overwrite guard, and the `.gitignore` update, and its tests cover those paths. The `config show` and `login` commands diverge substantially from the spec: `config show` prints the server-side registry configuration rather than the merged client `sync.yaml` with provenance, and `login` omits registry resolution from the merged config, the issuer discovery, the timeout, refresh-token persistence, identity printout, browser handling, and the filesystem/standalone no-op. Several of these gaps trace to absent multi-scope `sync.yaml` merge and precedence machinery, which does not exist anywhere in the repo.

### - [ ] F-7.7.1 — `podium config show` prints server config instead of the merged sync.yaml [High] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.7 states that `podium config show` "displays the merged result with provenance" and "Prints the merged `sync.yaml` with per-key provenance", showing keys such as `defaults.registry`, `defaults.harness`, `defaults.target`, and the `profiles.*` blocks, each annotated with the file scope it came from (for example `(from <ws>/.podium/sync.yaml)`, `(from ~/.podium/sync.yaml)`). The implemented `configShow` in cmd/podium/config.go:36-57 calls `serverboot.LoadConfig()` and prints `cfg.Settings()`, which is the server-side registry configuration (`bind`, `public_mode`, `identity_provider`, `store.type`, and similar; see internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:490-494). It never reads any `sync.yaml`, reports no per-key file-scope provenance, and exposes none of the `defaults`/`profiles` keys the spec lists. The command's own help text confirms the divergence: "Print the resolved server configuration with sources." (cmd/podium/config.go:38, cmd/podium/main.go:136). The §7.7 client-side `config show` is unimplemented. Suggested direction: add a client-config code path (either a new subcommand or a flag) that merges `~/.podium/sync.yaml`, `<ws>/.podium/sync.yaml`, and `<ws>/.podium/sync.local.yaml` per the §7.5.2 precedence order and prints each resolved key with the winning file scope.

### - [ ] F-7.7.2 — `podium config show --explain <key>` is absent [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §7.7 specifies that `config show` accepts `--explain <key>`, which "prints just one key with its full resolution chain: which file each scope had, and which won." The implemented `configShow` (cmd/podium/config.go:36-57) defines only a `--json` flag and has no `--explain` handling. Because the command operates on server settings rather than the merged `sync.yaml` (see F-7.7.1), there is no resolution chain to print. Suggested direction: implement `--explain <key>` as part of the client-config `config show`, emitting the value held at each scope (`~/.podium/sync.yaml`, `<ws>/.podium/sync.yaml`, `<ws>/.podium/sync.local.yaml`, env, CLI) and which scope won.

### - [ ] F-7.7.3 — `podium config show` does not surface profile collisions [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §7.7 (and the cross-reference in §7.5.2: "`podium config show` (§7.7) always surfaces collisions for debugging") requires `config show` to report profile-name collisions across scopes, for example `Profile collisions: 1 (profiles.staging defined in both ~/.podium/sync.yaml and <ws>/.podium/sync.local.yaml; project-local wins)`. The implemented `configShow` prints only server settings (cmd/podium/config.go:36-57) and has no notion of profiles or cross-scope collisions. No collision-detection logic exists in pkg/sync; `ReadConfig` reads a single workspace file and performs no merge (pkg/sync/config.go:99-112). Suggested direction: detect duplicate profile names across the user-global, project-shared, and project-local files during the merge and list them in `config show` output.

### - [ ] F-7.7.4 — `podium login` requires `--registry` and does not resolve it from the merged config [High] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.7 documents `podium login` with no arguments as the primary form ("uses the merged config to find the registry") and states the behavior "resolves the registry from the merged config (or `--registry` flag)". The implemented `loginCmd` defaults `--registry` to the `PODIUM_REGISTRY` env var only and exits 2 when it is empty (cmd/podium/login.go:29, 39-42). It never reads `sync.yaml` to resolve `defaults.registry`, so a developer who configured the registry through `podium init` cannot run a bare `podium login`. Suggested direction: when `--registry` and `PODIUM_REGISTRY` are unset, resolve `defaults.registry` from the merged `sync.yaml` (the same resolution the spec attributes to `podium sync`).

### - [ ] F-7.7.5 — `podium login` requires `--issuer`; no IdP discovery from the registry [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §7.7 frames `podium login` as needing only the resolved registry; it does not require the operator to supply the OAuth issuer or token endpoint. The implemented `loginCmd` requires `--issuer` (or `PODIUM_OAUTH_AUTHORIZATION_ENDPOINT`) and exits 2 when it is empty (cmd/podium/login.go:30, 43-46), then synthesizes the token URL with `guessTokenURL` (cmd/podium/login.go:48-51, 115-122). The spec's `podium login` and `podium login --registry <url>` examples (lines 651-652) supply no issuer, implying the client discovers the IdP from the registry (for example via an OAuth metadata or registry capabilities endpoint, consistent with §6.3 `oauth-device-code`). Suggested direction: have `login` fetch the registry's advertised authorization and token endpoints so the issuer flags become optional overrides rather than requirements.

### - [ ] F-7.7.6 — `podium login` enforces no 10-minute timeout [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §7.7 states that `login` "polls the IdP's token endpoint until the user completes the flow or a 10-minute timeout elapses" and "Exits non-zero on timeout". The implemented `loginCmd` calls `flow.Poll(ctx, auth)` with `ctx := context.Background()` (cmd/podium/login.go:61-72), and `Poll` loops until success, denial, expiry, or context cancellation (pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:304-325). With a background context that never cancels, the only stop conditions are the IdP returning `expired_token` or `access_denied`; there is no client-side 10-minute deadline. If the IdP's `device_code` lifetime exceeds 10 minutes (or the IdP keeps returning `authorization_pending`), `podium login` blocks past the spec's bound. Suggested direction: wrap the poll in `context.WithTimeout(ctx, 10*time.Minute)` (or honor the device code's `ExpiresIn`, whichever is shorter) and return a non-zero exit on deadline.

### - [ ] F-7.7.7 — `podium login` discards the refresh token [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.7 states that `login` "caches the access + refresh tokens in the OS keychain (per `oauth-device-code` in §6.3)". The implemented `loginCmd` saves only the access token: `store.Save(*registry, tokens.AccessToken)` (cmd/podium/login.go:77-78). The `Tokens` struct carries `RefreshToken` (pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:67-73) and the device-code flow already parses it (pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:196-202), but it is dropped. The `TokenStore` interface stores a single string per label (pkg/identity/keychain.go:14-18), so it has no slot for the refresh token. Without the refresh token, `DeviceCodeFlow.Refresh` (pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:231-298) cannot run, defeating the spec's "re-authing after token expiry" use case without a full re-login. Suggested direction: persist both tokens (for example serialize access plus refresh to a single keychain entry, or extend `TokenStore` to store a structured token) so the cached refresh token is available for silent renewal.

### - [ ] F-7.7.8 — `podium login` does not print the resolved identity on success [Low] — OPEN

(gap) §7.7 states that on success `login` "prints the resolved identity (`sub`, `email`, OIDC groups)". The implemented `loginCmd` prints only "Login successful; token saved to keychain." (cmd/podium/login.go:82) and never decodes the ID token. The flow captures `IDToken` (pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:188, 201) but `loginCmd` does not parse it for `sub`, `email`, or `groups`. Suggested direction: decode the returned ID token (or call the registry's identity/whoami endpoint) and print the `sub`, `email`, and OIDC groups so the operator can confirm who they authenticated as.

### - [ ] F-7.7.9 — `podium login` has no `--no-browser` flag and does not open the browser [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §7.7 lists `podium login --no-browser` ("don't auto-open the verification URL") and states the default behavior "attempts to open the URL in the system browser". The implemented `loginCmd` defines no `--no-browser` flag (cmd/podium/login.go:27-34) and never attempts to open a browser; it only prints the verification URL and code to stderr (cmd/podium/login.go:67-71). No browser-open helper exists in cmd/podium or pkg/identity. Suggested direction: add a `--no-browser` flag and, unless it is set, attempt to open `auth.VerificationURLComplete` (falling back to `auth.VerificationURL`) with a platform launcher (`open` on macOS, `xdg-open` on Linux, `rundll32` on Windows), tolerating launch failures.

### - [ ] F-7.7.10 — `podium login` is not a no-op against a filesystem or standalone registry [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.7 states: "`podium login` is a no-op when the resolved registry is a filesystem path (no auth) or points at a `--standalone` server (no auth). In both cases it prints a notice and exits." The implemented `loginCmd` always proceeds into `flow.Initiate` / `flow.Poll` regardless of the registry value (cmd/podium/login.go:53-76). Against a filesystem-path registry it would attempt the OAuth flow (and fail because `--issuer` is required), and against `http://127.0.0.1:8080` it would attempt to reach a device endpoint that the standalone server does not serve. Suggested direction: after resolving the registry, detect a filesystem path (no URL scheme) or the standalone address and short-circuit with an informational notice and a zero exit, before initiating the device-code flow.

### - [ ] F-7.7.11 — `podium init` does not walk up to find an existing `.podium/` directory [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.7 workspace-mode step 1 states that `podium init` "Walks up from CWD to find an existing `.podium/` directory; if none, creates `.podium/` in CWD." The implemented `initCmd` sets `dir := ".podium"` relative to CWD and calls `os.MkdirAll(dir, ...)` without walking up (cmd/podium/main.go:705, 717). Running `podium init` (or `podium init --local`) from a subdirectory of an already-initialized workspace creates a second `.podium/` in the subdirectory instead of reusing the parent workspace, which contradicts both the spec and the workspace-discovery model in §7.5.2 ("walking up from CWD until a `.podium/` directory is found"). Suggested direction: reuse a shared walk-up workspace-discovery helper to locate an existing `.podium/` before falling back to creating one in CWD, matching how `podium sync` is meant to discover the workspace.

### - [ ] F-7.7.12 — `podium init` has no interactive wizard [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §7.7 documents `podium init` with no flags as the "interactive wizard" (line 594), and the user-global form `podium init --global` is likewise annotated "interactive" (line 601). The implemented `initCmd` has no interactive prompting; when `--registry` is empty and `--standalone` is not set, it prints "error: --registry, --standalone, or interactive wizard required" and exits 2 (cmd/podium/main.go:697-700). No prompt or stdin-reading logic exists in the command. Suggested direction: implement an interactive prompt that asks for the registry (and optionally harness and target) when no value flags are supplied and stdin is a terminal, writing the resulting `sync.yaml`.

### - [ ] F-7.7.13 — `podium init` does not print next-step hints [Low] — OPEN

(gap) §7.7 workspace-mode step 4 states that `init` "Prints next-step hints (commit `<ws>/.podium/sync.yaml`, run `podium sync` to materialize)." The implemented `initCmd` prints only "Wrote %s\n" with the destination path (cmd/podium/main.go:748). It does not suggest committing the file or running `podium sync`. Suggested direction: after writing, print the next-step guidance the spec describes for workspace mode (commit the file and run `podium sync`).

### - [ ] F-7.7.14 — `podium logout` requires `--registry` and does not resolve it from the merged config [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.7 lists `podium logout` with no arguments ("clears the cached token from the OS keychain", line 654) and frames `login`/`logout` symmetrically around the resolved registry. The implemented `logoutCmd` defaults `--registry` to `PODIUM_REGISTRY` only and exits 2 when it is empty (cmd/podium/login.go:94, 99-102). A developer who configured the registry through `podium init` cannot run a bare `podium logout`; it errors with "--registry is required". Suggested direction: resolve `defaults.registry` from the merged `sync.yaml` when `--registry` and `PODIUM_REGISTRY` are unset, mirroring the resolution proposed for `login` in F-7.7.4.
## F-8.1 — 8.1 What Gets Logged

_Reviewed spec/08-audit-and-observability.md against the implementation._

I verified the §8.1 event taxonomy and the caller-identity contract against pkg/audit, pkg/registry/core, pkg/registry/server, pkg/registry/ingest, and internal/serverboot. All eighteen event-type strings in the §8.1 table are declared as constants in pkg/audit/audit.go (lines 29-46) with the exact namespaced spellings the spec lists. Emission coverage is partial: read events (`domain.loaded`, `domains.searched`, `artifacts.searched`, `artifact.loaded`), `visibility.denied`, `artifact.published`, `artifact.deprecated`, `artifact.signed`, `layer.ingested`, `layer.history_rewritten`, `freeze.break_glass`, `user.erased`, `registry.read_only_entered`, and `registry.read_only_exited` are emitted. Four declared event types are never emitted from non-test code, and the mandated trace ID and public-mode caller fields are absent.

### - [x] F-8.1.1 — Caller identity records only a string; email, groups, network, and public_mode flag are not attached [High] — CLOSED

(gap) §8.1 ("Caller identity in audit events") requires read events to record the caller identity from the OAuth token as `caller.identity = "<sub-claim>"` "with email and groups attached." In public-mode deployments the same events must instead record `caller.identity = "system:public"`, with the source IP address and any upstream `X-Forwarded-User` header "preserved in `caller.network`," plus the flag `caller.public_mode: true` "so downstream consumers (SIEM, audit dashboards) can filter them without parsing identity strings." The implementation reduces caller identity to a single string. `callerOf` in pkg/registry/core/core.go:988-996 returns either `id.Sub` or `"system:public"` and discards email and groups. The four read emitters set only `Caller: callerOf(id)` (core.go:242, 505, 649, 748); none attach email, groups, a `caller.network` value, or a `caller.public_mode` flag. A repo-wide search for `caller.network`, `caller.email`, `caller.groups`, `caller.public_mode`, `X-Forwarded-User`, `RemoteAddr`, and `source_ip` returns no matches in non-test Go code, so the public-mode network capture and the `public_mode` boolean filter are entirely absent. `pkg/registry/server/server.go:813-819` sets `id.IsPublic = true` in public mode, which only changes the identity string; the request's `RemoteAddr` and any forwarded-user header are never read. The `core.AuditEvent` struct (core.go:90-95) has no fields for these attributes. Suggested direction: extend `AuditEvent` and the audit record with structured caller fields (email, groups, network with source IP and forwarded user, and a `public_mode` boolean), populate them from `layer.Identity` and the HTTP request in the emit path, and add the public-mode flag whenever `id.IsPublic` is set.

Resolution (commit 2b31790): A new server identity middleware (`pkg/registry/server/audit_context.go`) attaches per-request `AuditMeta` to the request context: email and groups for authenticated callers, or source IP and `X-Forwarded-User` plus the `public_mode` flag for public-mode callers. The serverboot emitter adapter and the HTTP write handlers read it onto the structured caller fields added to `audit.Event`, which participate in the §8.6 hash chain. The read path keeps `core.AuditEvent` unchanged and enriches at emit time from the context. Covered by serverboot read-path tests (authenticated and public) and the extended public-mode e2e (`TestDocHTTPAPI_52_PublicModeAudit`).

### - [x] F-8.1.2 — `admin.granted` event never emitted when a grant is added or revoked [High] — CLOSED

(gap) The §8.1 table requires an `admin.granted` event "When an admin grant was added or revoked." The event type is declared (pkg/audit/audit.go:41) but never emitted. `Registry.GrantAdmin` and `Registry.RevokeAdmin` (pkg/registry/core/admin.go:37-48) write the grant table without emitting any audit event, and the HTTP handler `handleAdminGrants` (pkg/registry/server/admin.go:21-59) returns after the store write with no audit call. A repo-wide search shows `admin.granted` / `EventAdminGranted` appears only in the constant declaration and in the retention policy list (internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go:78); there is no emission site. Admin-grant changes are security-relevant and the spec mandates an audit trail. Suggested direction: emit an `admin.granted` event from `GrantAdmin` and `RevokeAdmin` (or from the HTTP handler), recording the acting admin as caller, the affected user as target, and the add-versus-revoke action in context.

Resolution (commit 2b31790): `handleAdminGrants` emits `admin.granted` after the store write on both POST (action `grant`) and DELETE (action `revoke`), with the acting admin as caller and the affected user as target, via the shared `emitAuditEvent` helper wired by `server.WithAudit`. Covered by `TestAdminGrants_EmitsAdminGranted`.

### - [x] F-8.1.3 — `layer.config_changed` event never emitted on admin layer add, remove, or reorder [High] — CLOSED

(gap) The §8.1 table requires `layer.config_changed` "When an admin added, removed, or reordered admin-defined layers." The event type is declared (pkg/audit/audit.go:39) but never emitted. The layer HTTP handlers in pkg/registry/server/layers.go perform the store writes for admin-defined layers without any audit emission: `register` (lines 183-275) calls `PutLayerConfig` and returns, `unregister` (lines 288-320) calls `DeleteLayerConfig` and returns, and `reorder` (lines 323 onward) re-sequences the list, none emitting an event. A repo-wide search shows `layer.config_changed` / `EventLayerConfigChanged` appears only in the constant declaration and the retention list (internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go:76). Suggested direction: emit `layer.config_changed` from the admin-defined branches of register, unregister, and reorder, distinguishing the add, remove, and reorder actions in context.

Resolution (commit 2b31790): `register` and `unregister` emit `layer.config_changed` for admin-defined layers (action `register`/`unregister`) and `reorder` emits it with action `reorder` and the new order as target, via `LayerEndpoint.WithAudit`. Covered by `TestLayerEndpoint_EmitsConfigChanged`.

### - [x] F-8.1.4 — `layer.user_registered` event never emitted when a user registers or unregisters a personal layer [High] — CLOSED

(gap) The §8.1 table requires `layer.user_registered` "When a user registered or unregistered a personal layer." The event type is declared (pkg/audit/audit.go:40) but never emitted. The user-defined branch of `register` in pkg/registry/server/layers.go:183-275 and the user-defined branch of `unregister` (lines 288-320) write the layer config without emitting an audit event. A repo-wide search shows `layer.user_registered` / `EventLayerUserRegistered` appears only in the constant declaration and the retention list (internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go:77). Suggested direction: emit `layer.user_registered` from the `UserDefined` paths of register and unregister, recording the owner as caller, the layer ID as target, and whether the action was a registration or an unregistration.

Resolution (commit 2b31790): the user-defined branches of `register` and `unregister` emit `layer.user_registered` with the layer ID as target, the registrant as caller, the layer owner recorded in context, and the register/unregister action. Covered by `TestLayerEndpoint_EmitsUserRegistered`.

### - [x] F-8.1.5 — `domain.published` event never emitted when a DOMAIN.md is added or changed [Medium] — CLOSED

(gap) The §8.1 table requires `domain.published` "When a `DOMAIN.md` was added or changed." The event type is declared (pkg/audit/audit.go:36) but never emitted. A repo-wide search for `domain.published` / `EventDomainPublished` finds matches only in the constant declaration and the retention policy list (internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go:73). The ingest pipeline emits `artifact.published`, `artifact.deprecated`, `artifact.signed`, and `layer.ingested` (pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:518-530, pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:139-151) but never detects or audits DOMAIN.md additions or changes. Suggested direction: detect DOMAIN.md changes during the ingest cycle and emit `domain.published` with the domain path as target.

Resolution (commit 2b31790): ingest reads the layer's stored DOMAIN.md records before writing, then emits `domain.published` (target = canonical domain path, layer in context) for each walked DOMAIN.md that is newly added or whose bytes changed, staying silent on an unchanged re-ingest. The emission uses the existing `AuditEmit` seam, matching how `artifact.published` reaches the audit log. Covered by the ingest domain.published tests (new, changed, unchanged, and root-skip cases).

### - [x] F-8.1.6 — Registry-owned audit events carry no trace ID despite the §8.1 requirement [Medium] — CLOSED

(inconsistency) §8.1 opens with "Every significant event, each carrying a trace ID (W3C Trace Context)," and the closing paragraph states both audit streams "share trace IDs." The audit record types do define a `TraceID` field (pkg/audit/audit.go:56, pkg/audit/file.go:151), but the registry-owned events never populate it. The `core.AuditEvent` struct (pkg/registry/core/core.go:90-95) has no `TraceID` field, and `Registry.emit` (core.go:159-164) passes the event through without extracting a trace ID from the context. The serverboot adapter `auditEmitterFor` (internal/serverboot/audit_emitter.go:13-22) copies only `Type`, `Caller`, `Target`, and `Context` into `audit.Event`, leaving `TraceID` empty. A repo-wide search for `TraceID` in pkg/registry/core and internal/serverboot returns no population sites, and pkg/registry/server/events.go:190 notes trace_id propagation is "reserved for future." Result: registry catalogue and read events are written with an empty trace ID, so the two streams cannot share trace IDs as specified. Suggested direction: add a `TraceID` field to `core.AuditEvent`, extract the W3C `traceparent` from the request context at emit time, and carry it through the serverboot adapter into `audit.Event`.

Resolution (commit 2b31790): the trace id is parsed from a well-formed W3C `traceparent` header or generated per request, carried on the per-request `AuditMeta`, and written to `audit.Event.TraceID` by the serverboot read-event adapter and the HTTP write handlers, so registry read and catalogue events share a trace id. The all-zero and malformed `traceparent` cases fall back to a generated id. Covered by `TestParseTraceparent`, the serverboot read-path tests, and the public-mode e2e.
## F-8.2 — 8.2 PII Redaction

_Reviewed spec/08-audit-and-observability.md against the implementation._

Section 8.2 describes two redaction surfaces: manifest-declared field redaction in audit logs, and default-on regex scrubbing of free-text `search_artifacts` and `search_domains` queries (SSN, credit-card, email, and phone) configurable via `PIIRedactionConfig`. The query-text scrubber exists as `pkg/audit.PIIScrubber` and is unit-tested, but it is never invoked anywhere in the runtime path, so query text reaches the audit log unredacted. The named configuration surface `PIIRedactionConfig` does not exist. Manifest-declared redaction is implemented only for three ingest-time events against a fixed set of context keys, and it does not cover read events or author-named content fields. The MCP server performs no redaction because it does not write a local audit sink at all.

### - [ ] F-8.2.1 — Query-text PII scrubbing is never applied in the runtime path [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 8.2 states that free-text `search_artifacts` and `search_domains` queries "are regex-scrubbed for common PII patterns (SSN, credit-card, email, phone) before being written to audit" and that this is "Default-on." The implementation provides `audit.PIIScrubber` with the named default patterns (`pkg/audit/redact.go:25`-`32`) and a `Scrub` method (`pkg/audit/redact.go:43`), but `Scrub` is called only from unit tests (`pkg/audit/file_test.go:100`,`129`). No production code path scrubs the query. `SearchArtifacts` writes the raw query into the audit context at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:506` (`Context: map[string]string{"query": opts.Query, ...}`) and `SearchDomains` does the same at `pkg/registry/core/core.go:650`. The emitter (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:159`) forwards the event unchanged, the serverboot adapter copies `e.Context` verbatim (`internal/serverboot/audit_emitter.go:14`-`20`), and `FileSink.Append` writes `e.Context` to disk verbatim (`pkg/audit/file.go:89`,`166`). The raw query string, which may contain an SSN, credit-card number, email, or phone, is persisted to the audit log in full, contradicting the default-on guarantee. Suggested direction: scrub `opts.Query` before it is placed in the audit context (for example, run a default `PIIScrubber` over the query at the emit sites in `core.go`, or apply scrubbing inside the emitter adapter for the `artifacts.searched` and `domains.searched` event types). Note that the default patterns themselves carry runtime caveats once wired: the phone pattern (`pkg/audit/redact.go:30`) is not `\b`-anchored and the credit-card pattern (`pkg/audit/redact.go:28`) matches any run of 13-19 digits, so pattern precedence and anchoring should be validated against real queries when the scrubber is connected.

### - [ ] F-8.2.2 — `PIIRedactionConfig` configuration surface is absent [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 8.2 states that the query-text scrub "Patterns [are] configurable via `PIIRedactionConfig`." No type or symbol named `PIIRedactionConfig` exists anywhere in the repository (a repo-wide grep for `PIIRedactionConfig`, `PIIRedaction`, and `RedactionConfig` returns no matches in Go source). The only way to extend or change patterns is the programmatic `PIIScrubber.Add` method (`pkg/audit/redact.go:36`), which requires recompilation and is never invoked outside tests.
