There is no deployment-level configuration (environment variable or YAML) that loads PII patterns; `internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go` and `cmd/podium/config.go` contain no PII or scrub wiring. Suggested direction: introduce a `PIIRedactionConfig` (patterns and an enable toggle, defaulting on) parsed from server configuration and used to build the scrubber that F-8.2.1 wires in, or update the spec if the configuration surface is intended to remain code-level only.

### - [ ] F-8.2.3 — Manifest-declared redaction covers only ingest events and a fixed key set [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 8.2 states that "Artifact manifests can specify fields that should be redacted in audit logs (e.g., `bank_account`, `ssn`)" and that "The registry honors redaction directives." The manifest field `audit_redact` is parsed (`pkg/manifest/types.go:115`) and stored (`pkg/store/store.go:63`), and `audit.RedactFields` (`pkg/audit/redact.go:55`) replaces named keys with `[redacted]`. Redaction is applied only inside the ingest pipeline for `artifact.published`, `artifact.deprecated`, and `artifact.signed`, and only over a hardcoded context map containing `version`, `content_hash`, and `layer` (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:518`-`533`). Two consequences follow. First, read events that reference the artifact, in particular `artifact.loaded`, build their context without consulting `audit_redact` (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:746`-`751` sets `Context: map[string]string{"version": opts.Version}` with no redaction), so an artifact's redaction directive has no effect on the events most likely to recur. Second, the spec's example fields `bank_account` and `ssn` are author-named content fields that never appear in the fixed ingest context keys, so declaring `audit_redact: [bank_account]` redacts nothing. The directive therefore only ever masks one of `version`, `content_hash`, or `layer`. Suggested direction: apply `RedactFields` (keyed by the resolved manifest's `audit_redact`) at every audit emit site that references an artifact, including `artifact.loaded`, and clarify which audit context keys are eligible for manifest-declared redaction so authors can target real fields.

### - [ ] F-8.2.4 — MCP server applies no redaction before its local audit sink [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 8.2 states that for manifest-declared redaction "the MCP server applies the same directives before writing to its local audit sink," and the query-text scrub applies to `search_artifacts` and `search_domains`, which are MCP meta-tools whose events §8.1 routes to the MCP local audit log. The MCP server performs neither redaction. It reads `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` into `mcpServer.auditSink` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:78`,`108`), but that field is never used anywhere in `cmd/podium-mcp`, so no local audit log is written and no redaction is reachable. The MCP `searchArtifacts` handler (`cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:12`-`44`) forwards the query and returns results without emitting or scrubbing any local audit record. No `LocalAuditSink` implementation exists (the only reference is a doc comment at `pkg/audit/file.go:16`). The missing local sink itself is a §8.3 concern, but the §8.2 obligation that the MCP server redacts before writing to that sink is unmet as a direct consequence. Suggested direction: implement the MCP local audit sink (per §8.3) and apply the same query-text scrubbing (F-8.2.1) and manifest-declared field redaction before each local write; until the sink exists, the redaction requirement cannot be satisfied on the MCP side.
## F-8.3 — 8.3 Audit Sinks

_Reviewed spec/08-audit-and-observability.md against the implementation._

Section 8.3 describes two independent audit sinks. The registry owns a sink for catalogue events, and the MCP server writes a local file log through a `LocalAuditSink` interface when `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` is set, defaulting to `~/.podium/audit.log`. The registry side is implemented: `internal/serverboot/openAuditSink` constructs an `audit.FileSink`, wires it into the core registry via `WithAudit(auditEmitterFor(...))`, and resolves the path from `PODIUM_AUDIT_LOG_PATH` with the documented `~/.podium/audit.log` default (serverboot.go:349-351, audit_anchor.go:73-82, file.go:31-49). The local MCP sink described by this section is not implemented. The MCP server reads `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` into a struct field and never uses it, never imports `pkg/audit`, and never writes any meta-tool audit events. The `FileSink` also only supports filesystem paths, so the "external endpoint" redirect target named for `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` has no backing.

### - [ ] F-8.3.1 — MCP local audit sink (`PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` / `LocalAuditSink`) is unwired; meta-tool events are never logged locally [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 8.3 states: "The local file log, when enabled via `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK`, is written by the MCP server through the `LocalAuditSink` interface. The local sink defaults to `~/.podium/audit.log`." Section 8.1 reinforces this: "The MCP server can also write a local audit log for the meta-tool events through a `LocalAuditSink` interface (§9) when configured." The MCP server reads the env var at `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:108` (`auditSink: os.Getenv("PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK")`) into `config.auditSink` (declared at main.go:78), but that field is never read anywhere else. `cmd/podium-mcp` does not import `pkg/audit` (confirmed by grep: no import in any file under `cmd/podium-mcp/`), constructs no sink, and calls no `Append`. The meta-tool handlers (`loadArtifact` at main.go:306, `searchArtifacts`, `proxyGet` for `load_domain` / `search_domains`) perform no audit write on any path, so setting `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` has no observable effect and meta-tool events are never persisted to a local log. There is no behavioral test asserting an MCP-side audit write (the only references in `cmd/podium-mcp/*_test.go` are unrelated `ops/audit` fixtures and a stale comment at sandbox_policy_test.go:71 referring to a non-existent "audit-sink + log path"). Suggested direction: when `cfg.auditSink != ""` (and per spec §6 also when set to `default` or empty-but-present), construct an `audit.FileSink` via `audit.NewFileSink(path)` (which already defaults an empty path to `~/.podium/audit.log` at file.go:32-38), and append an `audit.Event` for each meta-tool call (`domain.loaded`, `domains.searched`, `artifacts.searched`, `artifact.loaded`) with the trace ID and caller identity, applying the §8.2 redaction directives before writing.

### - [ ] F-8.3.2 — `FileSink` supports only filesystem paths; no external endpoint redirect for the local sink [Low] — OPEN

(gap) Section 8.3 states: "Both the registry and local sinks can be redirected to external SIEM / log aggregation independently," and the companion `LocalAuditSink` row in §9 (spec/09-extensibility.md:22) is more concrete: "Redirect to a workspace-local path or an external endpoint via `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK`." The only `Sink` implementations are `audit.FileSink` (writes via `os.OpenFile` to a local path, file.go:95) and `audit.Memory` (in-process, audit.go:100-123). No HTTP, syslog, or other network sink exists in `pkg/audit` (grep for `http`, `url`, `endpoint`, `syslog` in non-test files returns only prose comments). For the registry side, redirection to external aggregation is achievable out of band by shipping the local file, which is consistent with the §8.3 "redirected to external SIEM" wording. For the local sink the §9 promise of an "external endpoint via `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK`" has no implementation because the variable is unwired (see F-8.3.1) and, even if wired, `NewFileSink` would treat a URL as a filesystem path. This is Low because §8.3 itself frames SIEM redirection as an operational capability rather than a built-in transport, and the higher-impact defect is the fully unwired sink in F-8.3.1. Suggested direction: if an external-endpoint target is intended, add a `Sink` implementation that recognizes a URL form of `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK` and forwards events, or narrow the §8.3 and §9 prose to describe file-based shipping only.
## F-8.4 — 8.4 Retention

_Reviewed spec/08-audit-and-observability.md against the implementation._

Section 8.4 specifies a retention defaults table with five data categories (audit event metadata at 1 year, query text at 30 days with placeholder redaction after 7 days, deprecated artifact versions at 90 days after the deprecation flag is set, owner-unregistered layers at 30 days with soft-deleted artifacts recoverable via admin, and vulnerability scan history at 1 year), states that all defaults are configurable per deployment, and describes optional sampling for high-volume low-sensitivity events such as `domain.loaded` at a 10% sample. The implementation provides retention for the first category only. `pkg/audit/retention.go` defines a per-event-type `Policy` and an `Enforce` function that rewrites the local `FileSink` log, `internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go` wires a scheduler with a 365-day default, and `cmd/podium admin retention` exposes manual enforcement. The remaining four categories (query-text retention plus the 7-day placeholder rule, deprecated-version purge, layer soft-delete with recovery, and vulnerability scan history) and the sampling mechanism have no implementation anywhere in the repository. The audit-event default of 1 year matches the spec but is not applied unless an operator explicitly enables the scheduler.

### - [ ] F-8.4.1 — Query text 30-day retention and 7-day placeholder redaction absent [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 8.4 specifies that query text is retained for "30 days (redacted to placeholders after 7 days)", a category distinct from audit-event metadata and with a tighter window plus an intermediate redaction step. Free-text `search_artifacts` and `search_domains` queries are written into audit events as the event `Target` and `Context` values (see `pkg/audit/audit.go` event fields and `pkg/audit/redact.go` `PIIScrubber`, which scrubs at write time only). The retention machinery in `pkg/audit/retention.go` applies a single per-event-type `MaxAge` to the whole event; there is no separate retention window for the query-text portion and no time-based transition that replaces query text with placeholders after 7 days while keeping the event. A repo-wide search for any 7-day or 30-day query handling, age-based redaction, or `PIIRedactionConfig` TTL returns nothing. The result is that query text either lives for the full audit-event MaxAge (365 days under the default policy) or is dropped with the entire event, and the spec-mandated 30-day query-text ceiling and 7-day placeholder step are not enforced. Suggested direction: store query text in a dedicated field with its own timestamped retention rule, add a redaction pass at the 7-day mark that overwrites the query text in place and rebuilds the chain, and drop the field at 30 days independent of the event metadata.

### - [ ] F-8.4.2 — Deprecated artifact version 90-day purge not implemented [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 8.4 specifies that deprecated artifact versions are retained for "90 days after the deprecation flag is set" and then removed. There is no purge logic for deprecated versions anywhere in the codebase. A repo-wide search for deprecation-driven purge, prune, or expiry (`grep -rni "deprecat"` filtered for retention/purge/delete/expire/90) finds only the `artifact.deprecated` audit event type and unrelated SQL column lists. Additionally, no deprecation timestamp is persisted: a search for `deprecated_at`/`DeprecatedAt` returns nothing, and the store schemas track a boolean `deprecated` column only (for example `pkg/store/sqlite.go:190`). Without a stored deprecation timestamp the 90-day window cannot be computed even if a purge job were added. Suggested direction: persist a `deprecated_at` timestamp when the deprecation flag transitions to true, and add a scheduled job that deletes the artifact version content and metadata 90 days after that timestamp, with the window configurable per deployment.

### - [ ] F-8.4.3 — Owner-unregistered layers are hard-deleted with no 30-day recovery window [High] — OPEN

(gap, bug) Section 8.4 specifies that layers unregistered by their owners are retained for "30 days (artifacts soft-deleted, recoverable via admin)". The unregister flow performs an immediate hard delete with no soft-delete, no recovery window, and no admin restore path. The HTTP handler `LayerEndpoint.unregister` (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:288`-`320`) calls `e.store.DeleteLayerConfig`, and every store backend deletes the row outright: `pkg/store/sqlite.go:377`-`382` (`DELETE FROM layer_configs`), `pkg/store/postgres.go:401`-`406` (`DELETE FROM layer_configs`), and `pkg/store/memory.go:187`-`192` (`delete(s.layers, ...)`). There is no `deleted_at`/tombstone column (a search across `pkg/store` returns nothing) and no `podium admin restore`/`recover` command (the admin subcommands in `cmd/podium/admin.go:42`-`62` are grant, revoke, show-effective, erase, retention, reembed, runtime, and migrate-to-standard). The handler also does not soft-delete or otherwise act on the artifacts ingested from the unregistered layer, so the spec's "artifacts soft-deleted, recoverable via admin" guarantee is entirely absent. Once unregistered, neither the layer nor its artifacts can be recovered within the 30-day window the spec promises. Suggested direction: mark the layer config and its artifacts with a `deleted_at` timestamp on unregister, exclude soft-deleted rows from normal queries, add an admin restore command that clears the marker within the window, and add a scheduled job that hard-deletes records older than 30 days.

### - [ ] F-8.4.4 — Vulnerability scan history retention not implemented [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 8.4 specifies a "Vulnerability scan history" retention of 1 year. No vulnerability scan history is stored and no retention is applied to it. A repo-wide search for scan-history storage or retention (`vuln`, `scan_history`, `scanHistory`, `vulnerability`) finds only an unrelated comment in `pkg/dependency/graph.go:60` referencing a `podium vuln explain` consumer of the dependency graph. Because there is no scan-history persistence, the 1-year retention rule has nothing to act on. Suggested direction: if vulnerability scan history is in scope for this deployment surface, add storage for scan results with timestamps and a scheduled job that prunes entries older than the configured window (default 1 year); otherwise reconcile the spec table with the implemented surface.

### - [ ] F-8.4.5 — No sampling for high-volume low-sensitivity events [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 8.4 states that optional sampling for high-volume low-sensitivity events (giving `domain.loaded` at a 10% sample as the example) reduces storage cost. No sampling mechanism exists. A repo-wide search for `sampl` across non-test Go files returns nothing, and the audit write path (`pkg/audit/audit.go`, `pkg/audit/file.go`) records every event unconditionally. There is no per-event-type sample rate in the audit configuration or in the serverboot config (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go` Config struct, lines 452-462 for the audit fields). The spec frames this as optional, so the absence is a missing optional capability. Suggested direction: add a per-event-type sample-rate configuration consulted at write time (for example dropping a configurable fraction of `domain.loaded` events) and surface it through the existing audit config plumbing.

### - [ ] F-8.4.6 — Audit-event 1-year default exists but the enforcing scheduler is off by default [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 8.4 presents 1 year as the default retention for audit event metadata and states the defaults are "configurable per deployment", which implies the default is active out of the box. The max-age default matches the spec: `auditRetentionMaxAgeDays` defaults to `envInt("PODIUM_AUDIT_RETENTION_MAX_AGE_DAYS", 365)` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:571`). However, the enforcement scheduler only starts when `cfg.auditRetentionInterval > 0` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:366`-`368`), and that interval defaults to `envInt("PODIUM_AUDIT_RETENTION_INTERVAL_SECONDS", 0)` (`serverboot.go:570`), which means retention is disabled unless an operator opts in. `startRetentionScheduler` returns early when the interval is non-positive (`internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go:29`-`32`). The practical effect is that the spec's 1-year default never takes effect in a default deployment, and audit events accumulate indefinitely until an operator sets the interval. Suggested direction: either enable a sensible default enforcement interval so the documented 1-year default actually applies, or update the spec to state that retention enforcement is opt-in via `PODIUM_AUDIT_RETENTION_INTERVAL_SECONDS`.

### - [ ] F-8.4.7 — Audit retention covers only the local FileSink, not the registry catalogue event store [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The §8.4 audit-event retention category applies to registry-owned audit events. Section 8.1 states the registry owns the catalogue events and that the local file log is a separate stream written by the MCP server. The implemented retention operates exclusively on a `*audit.FileSink` backed by a flat file: `Enforce` reads and rewrites a single file path (`pkg/audit/retention.go:30`-`64`, using `readAllEvents`/`rewriteWithChain` over `sink.path`), and `startRetentionScheduler` takes an `*audit.FileSink` (`internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go:19`). There is no retention pass over the registry metadata store (`pkg/store` SQLite/Postgres) where registry-owned catalogue events would live in a standard deployment. The metadata store interface and its backends expose no method to age out audit events. As a result, the 1-year audit-event default is enforceable only against the file-based standalone/local stream, and registry catalogue events in a Postgres-backed deployment have no retention. Suggested direction: add a store-level retention operation (or document that registry catalogue-event retention is handled separately) so the §8.4 1-year rule applies to the registry-owned stream as well as the local file log.

### - [ ] F-8.4.8 — Retention rewrite invalidates a previously anchored chain head without re-anchoring [Low] — OPEN

(bug) The §8.4 enforcement mechanism rewrites the audit log under a fresh hash chain. `Enforce` calls `rewriteWithChain`, which recomputes every `PrevHash`/`Hash` over the surviving events (`pkg/audit/retention.go:56`-`64` and `:157`-`186`), and the function's own comment notes that "external anchoring of the prior chain head must be redone after Enforce." In the bootstrap wiring the retention scheduler (`startRetentionScheduler`, `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:366`) and the anchor scheduler (`startAnchorScheduler`, `serverboot.go:359`) run as independent goroutines with no coordination. A retention pass can therefore drop events and rebuild the chain, leaving a previously anchored head that no longer matches the live log, with no automatic re-anchor and no event emitted to flag the discontinuity. This weakens the §8.6 integrity guarantee that retention is expected to preserve. Suggested direction: after a retention rewrite that drops events, trigger an immediate re-anchor of the new chain head (or emit a marker event that records the retention boundary so verifiers can reconcile the anchored head with the truncated log).
## F-8.5 — 8.5 Erasure

_Reviewed spec/08-audit-and-observability.md against the implementation._

Section 8.5 specifies the `podium admin erase <user_id>` command for GDPR right-to-erasure with three guarantees: it unregisters and purges user-defined layers owned by the user and the artifacts ingested from them, it redacts the user identity in audit records by replacing it with `redacted-<sha256(user_id+salt)>`, and it preserves audit event sequencing for integrity. The implementation lives in `pkg/audit/retention.go` (`EraseUser`, lines 80-129) and `cmd/podium/admin.go` (`adminEraseCmd`, lines 199-225). The audit-record redaction and chain rebuild exist and work, but the operation runs only against the local file audit log. The layer and artifact purge is absent, the operation never touches the registry (the authoritative audit stream per 8.1 and 8.3), and the tombstone format diverges from the spec formula.

### - [ ] F-8.5.1 — Layer and artifact purge on erasure is not implemented [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 8.5 requires that erase "Unregisters and purges any user-defined layers owned by the user (and the artifacts ingested from them)." The implementation does no such thing. `EraseUser` (pkg/audit/retention.go:80-124) reads the local audit log, replaces matching `Caller` and `Context` values with a tombstone, appends a `user.erased` event, and rewrites the hash chain. `adminEraseCmd` (cmd/podium/admin.go:199-225) only opens a `FileSink` and calls `EraseUser`. A repo-wide search for any erasure-driven layer unregistration or artifact purge returns nothing: `EraseUser` and `EventUserErased` are referenced only from `cmd/podium/admin.go` and `pkg/audit`, and there is no call into the layer unregister machinery (`layerUnregister` in cmd/podium/layer.go:276, server endpoints in pkg/registry/server/layers.go) from the erase path. As a result, a user's personal layers and the artifacts ingested from them, which can themselves contain personal data, survive a GDPR erasure. Suggested direction: have erase invoke the existing layer-unregister and artifact soft-delete or purge flow for every layer owned by `user_id`, in addition to redacting audit records.

### - [ ] F-8.5.2 — Tombstone format does not match the spec formula [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 8.5 requires the audit identity to be replaced with `redacted-<sha256(user_id+salt)>`. The implementation (`tombstoneFor`, pkg/audit/retention.go:126-129) returns `"erased:" + hex.EncodeToString(h[:8])` where `h = sha256.Sum256([]byte(userID + "|" + salt))`. Three deviations: the prefix is `erased:` instead of `redacted-`, the digest is truncated to the first 8 bytes instead of the full 32-byte sha256, and the hashed input inserts a `|` delimiter between `user_id` and `salt` that the spec formula does not include. The truncation to 64 bits also weakens collision and preimage resistance relative to a full sha256. Suggested direction: change the prefix to `redacted-`, hash the full `user_id+salt` per the spec (decide whether the `|` separator is intended and update the spec if so), and emit the full hex digest unless a documented reason for truncation exists.

### - [ ] F-8.5.3 — Erasure redacts only the local file log, not the registry audit stream [High] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 8.1 lists `user.erased` with Source = Registry and describes it as "Admin invoked the GDPR erasure command," and 8.5 frames erase as a catalog-level operation. The implementation has no registry-side path. The registry server registers admin routes for reembed, grants, and show-effective (pkg/registry/server/server.go:333-335) but no `/v1/admin/erase` route, and the server never calls `EraseUser` or emits `EventUserErased`. The entire flow is the local CLI rewriting `~/.podium/audit.log` (cmd/podium/admin.go:213-218, default path in pkg/audit/file.go:31-38). Consequently the authoritative registry audit stream described in 8.1 and 8.3 is never redacted and registry-held identifiers persist after erase. Suggested direction: add a registry-side erasure operation (an authenticated admin endpoint) that redacts the registry audit records, performs the layer and artifact purge from F-8.5.1, and emits a registry-sourced `user.erased` event, with the local-log rewrite handled separately for the MCP local sink.

### - [ ] F-8.5.4 — Erase does not record which admin invoked it [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 8.1 describes `user.erased` as "Admin invoked the GDPR erasure command," which implies the invoking admin is recorded. The appended event (pkg/audit/retention.go:110-116) sets `Caller: "system:retention"` and stores only a `transformed` count in `Context`; the identity of the admin who ran erase is never captured anywhere. For a sensitive, irreversible operation this loses accountability. Suggested direction: capture the invoking admin identity (from the authenticated session on the registry path, or an explicit operator argument on the CLI) and record it on the `user.erased` event.

### - [ ] F-8.5.5 — Empty salt is accepted, producing a guessable tombstone [Medium] — OPEN

(bug) Section 8.5 specifies the redaction value as `redacted-<sha256(user_id+salt)>`, which depends on a salt for de-identification. The CLI defaults `--salt` to the empty string (cmd/podium/admin.go:203) and `EraseUser` validates only `userID`, not the salt (pkg/audit/retention.go:80-83). With an empty salt the tombstone reduces to a truncated `sha256(user_id + "|")`, which is reversible by brute force or dictionary over candidate user IDs, defeating the purpose of replacing the identity. The happy-path test passes a salt (cmd/podium/admin_happy_paths_test.go:138), so the empty-salt case is untested. Suggested direction: require a non-empty salt (reject an empty `--salt` with a usage error, or source a per-tenant salt from configuration) and add a test covering the rejection.
## F-8.6 — 8.6 Audit Integrity

_Reviewed spec/08-audit-and-observability.md against the implementation._

Section 8.6 makes three concrete claims: every audit event carries a hash chain `event_hash = sha256(event_body || prev_event_hash)`; gap detection is automated and alerted; periodic anchoring of the chain head to a public transparency log is recommended for high-assurance deployments with SIEM mirroring as the operational backstop. The hash-chain construction in `pkg/audit` matches the spec formula exactly (`audit.go:118`, `file.go:86`, `retention.go:166`), and `Verify` walks the chain and returns `ErrChainBroken` on any mismatch. The anchoring scheduler exists and is wired into `serverboot`. The primary gap is that the spec's "Detection of gaps is automated and alerted" guarantee is unimplemented: no production code path ever calls `Verify`, so a broken chain is never detected or alerted at runtime. A secondary gap is a referenced-but-never-emitted `audit.anchor_failed` event, plus a low-severity edge-case bug in Rekor log-index extraction.

### - [ ] F-8.6.1 — Automated gap detection and alerting is not implemented [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 8.6 states "Detection of gaps is automated and alerted." The package provides the detection primitive: `Memory.Verify` (`pkg/audit/audit.go:126`) and `FileSink.Verify` (`pkg/audit/file.go:109`) both walk the chain and return `ErrChainBroken`, and `ErrChainBroken` is documented as mapping to "§8.6 alarms" (`pkg/audit/audit.go:18-20`). However, nothing in production invokes `Verify` or consumes `ErrChainBroken`. A repository-wide search shows `Verify` is called only from `*_test.go` files, and `ErrChainBroken` has no consumer outside `pkg/audit`. The only audit scheduler that runs at startup is the anchor scheduler (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:354-360`, `internal/serverboot/audit_anchor.go:45-69`), and `audit.Scheduler.Run` calls only `Anchor`, never `Verify` (`pkg/audit/scheduler.go:33-56`). There is no verification scheduler, no periodic chain check, and no alert emission on a detected gap. Consequently the tamper-evidence guarantee is not enforced at runtime: an out-of-band edit that breaks the chain is never detected or alerted by the running system. Suggested direction: add a verification pass that runs on a configurable cadence (mirroring the anchor and retention schedulers), and on `ErrChainBroken` emit an alert through the same `OnFailure`/notification seam and record a dedicated audit event so SIEM mirroring (the stated operational backstop) surfaces the gap.

### - [ ] F-8.6.2 — Referenced `audit.anchor_failed` event is never emitted [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The anchor scheduler documentation and the bootstrap comment both tell operators to monitor an `audit.anchor_failed` event: `pkg/audit/scheduler.go:17` ("the `audit.anchor_failed` events the scheduler emits on failure") and `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:357` ("Operators monitor audit.anchored / audit.anchor_failed events"). No such event is ever appended. There is no `EventAuditAnchorFailed` constant in the `EventType` block (`pkg/audit/audit.go:28-48`), and the failure path only calls `s.notifyFailure(err)`, which invokes the optional `OnFailure` callback; in production that callback merely logs via `log.Printf` (`internal/serverboot/audit_anchor.go:59-61`). Because anchoring failures are never written to the audit log, the failure-detection mechanism that operators are told to watch produces no audit record, which interacts with F-8.6.1 to leave integrity-monitoring failures invisible to SIEM. Suggested direction: define an `audit.anchor_failed` event type and append it to the sink (best-effort) when `Anchor` returns an error, or remove the references to the event from the comments so the documented behavior matches the code.

### - [ ] F-8.6.3 — Rekor log index 0 is misreported as "no entry" [Low] — OPEN

(bug) `extractRekorLogIndex` decodes the signing envelope and returns `-1` whenever the decoded `log_index` equals zero (`pkg/audit/anchor.go:80-91`): `if p.LogIndex == 0 { return -1 }`. Rekor transparency-log indices are zero-based, so the first entry recorded against a Rekor instance has index `0`. The code conflates a valid index-`0` entry with the absent case (decode failure or a signer with no Rekor configured). The resulting `audit.anchored` event then records `log_index: "-1"` instead of `"0"` and `Anchor` returns `-1` to the caller, so an auditor cross-correlating the chain head against the transparency log cannot locate the genuine index-`0` entry. The blast radius is small because index `0` is rare in shared Rekor deployments, and the spec describes anchoring as a recommendation without pinning index semantics. Suggested direction: distinguish "field present and zero" from "field absent" (for example a `*int64` pointer or a separate presence flag in the partial struct) so a legitimate index `0` is preserved and only true absence maps to `-1`.
## F-9.1 — 9.1 Pluggable Interfaces

_Reviewed spec/09-extensibility.md against the implementation._

The §9.1 table enumerates the SPI surface (RegistryStore, RegistryObjectStore, RegistrySearchProvider, EmbeddingProvider, LocalSearchProvider, RegistryAuditSink, LayerComposer, LayerSourceProvider, GitProvider, TypeProvider, IngestLinter, IdentityProvider, LocalOverlayProvider, LocalAuditSink, HarnessAdapter, MaterializationHook, NotificationProvider, and SignatureProvider). Each named interface exists as a Go interface in the expected package, and most are wired into the standalone bootstrap in `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go`. The store, object store, embedding, vector, identity (client side), layer-composer, layer-source, git-webhook, type-provider, lint, sign, overlay, harness-adapter, and materialization-hook SPIs match their table descriptions, including the GitProvider built-ins for GitHub, GitLab, and Bitbucket and the EmbeddingProvider built-ins openai, voyage, cohere, and ollama. The findings below cover the concrete contract claims in the table that the code does not implement: the `self_embedding` capability, the `LocalSearchProvider` consumer-side wiring, the NotificationProvider email default, the RegistryAuditSink Postgres-table default, and the standalone defaults stated for the search and embedding rows.

### - [ ] F-9.1.1 — `self_embedding` capability is not declared by any RegistrySearchProvider backend [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The `RegistrySearchProvider` row states: "Each implementation declares a `self_embedding` capability: Pinecone Integrated Inference, Weaviate vectorizer, and Qdrant Cloud Inference set this true and don't require an `EmbeddingProvider`; storage-only backends (`pgvector`, `sqlite-vec`, plain `qdrant`, plain `weaviate`) require one." The `vector.Provider` interface (pkg/vector/vector.go:54-75) exposes only `ID`, `Dimensions`, `Put`, `Query`, `Delete`, and `Close`; there is no capability method, and a repository-wide search for `self_embedding`, `SelfEmbedding`, `self-embed`, or any inference/vectorizer field returns no Go code (only spec and docs prose). The backend config structs carry no vectorizer or inference-model field: `WeaviateConfig` (pkg/vector/weaviate.go:29-34), `QdrantConfig` (pkg/vector/qdrant.go:29-34), and `PineconeConfig` (pkg/vector/pinecone.go:30-35) all hold only URL/host, API key, collection/namespace, and dimensions. The serverboot factory `openVectorAndEmbedder` (internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:663-676) returns `(nil, nil, nil)` whenever the embedder is nil, so a deployment configured with a self-embedding backend but no `EmbeddingProvider` gets vector search disabled entirely rather than text-in self-embedding. The self-embedding env vars referenced elsewhere in the spec (for example `PODIUM_WEAVIATE_VECTORIZER`, `PODIUM_QDRANT_INFERENCE_MODEL`) are not read anywhere in serverboot. The `Put` signature only accepts a precomputed `[]float32`, so there is no text-in ingest path. Suggested direction: add a capability accessor to `vector.Provider` (for example `SelfEmbeds() bool` or a small capability struct), thread the vectorizer/inference-model config through the three managed backends, and relax `openVectorAndEmbedder` so a self-embedding backend can run without an `EmbeddingProvider`.

### - [ ] F-9.1.2 — `LocalSearchProvider` SPI has no implementation or wiring on the consumer side [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The `LocalSearchProvider` row describes an optional pluggable SPI for the local-overlay index: "Same SPI as `RegistrySearchProvider`; backends include `sqlite-vec`, a local pgvector instance, or any managed vector service. Embedding-provider selection follows the same rules as the registry-side path." No Go symbol named `LocalSearchProvider` exists anywhere in the codebase; the only references are in spec and docs prose. The MCP server implements the local-overlay search as fixed BM25 (cmd/podium-mcp/local_search.go:23-67) and imports neither pkg/vector nor pkg/embedding (confirmed by grep over cmd/podium-mcp). The MCP config struct (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:70-91) and `loadConfig` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:93-120) expose no vector-backend, embedding-provider, or local-search selector, so an operator cannot configure an external semantic backend for the workspace overlay as the spec describes (and as §6.4.1 and §13 reference). Suggested direction: either reuse the `vector.Provider` plus `embedding.Provider` SPIs from the MCP server behind a `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND`/`PODIUM_EMBEDDING_PROVIDER` path for the overlay index, or narrow the spec table to state that the local overlay is BM25-only today.

### - [ ] F-9.1.3 — NotificationProvider default "Email + webhook" has no email implementation [Low] — OPEN

(gap) The `NotificationProvider` row lists the default as "Email + webhook." The notification package provides `Noop` (id "noop"), `LogProvider` (id "log"), `Webhook` (id "webhook"), and `MultiProvider` (id "multi") in pkg/notification/notification.go:57-147; there is no email or SMTP provider despite the `Notification` struct carrying a `Recipients []string` field (pkg/notification/notification.go:42) that would feed one. The serverboot selector `openNotifier` (internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:77-108) dispatches only "noop", "log", "webhook", and "multi", and warns on any other value. An operator cannot select email delivery. Suggested direction: add an SMTP-backed provider that consumes `Recipients`, register it in `openNotifier`, or amend the table default to the set the binary actually ships.

### - [ ] F-9.1.4 — RegistryAuditSink default "Separate Postgres table within RegistryStore" is not implemented [Low] — OPEN

(gap) The `RegistryAuditSink` row states the default is a "Separate Postgres table within `RegistryStore`" and that the sink is "logically distinct, separately mockable, separately routable." The `audit.Sink` interface exists and is distinct and mockable (pkg/audit/audit.go:95-98), with `Memory` and `FileSink` implementations. The `store.Store` interface (pkg/store/store.go:131-156) defines no audit-event methods, and serverboot wires a file-backed sink via `openAuditSink`, which returns a `*audit.FileSink` (internal/serverboot/audit_anchor.go:22-26 and serverboot.go:349-352). No Postgres-table-backed audit sink exists, so the table's stated default backing is absent even for the standard (Postgres) deployment. Suggested direction: add a Postgres-table sink for the standard deployment, or revise the table to describe the file-backed default that ships today.

### - [ ] F-9.1.5 — Standalone defaults for RegistrySearchProvider and EmbeddingProvider are not realized by the binary [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The table lists `RegistrySearchProvider` default as "`pgvector` (standard) / `sqlite-vec` (standalone)" and `EmbeddingProvider` default as "`ollama` (standalone) / `openai` (standard)." The standalone bootstrap does not default either to those values: `LoadConfig` sets `vectorBackend: os.Getenv("PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND")` and `embeddingProvider: os.Getenv("PODIUM_EMBEDDING_PROVIDER")` with no fallback (internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:544-545), and the factories treat the empty string as "none" (internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:684-685 and 723-725). A zero-flag standalone server therefore runs BM25-only with vector search disabled until the operator sets both variables, rather than defaulting to sqlite-vec with ollama. This is consistent with the §13 standalone description that embeddings are opt-in, so the divergence is between the §9.1 table's "default" column and the operative standalone behavior. Suggested direction: align the table's standalone default column with the opt-in behavior the binary implements (BM25-only until configured), or have the standalone path default `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND` to `sqlite-vec` and `PODIUM_EMBEDDING_PROVIDER` to `ollama` to match the stated defaults.
## F-9.2 — 9.2 Plugin Distribution

_Reviewed spec/09-extensibility.md against the implementation (re-run against main e41f44e)._

Section 9.2 is short and largely conceptual. It makes three concrete assertions: plugins ship as in-process Go modules importable into a registry build, a deployment that needs a custom `IdentityProvider` or `GitProvider` builds a binary from source with the plugin imported, and a community plugin registry is hosted at the project's public URL. The compile-time in-process model holds on main: there is no dynamic plugin loader anywhere (`plugin.Open`, `hashicorp/go-plugin`, or `.so` loading all return nothing), so the "in-process Go module" framing is consistent with the code. The SPI interfaces named by §9.1 exist as Go interfaces (`identity.Provider` at `pkg/identity/identity.go:36`, `webhook.Provider` at `pkg/layer/webhook/webhook.go:32`, `typeprovider.Provider`, `vector.Provider`, `embedding.Provider`, and others). The weak point is the "imported into a build" claim for the two SPIs §9.2 names by example: only `TypeProvider` has a registration seam an imported plugin can use (`typeprovider.Default.Register`), while neither `IdentityProvider` nor `GitProvider` is consumed by any registry build path, so importing a custom implementation into a source build does not change behavior. The community-plugin-registry assertion has no corresponding code artifact. All four prior findings remain open. F-9.2.1 is corrected: the prior run cited a `trusted-headers` switch at `serverboot.go:284-295` and `server.HeaderIdentityResolver`, both of which were feature-branch code that is absent on main; the inconsistency persists but for a stronger reason, since on main the server never selects or instantiates any `identity.Provider` at all. F-9.2.2, F-9.2.3, and F-9.2.4 are still open with refreshed line numbers.

### - [ ] F-9.2.1 — Custom `IdentityProvider` cannot be wired into a built binary through any seam [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §9.2 states "A deployment that needs a custom `IdentityProvider` or `GitProvider` builds a registry binary from source with the plugin imported." This implies that importing a custom `identity.Provider` into a source build makes the binary use it. The `identity.Provider` SPI is defined at `pkg/identity/identity.go:36-43` (`ID()`, `Resolve(ctx)`), with two built-in implementations `OAuthDeviceCode` and `InjectedSessionToken` in the same file. On the current main tree no code anywhere instantiates or consumes an `identity.Provider`: a repo-wide search for `identity.Provider` outside `pkg/identity/` returns nothing, and the server never constructs `OAuthDeviceCode` or `InjectedSessionToken`. The four non-test importers of `pkg/identity` use unrelated symbols: `cmd/podium/login.go:53` uses the concrete `identity.DeviceCodeFlow` (defined at `pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:32`) plus `KeychainStore`; `cmd/podium/status.go:63` uses `KeychainStore`; `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:330` uses `NewRuntimeKeyRegistry`; and `pkg/registry/server/runtime_endpoint.go:13` uses `RuntimeKey` and `ParsePublicKeyPEM`. The server's `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` value (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:545`) is only passed to `server.StartupConfig.Validate()` for the public-mode mutual-exclusion guard (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:629`, guard at `pkg/registry/server/config_validate.go:28-34`) and echoed into the mode banner (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:644-645`); no code branches on it to select a provider implementation. The MCP server attaches identity by reading a session token from env or file and setting `Authorization: Bearer <tok>` directly (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:706-707`, `currentToken` at `:753`), without going through the `identity.Provider` SPI. There is no `typeprovider.Default`-style registration point for `identity.Provider`, so an imported custom provider has no attachment point and a source build cannot use it without editing the server. Note for reviewers: the prior audit ran on a feature branch and cited a `trusted-headers` switch at `serverboot.go:284-295` wiring `server.HeaderIdentityResolver`; that code does not exist on main, so the inconsistency is stronger here, since main wires no identity provider at all. Suggested direction: either add an identity-provider registration seam analogous to `typeprovider.Default.Register` (a process-global registry keyed by provider ID, consulted by the server when selecting the resolver), or soften §9.2 to state that the `IdentityProvider` SPI is not yet consumed by a registry build and use a different example SPI.

### - [ ] F-9.2.2 — `GitProvider` SPI is unused by any registry build path [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §9.2 names `GitProvider` as the second example of a custom plugin a deployment imports into a registry build, and §9.1 lists `GitProvider` as the SPI for "Webhook signature verification and Git fetch semantics, used by the built-in `git` `LayerSourceProvider`." The `GitProvider` SPI is implemented at `pkg/layer/webhook/webhook.go:32-37` (`Provider` interface with `ID()` and `Verify(body, signature, secret)`) plus built-ins `GitHub`, `GitLab`, and `Bitbucket`. The package doc (`pkg/layer/webhook/webhook.go:1-7`) states this is the §7.3.1 inbound webhook signature verification used by the built-in `git` source provider. On main, no non-test code imports `pkg/layer/webhook`: a repo-wide importer search outside tests returns nothing, and a search for `webhook.Provider`, `webhook.GitHub`, or a `.Verify(body...)` call in non-test code returns nothing. The server has no inbound Git-webhook signature route; the only ingest trigger surfaced is the polling endpoint `/v1/layers/reingest` (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:106`, handler at `:383`), and the server's `webhooks.go` handles the separate outbound-webhook concept. Because the SPI is consumed by nothing and has no registration seam, building a binary "with the plugin imported" for a custom `GitProvider` does not change any behavior. Suggested direction: wire the `pkg/layer/webhook` `GitProvider` SPI into the inbound ingest path with a registration seam custom providers can extend, or update §9.2 to name an SPI that a registry build actually consumes.

### - [ ] F-9.2.3 — SPI selection is by hardcoded switch with no registration seam (only TypeProvider is pluggable by import) [Low] — OPEN

(gap) §9.2 describes the distribution mechanism that §9.1 cross-references for custom backends; §9.1 says custom `RegistrySearchProvider` backends "register through this SPI as Go-module plugins (§9.2)." In the implementation, only `TypeProvider` offers a registration seam reachable by an imported plugin: `pkg/typeprovider/typeprovider.go:58` exposes the process-global `Default` registry and `Register` (`pkg/typeprovider/typeprovider.go:78`). The other selectable SPIs are resolved by closed `switch` statements that return an `unknown ...` error on any value the switch does not enumerate: embedding providers in `openEmbedder` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:700-736`, default arm at `:736` returns `unknown PODIUM_EMBEDDING_PROVIDER`) and vector backends in `openVectorBackend` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:739-783`, default arm at `:783` returns `unknown PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND`). A custom `EmbeddingProvider` or `RegistrySearchProvider` imported into a source build cannot be selected through `PODIUM_EMBEDDING_PROVIDER` or `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND` without editing the switch, so the "register through this SPI as Go-module plugins" mechanism is realized for one SPI rather than across the SPI surface §9.2 implies. Suggested direction: introduce a per-SPI registry analogous to `typeprovider.Default` (or a single provider-registry abstraction) that the bootstrap path consults before falling through to the built-in switch, so imported plugins register a backend by ID.

### - [ ] F-9.2.4 — "Community plugin registry hosted at the project's public URL" has no code artifact [Info] — OPEN

(gap) §9.2 line 32 asserts in present tense that "A community plugin registry is hosted at the project's public URL." This is an external-hosting claim with no corresponding code contract, and the repo contains no plugin-registry client, no registry URL constant, and no plugin-index format. The same sentence is mirrored in `docs/deployment/extending.md:51` without a concrete URL. The closest concrete artifact is a separate concept, the "reference registry with curated example artifacts" mentioned in `spec/01-overview.md:121` and `docs/getting-started/why-podium.md:132`, which is a content/artifact registry rather than a registry of SPI plugins. No defect in code follows from this, since hosting a community registry is an out-of-band operational concern; this is recorded so the assertion can be confirmed against actual hosting or restated as forward-looking. Suggested direction: confirm the plugin registry exists at a named URL, or rephrase the sentence to describe the intended hosting rather than asserting it is currently hosted.
## F-9.3 — 9.3 Forward Compatibility for Out-of-Process Plugins

_Reviewed spec/09-extensibility.md against the implementation._

Section 9.3 describes constraints on the §9.1 SPIs so they remain source-compatible if a future out-of-process plugin protocol lands. Most of the prose is forward-looking and explicitly uncommitted ("What's not committed"), which yields no contract to verify. The one present-tense, verifiable claim is: "The default `RegistryStore`, `HarnessAdapter`, `LayerSourceProvider`, etc. implementations conform to these constraints today." I checked every built-in SPI interface against the seven constraints (cancellable, wire-serializable, no shared state, structured errors, restartable, idempotent, bounded). Several built-ins conform (store.Store, vector.Provider, embedding.Provider, identity.Provider, objectstore.Provider, notification.Provider, source.Provider all take `context.Context` first on their work methods). Four named or in-scope built-ins violate one or more constraints, the most serious being `MaterializationHook` defined as a `func` type, which the spec explicitly forbids.

### - [ ] F-9.3.1 — MaterializationHook is a func type, which §9.3 explicitly forbids [High] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 9.3 "Wire-serializable inputs and outputs" states: "No Go channels, no closures, no `func` types, no `interface{}` without a stable encoding, no opaque pointers to in-process state." Section 9.3 also asserts the §9.1 SPIs "are designed today to make that transition source-compatible," and `MaterializationHook` is a §9.1 SPI (table row in §9.1, line 24). The implementation defines the SPI as a function type: `pkg/materialize/hook.go:8` declares `type HookFunc func(file adapter.File) (out adapter.File, drop bool, err error)`, consumed by `Materialize(destination string, files []adapter.File, hooks []HookFunc)` at `pkg/materialize/hook.go:14`. A `func` type cannot be wire-serialized and has no interface contract that an out-of-process binary could re-implement, so this SPI cannot be shipped out-of-process without a signature change. The same definition also violates the "Cancellable" constraint because it takes no `context.Context`. Suggested direction: model the hook as a named interface with a context-first method, for example `type Hook interface { ID() string; Apply(ctx context.Context, f adapter.File) (out adapter.File, drop bool, err error) }`, and adapt the existing function-based call sites to it.

### - [ ] F-9.3.2 — SignatureProvider Sign/Verify lack context despite performing network IO [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 9.3 "Cancellable" requires: "Every method takes a `context.Context` (or equivalent) as the first parameter. Long-running work checks for cancellation; deadlines are respected." `SignatureProvider` is a §9.1 SPI. The interface at `pkg/sign/sign.go:42-49` declares `Sign(contentHash string) (string, error)` and `Verify(contentHash, signature string) error` with no context parameter. The built-in Sigstore implementation performs network calls to Fulcio and Rekor (`pkg/sign/sigstore.go` imports `net/http` at line 15; `Sign` mints a certificate and writes to Rekor; `Verify` fetches from Rekor at line 205), which is exactly the long-running, cancellable work the constraint targets. Because the signature provides no context, the implementation hardcodes `context.Background()` at `pkg/sign/sigstore.go:117` and `pkg/sign/sigstore.go:205`, so caller deadlines and cancellation cannot propagate. This contradicts the present-tense claim that built-ins conform. Suggested direction: add `ctx context.Context` as the first parameter to `Sign` and `Verify`, thread it to `mintCert` and `fetchRekor`, and remove the internal `context.Background()` calls.

### - [ ] F-9.3.3 — HarnessAdapter.Adapt lacks a context parameter [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 9.3 "Cancellable" requires every SPI method to take a `context.Context` (or equivalent) as the first parameter, and §9.3 names `HarnessAdapter` explicitly among the built-ins that "conform to these constraints today." The interface at `pkg/adapter/adapter.go:39-48` declares `Adapt(src Source) ([]File, error)` with no context. Call sites already hold a context that is dropped at the boundary: `pkg/sync/sync.go:118` and `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:431` and `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:501` call `a.Adapt(...)` from request-scoped paths. Adapter work is CPU-bound today, so the practical impact is lower than the network-bound SPIs, but the spec's wording is unconditional ("Every method") and names this SPI directly, so the built-in does not match the claim. Suggested direction: change the signature to `Adapt(ctx context.Context, src Source) ([]File, error)` and pass the in-scope context at the three call sites.

### - [ ] F-9.3.4 — IngestLinter and TypeProvider validation methods lack a context parameter [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 9.3 "Cancellable" requires a context-first parameter on every SPI method. Two §9.1 SPIs omit it. The `IngestLinter` rule SPI at `pkg/lint/lint.go:62-67` declares `Check(reg *filesystem.Registry, records []filesystem.ArtifactRecord) []Diagnostic` with no context; several rules iterate the entire record set and resolve cross-artifact references (for example `ruleProseReferenceResolution` at `pkg/lint/body_rules.go:111`, `ruleDomainImportsResolve` at `pkg/lint/domain_imports.go:23`, and `ruleDomainImportCycle` at `pkg/lint/domain_imports.go:62`), so the work is unbounded with registry size and is the kind of long-running operation the constraint targets. The `TypeProvider` SPI at `pkg/typeprovider/typeprovider.go:37-41` declares `Validate(*manifest.Artifact) []Diagnostic` with no context. Both are CPU-bound and the blast radius is small, but the present-tense conformance claim does not hold for them. Suggested direction: add `ctx context.Context` as the first parameter to `Rule.Check` and `Provider.Validate`, and check `ctx.Err()` in the loop bodies of the cross-artifact rules.

### - [ ] F-9.3.5 — No static analysis enforces the §9.3 SPI constraints; built-in conformance is unguarded [Info] — OPEN

(gap) Section 9.3 makes a present-tense claim that built-ins conform, and the companion verification item at spec/11-verification.md:29 says an "SPI wire-compatibility test" performs "Static analysis [that] fails the build on regressions." No such analyzer exists in the repository. A repo-wide search for a context-first or signature-conformance checker (under tools/, test/, pkg/, internal/) returns only unrelated matches, and there is no `golang.org/x/tools/go/analysis` analyzer for SPI signatures. The existing `*_Conformance` tests (for example `pkg/store/conformance_test.go`, `pkg/vector/vector_test.go`) exercise runtime backend behavior, not method-signature compatibility. Without the guard, the divergences in F-9.3.1 through F-9.3.4 can accrue undetected, and the §9.3 claim of present-day conformance is not mechanically maintained. The static-analysis test itself is a §11 obligation rather than a §9.3 one, so this is recorded as an observation bearing on the §9.3 conformance claim. Suggested direction: add an analyzer that walks the exported method signatures of each registered built-in SPI implementation and fails when a work-performing method omits a leading `context.Context` or uses a `func`/channel argument.
## F-9.4 — 9.4 Building on Podium from outside the registry

_Reviewed spec/09-extensibility.md against the implementation._

Section 9.4 is mostly conceptual prose describing external composition patterns, but its "Programmatic curation" subsection includes a concrete, code-illustrated workflow that depends on specific CLI flags and SDK operations. The SDK side is implemented and matches the spec example: `Client.from_env()`, `search_artifacts(query, type=, top_k=)` returning descriptors with `.id` and `.score`, plus `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `load_artifact`, and `dependents_of` exist in both `sdks/podium-py` and `sdks/podium-ts`. The webhook events named in the spec (`artifact.deprecated`, `artifact.published`, `layer.history_rewritten`) are defined and published, `podium lint` exists for pre-merge CI, and `podium layer reingest <id>` exists for layer source bridges. The break is on the materialization side: the `podium sync` command shown in the spec example does not accept `--include`, and scope filtering is never applied in the sync execution path. The findings below document that gap and two related issues.

### - [ ] F-9.4.1 — `podium sync` does not accept `--include` (or `--exclude`/`--type`) flags [High] — OPEN

(gap) The "Programmatic curation" subsection of §9.4 presents a complete code example as "the recommended answer" to selecting a subset of artifacts: the script collects artifact IDs from `search_artifacts` and then invokes `podium sync --harness claude-code --target /Users/me/.claude/ --include <id> ...`, one `--include` per chosen ID, with the stated guarantee that "the on-disk result is reproducible from the include list." The implemented `syncCmd` in cmd/podium/main.go:186-194 defines only `--registry`, `--target`, `--harness`, `--dry-run`, `--json`, `--watch`, and `--overlay`. There is no `--include`, `--exclude`, or `--type` flag. Passing `--include` to `podium sync` triggers a `flag provided but not defined: -include` parse error and exit code 2 (cmd/podium/main.go:196-198 via `parseExit`). The `--add-include`/`--remove-include` flags at cmd/podium/main.go:374-375 belong to the `profile edit` subcommand, and the `--type` flag at cmd/podium/main.go:490 belongs to the `search` read CLI, so neither serves the documented `sync` invocation. The documented primary workflow does not run as written. Suggested direction: add repeatable `--include`/`--exclude` and a `--type` flag to `syncCmd`, build a `sync.ScopeFilter` from them, and pass it into `sync.Options` so `sync.Run` applies it (see F-9.4.2).

### - [ ] F-9.4.2 — Scope filtering is never applied in the sync execution path; `ScopeFilter` is dead code [High] — OPEN

(bug) Even setting the missing CLI flags aside, the sync executor never narrows the artifact set. `sync.Run` in pkg/sync/sync.go:72-186 walks every visible record (pkg/sync/sync.go:94-99), optionally merges overlay records, and adapts every record without consulting any include/exclude/type filter. The `sync.Options` struct (pkg/sync/sync.go:37-48) has no scope field. A `ScopeFilter` type with an `Apply` method exists at pkg/sync/scope.go:13-45, and the `Profile` / `TargetEntry` config types carry `Include`/`Exclude`/`Type` YAML fields (pkg/sync/config.go:40-46, 49-57), but a repo-wide search shows `ScopeFilter` is referenced in production code only inside its own definition file. `syncCmd` reads only `cfg.Defaults.Registry` from sync.yaml (cmd/podium/main.go:204-209) and never reads `cfg.Profiles`. The result is that neither command-line scoping nor sync.yaml profile scoping takes effect; a profile's `include:` list is silently ignored and a sync always materializes the full effective view. This contradicts §9.4's "Curate, then sync" guarantee and the reproducibility claim. Suggested direction: resolve the active profile (or command-line filters) into a `ScopeFilter`, call `f.Apply(records)` in `sync.Run` after the walk and overlay merge but before adaptation, and add an end-to-end test that asserts an excluded artifact is not written.

### - [ ] F-9.4.3 — Curation example targets a server-backed registry, but `podium sync` is filesystem-source only [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The §9.4 example constructs the discovery client with `Client.from_env()`, which reads `PODIUM_REGISTRY` and is documented in the SDK to accept a server URL (sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:84-93). It then hands the selected IDs to `podium sync` with no `--registry` argument. The implemented `sync.Run` opens the registry exclusively as a filesystem path via `filesystem.Open(opts.RegistryPath)` (pkg/sync/sync.go:90) and its doc comment states it "does not consult any HTTP service" (pkg/sync/sync.go:65-68). `syncCmd` requires `--registry` (or `defaults.registry` in sync.yaml) and exits with code 2 otherwise (cmd/podium/main.go:210-213). `ResolveRegistryPath` passes `http(s)://` URLs through unchanged (pkg/sync/config.go:75-77, and TestResolveRegistryPath_URLPassesThrough), yet `sync.Run` would then fail because `filesystem.Open` cannot open a URL. The example therefore mixes a server-backed discovery client with a materialization step that only reads a local filesystem registry, and it omits the required filesystem `--registry`. Suggested direction: either make the example pass an explicit filesystem `--registry` (and clarify that discovery and materialization can read different sources), or, if server-source sync is intended, implement an HTTP-backed path in `sync.Run` for `http(s)://` registries so the documented invocation works against the same registry used for discovery.
## F-10.0 — 10 MVP Build Sequence

_Reviewed spec/10-mvp-build-sequence.md against the implementation._

The build sequence lists deliverables across the initial phases (0–4) and the enterprise phases (5–19). I verified each phase's claimed capabilities against the code by searching the whole repository for the named commands, flags, endpoints, SPIs, providers, and artifacts. The implementation is substantially complete: every named HTTP endpoint (`load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, `load_artifact`), every named harness adapter (`none`, `claude-code`, `codex`, `claude-desktop`, `claude-cowork`, `cursor`, `gemini`, `opencode`, `pi`, `hermes`), both identity providers (`oauth-device-code`, `injected-session-token`), the LayerSourceProvider SPI with `git` and `local` sources, the LayerComposer, OIDC and SCIM, the DOMAIN.md parser with `extends:` hidden-parent resolution and discovery rendering rules, the versioning invariants (session-consistent latest, immutability, force-push tolerance), the dependency graph and impact CLI, the audit hash chain, the Python and TypeScript SDKs, and the deployment artifacts (Helm chart, Grafana dashboard, runbook) all exist. The example reference registry exists under `testdata/registries/reference`. The gaps cluster in the Phase 3 client config surface for `podium sync` and the Phase 10 user-defined-layer cap.

### - [x] F-10.0.1 — User-defined-layer cap is not enforced (Phase 10) [High] — CLOSED

(gap) Phase 10 lists "user-defined-layer cap" as a deliverable. The cap is specified concretely elsewhere: §1.1 and §7.3.1 state "Default cap: 3 user-defined layers per identity, configurable per tenant", §7.3.1 maps exceeding it to a `quota.*` error, and §11.5 lists "the user-defined-layer cap is enforced" as a required verification test. The layer-register HTTP handler in `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:183-275` performs no count check before storing a new user-defined layer; it sets the implicit `users:[owner]` visibility (layers.go:227-229), assigns an order, and calls `PutLayerConfig` without ever counting the caller's existing user-defined layers or comparing against a per-tenant limit. The quota model has no layer dimension: `store.Quota` (pkg/store/store.go:36-41) holds only `StorageBytes`, `SearchQPS`, `MaterializeRate`, and `AuditVolumePerDay`, and `core.QuotaInfo` / `Registry.Quota` (pkg/registry/core/quota.go) measure storage bytes only. A repository-wide search for a layer-count limit, `MaxUserLayers`, a `quota.*` layer error, or a default of 3 returns no enforcement code. A user can register an unbounded number of user-defined layers. Suggested direction: add a per-tenant `MaxUserLayers` quota field (default 3), count existing `UserDefined` layers for the owner in `register`, and return a `quota.*` error (HTTP 429 per the §7.3.1 quota convention) when the cap is reached.

**Resolution (commit `39d402d`):** Closed by the canonical fix F-1.4.1, which implements exactly the suggested direction: `store.Quota` gained a `MaxUserLayers` dimension (default 3) persisted across all store backends, and `register` counts the owner's existing user-defined layers and rejects the over-cap registration with `quota.layer_count_exceeded` at HTTP 429.

### - [ ] F-10.0.2 — `podium sync` is missing `--include`, `--exclude`, `--type`, and `--profile` flags (Phase 3) [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Phase 3 lists the `podium sync` client config surface as "(default target = CWD; `--include` / `--exclude` / `--type` / `--profile` / `--dry-run`)", and §7.5.1 defines the three scope filters with detailed glob semantics while §7.5.2 defines `--profile` lookup and CLI-override precedence. The `syncCmd` function in `cmd/podium/main.go:177-240` registers only `--registry`, `--target`, `--harness`, `--dry-run`, `--json`, `--watch`, and `--overlay`. There is no `--include`, `--exclude`, `--type`, or `--profile` flag, and `sync.Options` (pkg/sync/sync.go) has no corresponding fields. The default target is CWD (`--target` defaults to `.`) and `--dry-run` is present, so two of the five listed items are satisfied; the four scope-selection flags are absent. The `--config` multi-target mode from §7.5.2 (a `targets:` list, modeled by `config.go:27,48` as `Targets []TargetEntry`) is also not wired to any CLI flag or iteration in `Run`. Suggested direction: add the four flags to `syncCmd`, thread them through `sync.Options`, and apply profile resolution and CLI-override precedence per §7.5.2.

### - [ ] F-10.0.3 — `ScopeFilter` is implemented but never applied on the `podium sync` path (Phase 3) [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Beyond the missing CLI flags in F-10.0.2, the underlying filter mechanism that would honor a sync.yaml profile is unwired. `pkg/sync/scope.go` defines `ScopeFilter{Include, Exclude, Types}` with an `Apply` method whose doc comment reads "ScopeFilter narrows a record set per §7.5.1: --include, --exclude, --type" (scope.go:10), but `ScopeFilter.Apply` has no production caller: the only references repository-wide are its own definition and `pkg/sync/scope_test.go`. `sync.Run` (pkg/sync/sync.go:72-186) walks every record from `filesystem.Open(...).Walk(...)`, merges any overlay, and materializes all of them through the adapter without reading `sync.yaml` profiles or applying any filter; `Run` and `Watch` contain no reference to `Profile`, `Include`, `Exclude`, or `Filter`. The `SyncConfig` type does carry `Profiles` and `TargetEntry` definitions, and `override` / `save-as` / `profile edit` read them, so the data model exists; the main sync path ignores it. The practical consequence is that even a profile declared in `sync.yaml` does not narrow a plain `podium sync`, contradicting §7.5.2's "Profile lookup. `--profile <name>` selects an entry under `profiles:`. The profile's fields are merged on top of `defaults:`." Suggested direction: in `sync.Run`, resolve the active profile (CLI `--profile`, else the lock file's `profile:` field, else `defaults.profile`), build a `ScopeFilter` from it plus any CLI overrides, and call `ScopeFilter.Apply` on the record set before materialization.
## F-11.0 — 11 Verification

_Reviewed spec/11-verification.md against the implementation (re-run against main e41f44e)._

Section 11 is a verification plan that enumerates the tests the project is expected to carry. It contains few standalone behavioral contracts, but several of its bullets assert concrete, falsifiable properties (specific error codes, dual client/server enforcement, named cross-mode equivalence tests, and a reference fixture that exercises every visibility mode with signed artifacts). I re-verified the named test scenarios and their concrete claims against the current main tree. The error codes and audit events named in the plan (`auth.untrusted_runtime`, `registry.invalid_argument`, `materialize.signature_invalid`, `ingest.immutable_violation`, `layer.history_rewritten`, `config.layer_path_ambiguous`, `artifact.published`, `layer.ingested`) all exist on main and are cited by tests, the injected-session-token and OAuth device-code identity providers are present, the `--layer-path` dispatch logic is covered by `internal/serverboot/layer_path_test.go`, and the server-side `top_k > 50` rejection and browse-mode `total_matched` behavior match the plan. Of the five prior findings, none were resolved by the move to main, four remain open with refreshed line numbers, and one (F-11.0.2) was corrected: the original cited `pkg/registry/server/layer_visibility.go` and a `.podium/layers.yaml` loader, both of which are absent on main; on main the relevant behavior is that `NewFromFilesystem` hardcodes `Public: true` for every layer and there is no per-layer visibility loader at all, which makes the example-registry gap broader rather than narrower.

### - [ ] F-11.0.1 — SDK does not enforce `top_k > 50` client-side [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Spec line 11 (Search browse mode test) states that `top_k > 50` "is rejected with a structured `registry.invalid_argument` error (enforced both client-side in the SDK and server-side at the registry)." The server-side half is implemented: `pkg/registry/core/core.go:508-509` and `:652-653` return `ErrInvalidArgument` when `opts.TopK > 50`. The client-side half is absent from both SDKs. The Python `search_artifacts` (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:118-136`) and `search_domains` (`:103-116`) accept `top_k` and forward it verbatim in the query parameters with no validation; the only `raise` paths in the client concern HTTP errors and a missing registry env var (`client.py:88`, `:282-283`). The TypeScript `searchArtifacts` (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:134-148`) and `searchDomains` (`:124-131`) likewise forward `topK` without a bound check. The `50` constants present in both SDKs (`client.py:186`, `index.ts:172`) are the §7.6.2 batch-load ID cap, unrelated to the search `top_k` cap. Either add a client-side bound check that raises the structured error before the request is sent, or correct the spec to describe server-side enforcement only.

### - [ ] F-11.0.2 — Example artifact registry cannot configure visibility modes and carries no signed artifacts [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Spec line 69 (Example artifact registry) requires a fixture with "multiple layers exercising every visibility mode (`public`, `organization`, `groups`, `users`), at least one user-defined layer, signed artifacts at multiple sensitivities." The fixture at `testdata/registries/reference/` carries no visibility configuration: there is no `.podium/layers.yaml`, and `.registry-config` contains only `multi_layer: true` and `layer_order:`. On main there is no mechanism that would let the fixture express per-layer visibility through the filesystem load path. `pkg/registry/filesystem` reads no visibility file, and the standalone loader `pkg/registry/server/server.go:227-231` (`NewFromFilesystem`) assigns `Visibility: layer.Visibility{Public: true}` to every layer unconditionally. (The `.podium/layers.yaml` loader and a corresponding `layer_visibility.go` existed on the `feat/layer-visibility-pr` branch but are not present in main e41f44e.) The README at `testdata/registries/reference/README.md:11-12` describes `acme-finance` group scoping and a `users:[joan]` user-defined layer that are never realized in configuration. No artifact in the fixture carries a signature (a repository search for `signature`/`signed`/`sig:` under the fixture returns nothing); only `sensitivity:` fields are present (`low`/`medium` across ten manifests). The only test against the fixture, `test/conformance/reference_registry_test.go`, asserts layer count and a non-empty walk and runs sync through the `none` and `claude-code` adapters; it performs no visibility or signature checks, despite the file comment at lines 30-31 and 64-65 claiming the registry "covers every first-class type, every visibility mode, and every adapter target." Add a per-layer visibility source the filesystem path can read (or wire the fixture through a loader that honors visibility), assign the four visibility modes across layers, add signed artifacts at multiple sensitivities, and extend the conformance test to assert visibility filtering and signature verification.

### - [ ] F-11.0.3 — Filesystem ↔ server byte-equivalence test is absent [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Spec line 33 (Filesystem ↔ server equivalence test) requires a test where "a `podium sync` against a filesystem-source registry and a `podium sync` against `podium serve --standalone --layer-path` pointed at the same directory produce byte-identical materialized output (manifest bodies, bundled resources, harness-adapter output, lock-file `artifacts:` list) for the same target and profile." No such test exists. `test/integration/sync_filesystem_test.go` covers filesystem sync writing a target (`TestPodiumSync_FilesystemSourceWritesTarget`, line 41), dry-run (`:82`), `--layer-path` ambiguity rejection (`:112`, which uses `podium sync --registry`, not `serve --standalone`), unknown-harness rejection (`:138`), and idempotency (`TestPodiumSync_IsIdempotent`, `:164`), but none of these spawn `podium serve --standalone --layer-path` and compare its sync output byte-for-byte against the filesystem-source sync. The `--layer-path` bootstrap dispatch itself is covered at the function level by `internal/serverboot/layer_path_test.go`, but no test diffs the served output against the filesystem output. A repository-wide search for `byte-identical`/`Equivalence` against the server path returns no matching test. Add an integration test that runs both consumers against the same directory and the same profile and diffs the materialized trees and lock-file `artifacts:` lists.

### - [ ] F-11.0.4 — Reference-fixture documentation violates doc-style example-identifier and count rules [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The project doc-style rules (`.claude/rules/doc-style.md`) require placeholder example identifiers (`alice`, `bob`, ...) and forbid real names of project people, and they forbid explicit counts of types. The reference-fixture documentation uses the real name "joan" and an explicit type count. `testdata/registries/reference/README.md:12` reads "`personal/` — joan's user-defined layer (visibility: `users:[joan]`)." and `:14-15` reads "a representative cross-section of the seven first-class types". `testdata/registries/reference/personal/notes/journal/ARTIFACT.md:11` reads "Working notes for joan." Replace "joan" with `alice` (and the layer/visibility identifier accordingly), and reword "the seven first-class types" to remove the count. These `.md` files are in scope for the doc-style rules because the rules apply to all `.md` files in the repository.

### - [ ] F-11.0.5 — Enumerated verification categories have no implementation [Info] — OPEN

(gap) Several test categories the plan enumerates have no implementing tests on main. Spec line 63 (Performance tests) calls for "1K QPS sustained for `search_artifacts`; 100 ingests/min; `load_artifact` p99 < SLO targets"; only Go benchmarks exist (`test/bench/latency_test.go`), whose file header explicitly notes the numbers "are not enforced in CI today" (lines 1-4), and there is no sustained-QPS or ingest-rate test. Spec line 65 (Soak tests) calls for "24h continuous load ... no memory growth, no descriptor leaks"; no soak test exists. Spec line 67 (Chaos tests) calls for Postgres failover, object-storage stalls, network partitions, IdP outage, and full-disk scenarios; a repository search for `chaos`/`failover`/`partition`/`soak` returns no test. Spec line 21 (Materialization test) calls for verifying "partial-download recovery" and "presigned URL refresh on expiry"; `cmd/podium-mcp/large_resources.go:54-86` retries the same presigned URL with exponential backoff (the comment at lines 19-25 states this build does not re-fetch a fresh URL), and no test exercises refresh-on-expiry or partial-download recovery as named. The spec-coverage tool `tools/speccov` tracks citations at section granularity, so a few §11-citing tests mark the section covered and these per-bullet categories are not individually surfaced as uncovered. These are aspirational plan items rather than broken contracts, so this is recorded as an observation. Track them as deferred verification work or annotate the plan with the build phase that delivers each category.
## F-12.0 — 12 Operational Risks and Mitigations

_Reviewed spec/12-operational-risks-and-mitigations.md against the implementation._

Section 12 is a risk/mitigation table. Each row names a risk and the concrete mechanisms that mitigate it. I verified each stated mitigation against code. Most mechanisms are present and wired: configurable discovery bounds (`max_depth`, `fold_below_artifacts`, `target_response_tokens` in pkg/manifest/types.go and pkg/registry/core/core.go), `podium domain analyze` sparsity/pass-through/fold-split reporting (pkg/registry/core/analyze.go), `featured`/`deprioritize`/`include` merge (pkg/domain/domain.go), provenance markers and adapter trust regions (pkg/adapter), signature verification on materialization and sandbox profiles, rate limiting (pkg/registry/server/rate_limit.go), read-only mode (readonly.go), freeze and break-glass (pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go), storage quotas, `podium admin show-effective` (cmd/podium/admin.go, pkg/registry/core/admin.go), startup public-mode/identity-provider mutual-exclusion validation (config_validate.go), untrusted-runtime rejection and unsigned-token rejection (pkg/identity), `sensitivity`/`unlisted`/`search_visibility: direct-only` fields (pkg/manifest/types.go), conformance suite and capability matrix (pkg/adapter), `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go), hash-chained audit with anchoring scheduler (pkg/audit, internal/serverboot), and size lints (pkg/lint/size_rules.go). Several named mitigations are absent or only partially wired; those are listed below.

### - [ ] F-12.0.1 — Inbound ingest-webhook verification is never wired into a request path [High] — OPEN

(gap) The "Webhook secret compromise" row states "webhook signature verified on every delivery; failed verifications log `ingest.webhook_invalid` and never reach the content store." The layer-register response advertises an inbound delivery endpoint at `/v1/layers/{id}/webhook` (pkg/registry/server/layers.go:271) and generates a per-layer HMAC secret (layers.go:254-262). The verification code exists in pkg/layer/webhook/webhook.go (GitHub/GitLab/Bitbucket `Verify`), but no HTTP route is registered for `/v1/layers/{id}/webhook`: server.go registers only `/v1/layers`, `/v1/layers/reorder`, `/v1/layers/reingest`, and `/v1/layers/update` (layers.go:93-107), plus the unrelated outbound `/v1/webhooks` receiver CRUD (server.go:339-340). A repo-wide search shows `pkg/layer/webhook`'s `Verify` is never called from any server flow, and `ingest.webhook_invalid` is never emitted outside doc comments (the only `provider.Verify` call site is cmd/podium/sign.go, which verifies content signatures, not webhooks). The advertised endpoint returns the default mux 404, so the stated mitigation does not run. Suggested direction: register a handler for `/v1/layers/{id}/webhook` that loads the layer's `WebhookSecret`, selects the GitProvider by source, calls `Verify` on the raw body, emits `ingest.webhook_invalid` on `ErrInvalidSignature`/`ErrUnsupportedScheme` before any content fetch, and triggers reingest only on success.

### - [ ] F-12.0.2 — Per-layer webhook secret cannot be rotated via `podium layer update` [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The "Webhook secret compromise" row states the per-layer HMAC secret is "rotated via `podium layer update`." The server update handler explicitly documents the opposite: "The store-bound identifying fields (TenantID, ID, SourceType, CreatedAt) and webhook secrets are immutable" (pkg/registry/server/layers.go:118-119), and the handler applies only Ref, Root, LocalPath, Owner, and visibility fields (layers.go:151-174); it never touches `WebhookSecret`. The CLI `layerUpdate` exposes flags for ref, root, local, owner, public, organization, group, and user, with no flag to set or regenerate a webhook secret (cmd/podium/layer.go:66-126). There is no other command or endpoint that rotates the secret. Suggested direction: add a `--rotate-webhook-secret` flag to `podium layer update` and an update-handler branch that regenerates `WebhookSecret` via `generateSecret()` and returns the new value once, or correct the spec to name the actual rotation path.

### - [ ] F-12.0.3 — "offline" status is returned only by load_artifact, not by load_domain, search_domains, or search_artifacts [Medium] — OPEN
