(inconsistency) The "Registry as a single point of failure for hosts" row states "Fresh `load_domain` / `search_domains` / `search_artifacts` returns an explicit 'offline' status that hosts can surface." In the MCP bridge, only `load_artifact` sets `status: "offline"` (and only in always-revalidate/offline-first modes, cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:342). `load_domain` and `search_domains` both route through `proxyGet`, which returns `errorResult(err.Error())` on any registry failure with no cache fallback and no offline status (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:733-739). `search_artifacts` likewise returns `errorResult(err.Error())` on registry failure (cmd/podium-mcp/search_artifacts.go:14-16). The resolution cache stores only (id, version) to content-hash mappings, so there is no cached domain or search result to serve. Three of the four meta-tools named in the mitigation do not surface the explicit offline status. Suggested direction: on registry-unreachable in offline-first/always-revalidate modes, return a result carrying `status: "offline"` for the three discovery/search tools (even an empty result set with the status set), or scope the spec claim to load_artifact.

### - [ ] F-12.0.4 — No ingest-time lint for thin descriptions or colliding summaries [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The "Manifest description quality" row states "Ingest-time lint flags thin descriptions and clusters of artifacts with colliding summaries." The registered lint rule set (pkg/lint/lint.go:72-86) contains required-field, skill-compliance, name-syntax, semver, hook-consistency, effort-hint, bundled-resource-size, manifest-size, skill-body, prose-reference, and domain-import rules. None checks description length/quality, and none performs a corpus-level comparison to detect artifacts with colliding or near-duplicate summaries. A repo-wide search finds no description-length or summary-collision check in pkg/lint. The complementary "learn-from-usage reranking" half is also absent (see F-12.0.9). Suggested direction: add a lint rule that flags descriptions below a configurable minimum length and a corpus-level rule that clusters artifacts by summary similarity and warns on collisions.

### - [ ] F-12.0.5 — DOMAIN.md `include:` globs are not expanded into cross-cutting views and have no server-side cache [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The "Catalog grows too large" row credits "`DOMAIN.md include:` curates cross-cutting views," and the "Recursive globs in `DOMAIN.md` are expensive" row states "Glob expansion is cached server-side per artifact-version snapshot; cache invalidation is keyed on ingest events." The `include` field is parsed and merged across DOMAIN.md layers (pkg/domain/domain.go:42-46), but it is never resolved into an artifact list anywhere in pkg/registry/core: a search for `.Include` consumption finds only the merge in pkg/domain, and core.go's load_domain build never reads it. Consequently there is no glob expansion at load_domain time and no server-side glob cache keyed on ingest events. The lint rule globMatchesID exists (pkg/lint/domain_imports.go:201) but is used only for import-resolution warnings, not for building views. Suggested direction: expand `include:` globs into the load_domain cross-cutting section in core, and add a per-artifact-version-snapshot expansion cache invalidated on ingest events, or mark the include-resolution and cache claims as future in the spec.

### - [ ] F-12.0.6 — Layer-config changes and admin grants are not audited [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The "Visibility misconfiguration" row states "Layer config is auditable and version-controlled; admin actions are audited." The audit event types `EventLayerConfigChanged`, `EventLayerUserRegistered`, and `EventAdminGranted` are defined (pkg/audit/audit.go:39-41) and referenced only by the retention classifier (internal/serverboot/audit_retention.go:76-78). They are never emitted at any operation site. The layer endpoints (register/update/unregister/reorder in pkg/registry/server/layers.go) hold no audit sink and emit nothing on mutation. The admin grant/revoke path (pkg/registry/core/admin.go:37-48, GrantAdmin/RevokeAdmin) only writes the store and emits no audit event; the HTTP handler (pkg/registry/server/admin.go:39) does not emit either. The only ingest-side audit hook is the orchestrator's `opts.Emit` for `layer.ingested` (pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:100-101). Admin and layer-config actions therefore are not audited despite the mitigation claim. Suggested direction: wire an audit sink into LayerEndpoint and the admin handlers, emitting `layer.config_changed` on register/update/unregister/reorder, `layer.user_registered` on user-defined layer registration, and `admin.granted` on GrantAdmin (with a corresponding revoke event).

### - [ ] F-12.0.7 — No lint warning for overly broad recursive globs in DOMAIN.md [Low] — OPEN

(gap) The "Recursive globs in `DOMAIN.md` are expensive" row states "Lint warns on overly broad recursive globs." The DOMAIN.md lint rules warn on imports that resolve to zero artifacts (`lint.domain_import_unresolved`, pkg/lint/domain_imports.go:21-52) and on import cycles (`lint.domain_import_cycle`, domain_imports.go:60+), but no rule flags an `include:` pattern as overly broad (for example a purely recursive `**` at the root). A search for broad/expensive/recursive-warn predicates in pkg/lint returns nothing. The unresolved-import lint also matches against the full record corpus rather than a per-identity visible view, so the "in any visible view" wording in the adjacent "imports go stale silently" row is approximated rather than implemented exactly. Suggested direction: add a lint rule that warns when an `include:` pattern expands to an unbounded recursive match or exceeds a configurable breadth threshold.

### - [ ] F-12.0.8 — ETag caching of immutable artifact versions is not implemented [Low] — OPEN

(gap) The "Registry latency on every meta-tool call" row lists "ETag caching of immutable artifact versions" among the latency mitigations. No ETag handling exists in the codebase: a repo-wide search for `ETag`, `If-None-Match`, `304`, and `NotModified` across pkg, cmd, and internal returns no matches. The registry never sets an ETag header and the MCP client uses a bare `&http.Client{}` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:161) that sends no `If-None-Match`. The content-addressed disk cache (resolution_cache.go plus the content cache) provides the latency benefit by avoiding refetch, and Go's default transport supplies HTTP/1.1 keep-alive and HTTP/2, so the keep-alive and disk-cache halves of the row are satisfied; the specific ETag-revalidation mechanism named in the mitigation is absent. Suggested direction: have the load_artifact endpoint set an ETag equal to the content hash and honor `If-None-Match` with 304, and send the cached hash as `If-None-Match` from the MCP client, or drop ETag from the mitigation list since the content-addressed cache already covers the latency goal.

### - [ ] F-12.0.9 — Learn-from-usage reranking is absent [Low] — OPEN

(gap) Three rows credit "learn-from-usage reranking": "Catalog grows too large" ("learn-from-usage reranking surfaces signal-based ordering"), "Manifest description quality" ("Learn-from-usage reranking surfaces underperforming descriptions"), and "`DOMAIN.md` imports go stale silently" ("Learn-from-usage signal surfaces domains whose imports return empty results frequently"). No usage-signal-based ranking exists: searches for learn-from-usage, rerank, usage-signal ordering, popularity, click, telemetry, feedback, and boost across pkg/registry/core (including rrf.go) and the server return nothing relevant. The primary ranking mechanisms (RRF/hybrid search, `featured`/`deprioritize`) are implemented, but the usage-signal feedback loop named in these three rows is not. Suggested direction: implement a usage-signal store that records meta-tool access frequency and feeds it into search/domain ordering and into description-quality and stale-import surfacing, or mark learn-from-usage reranking as a future capability in the spec.
## F-13.1 — 13.1 Reference Topology (13.1.1 Evaluation Deployment / Docker Compose)

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md against the implementation._

I verified the §13.1 standard-topology claims (default and built-in vector backends, default and built-in embedding providers, the Helm chart, and the bare-metal deployment guide) and the §13.1.1 evaluation-deployment claims about the bundled `docker-compose.yml`. The §13.1 component claims are backed by code: `pkg/vector/` ships `pgvector.go`, `pinecone.go`, `weaviate.go`, `qdrant.go`, and `sqlitevec.go`; `pkg/embedding/` ships `openai.go`, `voyage.go`, `cohere.go`, and `ollama.go`; the Helm chart is at `deploy/helm/podium/`; and `docs/deployment/organization.md` provides a bare-metal stand-up guide. The §13.1.1 compose file diverges substantially from the spec. The repo's single `docker-compose.yml` brings up only Postgres, MinIO, and a bucket-creating sidecar. It omits the `registry`, `dex`, and `bootstrap` services that §13.1.1 says the compose stack includes, and it does not implement the documented one-command full-stack evaluation workflow.

### - [ ] F-13.1.1 — docker-compose.yml omits the `registry` service [High] — OPEN

(gap) §13.1.1 states the repo ships a `docker-compose.yml` that "brings up the full stack with one command" and lists, as the first service, `registry`: "the registry binary, configured against the local services below" (spec/13-deployment.md:24-26). The actual compose file at /Users/joan/projects/podium/docker-compose.yml defines only three services: `postgres` (line 16), `minio` (line 33), and `minio-init` (line 59). There is no `registry` service. A repository-wide search for a compose service running the registry binary or a `podium-server` image found none; the `podium-server` image is built and published only by `.github/workflows/release.yml:455-456`, and no compose-style file references it. The file's own header describes it as "Local services for the live integration suite" (line 1), which is a narrower purpose than the spec's evaluation stack. The result is that the documented `docker compose up -d` workflow (spec/13-deployment.md:18-22) does not start a registry, so `podium login` against the stack cannot succeed as written. Suggested direction: either add a `registry` service (plus the `dex` and `bootstrap` services below) so the compose file matches §13.1.1, or amend §13.1.1 to describe the compose file as backing-services-only with a separate `podium serve` step.

### - [ ] F-13.1.2 — docker-compose.yml omits the `dex` OIDC IdP service [High] — OPEN

(gap) §13.1.1 lists a `dex` service: "OIDC IdP for the OAuth device-code flow" (spec/13-deployment.md:29), and the documented workflow runs `podium login    # device-code flow against the bundled Dex IdP` (spec/13-deployment.md:21). No `dex` service exists in /Users/joan/projects/podium/docker-compose.yml. A repository-wide search for `dex` found references only in spec/13-deployment.md, in docs (`docs/deployment/organization.md:96`, `docs/deployment/oidc/keycloak.md:12`), and in the test-infrastructure plan (`TEST_INFRASTRUCTURE_PLAN.md:52,133,147`, which expects Dex via `testcontainers-go`, not via this compose file). Without a Dex container in the compose stack, the device-code login flow the spec advertises has no IdP to authenticate against. Suggested direction: add a `dex` service to the compose file (or update §13.1.1 if the device-code login flow is intended to be exercised only through testcontainers in CI rather than through the bundled compose stack).

### - [ ] F-13.1.3 — docker-compose.yml has no `bootstrap` container; the `minio-init` sidecar only creates the bucket [High] — OPEN

(gap) §13.1.1 lists a `bootstrap` service: a "one-shot container that creates the MinIO bucket, registers the registry as an OIDC client with Dex, creates the first tenant and admin user (configurable via env vars), then exits" (spec/13-deployment.md:30). The compose file contains a one-shot `minio-init` container (/Users/joan/projects/podium/docker-compose.yml:59-72) that performs only the first of these responsibilities: it runs `mc mb --ignore-existing local/podium` to create the bucket. It does not register the registry as an OIDC client with Dex (no Dex service exists, per F-13.1.2), and it does not create a first tenant or admin user. A search for OIDC-client registration or tenant/admin creation in the compose file and `deploy/` returned nothing (`grep -ni "oidc\|client\|register"` on the compose file produced no matches; no `PODIUM_BOOTSTRAP` or first-tenant/first-admin keys were found). The consequence is that the evaluation stack does not arrive at a state where a tenant and admin exist, so the post-`up` `podium init`/`podium login` steps cannot complete. Suggested direction: extend the one-shot container (or add a dedicated `bootstrap` container) to register the OIDC client and create the first tenant and admin user via env vars, matching §13.1.1; alternatively narrow the spec to describe only bucket creation if tenant/IdP bootstrap is intentionally out of scope for the compose stack.

### - [ ] F-13.1.4 — Compose stack does not implement the one-command full-stack evaluation workflow [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §13.1.1 frames the compose file as the way to "exercise the same code paths as a real deployment" for "team evaluation, smoke-testing, and local integration testing (anything that wants the standard topology's components without the standalone single-binary shortcut)" and shows a self-contained three-line workflow ending in `podium login` (spec/13-deployment.md:14-22, 32). The implemented compose file is scoped to backing services for the Go live-integration test suite: its header reads "Local services for the live integration suite. Mirrors the service containers used in nightly.yml and release.yml" (/Users/joan/projects/podium/docker-compose.yml:1-2), and the Makefile wrappers describe it as "Start Postgres + MinIO for live tests" (`Makefile:49`, also lines 35, 65-66, 91-95). Because it ships no registry, IdP, or tenant/admin bootstrap (F-13.1.1 through F-13.1.3), the stack does not stand up the standard topology end to end, and the documented evaluation workflow does not run against it as written. The repo's own `docs/deployment/organization.md:96` already describes the compose stack more accurately as bringing up "Postgres + MinIO + Dex (OIDC)", and even that overstates the current file by including Dex. Suggested direction: reconcile the spec, the README/docs, and the compose file on a single intended scope, then make the compose file deliver that scope (full evaluation stack) or revise §13.1.1 to describe the backing-services-only reality plus the separate steps an operator runs to bring up the registry and bootstrap a tenant.
## F-13.2 — 13.2 Runbook (13.2.1 Read-Only Mode, 13.2.2 Public Mode)

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md against the implementation._

I checked the read-only mode state machine, probe, write-path rejection, response headers, and transition audit events against `pkg/registry/server/readonly.go`, `readonly_probe.go`, `internal/serverboot/readonly_audit.go`, and `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go`; and public mode (banner, loopback-bind safety, sensitivity ceiling, audit flag, mutual exclusion with an IdP, `/healthz`, and `podium status`) against `pkg/registry/server/config_validate.go`, `server.go`, `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go`, `pkg/registry/core/core.go`, `cmd/podium/serve.go`, and `cmd/podium/status.go`. Several concrete contracts match: `registry.read_only` / `config.read_only` rejection on layer and runtime-key edits, the `X-Podium-Read-Only` header, the hash-chained `registry.read_only_entered` / `registry.read_only_exited` audit events, `system:public` caller identity, `config.public_mode_with_idp` mutual exclusion, `ingest.public_mode_rejects_sensitive` (the rejection logic exists in the ingest package), `/healthz` reporting `mode: public`, and `podium status` surfacing the mode. The findings below cover the loopback-bind safety check, the boot-time sensitivity ceiling, the probe defaults and recovery threshold, the public-mode audit flag, write-path coverage, the startup banner, the lag header, and the MCP/SDK propagation surface.

### - [ ] F-13.2.1 — Public mode has no `--allow-public-bind` flag and no loopback-bind safety check [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 13.2.2 line 65 and §13.10 lines 196 and 209 require that public mode binds to `127.0.0.1` by default and refuses to bind a non-loopback address unless `--allow-public-bind` is also passed; the mitigation text states "which the safety check should have prevented unless `--allow-public-bind` was set." No such flag and no such check exist. `cmd/podium/serve.go:20-25` defines only `--bind`, `--public-mode`, `--standalone`, and `--config`; there is no `--allow-public-bind`. `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:528` and `:609-621` set `bind` from `PODIUM_BIND` (default `127.0.0.1:8080`) and validate only the IdP mutual-exclusion guard, with no check that couples public mode to a loopback bind. An operator who sets `PODIUM_PUBLIC_MODE=true` together with `PODIUM_BIND=0.0.0.0:8080` gets an unauthenticated, visibility-bypassed registry on all interfaces with no gate. Add an `--allow-public-bind` flag (and matching env var) and make `Config.validate()` reject public mode with a non-loopback bind unless the flag is set, surfacing the address in the error.

### - [ ] F-13.2.2 — Public-mode sensitivity ceiling is not enforced at standalone boot ingest [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 13.2.2 line 59 (and §13.10 line 210) states that in public mode "Ingest of `sensitivity: medium` and `sensitivity: high` artifacts is rejected" with `ingest.public_mode_rejects_sensitive`. The rejection logic exists in `pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:366-375` and is keyed on `Request.RejectAtOrAbove` (`ingest.go:152`). The standalone bootstrap that actually performs ingest, `NewFromFilesystem` in `pkg/registry/server/server.go:212-216`, constructs the `ingest.Request` with only `TenantID`, `LayerID`, and `Files`; it never sets `RejectAtOrAbove`, and nothing in `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go` or `bootstrapOptions` (`serverboot.go:647-658`) passes the public-mode flag into the ingest path. Standalone re-ingests from the filesystem on every boot, so the "existing artifacts continue to be served" carve-out does not apply; medium and high artifacts are ingested and served in public mode rather than rejected. Thread the public-mode flag into `NewFromFilesystem` and set `RejectAtOrAbove = manifest.SensitivityMedium` on the boot-time ingest requests when public mode is engaged.

### - [ ] F-13.2.3 — Read-only fallback is disabled by default and the probe interval default does not match the spec [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 13.2.1 line 42 describes automatic fallback: "The registry probes the primary every 5 s and flips to read-only after three consecutive failures (tunable via `PODIUM_READONLY_PROBE_INTERVAL` and `PODIUM_READONLY_PROBE_FAILURES`)." In the code the failure threshold defaults to 0 (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:563`, `envInt("PODIUM_READONLY_PROBE_FAILURES", 0)`), and the probe is only started when that value is greater than 0 (`serverboot.go:375`). With the default configuration the read-only probe never runs, so the registry never falls back to read-only on a primary failure. The interval also defaults to 30 s (`serverboot.go:564`), not the spec's 5 s, and `ReadOnlyProbe.Run` falls back to 30 s when the interval is unset (`pkg/registry/server/readonly_probe.go:38`). Set the default failure threshold to 3 and the default interval to 5 seconds so the documented automatic behavior occurs out of the box, or revise the spec to state that the fallback is opt-in.

### - [ ] F-13.2.4 — Read-only mode exits after a single probe success instead of three consecutive successes [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 13.2.1 line 42 states the registry "flips back automatically after three consecutive probe successes once the primary is reachable again." `pkg/registry/server/readonly_probe.go:65-73` flips the tracker back to `ModeReady` on the first successful probe after entering read-only: the recovery branch sets `ModeReady` as soon as `p.Tracker.Get() == ModeReadOnly` and a probe succeeds, with no counter for consecutive successes. The `ReadOnlyProbe` struct (`readonly_probe.go:20-28`) has a `Failures` threshold but no recovery threshold. The intended-but-divergent behavior is asserted in `pkg/registry/server/readonly_probe_test.go:27-28` and `:70-71` ("the first success restores ready"). This produces flapping under an intermittently reachable primary, which the three-success requirement is meant to dampen. Add a recovery-success counter (default 3, ideally configurable) and only flip to ready once it is reached.

### - [ ] F-13.2.5 — Public-mode audit events omit the `caller.public_mode` flag and do not preserve source IP or `X-Forwarded-User` [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 13.2.2 line 57 requires that audit events for read calls carry the flag `caller.public_mode: true`, and §13.10 line 212 lists this flag "on every audit event so downstream tooling can detect it without inspecting startup config." Section 13.10 line 203 additionally requires that "Source IP and any `X-Forwarded-User` header from an upstream proxy are preserved" in the audit record. The read-path audit emissions in `pkg/registry/core/core.go` (for example `LoadDomain` at `:240-244`, and the sites at `:505`, `:649`, `:748`, `:770`) set `Caller: callerOf(id)`, which renders `system:public` (`core.go:988-996`), but never populate a `public_mode` entry in the event `Context` map. The `audit.Event` struct (`pkg/audit/audit.go:53-64`) has `Caller` and `Context` but no source-IP field, and a repository-wide search finds no capture of `X-Forwarded-User` or `RemoteAddr` for audit. Downstream tooling that filters on `caller.public_mode` will not find it. Add a `public_mode: "true"` context entry on audit events when the caller is public, and capture the source IP and `X-Forwarded-User` value into the event.

### - [ ] F-13.2.6 — Read-only mode does not reject admin-grant or webhook-receiver writes [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 13.2.1 line 40 enumerates the write endpoints rejected with `registry.read_only` in read-only mode: "ingest webhooks, layer admin operations, freeze toggles, admin grants, `podium login`-driven token issuance." Layer admin operations and runtime-key registration honor this (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:127`, `:185`, `:290`, `:330` and `pkg/registry/server/runtime_endpoint.go:75` call `CheckConfig`). The admin-grant handler does not: `handleAdminGrants` in `pkg/registry/server/admin.go:21-59` performs `GrantAdmin` / `RevokeAdmin` (store mutations) with no `mode.CheckWrite()` or `CheckConfig()` call. The webhook-receiver CRUD handlers also lack the check: `handleWebhooksList` POST (`pkg/registry/server/webhooks.go:33-66`, `Store.Put`) and `handleWebhookOne` PUT/DELETE perform store writes with no mode check. As a result, admin grants succeed while the registry is in read-only mode, contradicting the spec's enumeration. Add `mode.CheckConfig()` (returning `config.read_only`, or `CheckWrite()` returning `registry.read_only` per the operation) at the top of the admin-grant and webhook-receiver write handlers, consistent with the layer handlers.

### - [ ] F-13.2.7 — Public-mode startup banner is not emitted [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 13.2.2 line 57 states "The registry's startup banner shows the public-mode warning," and §13.10 lines 192-197 give the exact banner text ("⚠ PUBLIC MODE: all artifacts visible to all callers without authentication. / Bound to 127.0.0.1 by default; pass --allow-public-bind to bind a non-loopback address."). The startup path logs only a generic line, `podium-server listening on %s (mode=%s)` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:405`), where `modeBanner()` returns the bare string `public` (`serverboot.go:623-631`). A repository-wide search for the banner text ("PUBLIC MODE", "all artifacts visible", "allow-public-bind", "⚠") finds no occurrence in non-test code. Operators do not get the documented warning at startup. Emit the multi-line public-mode warning to stderr at startup when public mode is engaged.

### - [ ] F-13.2.8 — `X-Podium-Read-Only-Lag-Seconds` is always reported as 0 [Low] — OPEN

(gap) Section 13.2.1 line 47 describes `X-Podium-Read-Only-Lag-Seconds` as "observed replication lag at response time." The middleware in `pkg/registry/server/server.go:355-367` hardcodes the header value to `"0"` whenever the registry is in read-only mode, and the inline comment notes "Standard deployments wire a probe that updates this." No such wiring exists: `ReadOnlyProbe` (`pkg/registry/server/readonly_probe.go`) does not measure or expose replication lag, and the `/readyz` `replication_lag_seconds` field (`server.go:488`, `:498`) is likewise always 0. Clients that gate on observed lag receive a constant 0 even when the replica is materially behind. Either measure replication lag (for example via the probe querying `pg_last_wal_replay_lsn`) and feed it to the header and the `/readyz` body, or document that lag reporting is unimplemented and the value is a placeholder.

### - [ ] F-13.2.9 — Read-only signal is not propagated through the MCP health tool or the SDK exception surface [Low] — OPEN

(gap) Section 13.2.1 line 51 states "the MCP `health` tool reports `mode: read_only`, SDKs raise `RegistryReadOnly` on attempted writes." The MCP server exposes no `health` tool: `tools/list` in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:257-265` advertises only `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact`, and there is no `health` case in `callTool`. The Python SDK defines `RegistryError` and `DeviceCodeRequired` (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:13`, `:23`) but no `RegistryReadOnly` type, and the TypeScript SDK source contains no read-only exception. The canonical definitions of the MCP health tool and the SDK error types live in §13.9, §6, and §7.6, so this finding overlaps those sections; it is recorded here because §13.2.1 states the propagation contract directly. Add a `health` MCP tool that reports the registry mode (reading the `X-Podium-Read-Only` header or `/healthz`) and a `RegistryReadOnly` exception in each SDK raised on a write rejected with `registry.read_only`.
## F-13.3 — 13.3 Backup and Restore

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md against the implementation._

Section 13.3 is operational deployment guidance. It lists infrastructure-level practices (Postgres logical and physical backups with point-in-time recovery, object-storage cross-region replication or snapshots, consistent restore via PITR plus object-storage version history) and a target of RPO 1h / RTO 4h. None of these are application-level contracts: there is no command, flag, endpoint, wire field, default value, or runtime invariant that the binary must implement for this subsection. I confirmed there is no backup, restore, snapshot, PITR, or recovery command anywhere in the CLI (`cmd/podium/admin.go` defines `grant`, `revoke`, `show-effective`, `erase`, `retention`, `reembed`, `runtime`, and `migrate-to-standard`, none of which is a backup or restore operation), and there is no backup-related code in `pkg/store` or `pkg/objectstore`. The primitives that the section's consistency guarantee rests on are present: object storage is content-addressed and immutable (`pkg/objectstore/objectstore.go:54`), and audit-chain integrity verification exists at the package level (`pkg/audit/audit.go:125`, `pkg/audit/file.go:107`). The RPO/RTO target and the backup procedures are documented in `docs/deployment/operator-guide.md:96-112`, consistent with the spec. Because the spec text for this subsection describes infrastructure operator responsibilities rather than binary behavior, and the supporting code primitives it relies on exist, there are no gaps, inconsistencies, or bugs to report for §13.3.

No findings.
## F-13.4 — 13.4 Migrations

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md against the implementation._

Section 13.4 is three sentences of prose covering schema migrations, the expand-contract pattern for online migrations, and type-system migrations versioned with the binary. The section is also the documented home of the `podium admin migrate-to-standard` command, which §13.10 (lines 158, 219) and §13.11.6 (line 333) cross-reference as "covered in §13.4" with the signature `podium admin migrate-to-standard --postgres <dsn> --object-store <url>`. The schema-migration claim is satisfied in a minimal form: both `pkg/store/sqlite.go` and `pkg/store/postgres.go` embed DDL as Go string literals applied on store open (`applySchema`), so the schema travels in the binary. The migration command exists in `cmd/podium/admin_migrate.go`. The remaining concrete claims diverge from the code: the documented command flags do not match the implemented flags, the command silently drops admin grants while §13.10 promises they are preserved, and neither the expand-contract online-migration machinery nor any type-system versioning is present.

### - [ ] F-13.4.1 — migrate-to-standard flag names do not match the spec [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The spec documents the migration command as `podium admin migrate-to-standard --postgres <dsn> --object-store <url>` in §13.10 (lines 158 and 219) and references the same command in §13.11.6 (line 333), with §13.10/§13.11.6 stating the command is "covered in §13.4". The implementation in `cmd/podium/admin_migrate.go:40-56` defines an entirely different flag set. There is no `--postgres` flag and no `--object-store` flag. The target Postgres DSN is `--target-postgres-dsn` (admin_migrate.go:46), the target object store is configured through `--target-objects-type`, `--target-s3-endpoint`, `--target-s3-bucket`, `--target-s3-region`, `--target-s3-access-key-id`, and `--target-s3-secret-access-key` (admin_migrate.go:48-54), and the command additionally requires `--source-sqlite` (admin_migrate.go:42, validated as required at admin_migrate.go:61-64) and `--source-objects` (admin_migrate.go:43). A user copying the documented invocation `podium admin migrate-to-standard --postgres <dsn> --object-store <url>` receives `flag provided but not defined: -postgres` and an error that `--source-sqlite is required`. Either rename the implemented flags to match the spec (preferred, since the spec form is shorter and is referenced in two places) or update §13.10/§13.11.6 and add a §13.4 flag reference that documents the actual flags including the required source flags.

### - [ ] F-13.4.2 — admin grants are not migrated, contradicting the preserved-state guarantee [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Spec §13.10 line 158 states that during `podium admin migrate-to-standard`, "Layer config, admin grants, and audit history are preserved". The implementation does not migrate admin grants. The command's own doc comment is explicit: "Admin grants are not pumped (the Store interface lacks ListAdmins); operators re-issue them after migration." (admin_migrate.go:22-24). The pump path `pumpStore` copies tenants, manifests, and layer configs only (admin_migrate.go:186-205); it never touches admin grants. The `Store` interface (pkg/store/store.go:146-148) exposes `GrantAdmin`, `RevokeAdmin`, and `IsAdmin` but no enumeration method, so the source grants cannot be read for transfer. After migration, every tenant-admin grant from the standalone deployment is silently absent on the target, which is an authorization-state regression a migrating operator would not expect from a "preserved" guarantee. Add a `ListAdmins`/`ListAdminGrants` method to the `Store` interface (implemented across Memory, SQLite, and Postgres), pump grants in `pumpStore`, and report the count, or change §13.10 to remove admin grants from the preserved list and document that grants must be re-issued after migration.

### - [ ] F-13.4.3 — audit history is preserved only when both audit-log flags are passed [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Spec §13.10 line 158 lists "audit history" among the state that migration preserves, presenting preservation as automatic. The implementation copies the audit log only when the operator supplies both `--source-audit-log` and `--target-audit-log` (admin_migrate.go:116-122); both default to the empty string (admin_migrate.go:44, 55) and are documented as optional (admin_migrate.go:34-35). When either flag is omitted, the command completes with rc 0 and prints no warning, leaving audit history un-migrated despite the spec guarantee. The default invocation documented in §13.10/§13.11.6 (`--postgres <dsn> --object-store <url>`) names no audit flag at all, so following the spec verbatim would skip audit entirely. Make audit migration the default by resolving the standalone audit-log path (`~/.podium/audit.log`, per internal/serverboot/audit_anchor.go:73-81) when the flags are unset, or at minimum emit a warning that audit history was not copied when the flags are absent, and document the audit flags in §13.4.

### - [ ] F-13.4.4 — expand-contract online-migration pattern is not implemented [Low] — OPEN

(gap) Spec §13.4 line 78 states "expand-contract pattern for online migrations." The schema apply functions implement a greenfield create-if-absent model only: `pkg/store/sqlite.go:50-124` and `pkg/store/postgres.go:57-131` run a fixed list of `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` and `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS` statements on every open, with the doc comments noting "existing schemas are unchanged thanks to IF NOT EXISTS" (sqlite.go:23-24, postgres.go:26-28). There is no schema-version tracking (no `PRAGMA user_version`, no `schema_migrations` or `schema_version` table; confirmed by repo-wide search), no `ALTER TABLE`/`ADD COLUMN`/`RENAME COLUMN`/`DROP COLUMN` anywhere in the codebase, and therefore no expand phase, no contract phase, and no dual-write or backfill machinery. The current code can add a new table or index across versions, but it cannot perform the online column-evolution that the expand-contract pattern names, and it cannot detect or order versioned migrations. This is forward-looking prose without a present concrete contract, so the severity is low; if expand-contract is intended to be claimed now, introduce versioned, ordered migration steps with a recorded schema version. Otherwise reword §13.4 to describe the create-if-absent model the binary actually applies.

### - [ ] F-13.4.5 — type-system migrations are not versioned alongside the binary [Low] — OPEN

(gap) Spec §13.4 line 78 states "Type-system migrations versioned alongside the binary." The type-system implementation in `pkg/typeprovider/typeprovider.go` carries no version concept: providers expose only `ID()`, `Type()`, and `Validate()` (typeprovider.go:37-41), the default registry seeds the first-class types as no-op validators (typeprovider.go:60-74), and there is no type-system version field, no schema version for type definitions, and no migration of type definitions across binary versions (confirmed by repo-wide search for type-system/version identifiers). The `pkg/version` package is scoped to artifact semver pinning per §4.7.6 (version.go:1-3) and is unrelated to the type system. The binary does stamp its own build version via `internal/buildinfo` (cmd/podium/main.go:77), but nothing ties type definitions or their evolution to that version. This is conceptual prose with no present contract, so the severity is low; either document that type definitions evolve only with the binary and require no separate migration, or, if versioned type migrations are intended, add a type-system version and a migration path keyed to it.
## F-13.5 — 13.5 Multi-Region

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md against the implementation._

Subsection 13.5 (spec/13-deployment.md:80-82) states that a Podium deployment is single-region, that cross-region read replicas are provided through Postgres logical replication and object-storage replication, and that writes route to the primary region. This is conceptual operational guidance describing how an operator composes external infrastructure (database-level replication and object-store-level replication) around a single-region deployment. It mandates no application-level field, flag, endpoint, default, or invariant that the Podium binary must implement. I searched the whole repository for multi-region, cross-region, replication, read-replica, primary-region, and write-routing logic. The only region concept in the code is the single AWS S3 region (`PODIUM_S3_REGION`, default `us-east-1`, in internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:538 and pkg/objectstore/s3.go:30), which is consistent with the single-region statement. The replication-lag handling in pkg/registry/server/server.go:488 belongs to read-only mode (§13.2.1), and the `Primary` flags in pkg/scim/handler.go:122 are SCIM email fields, so neither contradicts this subsection. The code matches the spec and does not contradict any claim here.

No findings.
## F-13.6 — 13.6 Sizing

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md against the implementation._

The 13.6 Sizing subsection (spec/13-deployment.md lines 84-93) is informational deployment guidance. It states a baseline capacity (10K artifacts, 100 QPS, 1 GB Postgres, 500 GB object storage on a 3-replica deployment plus a db.m5.large equivalent) and three scale notes (100K artifacts suggests pgvector scaling and embedding sharding, 1K QPS suggests more front-end replicas and a CDN, and 10K QPS suggests reviewing search query patterns and considering a dedicated Elasticsearch for BM25). The subsection defines no fields, flags, endpoints, defaults, or invariants, so it carries no concrete contract for the code to satisfy. Per the scope note, I checked only for contradictions with configurable limits. The backends the guidance references are present: pgvector exists at pkg/vector/pgvector.go, and BM25 lexical ranking is implemented in-process at pkg/registry/core/rrf.go:1157 (scoreBM25). The Elasticsearch suggestion is framed as future advice and is correctly absent from the current code. The configurable limits that do exist are opt-in per-tenant quotas that default to disabled: the artifact-count quota (pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:406, active only when req.ArtifactCountQuota > 0) and the search QPS limiter (pkg/registry/server/rate_limit.go:91, inactive when searchQPS <= 0). No code references the baseline numbers and no hardcoded cap contradicts the guidance. No findings.

No findings.
## F-13.7 — 13.7 CDN

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md against the implementation._

Section 13.7 is short advisory prose with two concrete claims: presigned URLs are CDN-friendly, and cache headers are safe because `content_hash` keys are immutable. Both supporting facts hold in the code. The `Presign` method exists on both object-store backends (pkg/objectstore/s3.go:100 and pkg/objectstore/filesystem.go:113), and content-hash key immutability is enforced uniformly across the filesystem, S3, and memory backends (pkg/objectstore/filesystem.go:63-68, the Provider contract documented at pkg/objectstore/objectstore.go:50-56, and pkg/objectstore/memory.go:42) with tests at pkg/objectstore/objectstore_test.go:47-60. The one gap is that no cache header is actually emitted on content responses on either backend, so the "cache headers safe" property the section relies on to make CDN caching work from origin is not realized at the origin.

### - [ ] F-13.7.1 — No Cache-Control header emitted on immutable content responses [Low] — OPEN

(gap) Section 13.7 states "Cache headers safe because content_hash keys are immutable," presenting cacheable content responses as part of the CDN story (CloudFront, Fastly, or Cloudflare in front of object storage for hot artifacts). The implementation emits no cache header on either delivery path. The filesystem backend's registry-served route `/objects/{key}` sets only `Content-Type` and `X-Content-Hash` and then writes the body (pkg/registry/server/server.go:779-784); no `Cache-Control` header is set, and the only wrapping middleware is `withReadOnlyHeaders`, which adds read-only signal headers rather than cache headers (pkg/registry/server/server.go:355-366). The S3 backend stores objects with `minio.PutObjectOptions{ContentType: contentType}` only (pkg/objectstore/s3.go:69-70), leaving the `CacheControl` field of `PutObjectOptions` unset (the field exists in the vendored client at minio-go v7.1.0 api-put-object.go:82), so presigned GET responses carry no cache metadata either. Because the content is content-addressed and immutable, a CDN placed in front of either backend would have to be configured CDN-side to cache, rather than honoring an origin `Cache-Control` header as the section implies. Suggested direction: set `Cache-Control: public, max-age=31536000, immutable` on the `/objects/{key}` response in handleObjectsRoute, and pass the same value through `S3Config`/`Put` into `PutObjectOptions.CacheControl` so presigned responses inherit it. This is Low severity because 13.7 is advisory prose that does not mandate a specific header value, but the implementation currently provides no origin cache headers at all.
## F-13.8 — 13.8 Observability

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md against the implementation._

Section 13.8 specifies three observability surfaces: a Prometheus metrics endpoint on both the registry and the MCP server with named histograms, counters, and gauges; OpenTelemetry trace export with W3C Trace Context propagation and a defined root/child span structure; and a reference Grafana dashboard that ships with the registry. The implementation provides none of the runtime instrumentation. The Go module pulls in neither a Prometheus client library nor an OpenTelemetry library (`go.mod` contains zero matches for either), no `/metrics` route is registered on the registry HTTP server (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:322`-`346` registers `/healthz`, `/readyz`, and the `/v1/*` endpoints only), the MCP server has no HTTP listener at all, and the only trace-related code is an unpopulated `trace_id` JSON field with a comment marking it reserved for future work. A `deploy/grafana-dashboard.json` file does ship, but every panel queries Prometheus series that the code never emits.

### - [ ] F-13.8.1 — Prometheus metrics endpoint absent on the registry [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 13.8 requires a "Prometheus endpoint on registry" exposing "Histograms for latency; counters for cache hit rate, error rate, visibility-denial rate, ingest success/failure rate; gauges for queue depths." The registry registers its routes in `pkg/registry/server/server.go:322`-`346` (`/healthz`, `/readyz`, the `/v1/*` meta-tool and admin endpoints, and conditionally `/v1/webhooks`, `/scim/v2/`, `/objects/`); there is no `/metrics` route. A repo-wide search finds no Prometheus client dependency (`grep -ci "prometheus\|opentelemetry\|otel" go.mod` returns 0) and no `promhttp`, metric registry, histogram, counter, or gauge instrumentation in any non-test file (the only `counter`/`gauge`/`metric` matches are the quota counter, the vector distance "metric", domain-analysis "metrics", and webhook failure counters, none of which are Prometheus metrics). The named series (cache hit rate, error rate, visibility-denial rate, ingest success/failure, queue-depth gauges) are not emitted anywhere. Suggested direction: add a `github.com/prometheus/client_golang` dependency, register a `promhttp` handler at `/metrics`, and instrument request latency, cache hits/misses, error rate, visibility denials, ingest outcomes, and the vector/audit outbox depths.

### - [ ] F-13.8.2 — Prometheus metrics endpoint absent on the MCP server [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 13.8 requires the Prometheus endpoint on the "registry and MCP server." The MCP server in `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go` is a stdio JSON-RPC process; it has no HTTP listener (`grep` for `http.Server`, `ListenAndServe`, or `HandleFunc` across `cmd/podium-mcp/` returns nothing) and therefore cannot expose a Prometheus scrape target. No metrics are recorded for MCP-side cache hits, request latency, or error rate, even though the MCP server maintains a resolution cache (`cmd/podium-mcp/resolution_cache.go`) and has a defined cache-hit notion. Suggested direction: either add an opt-in HTTP metrics listener to the MCP process (a bind flag plus a `promhttp` handler) or amend the spec if the MCP server is intentionally scrape-less; as written the code does not satisfy the requirement.

### - [ ] F-13.8.3 — OpenTelemetry tracing, W3C Trace Context propagation, and span structure absent [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 13.8 requires "OpenTelemetry trace export. W3C Trace Context propagation across all calls. One root span per `load_domain` / `search_domains` / `search_artifacts` / `load_artifact`; child spans for registry round-trip, object-storage fetch, adapter translation, materialization." No OpenTelemetry library is present (`go.mod` has no `go.opentelemetry.io` requirement), and there is no W3C Trace Context handling anywhere (`grep` for `traceparent`, `tracestate`, `W3C`, `TraceContext`, or `propagation` across `*.go` returns no matches). No spans are created for any of the named operations or child operations. The only trace-adjacent code is a `trace_id` field on the event and audit structs that is never assigned a value (`pkg/registry/server/events.go:52`, `pkg/audit/file.go:151`), and `pkg/registry/server/events.go:190` explicitly discards the request context with the comment `// ctx reserved for future trace_id propagation`. Suggested direction: add the OpenTelemetry SDK and `otelhttp` instrumentation, install the W3C trace-context propagator on inbound and outbound HTTP, and create the root span per read meta-tool with child spans for the registry round-trip, object-storage fetch, adapter translation, and materialization stages.

### - [ ] F-13.8.4 — Reference Grafana dashboard queries metrics the code never emits [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 13.8 states "Reference Grafana dashboard ships with the registry." The file `deploy/grafana-dashboard.json` exists, satisfying the literal shipping requirement, but every panel queries a Prometheus series name that no code path produces: `podium_request_total` and `podium_request_duration_seconds_bucket` (lines 13 and 25), `podium_visibility_denied_total` (line 45), `podium_cache_hits_total` / `podium_cache_misses_total` (line 57), `podium_ingest_success_total` / `podium_ingest_failure_total` (lines 82 and 86), and `podium_vector_outbox_depth` / `podium_audit_outbox_depth` (lines 97-98). Because no Prometheus metrics are emitted (see F-13.8.1), the dashboard renders empty against any real deployment, and the dashboard's series names are the de facto contract for the missing instrumentation. Suggested direction: when implementing the metrics endpoint in F-13.8.1, emit exactly these series names and labels (for example, the `endpoint` label used by `podium_request_total` and the latency histogram) so the shipped dashboard works without edits; otherwise reconcile the dashboard with whatever names the implementation chooses.
## F-13.9 — 13.9 Health and Readiness

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md against the implementation._

Section 13.9 specifies three surfaces: the registry `/healthz` (liveness) and `/readyz` (readiness, including Postgres and object-storage reachability) endpoints, with `/readyz` reporting `mode: ready | read_only | not_ready` plus observed replication lag in the body, and an MCP `health` tool reporting registry connectivity, observed registry mode, cache size, and last successful call timestamp. The `/healthz` endpoint exists and reports the mode correctly. The `/readyz` endpoint exists but only mirrors the read-only mode tracker. It does not probe Postgres or object-storage reachability at request time, can never emit the `not_ready` state, and reports a hardcoded replication lag of 0. The MCP `health` tool is absent entirely. Evidence is in pkg/registry/server/server.go, pkg/registry/server/readonly.go, pkg/registry/server/readonly_probe.go, and cmd/podium-mcp/main.go.

### - [x] F-13.9.1 — MCP `health` tool is not implemented [High] — CLOSED

Resolution (537421b): Registered a `health` MCP tool (cmd/podium-mcp/health.go, wired into `tools/list` and `callTool` in main.go) that pings `<registry>/readyz`, maps the registry state into `ready` / `read_only` / `unreachable`, and reports `registry`, `connected`, `cache_size` (resolution-cache `Len()`), and `last_successful_call` (stamped on every 2xx registry call). Covered by cmd/podium-mcp unit tests and real-binary integration tests (reachable + unreachable).

(gap) Section 13.9 requires the MCP server to expose a `health` MCP tool "returning registry connectivity + observed registry mode (`ready` / `read_only` / unreachable) + cache size + last successful call timestamp." The same tool is referenced in §13.2.1 ("the MCP `health` tool reports `mode: read_only`") and §13.10 ("The mode is surfaced ... in the MCP `health` tool"). The MCP server registers only `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact` in `tools/list` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:259-264) and dispatches only those four in `callTool` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:289-300). A call to a `health` tool falls through to `errorResult("unknown tool: " + p.Name)` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:299). A repo-wide search for the tool and its fields (`health` tool registration, `read_only`/`unreachable` mode reporting, cache size, last successful call timestamp) finds no implementation in cmd/podium-mcp, the SDKs, or anywhere else. Suggested direction: register a `health` tool that pings the configured registry (reusing the resolution cache for cache size), maps the registry's `/healthz` or `/readyz` mode into `ready` / `read_only` / `unreachable`, and records the timestamp of the last successful registry call.

### - [x] F-13.9.2 — `/readyz` does not check Postgres or object-storage reachability [High] — CLOSED

Resolution (537421b): Added `Server.WithReadinessChecks` and a request-time `readyMode` that runs each dependency probe (bounded by a 2s deadline) before reporting. serverboot wires a metadata-store probe (`GetTenant`) and, when an object store is configured, an object-store reachability probe (a sentinel `Get`, treating `ErrNotFound` as reachable) via internal/serverboot/readiness.go. A failing probe makes `/readyz` answer `not_ready` (503). Covered by server unit tests, serverboot helper tests, and a SQLite store-outage integration test.

(gap) Section 13.9 specifies `/readyz` as "readiness, including Postgres and object-storage reachability." The handler `handleReady` (pkg/registry/server/server.go:496-504) computes its result solely from `s.modeBanner()` (pkg/registry/server/server.go:475-483), which reads the in-memory `publicMode` flag and the `ModeTracker`. It never calls into the metadata store and never touches `s.objectStore`, so a `/readyz` request performs no live reachability check against Postgres or object storage. The only store probing happens asynchronously in the background `ReadOnlyProbe` (pkg/registry/server/readonly_probe.go:32-76), and an object-storage outage is never probed by anything. As a result, `/readyz` returns 200 `ready` while object storage is down, and it reports a Postgres outage only indirectly and only as `read_only` (a 200, in-rotation state) after the background probe's failure threshold is crossed. Suggested direction: have `handleReady` perform (or consult a recently-cached result of) a metadata-store ping and an object-store reachability check, and downgrade to `not_ready` (503) when either dependency is unreachable, distinct from the read-only replication-fallback state.

### - [x] F-13.9.3 — `/readyz` can never report `not_ready` (503 unreachable) [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (537421b): `handleReady` now derives its mode from `readyMode` (not `modeBanner`), which returns `not_ready` when any §13.9 dependency probe (F-13.9.2) fails, then `read_only` when the tracker is flipped, then `ready`. `not_ready` takes precedence over `read_only` (a hard outage leaves rotation; a read-only fallback stays in rotation), and `/readyz` reports only the three readiness states the spec enumerates (public is a `/healthz` signal). The 503 path is now reachable and exercised by unit + integration tests.

(inconsistency) Section 13.9 states `/readyz` reports one of `mode: ready | read_only | not_ready`, and the handler is written to return 503 for `not_ready` (pkg/registry/server/server.go:499-502, gated on `mode == "not_ready"`). The `not_ready` string is produced only by `Mode.String()` for `ModeNotReady` (pkg/registry/server/readonly.go:38-39), but `handleReady` derives its mode from `modeBanner()` (server.go:497), and `modeBanner()` returns only `public`, `read_only`, or `ready` (server.go:475-483). It never returns `not_ready`. Separately, a repo-wide search shows nothing ever calls `Tracker.Set(ModeNotReady)`; `ModeNotReady` appears only in the `String()` unit test (pkg/registry/server/readonly_test.go:48). Consequently `/readyz` can never emit `not_ready` and never returns 503, so the only documented "not ready" outcome is dead code. Suggested direction: drive a `ModeNotReady` (or an explicit dependency-down) state from the readiness checks recommended in F-13.9.2 and surface it through `modeBanner()` (or have `handleReady` use the tracker's `String()` directly) so the spec's three-state contract is actually reachable.

### - [x] F-13.9.4 — `/readyz` body and read-only header always report replication lag 0 [Medium] — CLOSED

Resolution (537421b): Added `Server.WithLagReporter`; `handleReady` threads the observed lag into `ReadyResponse.ReplicationLagSecs` and `withReadOnlyHeaders` writes the same value into `X-Podium-Read-Only-Lag-Seconds` instead of a hardcoded `"0"`. The Postgres store computes lag via `pg_last_xact_replay_timestamp()` (`ReplicationLagSeconds`, wired by serverboot's `storeLagReporter`); a primary and every non-Postgres backend report 0, the genuine no-replica value. Covered by server unit tests (body + header) and a DSN-guarded Postgres test.

(gap) Section 13.9 states the `/readyz` response body "includes observed replication lag in seconds," and §13.2.1 (which §13.9 cross-references) specifies the header `X-Podium-Read-Only-Lag-Seconds: <n>` carrying "observed replication lag at response time." The body field exists as `ReadyResponse.ReplicationLagSecs` with JSON tag `replication_lag_seconds` (pkg/registry/server/server.go:486-489), but `handleReady` constructs `ReadyResponse{Mode: mode}` and never assigns the lag (server.go:498), leaving it at the zero value. The header is hardcoded to `"0"` in `withReadOnlyHeaders` (server.go:363). A repo-wide search finds no replication-lag computation anywhere (no assignment to `ReplicationLagSecs`, no `pg_last_wal`/`pg_last_xact`-style query in pkg/store). The background `ReadOnlyProbe` only pings the store with `GetTenant` and does not measure lag (pkg/registry/server/readonly_probe.go:53). For standard deployments with a read replica, both surfaces therefore misreport observed lag as 0. Suggested direction: compute replication lag against the replica (for example via `pg_last_xact_replay_timestamp()` for the Postgres store), thread the value into both `ReadyResponse.ReplicationLagSecs` and the `X-Podium-Read-Only-Lag-Seconds` header, and keep 0 only as the genuine standalone (no-replica) value.

### - [x] F-13.9.5 — `/healthz` carries an undocumented `ready` boolean field [Low] — CLOSED

Resolution (537421b): Removed the `Ready` field from `HealthResponse`; `/healthz` now returns `{mode}` only, conforming to §13.9 (liveness is the 200 status, with no readiness boolean). Updated the unit + e2e doc-conformance tests that asserted the field to instead assert its absence.

(inconsistency) Section 13.9 describes `/healthz` as the liveness endpoint and, for the mode signal, refers to `mode: public` (§13.2.2) and the read-only mode reporting (§13.2.1); it documents no boolean field. `HealthResponse` adds a `Ready bool json:"ready"` field that `handleHealth` always sets to `true` (pkg/registry/server/server.go:372-375, 465-467). The field is harmless for liveness, but it is undocumented and always-true, so it conveys no information and could mislead a consumer into treating `/healthz` as a readiness signal. Suggested direction: either remove the `ready` field from `/healthz` (liveness is conveyed by the 200 status) or document it in §13.9; if readiness signaling is wanted on `/healthz`, populate it from the same checks that drive `/readyz` rather than hardcoding `true`.
## F-13.10 — 13.10 Standalone Deployment

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md against the implementation (re-run against main e41f44e)._

I re-verified the prior findings against the merged code and inspected the new layer-path bootstrap (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go` `bootstrapLayerPath`), the new `--layer-path` flag on `cmd/podium/serve.go`, the new `layers.path` / `layers.default_visibility` settings and yaml keys, the `podium artifact scaffold` command, and the new tests (`cmd/podium/serve_layer_path_test.go`, `internal/serverboot/layer_path_test.go`). The merge resolved one prior finding: `podium serve --layer-path` is now a real flag that sets `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH`, and the bootstrap ingests, persists a `LayerConfig` per layer, and seeds `core.New`. One prior finding is partially addressed: bootstrap layer-path layers are now `public`, though the `podium layer register` default and the `users` override token still diverge from §13.10. The remaining gaps are unchanged and concentrate in the zero-flag/strict decision tree, the public-mode safety constraints, the standalone "sensible defaults", and the web UI flags. The `podium artifact scaffold` command (spec §7.3.1, not §13.10) is implemented and lint-clean; it surfaces no §13.10 finding. The scope holds 15 current findings: 13 carried forward unchanged, 1 carried forward partially addressed, and 1 new inconsistency revealed by the layer-path bootstrap.

### - [ ] F-13.10.1 — Zero-flag detection, `--strict`, and `PODIUM_NO_AUTOSTANDALONE` are unimplemented [High] — OPEN

(gap) §13.10 specifies a three-way decision: `podium serve` with no flags auto-enters standalone "when no server config is found at `~/.podium/registry.yaml` and no `PODIUM_*` server-side environment variables are set"; `podium serve --strict` "retains the prior behavior of refusing to start without explicit configuration"; and "Setting `PODIUM_NO_AUTOSTANDALONE=1` in the environment has the same effect". None of this exists. `cmd/podium/serve.go:22-26` now defines `--bind`, `--public-mode`, `--standalone`, `--config`, and `--layer-path`, but there is still no `--strict` flag. `--standalone` is a documented no-op: it sets `PODIUM_STANDALONE=true` (`serve.go:46-48`), which no server code reads (a repo-wide search finds `PODIUM_STANDALONE` only at that one assignment). `serverboot.Run` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:209-416`) always calls `LoadConfig`, which unconditionally fills in standalone defaults (`serverboot.go:541-624`) and proceeds to serve. `PODIUM_NO_AUTOSTANDALONE` is set only by the test harness (`internal/testharness/cmdharness/cmdharness.go:40`) and is never read by any server code, so it is a silent no-op. There is no detection of "config present vs absent" and no detection of "any `PODIUM_*` server env set". A deployment can never refuse to auto-bootstrap, which the §13.2.2 prevention guidance calls out as the required behavior for CI and image builds. Suggested direction: add a `--strict` flag and read `PODIUM_NO_AUTOSTANDALONE`; in `Run`, when strict is requested and no explicit config/env is present, return a hard error rather than inventing defaults.

### - [ ] F-13.10.2 — Missing `--config <path>` does not error; the code boots anyway [High] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §13.10 states: "Auto-bootstrap is also suppressed when `--config <path>` is passed and the file does not exist (the user explicitly named a config; missing config is an error rather than a cue to invent one)." The implementation does the opposite. `cmd/podium/serve.go:37-39` maps `--config` to `PODIUM_CONFIG_FILE`. `readYAMLConfig` (`internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:73-94`) treats a missing `PODIUM_CONFIG_FILE` path as `os.IsNotExist` and returns `(nil, nil)`, after which `LoadConfig` falls back to standalone defaults and `Run` serves normally. The test `TestServe_BootsAndAnswersHealthz` (`cmd/podium/serve_test.go:38`) sets `PODIUM_CONFIG_FILE` to a non-existent `missing.yaml` and asserts the server returns HTTP 200 (`serve_test.go:62-63`), encoding the behavior the spec forbids. The new `--layer-path` tests rely on the same "missing config file boots" behavior to reach `validate()` (`cmd/podium/serve_layer_path_test.go:31, 49`). Suggested direction: when `--config`/`PODIUM_CONFIG_FILE` is explicitly set and the file does not exist, return an error from `readYAMLConfig`/`Run` instead of silently treating it as "no config".

### - [ ] F-13.10.3 — First-run default files are not created and the startup stderr line is absent [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §13.10 says the server "emits a clear stderr line on startup (\"No config found at `~/.podium/registry.yaml`. Starting in standalone mode at `http://127.0.0.1:8080`. Run `podium serve --strict` to require explicit setup.\"), creates the standalone defaults (`~/.podium/registry.yaml`, `~/.podium/sync.yaml`, `~/podium-artifacts/`) on first run". The "Client setup" paragraph repeats that zero-flag "writes both files in one step on first run". Neither happens. `serverboot.Run`/`LoadConfig` create only the SQLite parent directory (`serverboot.go:653-654`) and the filesystem object-store root (`serverboot.go:792`); a repo-wide search finds no `WriteFile`/`MkdirAll` for `registry.yaml`, `sync.yaml`, or `podium-artifacts`, and no occurrence of the literal `podium-artifacts` path or the "No config found" message anywhere in the code. The only startup line is `log.Printf("podium-server listening on %s (mode=%s)", ...)` (`serverboot.go:414`). Suggested direction: on the auto-standalone path, write the three default files and emit the specified stderr line before serving.

### - [ ] F-13.10.4 — Standalone `podium layer register` default is `private` and the `users` override token is unhandled [High] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §13.10 "Sensible defaults" states: "New layers registered via `podium layer register` default to `visibility: public` (instead of `users: [<registrant>]` as in standard mode for user-defined layers). Override with `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY=users`." This finding was partially addressed by the merge: bootstrap layer-path layers now register as `public` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:188, 197`), so the layer-path ingest no longer hides content. The `podium layer register` path still diverges. `LoadConfig` defaults `defaultLayerVisibility` to `private` (`serverboot.go:577`), and the struct comment still says it "Defaults to \"private\" so admin-defined layers don't leak by accident" (`serverboot.go:453-457`). That value is installed on the layer endpoint via `WithDefaultVisibility(cfg.defaultLayerVisibility)` (`serverboot.go:323-324`), and there is no standalone/zero-flag detection that flips it to `public`. A layer registered without explicit visibility in standalone becomes `private` (only explicit grants can see it), contradicting §13.10. The `users` override token still has no handling: the endpoint switch handles only `public` and `organization` (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:237-241`), and any other value (including `users`) leaves the layer with no visibility filters. The §13.12 Layers table now self-acknowledges the divergence, documenting the default as "`private` (§13.10 specifies `public` for standalone deployments)" (`spec/13-deployment.md:464`). Suggested direction: default standalone to `public` on the standalone/zero-flag path, add a `users` case that maps to `users:[<registrant>]`, and reconcile the §13.12 parenthetical with the §13.10 default.

### - [ ] F-13.10.5 — Public mode does not enforce loopback bind and `--allow-public-bind` is missing [High] — OPEN

(gap) §13.10 lists a safety constraint: "Loopback bind by default. Public mode binds to `127.0.0.1` unless `--allow-public-bind` is _also_ passed", and the banner text plus the §13.2.2 prevention guidance assume a safety check that "should have prevented" a non-loopback public bind unless `--allow-public-bind` was set. The implementation has neither the flag nor the enforcement. A repo-wide search for `allow-public-bind` / `IsLoopback` / non-loopback handling in non-test code returns nothing. `serverboot.Run` uses `cfg.bind` verbatim for the listener (`serverboot.go:409-414`); `bootstrapOptions`/`WithPublicMode` (`serverboot.go:664-675`) never inspect or coerce the bind address. Setting `PODIUM_PUBLIC_MODE=true` together with `PODIUM_BIND=0.0.0.0:8080` binds an unauthenticated, visibility-bypassing registry to all interfaces with no guard. This is a security-relevant deviation. Suggested direction: when public mode is engaged and the resolved bind is non-loopback, refuse to start unless an `--allow-public-bind` flag (or equivalent env) is present.

### - [ ] F-13.10.6 — Public-mode sensitivity ceiling is not wired into the running ingest paths [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §13.10 ("What public mode does" / safety constraints) requires that in public mode "Ingest of `sensitivity: medium` or `sensitivity: high` artifacts is rejected with `ingest.public_mode_rejects_sensitive`". The ingest library supports this through `ingest.Request.RejectAtOrAbove` and returns the `ingest.public_mode_rejects_sensitive` code (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:152, 367-371`), but no live ingest path sets `RejectAtOrAbove` when public mode is on. A repo-wide search shows `RejectAtOrAbove` is assigned only in a unit test (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest_test.go`); the new layer-path boot ingest builds `ingest.Request{TenantID, LayerID, Files}` with no floor (`serverboot.go:168-172`), `NewFromFilesystem` does the same (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:205-209`), and neither `WithPublicMode` nor the server's ingest endpoints thread the floor through. A public-mode deployment still accepts medium/high-sensitivity artifacts, violating the stated ceiling. Suggested direction: when `publicMode` is set, propagate `RejectAtOrAbove = medium` into every ingest request (layer-path boot ingest, `NewFromFilesystem`, webhook ingest, batch load, runtime ingest).

### - [ ] F-13.10.7 — Audit events do not carry the `caller.public_mode: true` flag [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §13.10 ("Loud at every checkpoint") and §13.2.2 ("Detection") require that public mode is surfaced "as a flag (`caller.public_mode: true`) on every audit event so downstream tooling can detect it without inspecting startup config", with source IP and any `X-Forwarded-User` preserved. The audit `Event` struct has a `Caller` string and a `Context map[string]string` but no public-mode boolean and no source-IP/forwarded-user fields, and nothing populates a `public_mode` key (`pkg/audit/audit.go:53-64`). `callerOf` only renders the string `system:public` for public/anonymous callers (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:986-994`); there is no `public_mode` flag emitted. The `podium status` half of the §13.2.2 detection contract is now met: `status.go:50-54` prints the registry mode from `/healthz`. The per-audit-event flag remains absent, so downstream tooling cannot distinguish public-mode `system:public` from ordinary anonymous access via a flag on the event. Suggested direction: add a `public_mode` boolean (and optionally source-IP/forwarded-user) to the audit event and populate it from `Identity.IsPublic` at emission time.

### - [ ] F-13.10.8 — The public-mode startup banner is not emitted [Low] — OPEN

(gap) §13.10 specifies a multi-line public-mode startup banner ("⚠  PUBLIC MODE: all artifacts visible to all callers without authentication. / Bound to 127.0.0.1 by default; pass --allow-public-bind to bind a non-loopback address."), and §13.2.2 states "The registry's startup banner shows the public-mode warning." The implementation prints only a single line, `log.Printf("podium-server listening on %s (mode=%s)", cfg.bind, cfg.modeBanner())` (`serverboot.go:414`), where `modeBanner()` returns `"public"` (`serverboot.go:640-648`). No warning banner text exists in the code. Suggested direction: emit the specified banner to stderr when `cfg.publicMode` is true, before the listener starts.

### - [ ] F-13.10.9 — Web UI: no `--web-ui` / `--web-ui-allow-public-bind` flags and no non-loopback guard [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §13.10 ("Web UI") says the UI is "opt-in via `--web-ui`" (or `PODIUM_WEB_UI=true`) and that "The binary refuses to bind the UI to a non-loopback address unless `--web-ui-allow-public-bind` is also passed _and_ an identity provider is configured". The implementation honors only the env var: `serverboot.Run` mounts `/ui/` when `isTrue(os.Getenv("PODIUM_WEB_UI"))` (`serverboot.go:346-349`), and `cmd/podium/serve.go` defines no `--web-ui` or `--web-ui-allow-public-bind` flag. There is no check that the UI is on a loopback bind, no `--web-ui-allow-public-bind` escape hatch, and no requirement that an identity provider be configured before exposing the UI on a non-loopback address. An operator who sets `PODIUM_WEB_UI=true` with a non-loopback `PODIUM_BIND` and no IdP gets an unauthenticated UI exposed with no guard. Suggested direction: add the `--web-ui` and `--web-ui-allow-public-bind` flags and refuse to mount the UI on a non-loopback bind unless both the escape hatch and an identity provider are present.

### - [ ] F-13.10.10 — Standalone default search is BM25-only, not the `sqlite-vec` hybrid the spec describes [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The §13.10 "What changes" table lists the standalone vector store as "`sqlite-vec` extension loaded into the same SQLite file", and the "Hybrid search" paragraph states "Standalone runs the same BM25 + vector RRF retriever as the standard registry. Vectors live in `sqlite-vec`", with `--no-embeddings` framed as the opt-out. A zero-flag standalone runs neither: `LoadConfig` defaults `vectorBackend` to the empty string (`serverboot.go:559`) and `embeddingProvider` to the empty string (`serverboot.go:560`), so `openVectorAndEmbedder` returns `(nil, nil, nil)` and the registry never gets `WithVectorSearch` (`serverboot.go:680-693, 238-243`). The `sqlite-vec` backend that shares the SQLite file is only reached when the operator explicitly sets `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND=sqlite-vec` plus an embedding provider (`serverboot.go:750-755`). The documented default (hybrid) is the opposite of the actual default (BM25-only). Suggested direction: on the standalone path, default to `sqlite-vec` plus a default embedding provider, and make `--no-embeddings` (see F-13.10.11) the explicit BM25-only opt-out, or correct the spec if BM25-only is the intended default.

### - [ ] F-13.10.11 — `--no-embeddings` flag does not exist [Low] — OPEN

(gap) §13.10 references `--no-embeddings` twice: the embedding row of the "What changes" table ("`--no-embeddings` falls back to BM25-only") and the "Hybrid search" paragraph ("`--no-embeddings` falls back to BM25-only when no provider is configured"). A repo-wide search for `no-embeddings` / `no_embeddings` returns no matches. The equivalent effect is reachable by leaving `PODIUM_EMBEDDING_PROVIDER` unset or set to `none` (`serverboot.go:701-703`), but the documented flag itself is absent. Suggested direction: add a `--no-embeddings` flag to `serve.go` that disables the embedding provider (and forces BM25-only) regardless of other config.

### - [ ] F-13.10.12 — `PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES` default is not relaxed to `never` for standalone [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §13.10 "Sensible defaults" states: "`PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES` defaults to `never` (instead of `medium-and-above`)" in standalone. The verification policy is read on the consumer side by the MCP server with a fixed default of `medium-and-above` regardless of deployment: `verifyPolicy: sign.VerificationPolicy(envDefault("PODIUM_VERIFY_SIGNATURES", string(sign.PolicyMediumAndAbove)))` (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:112`). There is no standalone-aware default that flips it to `never`. The MCP process has no signal that it is talking to a standalone registry, so the relaxed default the spec promises is never applied. Suggested direction: clarify in the spec that this default is consumer-side, or provide a standalone signal the MCP can honor; at minimum reconcile the documented default with the hardcoded `medium-and-above`.

### - [ ] F-13.10.13 — `migrate-to-standard` flags differ from the documented `--postgres` / `--object-store` [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §13.10 documents the upgrade command twice as `podium admin migrate-to-standard --postgres <dsn> --object-store <url>` (the "Upgrade path" paragraph and the public-mode "Migration to a governed deployment" paragraph). The implemented command defines different flag names: `--target-postgres-dsn`, `--target-store`, `--target-objects`, `--target-objects-type`, and `--target-s3-*` (`cmd/podium/admin_migrate.go:45-55`). The spec's literal `--postgres` and `--object-store` flags do not exist and would fail to parse. The detailed contract belongs to §13.4, but §13.10 cites the flag names directly. Suggested direction: add `--postgres` and `--object-store` aliases, or correct the §13.10 examples to the implemented flag names.

### - [ ] F-13.10.14 — `--sign registry-key` flag is not exposed on `serve` [Low] — OPEN

(gap) The §13.10 "What changes" table says standalone signing is "Disabled by default; opt in via `--sign registry-key`". `cmd/podium/serve.go` defines no `--sign` flag, and a repo-wide search finds `--sign` only in the unrelated `podium sign` command (`cmd/podium/sign.go`), not on `serve`. The "disabled by default" half holds (the boot path performs no signing), but the documented opt-in flag is absent, so an operator cannot enable registry-key signing for the standalone server via the documented mechanism. Suggested direction: add a `--sign registry-key` flag (or the corresponding env var) to the serve/bootstrap path that enables registry-managed-key signing on ingest.

### - [ ] F-13.10.15 — Layer-path bootstrap ignores `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY` [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The merge added `bootstrapLayerPath` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:156-203`), which hardcodes `Public: true` for every bootstrap layer, both on the persisted `store.LayerConfig` (`serverboot.go:188`) and on the in-memory `layer.Layer` (`serverboot.go:197`). It never receives or consults `cfg.defaultLayerVisibility`. The §13.12 Layers table documents `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY` as "Fallback `visibility:` applied when a layer is registered without an explicit setting" and offers `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY=users` (and `organization`/`private`) as the multi-user override. Because the env var is applied only to the `podium layer register` endpoint (`serverboot.go:323-324`) and not to the bootstrap path, an operator who sets `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY=private` (or `organization`) for a multi-user standalone deployment still gets `public` bootstrap layers, which leak content the operator intended to restrict. The §13.12 text "Bootstrap layers carry `visibility: public` per the §13.10 standalone default" reads as an unconditional rule, but it conflicts with the env var's documented role as the fallback for layers registered without explicit visibility. Suggested direction: pass `cfg.defaultLayerVisibility` into `bootstrapLayerPath` and map it onto the bootstrap layers (public/organization/private/users), or state in §13.12 that bootstrap layers are unconditionally public and exempt from the override.
## F-13.11 — 13.11 Filesystem Registry (13.11.1 Layout, 13.11.2 Config, 13.11.3 Availability, 13.11.4 Watch, 13.11.5 Shared Dir, 13.11.6 Migrate to Server)

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md against the implementation (re-run against main e41f44e)._

I re-verified the four prior open findings against the current tree and examined the merge's new code: the `--layer-path` flag on `podium serve` (`cmd/podium/serve.go`), the standalone layer bootstrap (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go` `bootstrapLayerPath`), the new `layers.path` / `default_visibility` YAML and env keys (`internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go`), the `podium artifact scaffold` command (`cmd/podium/artifact_scaffold.go`), and the new tests (`cmd/podium/serve_layer_path_test.go`, `internal/serverboot/layer_path_test.go`). The merge resolved one prior finding: the standalone server now exposes a `--layer-path` flag, so the §13.11.6 migration command works as written. The remaining three prior findings are still open (watch uses polling instead of `fsnotify`, the `podium sync` filesystem path does not resolve `extends:`, and the unset-registry CLI error omits `config.no_registry` / `podium init` and consults only the project-shared scope). The directory-layout dispatch, lock-file path, read-only shared-directory model, and the new bootstrap all match their spec sections. One prior Info observation about full-rerun watch behavior remains. Of five prior findings, one was resolved and four remain (renumbered below).

### - [ ] F-13.11.1 — Watch mode uses polling instead of fsnotify [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §13.11.4 states: "`podium sync --watch` against a filesystem source uses `fsnotify` to watch the registry path and the workspace overlay; when files change, it re-runs composition and materialization for the affected artifacts." The implementation in `pkg/sync/watch.go` does not use `fsnotify`. The package comment at `pkg/sync/watch.go:18` says detection is "poll-based (no fsnotify dependency)," and `runWatch` (`pkg/sync/watch.go:69-112`) drives a `time.Ticker` at `opts.Period` (default 500ms, `watch.go:56-57`) that recomputes a content fingerprint over each watched tree via `watchSignature` / `signOne` (`pkg/sync/watch.go:119-162`). `fsnotify` is not a dependency (`grep "fsnotify"` finds only the comment in `watch.go`). The functional outcome (a rerun on change) is achieved, but the mechanism contradicts the spec, and polling adds latency up to the poll interval plus the debounce window (default 500ms + 200ms) plus a continuous filesystem walk of the whole registry tree, which `fsnotify` avoids. Suggested direction: either adopt `fsnotify` for change detection as the spec mandates (falling back to polling only where `fsnotify` is unavailable), or update §13.11.4 to describe the poll-based fingerprint mechanism if polling is the intended design.

### - [ ] F-13.11.2 — Filesystem sync path does not resolve `extends:`, breaking the equivalent-output guarantee [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §13.11.3 states: "The composer, parsers, glob resolver, `extends:` resolver, and harness adapters used here are the same Go module functions the registry runs behind its HTTP API ... There is no separate filesystem-mode reimplementation, which is why migration to a server (§13.11.6) is mechanical and produces equivalent output for the same artifact directory." The `podium sync` filesystem path does not invoke an `extends:` resolver. `pkg/sync/sync.go:90-99` opens the registry and calls `filesystem.Walk` with `CollisionPolicyHighestWins`, and `Walk` (`pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:41-72`) performs only canonical-ID collision dedup; the comment at `walk.go:98-99` confirms domain composition is deferred to a later phase.
