No code in `pkg/sync` imports a composer or extends resolver (a grep for `Compose`/`Extends`/`extends` across `pkg/sync` returns nothing). The adapter `Source` constructed at `sync.go:118-123` carries only a single artifact's `ArtifactBytes`, `SkillBytes`, and `Resources`, with no parent data, so the adapter cannot reconstruct a merge. The server source resolves `extends:` end to end: ingest pins the parent (`pkg/registry/ingest/ingest.go:425-436` `resolveExtendsPin`) and load-time assembly walks and field-merges the chain (`pkg/registry/core/core.go:862-871` `assembleResult`, `core.go:879-900` `resolveExtendsChain`, `core.go:905-944` `mergeChain`, which unions tags and takes most-restrictive sensitivity). The merge clarifies the divergence direction: the server applies the parent's structured fields to the child, while filesystem `podium sync` emits the child's own bytes unchanged. For any artifact that declares `extends:`, filesystem-source materialization and server-source materialization therefore diverge, contradicting the "equivalent output" claim that §13.11.6 relies on. The merge did not change this; the new `--layer-path` bootstrap reaches the server's extends-resolving path through `ingest.Ingest`, so it does not close the gap on the `podium sync` side. Suggested direction: route filesystem sync through the shared composer with `extends:` resolution before adaptation, or narrow the §13.11.3 claim to state that `extends:` resolution is not yet applied in filesystem source and document the resulting limitation on migration equivalence.

### - [ ] F-13.11.3 — Unset-registry CLI error omits `config.no_registry` and the `podium init` pointer, and resolves only the project-shared scope [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §13.11.2 states: "If `defaults.registry` is unset across all scopes, the client errors with `config.no_registry` and points the user at `podium init`," and "Normal precedence applies." Two deviations exist in the `podium sync` command path. First, when `--registry` is empty and no registry is configured, `cmd/podium/main.go:211-213` prints `error: --registry is required (filesystem path) — set it on the command line or in <ws>/.podium/sync.yaml` and returns exit 2, short-circuiting before `sync.Run` is called. The `sync.ErrNoRegistry` value (`pkg/sync/sync.go:30`) does carry the `config.no_registry:` prefix, and the library returns it correctly (verified by `pkg/sync/no_registry_test.go`), but the CLI never reaches it for the unset case, so the user sees neither the `config.no_registry` code nor the `podium init` guidance the spec promises. Second, the resolution at `cmd/podium/main.go:205-210` reads only `sync.ReadConfig(ws)`, which loads `<ws>/.podium/sync.yaml` (`pkg/sync/config.go:60-61`, `ConfigPath`). It does not consult the user-global `~/.podium/sync.yaml`, the project-local `<ws>/.podium/sync.local.yaml`, or `PODIUM_REGISTRY`, so the §7.5.2 precedence chain that §13.11.2 invokes with "Normal precedence applies" is not honored for the sync command's registry lookup (`pkg/sync/scope.go` is a record filter, not a config-scope resolver, and the package has no multi-scope `defaults.registry` reader). Suggested direction: emit the `config.no_registry` code and reference `podium init` in the unset-registry error, and resolve `defaults.registry` through the full §7.5.2 scope precedence chain including `PODIUM_REGISTRY` and the local and global scopes.

### - [ ] F-13.11.4 — Watch re-runs full materialization rather than only the affected artifacts [Info] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §13.11.4 states that on change the watcher "re-runs composition and materialization for the affected artifacts." The implementation re-runs the full sync: `runWatch` calls `Run(opts.Sync)` on every detected change (`pkg/sync/watch.go:107`), and `Run` walks the entire registry, re-adapts every artifact, and rewrites the target with stale-file cleanup (`pkg/sync/sync.go:114-185`). The output is correct because a full rerun is a superset of an incremental rerun, so this is an observation rather than a correctness defect. Suggested direction: leave as is given the loose spec wording, or scope the rerun to changed artifacts if watch performance on large registries becomes a concern.
## F-13.12 — 13.12 Backend Configuration Reference (metadata store, object storage, vector, embedding, identity, config file format)

_Reviewed spec/13-deployment.md against the implementation (re-run against main e41f44e)._

I re-verified every backend selector and per-backend env var in §13.12 (spec lines 337-513) against `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go` (`LoadConfig` / `validate` / `openStore` / `openObjectStore` / `openEmbedder` / `openVectorBackend` / `bootstrapLayerPath`), `internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go` (the `registry.yaml` parser and `applyYAML`), and the backing packages `pkg/store`, `pkg/objectstore`, `pkg/vector`, `pkg/embedding`, and `pkg/identity`. The merge added the new "Layers" block (spec lines 457-466), the `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` env var, the `--layer-path` flag, and the `layers.path` / `layers.default_visibility` YAML keys; I verified those against `bootstrapLayerPath`, `cmd/podium/serve.go`, `Settings()`, and the new tests `internal/serverboot/layer_path_test.go` and `cmd/podium/serve_layer_path_test.go`. The layer-path bootstrap, its flag-to-env mapping, the `local`-source `LayerConfig` persistence, the `GET /v1/layers` / `POST /v1/layers/reingest` / `DELETE /v1/layers` endpoints it references, and the `layers.path` reporting in `Settings()` all match the spec. The new `artifact scaffold` command is filesystem-only and out of §13.12 scope. The merge resolved none of the prior 14 findings; all remain open with refreshed line numbers. The new "Layers" block introduced one new inconsistency: the documented standalone `public` default for `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY` is not applied to endpoint-registered layers, which default to `private` in every mode.

### - [ ] F-13.12.1 — registry.yaml `${ENV_VAR}` interpolation is not implemented [High] — OPEN

(gap) §13.12 states twice that the config file supports environment-variable interpolation: the example annotates `dsn: ${PODIUM_POSTGRES_DSN}` with "`${ENV_VAR}` interpolation supported" (spec line 478) and the closing note says "Secret values should use `${ENV_VAR}` interpolation rather than being committed in plaintext" (spec line 513). The parser in `internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go` calls `yaml.Unmarshal(data, &out)` (line 90) with no expansion step, and a repo-wide `git grep` for `os.Expand` / `ExpandEnv` finds no interpolation logic anywhere. A `registry.yaml` written exactly as the spec documents stores the literal string `${PODIUM_POSTGRES_DSN}` as the DSN, which then fails to connect. This both breaks the documented secret-handling guidance and silently produces a wrong connection string. Suggested direction: run each string field through `os.Expand` with a `${VAR}`-only resolver after `yaml.Unmarshal`, or interpolate the raw bytes before parsing, so the documented `${ENV_VAR}` form resolves.

### - [ ] F-13.12.2 — registry.yaml keys are parsed at the top level, but the spec nests them under a `registry:` block [High] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The §13.12 config-file example (spec lines 470-511) places every key under a top-level `registry:` mapping (`registry.endpoint`, `registry.bind`, `registry.store`, `registry.object_store`, etc.). The implementation's `yamlConfig` struct (`internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:14-25`) declares `Bind`, `Store`, `ObjectStore`, and the rest as top-level YAML keys with no `registry` wrapper, and `readYAMLConfig` unmarshals straight into that struct. A repo-wide `git grep` finds no `yaml:"registry"` wrapper struct. A `registry.yaml` written as the spec shows parses to an all-empty `yamlConfig` (the `registry:` key is unknown and ignored), so none of the operator's settings take effect and the server silently falls back to standalone defaults. The parser tests (`yaml_config_test.go`, `yaml_extra_test.go`, `layer_path_test.go:296`) all use flat top-level keys, confirming the implemented format. Suggested direction: either wrap the struct in `type fileConfig struct { Registry yamlConfig \`yaml:"registry"\` }` to match the documented format, or correct the spec example to the flat layout the code accepts. Pick one and make the spec and code agree.

### - [ ] F-13.12.3 — registry.yaml has no `discovery:` handling; the block is parsed and discarded [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) The §13.12 config-file example presents a `discovery:` block with `max_depth`, `fold_below_artifacts`, `fold_passthrough_chains`, `notable_count`, `target_response_tokens`, and `allow_per_domain_overrides` (spec lines 504-510) as a server-side configuration section. `yamlConfig` includes a `Discovery yamlDiscovery` field (`yaml_config.go:22`, struct at lines 50-56), but `applyYAML` (lines 98-158) never reads `y.Discovery` (confirmed by `git grep` for `y.Discovery`), and `Config` has no discovery fields, so the parsed block is dropped. `allow_per_domain_overrides` is not present in the struct at all. Discovery defaults are sourced per-domain from DOMAIN.md (`pkg/domain`), so the documented registry-wide `discovery:` config silently has no effect. Suggested direction: either wire the `discovery:` block into the registry's discovery defaults and add `allow_per_domain_overrides`, or remove the block from the §13.12 example and document that discovery defaults live in DOMAIN.md.

### - [ ] F-13.12.4 — registry.yaml vector/identity/embedding sub-keys from the spec example are not parsed [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The §13.12 example shows per-backend config nested in the file: `vector_backend.api_key`, `vector_backend.index`, `vector_backend.namespace`, `vector_backend.inference_model` (spec lines 486-491); `embedding_provider.type`, `embedding_provider.api_key`, and `embedding_provider.model` (lines 494-497, commented); and `identity_provider.type`, `identity_provider.audience`, `identity_provider.authorization_endpoint` (lines 499-502). The implementation's structs carry almost none of these: `yamlVectorCfg` has only `Type` (`yaml_config.go:41-43`), `yamlEmbedCfg` has only `Provider` and `Model` and keys on `provider` rather than the spec's `type` (lines 45-48), and `IdentityProvider` is a plain scalar string (line 17) so the spec's `identity_provider:` mapping with sub-keys cannot unmarshal into it. As a result a `registry.yaml` written per the example cannot supply a vector API key, index, namespace, inference model, embedding API key, or any OAuth audience/endpoint through the file; those must come from env vars instead. Suggested direction: extend the YAML structs to accept the documented sub-keys (rename `provider` to `type` for the embedding block, add `api_key`/`index`/`namespace`/`inference_model` to the vector block, and model `identity_provider` as an object), then overlay them in `applyYAML`. Alternatively narrow the spec example to only the keys the parser supports.

### - [ ] F-13.12.5 — config-file key names contradict the spec's own "snake-cased env var" rule [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §13.12 states "All env vars below are also valid config-file keys (snake-cased under the relevant section)" (spec line 343). The implementation follows that rule for object storage and the store DSN: `yamlObjectCfg` uses `s3_bucket` / `s3_region` / `s3_endpoint` (`yaml_config.go:36-38`) and `yamlStoreCfg` uses `postgres_dsn` (line 30), matching the snake-cased env vars `PODIUM_S3_BUCKET`, `PODIUM_S3_REGION`, `PODIUM_S3_ENDPOINT`, and `PODIUM_POSTGRES_DSN`. The spec's config-file example contradicts its own rule by using `store.dsn`, `object_store.bucket`, `object_store.region`, and `object_store.endpoint` (spec lines 477-484) without the snake-cased prefixes, none of which bind to the implemented struct fields. The code is self-consistent with the stated rule; the example is the part that is wrong. Suggested direction: rewrite the example keys to the snake-cased forms the parser accepts (`postgres_dsn`, `s3_bucket`, `s3_region`, `s3_endpoint`) so the example matches both the rule and the code.

### - [ ] F-13.12.6 — self-embedding vector backends are not implemented (`*_INFERENCE_MODEL`, `*_VECTORIZER`) [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §13.12 documents `PODIUM_PINECONE_INFERENCE_MODEL`, `PODIUM_WEAVIATE_VECTORIZER`, and `PODIUM_QDRANT_INFERENCE_MODEL` to "enable self-embedding" (spec lines 393, 403, 413), and the embedding-provider section states the embedding provider is "Optional when the configured vector backend self-embeds (any of the `*_INFERENCE_MODEL` / `*_VECTORIZER` env vars above is set)" (spec line 417). A repo-wide `git grep` finds no reference to `INFERENCE_MODEL` or `VECTORIZER` in any Go file. None of the vector constructors (`vector.NewPinecone`, `vector.NewWeaviate`, `vector.NewQdrant`) accept an inference-model or vectorizer field, so the registry never asks the backend to embed. Worse, `openVectorAndEmbedder` (`serverboot.go:680-693`) calls `openEmbedder` first and returns `(nil, nil, nil)` when no embedding provider is configured, which disables vector search entirely. A deployment that configures Pinecone Integrated Inference (or a Weaviate/Qdrant vectorizer) with no separate embedding provider gets BM25-only search rather than the documented self-embedded vector search. Suggested direction: add the inference-model / vectorizer fields to the vector configs, send raw text on Put/Query when they are set, and change `openVectorAndEmbedder` to allow a nil embedder when the selected backend self-embeds.

### - [ ] F-13.12.7 — S3 backend never falls back to IAM role / instance profile when static keys are unset [Medium] — OPEN

(bug) §13.12 documents `PODIUM_S3_ACCESS_KEY_ID` / `PODIUM_S3_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY` with the default "(use IAM role / instance profile when unset)" (spec line 367). `objectstore.NewS3` unconditionally installs `credentials.NewStaticV4(cfg.AccessKeyID, cfg.SecretAccessKey, "")` (`pkg/objectstore/s3.go:47`), and `serverboot` passes the bare env values (`serverboot.go:805-806`) with no "unset" branch. When the keys are unset, the minio-go client is configured with empty static V4 credentials and signs requests with an empty access key rather than consulting the AWS credential chain (environment, shared config, EC2/ECS instance metadata, IAM role). The documented credential-less deployment on AWS therefore fails to authenticate to S3. Suggested direction: when both `AccessKeyID` and `SecretAccessKey` are empty, build the client with the AWS credential chain (for example `credentials.NewChainCredentials` over `IAM`, `EnvAWS`, and `FileAWSCredentials` providers) instead of static credentials.

### - [ ] F-13.12.8 — `PODIUM_S3_FORCE_PATH_STYLE` is not implemented; an undocumented `PODIUM_S3_USE_SSL` is used instead [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §13.12 documents `PODIUM_S3_FORCE_PATH_STYLE` with default `false` and the note "`true` for MinIO and similar" (spec line 368). A repo-wide `git grep` finds no `FORCE_PATH_STYLE` / `ForcePathStyle` reference in any Go file, so the var is silently ignored. The S3 config exposes no path-style toggle (`pkg/objectstore/s3.go:26-33`); minio-go auto-selects path style by endpoint instead. The implementation reads an undocumented `PODIUM_S3_USE_SSL` (`serverboot.go:557`) that §13.12 never lists, and a `git grep` confirms `use_ssl` appears nowhere in `spec/`. The result is that an operator who sets the documented `PODIUM_S3_FORCE_PATH_STYLE` sees no effect, and the var that actually exists is undocumented. Suggested direction: either add a `ForcePathStyle bool` to `S3Config` wired from `PODIUM_S3_FORCE_PATH_STYLE` (passed to minio-go via `BucketLookup`), and document `PODIUM_S3_USE_SSL`, or remove `PODIUM_S3_FORCE_PATH_STYLE` from the table and document the auto-detection behavior.

### - [ ] F-13.12.9 — `PODIUM_S3_REGION` is documented as required but is defaulted to `us-east-1` [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The object-storage table marks `PODIUM_S3_REGION` as "required" (spec line 365). `LoadConfig` sets `s3Region: envDefault("PODIUM_S3_REGION", "us-east-1")` (`serverboot.go:553`) and `validate()` (`serverboot.go:626-638`) only checks the Postgres DSN, so a missing region is silently replaced by `us-east-1` rather than rejected. An operator who omits the region against a non-`us-east-1` bucket or a region-sensitive S3-compatible service gets a wrong default instead of the documented startup error. Suggested direction: either drop the implicit default and require the region for `s3` in `validate()` (matching the "required" label), or change the spec default column to `us-east-1` to match the code.

### - [ ] F-13.12.10 — registry does not refuse to start when a selected backend's required values are missing [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §13.12 states "The registry refuses to start when a backend is selected but its required values are missing, naming the missing keys in the error" (spec line 347). The implementation enforces this only for the Postgres DSN: `validate()` (`serverboot.go:634-636`) returns an error when `store=postgres` and the DSN is empty, and `openObjectStore` rejects `s3` without a bucket (lines 795-797). For the vector backends and the embedding provider, the missing-value errors from `openVectorBackend` / `openEmbedder` surface only inside `openVectorAndEmbedder`, whose error is logged as a non-fatal warning and the feature is disabled: `if v, e, err := openVectorAndEmbedder(cfg); err != nil { log.Printf("warning: vector search disabled: %v", err) }` (`serverboot.go:238-239`). Likewise `openObjectStore` failures are logged as "warning: object store disabled" (`serverboot.go:669-670`) rather than aborting. A deployment that selects `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND=pinecone` without an API key, or `PODIUM_OBJECT_STORE=s3` with an unreachable endpoint, boots and serves with the backend silently off rather than refusing to start as documented. Suggested direction: have `validate()` (or `Run` before serving) treat a configured-but-missing required value for the selected vector, object-store, and embedding backends as a hard startup error that names the missing keys, reserving the warn-and-disable path for the explicit `none` / unset selection.

### - [ ] F-13.12.11 — `PODIUM_PINECONE_NAMESPACE` defaults to empty rather than `default` [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The Pinecone table documents `PODIUM_PINECONE_NAMESPACE` with default `default` (spec line 392). `LoadConfig` sets `pineconeNS: os.Getenv("PODIUM_PINECONE_NAMESPACE")` with no default (`serverboot.go:569`), and `Pinecone.namespaceFor` treats an empty global namespace as no prefix, returning the bare tenant ID (`pkg/vector/pinecone.go:66-71`). When the var is unset the effective namespace prefix is empty, not the documented `default`. The behavioral impact is small because tenant isolation still holds via the tenant ID, but vectors land in a different Pinecone namespace than the spec implies, which matters when interoperating with a separately-populated index. Suggested direction: default `pineconeNS` to `default` in `LoadConfig`, or change the spec default column to "(empty)".

### - [ ] F-13.12.12 — vector collection defaults are set where the spec marks them required [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The Weaviate and Qdrant tables mark the collection name "required": `PODIUM_WEAVIATE_COLLECTION` (spec line 401) and `PODIUM_QDRANT_COLLECTION` (spec line 411). `LoadConfig` supplies defaults instead: `weaviateColl: envDefault("PODIUM_WEAVIATE_COLLECTION", "PodiumArtifacts")` (`serverboot.go:572`) and `qdrantColl: envDefault("PODIUM_QDRANT_COLLECTION", "podium_artifacts")` (line 575). Because the value is always non-empty, `NewWeaviate` / `NewQdrant` never hit their "Collection is required" checks (`pkg/vector/weaviate.go:42`, `pkg/vector/qdrant.go:42`) from this path, so an operator who omits the collection silently writes to the default collection rather than getting the documented "required" failure. Suggested direction: either remove the defaults so the required collection is enforced at startup with a named error, or relabel these as defaulted in the spec tables.

### - [ ] F-13.12.13 — `PODIUM_QDRANT_GRPC_PORT` and `PODIUM_WEAVIATE_GRPC_URL` are documented but unused [Info] — OPEN

(gap) The Qdrant table documents `PODIUM_QDRANT_GRPC_PORT` (default `6334`, spec line 412) and the Weaviate table documents `PODIUM_WEAVIATE_GRPC_URL` (spec line 402). A repo-wide `git grep` finds no `GRPC_PORT` / `GRPC_URL` reference in any Go file, and both `pkg/vector/qdrant.go` and `pkg/vector/weaviate.go` use only the REST data plane (the file comments state the gRPC variant adds dependency weight). The vars have no effect. This is low impact because the REST path is functional, but the documented gRPC tuning knobs do nothing. Suggested direction: drop the gRPC vars from the §13.12 tables until a gRPC transport is implemented, or note in the tables that they are reserved and currently ignored.

### - [ ] F-13.12.14 — undocumented `memory` value accepted for store and vector backends [Info] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §13.12 lists the metadata store selector as `postgres | sqlite` (spec line 351) and the vector selector as `pgvector | sqlite-vec | pinecone | weaviate-cloud | qdrant-cloud` (line 381). The implementation additionally accepts `memory` for both: `openStore` has a `case "memory"` returning `store.NewMemory()` (`serverboot.go:656-657`) and `openVectorBackend` has a `case "memory"` returning `vector.NewMemory(dim)` (lines 743-744). These are test affordances and the new `serve_layer_path_test.go` E2E test relies on `PODIUM_REGISTRY_STORE=memory`, so they do not contradict any documented behavior, but `PODIUM_REGISTRY_STORE=memory` is a non-durable store that an operator could select unaware that it persists nothing. Suggested direction: leave as an undocumented test affordance, or log a clear warning when `memory` is selected for either backend in a non-test process.

### - [ ] F-13.12.15 — standalone `public` default for `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY` is not applied to endpoint-registered layers [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The new "Layers" block documents `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY` as the "Fallback `visibility:` applied when a layer is registered without an explicit setting", with default "`private` (§13.10 specifies `public` for standalone deployments)" (spec lines 464). §13.10 line 175 states the standalone default is `visibility: public` for layers registered via `podium layer register`. The implementation defaults `defaultLayerVisibility` to `private` in every mode, including standalone: `defaultLayerVisibility: envDefault("PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY", "private")` (`serverboot.go:577`), with no standalone-specific override (a `git grep` for any branch that flips the default to `public` finds none). The layer-register endpoint applies that fallback (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:237-243`): only `public` and `organization` are honored, and any other value, including unset, leaves the layer with no visibility filters (effectively private). The bootstrap path is the one place that hardcodes `Public: true` (`serverboot.go:188`), which matches the spec's separate claim at line 466 that bootstrap layers carry `visibility: public`. The result is that a standalone deployment registering a layer via `podium layer register` without an explicit visibility gets `private`, contradicting the parenthetical in §13.12 line 464 and §13.10 line 175. Separately, §13.10 line 175 documents `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY=users` as the override for standard "users: [registrant]" behavior, but the endpoint does not handle the value `users` (it falls into the unknown→private branch), so that documented override silently produces private layers. Suggested direction: either flip the standalone default to `public` (for example when standalone mode is detected and the env var is unset) and add a `users` case to the endpoint switch, or correct §13.12 line 464 and §13.10 line 175 to state that the implemented default is `private` for endpoint-registered layers in all modes and that only `public` and `organization` are accepted values.
## F-14.1 — 14.1 Local registry folder, one-shot, single workspace

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

I verified each concrete command, flag, and path in scenario 14.1 against the implementing code in `cmd/podium` (init, sync, profile, serve dispatch) and `pkg/sync`, `pkg/registry/filesystem`, and `internal/serverboot`. The one-time setup commands work: `podium init --global --registry <path>` writes `~/.podium/sync.yaml` with `defaults.registry: <path>` (`cmd/podium/main.go:707`, `:728`), the filesystem registry interprets a bare path as a single layer and honors `.registry-config` with `multi_layer: true` (`pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:127`), and the `claude-code` adapter is registered (`pkg/adapter/claudecode.go:24`). The per-project sync step does not work as written: the `--profile` flag does not exist on `podium sync`, the sync engine never applies include/exclude scope, and the "graduate to a server" command uses a `--layer-path` flag that the serve command does not define. The target default and lock-file path in step 5 are correct (`<cwd>/.podium/sync.lock`).

### - [ ] F-14.1.1 — `podium sync --profile` flag is not implemented [High] — OPEN

(gap) Step 5 of §14.1 instructs the developer to run `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile myapp`, and §7.5 (`spec/07-external-integration.md:160`, `:269`) defines `--profile <name>` as a sync flag that selects an entry under `profiles:` merged on top of `defaults:`. The `syncCmd` flag set defines only `--registry`, `--target`, `--harness`, `--dry-run`, `--json`, `--watch`, and `--overlay` (`cmd/podium/main.go:188`–`:194`); there is no `--profile` flag. Because the flag set uses `flag.ContinueOnError`, passing `--profile myapp` fails parsing with "flag provided but not defined: -profile" and `syncCmd` returns exit code 2 via `parseExit` (`cmd/podium/main.go:196`–`:197`, `:129`). The exact command in the scenario therefore cannot run. The `SyncConfig` model already supports profiles (`pkg/sync/config.go:26`, `:40`) and `Defaults.Profile` (`pkg/sync/config.go:35`), so the data layer is present but the CLI never reads or resolves a profile. Suggested direction: add `--profile`, `--include`, `--exclude`, and `--type` flags to `syncCmd`, resolve `defaults` plus the named profile plus CLI overrides into a `ScopeFilter`, and pass it into `sync.Run`.

### - [ ] F-14.1.2 — sync run ignores include/exclude scope; whole view is always materialized [High] — OPEN

(gap) §14.1 frames the scenario as materializing "a subset into one project" and step 4 shows a profile with `include: ["finance/**", "shared/policies/*"]` and `exclude: ["finance/**/legacy/**"]`. §7.5 (`spec/07-external-integration.md:183`–`:184`, `:191`) mandates that when `--include`/`--profile` is given only matching artifacts are synced, and otherwise the full effective view is the implicit scope. The `sync.Options` struct has no scope field (`pkg/sync/sync.go:37`–`:48`) and `sync.Run` walks every visible record and materializes all of them with no scope filtering applied (`pkg/sync/sync.go:94`–`:138`). A `ScopeFilter` with include/exclude/type matching exists and is unit-tested (`pkg/sync/scope.go:13`, `:27`), but `ScopeFilter.Apply` is never called from `Run`, `Watch`, or `Override` (only referenced by `pkg/sync/scope.go`, its own test, and unrelated packages). The lock file declares `Profile` and `Scope` fields meant to record the resolved profile and scope (`pkg/sync/lockfile.go:16`–`:17`, `:28`), but `Run` never populates them (`pkg/sync/sync.go:164`–`:178`), so the active profile and scope are lost. Even if F-14.1.1 added the `--profile` flag, subsetting would still not occur because the engine discards scope. Suggested direction: add a `Scope ScopeFilter` field to `sync.Options`, apply it after `Walk` and before adapter invocation, and record the resolved profile name and scope in the written lock file.

### - [ ] F-14.1.3 — `podium serve --layer-path` flag is not implemented [High] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The "graduate to a server" paragraph of §14.1 instructs `podium serve --standalone --layer-path ~/podium-artifacts/`, and §13.10/§11 describe `--layer-path` as a server flag (`spec/13-deployment.md:126`, `spec/11-verification.md:35`). The `serveCmd` flag set defines only `--bind`, `--public-mode`, `--standalone`, and `--config` (`cmd/podium/serve.go:22`–`:25`); there is no `--layer-path` flag. The layer path is read exclusively from the `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` environment variable inside the bootstrap (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:169`). Because `serveCmd` uses `flag.ContinueOnError`, passing `--layer-path` fails parsing and the command returns exit code 2 (`cmd/podium/serve.go:27`–`:28`), so the documented graduation command does not run. The `podium-server` binary also takes no flags (`cmd/podium-server/main.go:19`–`:22`). Suggested direction: add a `--layer-path` flag to `serveCmd` that sets `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` for the process lifetime, mirroring how `--bind` sets `PODIUM_BIND` (`cmd/podium/serve.go:30`–`:31`).

### - [ ] F-14.1.4 — `podium profile edit` takes a positional profile name in the spec but requires `--profile` [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The "Changing the subset" paragraph of §14.1 writes `podium profile edit myapp ...`, naming the profile positionally. The implementation requires the profile to be passed as `--profile myapp` and rejects a run without it with exit code 2 (`cmd/podium/main.go:372`, `:383`–`:386`); the happy-path test invokes `edit --profile team --add-include ...` (`cmd/podium/profile_edit_test.go:26`–`:32`). A user copying the scenario literally as `podium profile edit myapp` would hit an error because `myapp` is treated as an unrecognized positional argument rather than the profile name. The scenario's `...` is a placeholder for further flags, so the divergence is limited to the profile-name form. Suggested direction: either accept a positional profile name in `profileCmd` as an alias for `--profile`, or align the spec to write `podium profile edit --profile myapp ...`.
## F-14.2 — 14.2 Local registry folder, one-shot, multiple workspaces

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

I verified the concrete commands, flags, and per-workspace state described in scenario 14.2 against `cmd/podium/main.go` (sync dispatch and registry fallback), `pkg/sync` (config, lockfile, run), and `pkg/adapter`. The central 14.2 claim that each workspace keeps its own `<workspace>/.podium/sync.lock` is implemented correctly: the lock path is `<target>/.podium/sync.lock` (`pkg/sync/lockfile.go:59`–`:61`), `--target` defaults to the current directory and is resolved to an absolute path (`cmd/podium/main.go:189`, `:214`), and the lock is written per target (`pkg/sync/sync.go:164`–`:184`), so two workspaces with distinct working directories produce two independent locks with no shared lock or process. The claim that filesystem source needs no shared cache or registry process is also correct: `sync.Run` opens the filesystem registry and walks it directly with no HTTP call (`pkg/sync/sync.go:90`–`:99`). Two of the scenario's literal commands do not run as written: the `--profile` flag is absent on `podium sync`, and the registry that the multi-workspace flow relies on (the user-global `~/.podium/sync.yaml` written by `podium init --global`) is never read during sync.

### - [ ] F-14.2.1 — `podium sync --profile` flag is not implemented; both 14.2 commands fail to parse [High] — OPEN

(gap) §14.2 instructs the developer to run `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile finance` and `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile marketing`, one per workspace. §7.5 defines `--profile <name>` as a sync flag that selects an entry under `profiles:` merged on top of `defaults:` (`spec/07-external-integration.md:159`, `:269`). The `sync` flag set defines only `--registry`, `--target`, `--harness`, `--dry-run`, `--json`, `--watch`, and `--overlay` (`cmd/podium/main.go:188`–`:194`); there is no `--profile` flag. Because the flag set uses `flag.ContinueOnError`, passing `--profile finance` fails parsing with "flag provided but not defined: -profile" and the command returns a non-zero parse exit (`cmd/podium/main.go:196`–`:197`). The flag does exist on the sibling subcommands `sync save-as` (`cmd/podium/main.go:324`) and `profile edit` (`cmd/podium/main.go:372`), which confirms the omission is on the bare `sync` path. Both literal commands in this subsection therefore cannot run. This is the same root cause as F-14.1.1; it is reported here because the commands belonging to §14.2 fail directly. Suggested direction: add `--profile`, `--include`, `--exclude`, and `--type` flags to the `sync` flag set, resolve `defaults` plus the named profile plus CLI overrides into a scope, and thread it into `sync.Run`.

### - [ ] F-14.2.2 — sync registry fallback reads only the workspace `sync.yaml`, not the user-global `~/.podium/sync.yaml` the scenario depends on [High] — OPEN

(gap) §14.2 reuses §14.1's one-time setup, where `podium init --global --registry ~/podium-artifacts/` writes `defaults.registry: ~/podium-artifacts/` to `~/.podium/sync.yaml` (`cmd/podium/main.go:708`–`:715`, `:728`), and §14.2 states that all workspaces "read from the same artifact directory." §7.5.2 mandates that `sync.yaml` is read from up to three file scopes (user-global `~/.podium/sync.yaml`, project-shared `<ws>/.podium/sync.yaml`, and project-local `<ws>/.podium/sync.local.yaml`) and that `defaults.registry` is taken from the merged result with per-key precedence (`spec/07-external-integration.md:200`–`:223`, `:263`). The sync registry fallback reads only the workspace config: it calls `sync.ReadConfig(ws)` with `ws = os.Getwd()` (`cmd/podium/main.go:204`–`:208`), and `ReadConfig` reads exclusively `<workspace>/.podium/sync.yaml` via `ConfigPath` (`pkg/sync/config.go:99`–`:100`, `:60`–`:62`). No code path reads `~/.podium/sync.yaml` or `sync.local.yaml` during sync, and there is no config-merge function across the scopes; the only `os.UserHomeDir` callers are `init` (write) and `cache` (cache directory). The code comment at `cmd/podium/main.go:200`–`:203` claims the fallback covers "Unset across all scopes," but only the workspace scope is consulted. The practical effect on this scenario: in each workspace whose `.podium/sync.yaml` holds only a profile and no `defaults.registry` (the §14.1 step-4 layout), the registry stays empty and the command exits with code 2 and "error: --registry is required" (`cmd/podium/main.go:210`–`:213`), so the multi-workspace flow built on a single global registry does not work without repeating `defaults.registry` in every workspace file or passing `--registry` on each invocation. Suggested direction: load and merge the user-global, project-shared, and project-local `sync.yaml` files per the §7.5.2 precedence table before resolving `defaults.registry`, so a global registry written by `podium init --global` is honored from any workspace.
## F-14.3 — 14.3 Local registry folder, MCP discovery, multiple workspaces

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

This scenario graduates a filesystem artifact directory to a standalone HTTP server and adds MCP discovery. The three concrete claims are: (step 1) `podium serve --standalone --layer-path ~/podium-artifacts/` starts the server against the directory and auto-bootstraps `~/.podium/sync.yaml` with `defaults.registry: http://127.0.0.1:8080`; (step 2) the MCP server picks up the registry from `~/.podium/sync.yaml`'s `defaults.registry` so no extra env var is needed; and (step 3) an optional `.podium/overlay/` per workspace. The MCP discovery tools (`load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, `load_artifact`) are present and forwarded over HTTP (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:257-301). The server-side and MCP-side configuration plumbing that step 1 and step 2 describe is not implemented: the documented `--layer-path` flag does not exist on `podium serve`, the server never writes `~/.podium/sync.yaml`, and the MCP server has no `sync.yaml` registry fallback. The overlay layer honors only the env var and omits the MCP-roots fallback.

### - [ ] F-14.3.1 — `podium serve --layer-path` flag is not implemented [High] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Step 1 of §14.3 instructs the operator to run `podium serve --standalone --layer-path ~/podium-artifacts/`, and §13.10 establishes `--layer-path` as a flag of `podium serve` (spec/13-deployment.md:125-126, 142, 149, 186, 333). The `serve` command registers only `--bind`, `--public-mode`, `--standalone`, and `--config` (cmd/podium/serve.go:22-25). The flag set uses `flag.ContinueOnError` (cmd/podium/serve.go:20), so `fs.Parse` returns an error on the unknown `--layer-path`, and `parseExit` returns exit code 2 (cmd/podium/main.go:125-130). The exact command in the spec therefore fails to start. The implemented mechanism is the `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` environment variable, read in serverboot.go:169, with no corresponding CLI flag. Suggested direction: add a `--layer-path` string flag to `serve.go` that sets `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` for the process, mirroring how `--bind` sets `PODIUM_BIND` (cmd/podium/serve.go:30-31).

### - [ ] F-14.3.2 — `podium serve` does not auto-bootstrap `~/.podium/sync.yaml` [High] — OPEN

(gap) Step 1 of §14.3 states that `podium serve --standalone --layer-path ...` "auto-bootstraps `~/.podium/sync.yaml` with `defaults.registry: http://127.0.0.1:8080`." §13.10 makes the same guarantee: the zero-flag standalone path "creates the standalone defaults (`~/.podium/registry.yaml`, `~/.podium/sync.yaml`, `~/podium-artifacts/`) on first run" and "writes both files in one step on first run ... `~/.podium/sync.yaml` for the client (`defaults.registry: http://127.0.0.1:8080`)" (spec/13-deployment.md:116, 223). The server bootstrap in `serverboot.Run` creates only the `default` tenant (internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:157-161) and reads `~/.podium/registry.yaml` (internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:67-76) but never writes either `~/.podium/sync.yaml` or `~/.podium/registry.yaml`. The only writer of `sync.yaml` is the separate `podium init` command (cmd/podium/main.go:728-738). Because step 2 relies on this auto-bootstrap to supply `defaults.registry`, the absence breaks the documented "no extra env var is needed" flow. Suggested direction: have the standalone bootstrap write `~/.podium/sync.yaml` (and `~/.podium/registry.yaml`) on first run when absent, gated by the standalone mode determination at internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:630.

### - [ ] F-14.3.3 — MCP server does not read `defaults.registry` from `sync.yaml` [High] — OPEN

(gap) Step 2 of §14.3 states that "the MCP server picks up the registry from `~/.podium/sync.yaml` (`defaults.registry`), so no extra env var is needed." §6.11 confirms this explicitly: "When `podium serve` has auto-bootstrapped `~/.podium/sync.yaml` with `defaults.registry: http://127.0.0.1:8080` ... the MCP server resolves the registry from there and the env var can be omitted" (spec/06-mcp-server.md:357), and the env-var table lists `PODIUM_REGISTRY` as "read from `sync.yaml`'s `defaults.registry` per §7.5.2 if unset; required if neither is set" (spec/06-mcp-server.md:17). The MCP server's `loadConfig` reads only `os.Getenv("PODIUM_REGISTRY")` and returns `PODIUM_REGISTRY is required` when it is empty, with no `sync.yaml` lookup (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:99, 119-121). The test `TestLoadConfig_MissingRegistryErrors` locks in this behavior (cmd/podium-mcp/main_helpers_test.go:147-152). The MCP server therefore cannot run without `PODIUM_REGISTRY` even when `~/.podium/sync.yaml` carries `defaults.registry`. The §6.11 host snippets all set `PODIUM_REGISTRY` explicitly, so a configured snippet works, but the §14.3 standalone flow that omits the env var does not. Suggested direction: in `loadConfig`, when `PODIUM_REGISTRY` is unset, resolve `~/.podium/sync.yaml`'s `defaults.registry` using `pkg/sync` (see `ResolveRegistryPath` in pkg/sync/config.go) before failing.

### - [ ] F-14.3.4 — MCP overlay resolution honors only the env var, omitting the MCP-roots fallback [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Step 3 of §14.3 offers an optional `.podium/overlay/` per workspace for in-progress artifacts, and §6.4 defines the overlay path lookup that every consumer "honors the same": `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` if set, then the MCP server "falls back to MCP roots when available: the `roots/list` response identifies the workspace, and the overlay defaults to `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` if that directory exists" (spec/06-mcp-server.md:80-83). The MCP server resolves the overlay only from `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:107, 168-176); when the env var is unset, `cfg.overlayPath` is empty and the overlay layer is disabled. The server never negotiates MCP roots: the `handle` method does not implement `roots/list` and never queries the host for roots (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:231-277). The overlay is also resolved once at startup in `newServer` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:168-176) with no re-indexing; the fsnotify watcher described in §6.4 line 85 is absent from the repository (no `fsnotify` dependency, no watcher in the MCP package). In the §14.3 flow the Claude Code snippet sets `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` so the overlay still works, but hosts using a snippet without that env var (for example the Cursor snippet at spec/06-mcp-server.md:295-307) get no overlay. Suggested direction: implement the §6.4 step-2 fallback by requesting `roots/list` during `initialize` and defaulting the overlay to `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` when `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` is unset.
## F-14.4 — 14.4 Local registry, custom harness via SDK, multiple workspaces

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

Section 14.4 (lines 49-59) describes a scenario where each workspace runs an app built on `podium-py` or `podium-ts` plus an agent SDK against a standalone server. The concrete contract is the SDK example: `client = Client.from_env()` with the comment "picks up registry URL from sync.yaml + overlay path", followed by a `search_artifacts → load_artifact` discovery flow, across "multiple workspaces" each with its own overlay. Both SDKs exist (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py`, `sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts`), expose a `Client` with `from_env` / `fromEnv`, and implement `search_artifacts` and `load_artifact` over HTTP, so the core discovery path against a server functions and matches §7.6. Two behaviors that §14.4 names explicitly are absent: `from_env` does not resolve the registry from `sync.yaml`, and the overlay path that `from_env` reads is inert (no overlay merge), which defeats the multi-workspace overlay part of the scenario. The controlling normative sections for these two behaviors are §7.5.2 / §13.10 (registry resolution) and §6.4 (overlay merge); the findings below are scoped to the §14.4 claims they break.

### - [ ] F-14.4.1 — `Client.from_env()` does not read the registry from `sync.yaml` [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 14.4 line 57 states that `Client.from_env()` "picks up registry URL from sync.yaml + overlay path". The scenario is explicitly framed as a graduation from §14.1's filesystem setup where the registry URL lives in `~/.podium/sync.yaml` as `defaults.registry: http://127.0.0.1:8080` (written by `podium serve --standalone` per §13.10 and §14.3). §13-deployment.md line 223 reinforces that SDK clients reach the server "via `sync.yaml`'s `defaults.registry`, `PODIUM_REGISTRY`, or an SDK constructor param". The Python implementation in `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:84-93` reads only the `PODIUM_REGISTRY` environment variable and raises `RuntimeError("PODIUM_REGISTRY environment variable is required")` when it is unset; it never opens `~/.podium/sync.yaml` or any project-scoped `sync.yaml`. The module imports only `json` and `urllib` (client.py:5-8) and has no YAML or config-resolution dependency. The TypeScript `Client.fromEnv` (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:106-116`) behaves identically, reading `process.env.PODIUM_REGISTRY` only. A developer who follows §14.4 literally, with the registry configured solely in `~/.podium/sync.yaml` and no `PODIUM_REGISTRY` exported, gets a hard error from `from_env()` rather than a working client. The §7.6 SDK-surface comment (07-external-integration.md:423-424) describes `from_env` as reading env vars only, so the implementation matches §7.6 while contradicting §14.4's prose; the two spec sections disagree and the code follows the narrower one. Suggested direction: either implement `sync.yaml` `defaults.registry` resolution in `from_env` (mirroring the Go client's merged-config lookup) so §14.4 works as written, or correct the §14.4 comment to state that `from_env` reads `PODIUM_REGISTRY` (and the constructor or an exported env var is required when only `sync.yaml` is configured).

### - [ ] F-14.4.2 — Workspace overlay read by `from_env` is never applied by the SDK [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Section 14.4 is the multi-workspace SDK scenario, and its example notes that `from_env()` picks up the "overlay path"; the scenario inherits the per-workspace overlay model used throughout §14 (each workspace has its own `.podium/overlay/`). §6.4 makes the overlay a hard requirement for the SDK as a consumer: line 80 says `Client(overlay_path=...)` takes precedence over `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH`, line 82 says "`podium sync` and the SDK fall back to `<CWD>/.podium/overlay/` if that directory exists", line 89 says the overlay "is merged in by the consumer (MCP server, sync, or SDK)", and line 95 says `search_artifacts` calls fan out to both the registry and a local overlay index and fuse via reciprocal rank fusion. The implementation reads the overlay path into a field but never uses it. In `sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py` the constructor stores `self.overlay_path` (line 82) and `from_env` populates it from `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` (line 92), but no method builds a local index, fans out to the overlay, resolves overlay artifacts in `load_artifact` (client.py:154-166), or falls back to `<CWD>/.podium/overlay/`. The TypeScript SDK is the same: `overlayPath` is stored (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:96,102,114`) and otherwise unused. The server endpoints carry no overlay parameter, confirming the merge is meant to happen client-side. The result is that the workspace-local overlay central to the §14.4 multi-workspace scenario is silently ignored by the SDK; in-progress artifacts under `.podium/overlay/` never appear in `search_artifacts` or `load_artifact`. Suggested direction: implement the `LocalOverlayProvider` behavior from §6.4 in both SDKs (index the overlay manifests, fuse overlay hits into `search_artifacts` via RRF, resolve overlay artifacts ahead of the registry in `load_artifact`, and apply the `<CWD>/.podium/overlay/` fallback), or, if the SDKs are intended to omit overlay merge, remove the overlay claim from §14.4 and the inert `overlay_path` parameter and document overlay support as SDK-out-of-scope in §6.4 and §7.6.

### - [ ] F-14.4.3 — `from_env` missing-registry error is generic, not `config.no_registry` [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The §14.4 scenario relies on `from_env()` to resolve a registry, and the spec defines the no-registry condition as the namespaced error `config.no_registry` (07-external-integration.md:263 "Unset across all scopes: `config.no_registry` error"; 13-deployment.md:277). The Go client implements this code (`pkg/sync/sync.go:30` `ErrNoRegistry = errors.New("config.no_registry: no registry configured")`). The SDK instead raises a generic `RuntimeError("PODIUM_REGISTRY environment variable is required")` in Python (`sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:88`) and a generic `Error` in TypeScript (`sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:109`), with no `config.no_registry` code and no pointer to `podium init`. This is a consequence of F-14.4.1: the SDK does not perform the merged-config resolution that produces `config.no_registry`, so it cannot report that an unset registry across all scopes is the cause. The blast radius is small because the message is human-readable and the SDK currently checks one env var rather than a config chain. Suggested direction: when `from_env` resolution is broadened (F-14.4.1), surface the spec error code (for example, raise a `RegistryError("config.no_registry", ...)` or an SDK equivalent that carries the code) and point the caller at `podium init`, so the SDK and CLI report the same condition consistently.
## F-14.5 — 14.5 Remote registry, one-shot, multiple workspaces

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

This subsection is a short operator-and-developer walkthrough for a remote (server) registry consumed by multiple workspaces. The concrete client claims are step 4 (`podium init --global --registry https://podium.acme.com` writes `~/.podium/sync.yaml` with `defaults.registry`), step 5 (bare `podium login` completes the device-code flow once and caches the token), step 6 (write a project `.podium/sync.yaml` with a profile and run `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile <name>`), and step 7 (each workspace keeps its own lock file). The operator steps 1 through 3 point at §13.1, §4.6, and §7.3.1, all of which are backed by real implementation (`pkg/layer/composer.go`, `pkg/registry/server/webhooks.go`, ingest) and are not contradicted here. `podium init --global --registry` is implemented (`cmd/podium/main.go:672` `initCmd`, writing `defaults.registry`), the device-code flow and keychain caching are implemented (`cmd/podium/login.go:26`, `pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go`), and the lock file is per-target (`pkg/sync/lockfile.go:59` `LockFilePath`). The walkthrough breaks because both `podium login` (step 5) and `podium sync` (step 6) are run with no `--registry` flag and rely on resolving `defaults.registry` from the global `~/.podium/sync.yaml` written in step 4, and the client does not perform that resolution.

### - [ ] F-14.5.1 — `podium login` does not resolve the registry from sync.yaml [High] — OPEN

(gap) Scenario 14.5 runs `podium init --global --registry https://podium.acme.com` (step 4) and then bare `podium login` (step 5), with no `--registry` flag and no `PODIUM_REGISTRY` environment variable mentioned. The §7.7 client-lifecycle text states that `podium login` "runs the OAuth flow when the resolved registry is a server" (spec/07-external-integration.md:586), where "the resolved registry" is the merged `defaults.registry` per the §7.5.2 precedence. The implementation in `cmd/podium/login.go:29` only reads `--registry` defaulting to `os.Getenv("PODIUM_REGISTRY")`, and at `cmd/podium/login.go:39-42` it exits 2 with "error: --registry is required" when that value is empty. It never calls `sync.ReadConfig` or any merged-config reader; the top-level dispatch passes arguments straight through (`cmd/podium/main.go:64-65`) with no registry injection. As written, step 5 fails because the registry lives only in `~/.podium/sync.yaml`. Suggested direction: have `loginCmd` fall back to the resolved `defaults.registry` from the merged `sync.yaml` scopes (global, project-shared, and project-local per §7.5.2) when `--registry` and `PODIUM_REGISTRY` are both empty, mirroring the fallback the sync path already attempts at `cmd/podium/main.go:204-208`.

### - [ ] F-14.5.2 — `podium sync` reads `defaults.registry` only from the workspace file, not the global `~/.podium/sync.yaml` [High] — OPEN

(gap) In scenario 14.5 the registry is written to the user-global file via `podium init --global` (step 4), and the per-project `.podium/sync.yaml` contains only a profile (step 6). The §7.5.2 precedence table lists `~/.podium/sync.yaml` as a valid scope for `defaults.registry` (spec/07-external-integration.md:206, 214-220), so a bare `podium sync` from the project should pick up the registry from the global file. The implementation resolves the fallback from a single scope only: `cmd/podium/main.go:204-208` calls `sync.ReadConfig(ws)` where `ws = os.Getwd()` (the project directory) and reads `cfg.Defaults.Registry` from that one file. There is no merged multi-scope reader in `pkg/sync` (grep for `MergedConfig`/`mergeConfig` in `pkg/sync/*.go` returns nothing; `ResolveRegistryPath` at `pkg/sync/config.go:68` resolves a single value). Because the project `sync.yaml` has no `defaults.registry`, `*registry` stays empty and sync exits 2 at `cmd/podium/main.go:210-212`. The scenario's step 6 therefore cannot run as written. Suggested direction: implement the §7.5.2 scope merge (global, project-shared, project-local) and resolve `defaults.registry` against the merged result before the empty-registry check; the precedence contract itself is owned by §7.5/§7.7, but the 14.5 walkthrough depends on the global-scope read existing.

### - [ ] F-14.5.3 — `podium login` device-code poll has no client-side timeout [Info] — OPEN

(bug) Scenario 14.5 step 5 says the developer "completes the device-code flow once." The §6.3 contract for CLI commands states they "poll the IdP's token endpoint until the user completes the flow or a 10-minute timeout elapses" (spec/06-mcp-server.md:38). The login command builds the poll context with `ctx := context.Background()` (`cmd/podium/login.go:61`) and passes it to `flow.Poll` (`cmd/podium/login.go:72`). `DeviceCodeFlow.Poll` (`pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:304-325`) loops until `ctx.Done()`, an `expired_token`, or an `access_denied` response, so with a background context the only termination is the IdP returning `expired_token`. There is no client-side 10-minute deadline. An IdP that returns a long `expires_in` or keeps replying `authorization_pending` leaves the command blocked indefinitely. This is primarily a §6.3 login-contract detail rather than a distinct 14.5 claim, so it is recorded at Info. Suggested direction: wrap the poll context with `context.WithTimeout(ctx, 10*time.Minute)` (or honor `auth.ExpiresIn`, whichever is shorter) in `loginCmd` so the flow terminates as the spec describes.
## F-14.6 — 14.6 Remote registry + workspace local overlay, one-shot

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

Section 14.6 is a short scenario. It reuses the operator setup from §14.5 (a remote registry at a URL such as `https://podium.acme.com`), then has the developer drop in-progress artifacts under `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` and run `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile <name>`. Step 2 states the overlay path auto-resolves to `<CWD>/.podium/overlay/` per §6.4 with no env var needed. I traced the two concrete contracts the scenario depends on: server-source sync and workspace-overlay auto-resolution. Both are missing in the implementation, so the §14.6 walkthrough as written does not work. The overlay merge logic itself is implemented and tested, but only against a filesystem registry and only when the overlay path is supplied explicitly.

### - [ ] F-14.6.1 — `podium sync` against a remote registry is unimplemented [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 14.6 inherits the operator setup of §14.5, which deploys a registry reached over HTTP (`podium init --global --registry https://podium.acme.com`), then runs `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile <name>` against it (spec/14-common-scenarios.md:78-81, :71). Section 7.5 makes the dispatch explicit: "`podium sync` works against either kind of registry source: a server (URL) or a local filesystem (path)" and "a URL routes to a Podium server, a filesystem path routes to local filesystem" (spec/07-external-integration.md:171, :10, :261). The implementation does not dispatch on the scheme. `pkg/sync.Run` always calls `filesystem.Open(opts.RegistryPath)` (pkg/sync/sync.go:90) and its package doc states "The function does not consult any HTTP service" (pkg/sync/sync.go:1-4, :65-68). `filesystem.Open` runs `filepath.Abs` then `os.Stat` on the value and returns `ErrConfigMissing` when the path does not exist (pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:107-121), so a value like `https://podium.acme.com` becomes a bogus local path and the sync fails. The CLI sync command resolves `defaults.registry` through `sync.ResolveRegistryPath`, which passes HTTP and `file://` URLs through unchanged (pkg/sync/config.go:64-94), but then hands the URL straight to `sync.Run` with no URL-versus-path branch (cmd/podium/main.go:204-229). No HTTP sync client exists anywhere in `pkg/sync` or elsewhere; `net/http` is not imported in the package and a repo-wide search found no server-source sync path. The watch loop is likewise filesystem-only: it fingerprints the registry with `filepath.WalkDir` (pkg/sync/watch.go:119-162). This gap is shared with §14.5, §14.7, and §14.9-§14.13, but it is a hard blocker for §14.6 because the scenario's registry is remote. Suggested direction: implement the §7.5.2 dispatch so that a URL routes `podium sync` to an HTTP client that resolves the effective view, fetches and materializes artifacts through the same identity providers, content cache, and harness adapters as the MCP server (per spec/07-external-integration.md:171), and route only filesystem paths to `filesystem.Open`.

### - [ ] F-14.6.2 — `podium sync` does not auto-resolve the workspace overlay path [High] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Section 14.6 step 2 states: "The overlay path auto-resolves to `<CWD>/.podium/overlay/` per §6.4; no env var needed" (spec/14-common-scenarios.md:80-81). Section 6.4 defines the lookup every consumer honors: `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` if set, then (for the MCP server) MCP roots, then for `podium sync` and the SDK fall back to `<CWD>/.podium/overlay/` if that directory exists, otherwise the layer is disabled (spec/06-mcp-server.md:78-83). The CLI sync command does none of this. `OverlayPath` is populated solely from the `--overlay` flag, whose default is the empty string (cmd/podium/main.go:194, :224); the command reads `os.Getwd()` only to resolve the registry config, never to build an overlay candidate (cmd/podium/main.go:205-209), and it does not read `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH`. When `opts.OverlayPath` is empty, `sync.Run` skips the overlay merge entirely (pkg/sync/sync.go:104-112), so neither rule 1 (env var) nor rule 3 (CWD fallback) of §6.4 is honored. A resolution helper that implements the env-var and CWD-fallback rules exists at `overlay.ResolveWorkspaceOverlay` (pkg/overlay/overlay.go:59-76), but it has no non-test caller anywhere in the repository. The result is that a developer who follows §14.6 step 1 (drop artifacts under `.podium/overlay/`) and runs `podium sync` without `--overlay` gets no overlay merge, contradicting the documented behavior. Suggested direction: in the sync command, when `--overlay` is unset, call `overlay.ResolveWorkspaceOverlay(cwd, os.Getenv("PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH"))` and pass the resolved path (treating `ErrNoOverlay` as "layer disabled") into `sync.Options.OverlayPath`, so the consumer honors the full §6.4 chain.
## F-14.7 — 14.7 Remote registry + local overlay, MCP, multiple workspaces

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

The 14.7 scenario describes per-workspace MCP usage against a remote registry with a workspace-local overlay. It makes three concrete claims: the harness MCP entry is configured with `PODIUM_REGISTRY` and `PODIUM_HARNESS` while `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` is optional and falls back to MCP roots; the first call triggers an OAuth device-code flow via MCP elicitation with the token cached in the OS keychain; and the MCP server's fsnotify watcher picks up overlay changes. I traced these against `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go`, the overlay resolution in `pkg/overlay/overlay.go`, the identity package in `pkg/identity/`, and the watch implementation in `pkg/sync/watch.go`. The `PODIUM_REGISTRY` and `PODIUM_HARNESS` env vars are read and honored (main.go:99-100). The other three behaviors named in the scenario are absent from the MCP server: the default `oauth-device-code` identity provider with MCP elicitation and keychain caching is unimplemented, the MCP-roots overlay fallback is missing, and the overlay is loaded once at startup with no fsnotify watcher.

### - [ ] F-14.7.1 — MCP server has no OAuth device-code flow, MCP elicitation, or keychain credential caching [High] — OPEN

(gap) 14.7 step 2 states "First call triggers OAuth device-code via MCP elicitation. Token caches in the OS keychain." This is the default authentication model for the MCP scenario. §6.3 line 18 sets the MCP server default `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` to `oauth-device-code`, §6.3 line 37 states the MCP server "uses MCP elicitation; the host displays the URL and code in the agent UI", and §6.3 line 5 lists "OS-keychain-stored credentials (in `oauth-device-code` mode)" as MCP server local state. The MCP server does not implement any of this. `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go` never reads `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` (a repo-wide grep finds readers only in `cmd/podium/status.go`, `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go`, and `pkg/registry/server/`), never imports `pkg/identity`, and never imports the keychain `TokenStore` (`pkg/identity/keychain.go` is wired only into `cmd/podium/login.go`). The only authentication path is `currentToken()` (main.go:753-773), which reads a static injected JWT from `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN`, a custom env var named by `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_ENV`, or `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE`. That is the `injected-session-token` provider (§6.3 line 41), which is not the default and requires the runtime to issue and rotate tokens. There is no 401-triggered reauth, no elicitation request, and no token persistence. The `pkg/identity/oauth_devicecode.go:31` comment claims the flow "surfaces via MCP elicitation", but no MCP server code calls it. Suggested direction: wire an `oauth-device-code` provider into the MCP bridge that initiates `DeviceCodeFlow` on the first registry call, surfaces the verification URL and user code through an MCP elicitation request, polls the IdP token endpoint, and persists the resulting tokens via the keychain `TokenStore`; gate this behind `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` with `oauth-device-code` as the default to match §6.3.

### - [ ] F-14.7.2 — MCP server does not fall back to MCP roots when PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH is unset [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) 14.7 step 1 states "`PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` is optional; when unset, the MCP server resolves the overlay from MCP roots (§6.4)." §6.4 step 2 specifies the mechanism: "The MCP server falls back to MCP roots when available: the `roots/list` response identifies the workspace, and the overlay defaults to `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` if that directory exists." The MCP server reads the overlay path only from `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` (main.go:107) and loads the overlay only when that value is non-empty (main.go:168). A repo-wide grep for "roots" in `cmd/podium-mcp/` returns nothing, and the `initialize` handler (main.go:234-256) does not advertise a `roots` capability or issue a `roots/list` request to the host. When `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` is unset, the overlay layer is simply disabled, so the documented zero-configuration overlay path for the MCP scenario never activates. Suggested direction: after `initialize`, when `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` is empty, send a `roots/list` request to the host, take the first workspace root, and resolve the overlay to `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/` when that directory exists, matching the §6.4 lookup order.

### - [ ] F-14.7.3 — MCP server loads the overlay once at startup with no fsnotify watcher [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) 14.7 step 3 states "Drop workspace-local artifacts under `.podium/overlay/`. The MCP server's fsnotify watcher picks up changes." §6.4 line 85 makes this explicit: "The MCP server watches the resolved path via fsnotify and re-indexes on change." The MCP server resolves the overlay exactly once in `newServer` (main.go:168-176) and the comment at main.go:166-167 states the records are loaded "now and reuse[d] for the bridge lifetime." The resolved `srv.overlay` slice (main.go:151) is never refreshed; `overlayMatch` (main.go:184-191) reads the static slice, and the local search index built from the overlay is likewise fixed at startup. There is no fsnotify watcher in `cmd/podium-mcp/`; the only fsnotify usage in the repo is `pkg/sync/watch.go`, which serves `podium sync --watch` and is not referenced by the MCP binary. Workspace-local artifacts added or edited after the MCP server starts are not seen until the host restarts the bridge process, contradicting the "picks up changes" guarantee. Suggested direction: add an fsnotify watcher over the resolved overlay path that re-runs `overlay.Filesystem{...}.Resolve` and rebuilds the local search index on create, write, rename, and remove events, guarding `srv.overlay` and the index against concurrent reads from in-flight tool calls.
## F-14.8 — 14.8 Remote registry + local overlay, custom harness via SDK

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

Section 14.8 is a short scenario walkthrough whose only concrete contract is the SDK code snippet (spec/14-common-scenarios.md:95-103). It constructs a `Client` with `registry`, `identity_provider="oauth-device-code"`, and `overlay_path`, then calls `client.login()` described as the "device-code flow before any catalog calls", then uses `search_artifacts` / `load_artifact`. I checked both SDKs (sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py, sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts), their tests, READMEs, and cross-referenced the SDK surface in spec §7.6 and the device-code contract in §7.7. The constructor signature, `search_artifacts`, and `load_artifact` are present and match. The `login()` method and any client-side authentication are entirely absent, so the central action the scenario prescribes for a remote (authenticated) registry cannot be performed.

### - [ ] F-14.8.1 — SDK Client has no login() method [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 14.8 prescribes `client.login()` with the comment "device-code flow before any catalog calls" (spec/14-common-scenarios.md:101). No `login` method exists on the `Client` class in either SDK. The Python `Client` exposes `from_env`, `load_domain`, `search_domains`, `search_artifacts`, `load_artifact`, `load_artifacts`, `dependents_of`, `preview_scope`, and `subscribe`, and nothing else (sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:73-265). The TypeScript `Client` mirrors that set with no `login` (sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:93-280). A repository-wide search for `login` inside the SDK source returns nothing; the only `login` implementation is the `podium login` Go CLI under cmd/podium, which is a separate binary. The Python source comments confirm the omission is intentional for now ("Stage 3 does not implement OAuth; this exception is wired so callers can catch it once oauth-device-code lands in Phase 11", sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:26-27), and both READMEs state that "OAuth device code ... remain on the roadmap" (sdks/podium-py/README.md) and "device-code scaffolding; identity-provider integration matures in later phases" (sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:2-3). The exact program in spec §14.8 therefore raises `AttributeError` on `client.login()`. Suggested direction: implement `Client.login()` (and `Client.login()` in TS) that runs the `oauth-device-code` flow described in §6.3 and §7.7 and caches the token, or, if the SDK auth surface is deferred, update §14.8 (and the §7.6 snippet) to reflect the supported surface instead of `client.login()`.

### - [ ] F-14.8.2 — identity_provider is accepted but never authenticates requests [High] — OPEN

(gap) Section 14.8 is the remote-registry scenario; its operator setup (§14.5, referenced at spec/14-common-scenarios.md:93) deploys an OIDC IdP, so catalog calls must carry an identity. The snippet passes `identity_provider="oauth-device-code"` to the constructor (spec/14-common-scenarios.md:98). Both SDKs store this value but never use it on any request. In Python, `self.identity_provider` is assigned in `__init__` (sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:81) and read nowhere afterward; `_get` issues `urllib.request.Request(url)` with no headers (sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:266-276) and the batch-load POST sets only `Content-Type: application/json` (sdks/podium-py/podium/client.py:197-202). In TypeScript, `this.identityProvider` is assigned (sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:101) and never consulted; the `get` helper and `loadArtifacts` send no `Authorization` header (sdks/podium-ts/src/index.ts:185-189, 258-279). A search across both SDK source trees for `Authorization`, `Bearer`, `token`, `keychain`, and `credential` finds no token acquisition, no keychain read, and no cached-credential lookup. Against a real remote registry that enforces OIDC, every `search_artifacts` / `load_artifact` call is unauthenticated and would be rejected, so the §14.8 scenario cannot complete even ignoring the missing `login()`. This overlaps with F-14.8.1 but is a distinct defect: the constructor advertises an identity provider that has no effect on the wire. Suggested direction: once a credential source exists (login flow or a cached token written by `podium login`), attach the access token as an `Authorization: Bearer` header on every request, keyed by registry URL per §7.7; until then, document that the SDK sends unauthenticated requests so the `identity_provider` parameter does not imply working auth.
## F-14.9 — 14.9 Enterprise multi-layer setup

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation (re-run against main e41f44e)._

I re-verified the §14.9 enterprise contracts against the current main tree: the per-tenant `registry.yaml` `layers:` declaration block (a list with `source: { git: { repo, ref, root } }` and `visibility:`), the `podium layer register` command for personal user-defined layers, the cap of 3 user-defined layers per identity, the implicit `users: [<registrant>]` visibility, and the effective-view composition of admin layers (visibility-filtered), user-defined layers, and the workspace overlay together with the OIDC identity path the scenario assumes. The visibility evaluator and cross-layer composition in pkg/layer (composer.go) still match §4.6, and the admin diagnostic override is `ShowEffective` (pkg/registry/core/admin.go). The enterprise visibility machinery this scenario depends on is largely absent on main: per-layer visibility loading from a config file, an OIDC/attested-identity request path, and admin gating of the layer surface are not wired. All five prior findings remain OPEN. Three were corrected to main reality because their prior text cited feature-branch code that does not exist on main: F-14.9.2 cited `.podium/layers.yaml` and `layer_visibility.go`, F-14.9.4 cited a `DescribeVisibility`/`deny-all` endpoint, and F-14.9.5 cited a serverboot identity-resolver fallback block; none of those exist on main, so each is restated as an open gap with current citations. The other two (F-14.9.1, F-14.9.3) needed only refreshed line numbers. Zero prior findings were resolved.

### - [x] F-14.9.1 — User-defined-layer cap of 3 per identity is not implemented or enforced [High] — CLOSED

(gap) §14.9 line 130 states personal user-defined layers are "Capped at 3 per identity by default." The same cap is restated in §7.3.1 (spec/07-external-integration.md:95, "Default cap: 3 user-defined layers per identity, configurable per tenant"), §01-overview line 89 ("Cap of 3 user-defined layers per identity by default … Configurable per tenant"), §07 line 97 (cap exhaustion maps to `quota.*`, "including the user-defined-layer cap"), and §11-verification line 53 lists "the user-defined-layer cap is enforced" as a required verification test. The registration handler `LayerEndpoint.register` at /Users/joan/projects/podium/pkg/registry/server/layers.go:183-275 never counts existing user-defined layers for the owner and never rejects a registration that would exceed a cap. No cap field exists on `QuotaInfo` (/Users/joan/projects/podium/pkg/registry/core/quota.go:11-21), and a repo-wide search for any layer cap or per-identity layer limit returns nothing in pkg, internal, or cmd. No test exercises the cap; /Users/joan/projects/podium/pkg/registry/server/layers_test.go covers register, list, unregister, implicit users, reorder, and admin-auth, but not the cap. An authenticated user can register an unbounded number of user-defined layers. Suggested direction: in `register`, when `req.UserDefined` is true, count the caller's existing user-defined layers via `ListLayerConfigs` filtered by owner and reject with a `quota.*` code (HTTP 429 per the §6.10 envelope) once the configured cap (default 3) is reached; add a tenant-configurable cap setting and the §11 verification test.

**Resolution (commit `39d402d`):** Closed by the canonical fix F-1.4.1. `LayerEndpoint.register` counts the owner's existing user-defined layers via `ListLayerConfigs` and rejects with `quota.layer_count_exceeded` at HTTP 429; the tenant-configurable cap setting is `store.Quota.MaxUserLayers` (also `PODIUM_MAX_USER_LAYERS`), and the §11.5 verification test ("the user-defined-layer cap is enforced") is the now-unskipped e2e `TestOrg_60_UserDefinedLayerCap`.

### - [ ] F-14.9.2 — `registry.yaml` `layers:` block (source + visibility) is not parsed by the server [High] — OPEN

(gap) §14.9 step 2 (spec/14-common-scenarios.md:110-122) instructs the operator to "Configure multiple Git repos as layers, with visibility per §4.6" and shows a `layers:` list where each entry has `id`, `source: { git: { repo, ref, root } }`, and `visibility:` with `organization`, `groups`, or `public`. §4.6 "Config schema" (spec/04-artifact-model.md:626-664) defines this same per-tenant `registry.yaml` `layers:` structure as the canonical admin-layer declaration, and §4.6 line 584 states admin-defined layers are "declared in the registry config by tenant admins." The server bootstrap config parser does not read this block. The `Layers` field of `yamlConfig` is a single `yamlLayerCfg` struct, not a list (/Users/joan/projects/podium/internal/serverboot/yaml_config.go:23), and `yamlLayerCfg` exposes only `default_visibility` and `path` (yaml_config.go:58-64). `applyYAML` reads only those two fields (yaml_config.go:146-151). A repo-wide search for any YAML parser of nested `source`/`git`/`repo`/`ref` layer entries returns nothing. The only config-driven layer ingestion on main is `bootstrapLayerPath` for the single `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH` standalone directory (/Users/joan/projects/podium/internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:156-203), which carries no `source` block and no `visibility` declaration and hardcodes `Public: true` for every resolved layer (serverboot.go:188,197). Admin layers can otherwise only be created one at a time through the HTTP `POST /v1/layers` endpoint (flat JSON fields, layers.go:65-79). The §14.9 and §4.6 declarative config file cannot be loaded as written. Suggested direction: add a `layers:` list to the server config schema (`id`, `source.{git,local}`, `visibility`), and have serverboot upsert each entry into the store's `LayerConfig` rows at startup so the documented operator workflow works without manual per-layer HTTP calls.

### - [ ] F-14.9.3 — `podium layer register` does not register a personal layer for an authenticated user as documented [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §14.9 line 130 documents `podium layer register --id my-experiments --repo git@github.com:alice/podium-experiments.git --ref main` as the way a user registers a personal (user-defined) layer, and §7.3.1 line 95 states "Authenticated users register their own layers via `podium layer register`" with implicit visibility `users: [<registrant>]`. The §7.3.1 CLI signature (spec/07-external-integration.md:84-85) has no `--user-defined` flag. The implementation requires an explicit `--user-defined` flag for the layer to be marked user-defined: /Users/joan/projects/podium/cmd/podium/layer.go:169 defines the flag and lines 203-206 set `user_defined` only when it is passed. Without it, the server treats the registration as admin-defined and rejects non-admin callers with `auth.forbidden` (/Users/joan/projects/podium/pkg/registry/server/layers.go:201-206) when admin auth is wired. The documented invocation therefore does not create a personal layer for a normal authenticated user. Suggested direction: either default `podium layer register` to user-defined for authenticated non-admin callers (with an `--admin`/`--shared` opt-in for admin-defined layers), or update the spec to show the `--user-defined` flag in the §7.3.1 signature and the §14.9 example.

### - [ ] F-14.9.4 — User-defined layer owner is taken from the request body, not the attested identity; omitting it yields a layer no one can see [Medium] — OPEN

(bug) §4.6 line 616 states user-defined layers "have implicit visibility `users: [<registrant>]`; the field is set automatically and cannot be widened," and §14.9 / §7.3.1 frame registration as an authenticated-user action where the registrant is the caller. The `register` handler derives the owner only from the request body field `req.Owner` (/Users/joan/projects/podium/pkg/registry/server/layers.go:217); it never reads the caller's attested identity from the request (the layer endpoint has no identity resolver). The implicit `users: [owner]` assignment runs only when `cfg.Owner != ""` (layers.go:227-229), and the deployment default-visibility fallback is skipped for user-defined layers because the guard at layers.go:235 requires `!cfg.UserDefined`. Consequently, a user-defined layer registered without an owner (the CLI sends `owner` only when `--user-defined` is passed, and then forwards whatever `--owner` carried, including the empty string; layer.go:170,203-206) gets no visibility entries at all. The visibility evaluator `VisibleWith` returns false for a layer with no `Public`, `Organization`, `Groups`, or `Users` set (/Users/joan/projects/podium/pkg/layer/composer.go:59-104), so not even the registrant can see the layer; the stored row is unreachable. (The prior run cited a `DescribeVisibility` endpoint reporting `deny-all`; that endpoint lived in the feature-branch `layer_visibility.go`, which is absent on main, so the symptom is now an invisible layer in the effective view rather than a `deny-all` report.) Suggested direction: derive the owner server-side from the attested identity for `user_defined` registrations, set `users: [<sub>]` automatically, and reject the registration if no identity is present rather than persisting an unreachable layer.

### - [ ] F-14.9.5 — Server bootstrap wires no attested identity and no admin authorization for the enterprise layer surface [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §14.9 describes a full enterprise deployment where the operator configures "admin grants" (step 3) and the consumer "authenticates via OIDC" (line 128), with the effective view composing "admin layers (visibility-filtered) + user-defined layers + workspace local overlay." The composition order and visibility filtering exist at the core level (/Users/joan/projects/podium/pkg/layer/composer.go:99-110 `EffectiveLayersWith`, /Users/joan/projects/podium/pkg/registry/core/admin.go:61-72 `ShowEffective`), but the server bootstrap installs neither the identity path nor the admin gating the scenario assumes.
