The layer endpoint is constructed with `WithDefaultVisibility` only and is never given `WithAdminAuth` (/Users/joan/projects/podium/internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:323-324), so `authAdmin` stays the no-op `func(*http.Request) error { return nil }` from `NewLayerEndpoint` (/Users/joan/projects/podium/pkg/registry/server/layers.go:52-57); admin-defined layer register, update, unregister, and reorder are not restricted to admins in this deployment. serverboot never calls `server.WithIdentityResolver`, so the server falls back to its default resolver, which returns `layer.Identity{IsPublic: true}` for every request (/Users/joan/projects/podium/pkg/registry/server/server.go:178-181), and visibility filtering treats every caller as anonymous-public. `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` is read into the config (serverboot.go:545) but is used only by the §13.10 public-mode mutual-exclusion guard (`StartupConfig.Validate`, /Users/joan/projects/podium/pkg/registry/server/config_validate.go:28-34) and the startup mode banner (serverboot.go:644-645); it installs no request-time verifier. main provides only the OAuth device-code and injected-session-token client identity providers in pkg/identity; there is no server-side OIDC verifier and no trusted-headers provider. serverboot is documented as the "standalone … no auth" path (serverboot.go:9-11), and both `podium-server` (cmd/podium-server/main.go:20) and `podium serve` (cmd/podium/serve.go:49) call `serverboot.Run`, so no distinct enterprise entrypoint exists. The available server bootstrap does not realize the §14.9 enterprise wiring (OIDC identity plus admin-gated, visibility-filtered layer management). Suggested direction: add an OIDC verifier wired through `server.WithIdentityResolver` and gate the layer surface by wiring `WithAdminAuth` to the core admin check, or document that §14.9 requires a deployment path that main does not yet ship.
## F-14.10 — 14.10 Standalone registry with a Git-source layer

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation (re-run against main e41f44e)._

The subsection describes a single-developer standalone server (`podium serve --standalone --layer-path ~/podium-artifacts`) that registers a public Git repo as a layer and pulls it manually via `podium layer reingest` or `podium layer watch`. The merge resolved one prior finding: `podium serve` now defines a `--layer-path` flag that sets `PODIUM_LAYER_PATH`, and the standalone bootstrap ingests the filesystem registry at startup. The startup bootstrap (`bootstrapLayerPath` in `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:156-203`) handles only local filesystem layers; it never opens a Git source, which is consistent with the scenario where the Git layer is registered after startup. The manual-pull path the scenario depends on remains unwired: the reingest endpoint still records intent without ingesting, the ingest orchestrator still has no production caller, the per-layer webhook URL is advertised with no receiver, and `--interval 1h` still fails to parse. The merge also surfaced a register-time visibility deviation: the scenario registers the Git layer without an explicit visibility flag, and the standalone register default lands `private` instead of the `public` the spec prescribes for standalone. Of six prior findings, one is resolved and five remain; one new finding is added.

### - [ ] F-14.10.1 — `podium layer reingest` never ingests the Git source [High] — OPEN

(bug) Step 3 of §14.10 states that on a developer machine without a public ingress the operator should "ignore the webhook and pull manually instead: `podium layer reingest community-skills`". The reingest path must clone the Git repo and ingest its artifacts into the standalone registry. The server handler `reingest` in `pkg/registry/server/layers.go:383-407` only loads the layer config and returns `{"queued": cfg.ID, "queued_at": <now>}`; its comment states "The actual ingest pipeline runs externally; this endpoint records the intent so an orchestrator can pick it up... the pipeline integration lands when the standalone server's ingest scheduler ships." The orchestrator that performs the clone and ingest, `ingest.SourceIngestWithOptions` in `pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go:74`, has no production caller anywhere in `pkg`, `internal`, or `cmd` (only `orchestrator.go` itself and `*_test.go` files reference it). The merge added `bootstrapLayerPath` (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:156-203`), but it ingests only the local filesystem layers found by `filesystem.Open` at startup, persists each with `SourceType: "local"`, and never resolves a `source.Provider` for Git sources; it also runs once at boot rather than on a reingest call. Consequently a registered `community-skills` Git layer is stored but its artifacts are never loaded, so `podium sync` in the "Per project" step returns nothing from that layer. Suggested direction: have the reingest handler resolve the layer's source provider (Git when `source_type == "git"`) and call `ingest.SourceIngestWithOptions` synchronously, or run a scheduler in `serverboot.Run` that drains queued reingests.

### - [ ] F-14.10.2 — `podium layer watch` polls a no-op endpoint and never ingests [High] — OPEN

(bug) Step 3 offers `podium layer watch community-skills --interval 1h` "for periodic sync" as the alternative manual-pull mechanism. `layerWatch` in `cmd/podium/layer.go:130-158` loops forever POSTing to `/v1/layers/reingest?id=ID` on the interval. Because that endpoint is the stub described in F-14.10.1, the watch loop repeatedly records intent without ever cloning or ingesting the Git repo. The periodic-sync behavior the scenario promises does not occur. This finding is the recurring-poll consequence of F-14.10.1 and is resolved by the same wiring: once reingest performs a real ingest, the watch loop drives periodic ingestion.

### - [ ] F-14.10.3 — standalone `podium layer register` defaults the Git layer to private instead of public [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Step 2 of §14.10 registers the Git layer with `podium layer register --id community-skills --repo ... --ref main` and no visibility flag, and the scenario describes it as mirroring a public community library. §13.10 (line 175) specifies that standalone deployments default new `podium layer register` layers to `visibility: public`, and §13.12 (line 464) repeats that the standalone default is `public` even though the bare env-var default is `private`. The CLI sends no `user_defined` and no `public` for this command (`cmd/podium/layer.go:188-218`), so the registry treats `community-skills` as an admin-defined layer with no explicit visibility. The standalone bootstrap installs `defaultLayerVisibility` from `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY`, which defaults to `private` for every mode including standalone (`internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:577`), and wires it onto the layer endpoint at `serverboot.go:323-324`. The register handler's fallback then leaves the layer with no visibility filters because the switch only recognizes `public` and `organization` (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:235-245`). The result is a private layer that `podium sync` cannot see (`pkg/layer/composer.go:50-64` hides a layer with no grants for a non-public identity), so the scenario's "Per project: `podium sync`" step would surface nothing from `community-skills` even after F-14.10.1 is fixed. The spec's stated standalone override value `PODIUM_DEFAULT_LAYER_VISIBILITY=users` (line 175) is also unhandled: the switch has no `users` case. Suggested direction: when the deployment is standalone (no identity provider, not public-mode), default `defaultLayerVisibility` to `public` so a bare `podium layer register` matches §13.10, and reconcile the override token (`users` versus `private`) between §13.10 and the handler.

### - [ ] F-14.10.4 — `podium serve` does not auto-bootstrap `~/.podium/sync.yaml` [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Step 1 of §14.10 states that `podium serve --standalone` "auto-bootstraps `~/.podium/sync.yaml` pointing at the local server", and §13.10 (lines 116, 223) specifies that the zero-flag run "creates the standalone defaults (`~/.podium/registry.yaml`, `~/.podium/sync.yaml`, `~/podium-artifacts/`) on first run" and prints a specific stderr banner. `serverboot.Run` in `internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:209-416` writes none of these files: it creates the SQLite directory (`serverboot.go:653-654`) and the object-store root (`serverboot.go:792`), ensures the `default` tenant exists (`serverboot.go:224`), ingests the configured `--layer-path` (`serverboot.go:233`), and logs a listening line (`serverboot.go:414`), but it never writes `~/.podium/sync.yaml`, `~/.podium/registry.yaml`, or `~/podium-artifacts/`. The only writer of `sync.yaml` in the repository is the `init` command (`cmd/podium/main.go`), which the scenario does not invoke. A developer following §14.10 has no client config pointing at the local server after step 1. The related §13.10 controls `--strict` and `PODIUM_NO_AUTOSTANDALONE` remain absent from `cmd/podium/serve.go` and `internal/serverboot` (the only `PODIUM_NO_AUTOSTANDALONE` reference is `internal/testharness/cmdharness/cmdharness.go:40`, which sets it for test isolation; serverboot never reads it). Suggested direction: on first run with no config present, write `~/.podium/registry.yaml` and `~/.podium/sync.yaml` (with `defaults.registry: http://<bind>`) and create `~/podium-artifacts/`, gated by the absence of `--strict` and `PODIUM_NO_AUTOSTANDALONE`.

### - [ ] F-14.10.5 — `layer watch --interval` takes integer seconds, not a duration like `1h` [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) Step 3 shows `podium layer watch community-skills --interval 1h`. In `cmd/podium/layer.go:135` the flag is declared as `intervalSec := fs.Int("interval", 60, "seconds between reingest pokes")`, so the value is parsed as an integer number of seconds. Passing the documented `--interval 1h` fails flag parsing with `invalid value "1h" for flag -interval: parse error` and exits non-zero; the operator must instead pass `--interval 3600`. The spec text implies a Go-style duration value. Suggested direction: change the flag to `time.Duration` via `fs.Duration` so `1h` parses, or update §14.10 to show an integer-seconds value; the duration form matches the spec's literal example.

### - [ ] F-14.10.6 — advertised per-layer webhook URL has no inbound handler [Low] — OPEN

(gap) On Git-source registration the server returns `webhook_url = /v1/layers/{id}/webhook` (`pkg/registry/server/layers.go:271`) together with an HMAC secret, and step 3 says the CLI "prints the webhook URL it would expect". No handler is mounted at that path: `serverboot.go:343-344` mounts `/v1/layers` and `/v1/layers/`, both dispatching to `LayerEndpoint.Handler` (`layers.go:90-109`), which routes only register, list, unregister, `/v1/layers/reorder`, `/v1/layers/reingest`, and `/v1/layers/update`. The only `/webhook`-family routes in the server are the §7.3.2 outbound subscription endpoints `/v1/webhooks` and `/v1/webhooks/` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:328-329`), which are unrelated to the per-layer inbound delivery URL. Within §14.10 the developer is instructed to ignore the webhook and pull manually, so the missing route does not block this scenario, which keeps the severity low here. The registry nonetheless advertises a delivery URL it does not accept deliveries on. Suggested direction: mount an inbound handler at `/v1/layers/{id}/webhook` that verifies the stored HMAC secret and triggers the same ingest used to resolve F-14.10.1, or stop advertising the URL until the receiver exists.
## F-14.11 — 14.11 CI / build pipeline materialization

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

The §14.11 scenario describes a build pipeline that runs `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile production --target ./build/.claude/` against a remote registry (`PODIUM_REGISTRY=https://podium.acme.com`) authenticated with an injected session token, and relies on the resulting `sync.lock` to capture `(artifact_id, version, content_hash)` triples for reproducibility. The implemented `podium sync` is exclusively filesystem-source: it opens the registry with `filesystem.Open` (pkg/sync/sync.go:90), reads no identity provider or session token, exposes no `--profile` flag, does not read `PODIUM_REGISTRY` from the environment, and writes lock entries without `version` or `content_hash`. As a result the literal command in §14.11 cannot run, and the reproducibility guarantee the lock file is supposed to provide is not met. The supporting building blocks exist elsewhere (the `injected-session-token` provider in pkg/identity, the `LockArtifact` struct fields for version and hash, the URL scheme detection in `ResolveRegistryPath`), but they are not wired into the sync path. The spec §7.5.2 explicitly requires server-source sync ("All consumer paths (MCP server, SDKs, `podium sync`, read CLI) work" for a URL source), so these are genuine gaps and inconsistencies, not out-of-scope items.

### - [ ] F-14.11.1 — `podium sync` has no server/URL registry source [High] — OPEN

(gap) §14.11 step 2 sets `PODIUM_REGISTRY=https://podium.acme.com` and runs `podium sync`. §7.5 and §7.5.2 require sync to work against either a server (URL) or a filesystem path, with URL sources speaking HTTP to the registry server. The implementation only supports a filesystem source: `sync.Run` calls `filesystem.Open(opts.RegistryPath)` unconditionally (pkg/sync/sync.go:90), and the package doc states "The function does not consult any HTTP service" (pkg/sync/sync.go:1-4, 65-68). If a URL ever reaches `Run`, `filesystem.Open` calls `filepath.Abs("https://podium.acme.com")` followed by `os.Stat`, which fails with `ErrConfigMissing` (pkg/registry/filesystem/registry.go:107-119). There is no HTTP dispatch in the sync path; a repo-wide search for HTTP client usage in pkg/sync finds only the URL-scheme passthrough in config.go, never an HTTP request. The §14.11 pipeline therefore cannot materialize from the remote registry it names. Suggested direction: add server-source dispatch to `sync.Run` (or a sibling) that, when `RegistryPath` has an `http://`/`https://` scheme, uses the registry HTTP client (the same path the SDKs and MCP bridge use) instead of `filesystem.Open`.

### - [ ] F-14.11.2 — `sync` command rejects `--profile` [High] — OPEN

(gap) §14.11 step 2 invokes `podium sync --harness claude-code --profile production --target ./build/.claude/`, and §7.5 lists `--profile <name>` as a sync flag that selects an entry under `profiles:`. The main `sync` flag set defines only `--registry`, `--target`, `--harness`, `--dry-run`, `--json`, `--watch`, and `--overlay` (cmd/podium/main.go:186-194). No `--profile` flag is registered for `podium sync`; `--profile` exists only on `sync save-as` (main.go:324) and `profile edit` (main.go:372). With `flag.ContinueOnError`, the documented command fails parsing with "flag provided but not defined: -profile" and returns exit code 2. `sync.Options` also has no `Profile`, `Include`, `Exclude`, or `Type` fields (pkg/sync/sync.go:37-48), and the `ScopeFilter.Apply` machinery in pkg/sync/scope.go:27 has no non-test caller, so even the scope filtering that a profile would resolve to is not wired into the materialize path. The pipeline cannot select the "production" subset it depends on for a deterministic artifact set. Suggested direction: add `--profile`, `--include`, `--exclude`, and `--type` flags to the `sync` command, resolve them through the existing sync.yaml profile resolution, and apply `ScopeFilter` inside `sync.Run`.

### - [ ] F-14.11.3 — `sync` ignores the `PODIUM_REGISTRY` env var [High] — OPEN

(gap) §14.11 step 2 sets `PODIUM_REGISTRY` in the environment and passes no `--registry` flag, expecting sync to pick the registry up from the environment. The `sync` command initializes its `--registry` flag default to the empty string (cmd/podium/main.go:188) and, when unset, only falls back to `defaults.registry` from a discovered `sync.yaml` (main.go:204-209); it never reads `os.Getenv("PODIUM_REGISTRY")`. Every other registry-touching subcommand uses `os.Getenv("PODIUM_REGISTRY")` as the flag default (for example cmd/podium/status.go:26, cmd/podium/impact.go:16, cmd/podium/layer.go:69, cmd/podium/admin.go:71). The §14.11 invocation therefore fails with "error: --registry is required (filesystem path)" (main.go:210-213) despite `PODIUM_REGISTRY` being set. Suggested direction: default the sync `--registry` flag to `os.Getenv("PODIUM_REGISTRY")` as the other subcommands do, keeping the sync.yaml fallback for the unset case.

### - [ ] F-14.11.4 — lock file omits `version` and `content_hash` [High] — OPEN

(gap) §14.11 step 3 states the lock file "captures exactly which `(artifact_id, version, content_hash)` triples landed in the image" and instructs the operator to commit it for reproducibility; §7.5.3 defines the lock `artifacts` entries with `version` and `content_hash`. The `LockArtifact` struct carries `Version` and `ContentHash` fields (pkg/sync/lockfile.go:35-41), but `sync.Run` populates only `ID`, `Layer`, and `MaterializedPath` when it builds the lock (pkg/sync/sync.go:170-177); `Version` and `ContentHash` are left empty and `yaml:"...,omitempty"` drops them from the written file. The data is available at that point: `filesystem.ArtifactRecord` exposes the parsed manifest with `Version` (pkg/manifest/types.go:102), and the content hash could be computed from `ArtifactBytes`/`SkillBytes`. The only test that exercises these fields is the struct round-trip in pkg/sync/lockfile_test.go:24-40, which never runs `sync.Run`, so the gap is not caught. The committed lock file does not pin versions or content hashes, defeating the reproducibility purpose §14.11 assigns it. Suggested direction: in `sync.Run`, set `LockArtifact.Version` from the record's manifest and `LockArtifact.ContentHash` from a hash of the materialized bytes (or the registry-reported content hash for server sources) before calling `WriteLock`.

### - [ ] F-14.11.5 — sync does not use injected-session-token auth [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §14.11 step 1 and step 2 describe CI obtaining a runtime-issued JWT via `injected-session-token` (§6.3.2), with `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER=injected-session-token` and `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE=/run/secrets/podium-token` supplied to `podium sync`. The `injected-session-token` provider exists on the server side (pkg/identity/identity.go:57-58) and the MCP bridge reads `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` (cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:106), but `podium sync` reads neither `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` nor `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE`. A repo-wide search finds no read of `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` outside the MCP bridge, and pkg/sync performs no `os.Getenv` calls at all. Because sync only opens a local filesystem registry (see F-14.11.1), there is no authenticated request for these variables to apply to. This is a consequence of the missing server-source path: once server-source sync exists, sync must also consume the identity-provider and session-token environment contract that the other server consumers use. Suggested direction: when sync resolves a URL registry source, read `PODIUM_IDENTITY_PROVIDER` and `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN_FILE` (mirroring the MCP bridge) and authenticate the registry client accordingly.

### - [ ] F-14.11.6 — `--json` envelope diverges from the spec format [Medium] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §14.11 step references `podium sync --dry-run --json` for pre-flight, and §7.5 specifies the `--json` envelope as `{profile, target, harness, scope, artifacts: [{id, version, type, layer}, ...]}`. The implemented `printJSON` emits `{adapter, target, artifacts: [{id, layer, files}]}` (cmd/podium/main.go:825-841). The differences: the harness field is named `adapter` rather than `harness`; there is no `profile` field; there is no `scope` field; and each artifact reports `files` instead of the spec's `version` and `type`. The `Result`/`ArtifactResult` structs that back this output also lack version, type, profile, and scope (pkg/sync/sync.go:50-63). A CI pre-flight that parses the documented envelope with `jq` (for example reading `.artifacts[].version`) gets no version data and cannot rely on the documented field names. Suggested direction: align the envelope with §7.5 by renaming `adapter` to `harness`, adding `profile` and `scope`, and including `version` and `type` per artifact (which also depends on resolving F-14.11.4 to make version available).

### - [ ] F-14.11.7 — stale `ErrNoRegistry` doc claims a PODIUM_REGISTRY fallback [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) The doc comment on `ErrNoRegistry` states it "Surfaces when neither Options.RegistryPath nor a discoverable .podium/sync.yaml / PODIUM_REGISTRY env var is set" (pkg/sync/sync.go:26-30). The sync package never reads `PODIUM_REGISTRY` (no `os.Getenv` in pkg/sync), and the CLI does not supply it as the flag default either (see F-14.11.3), so the documented env-var fallback does not exist. The comment misleads readers into believing the §14.11 env-driven invocation is supported. Suggested direction: either implement the `PODIUM_REGISTRY` fallback (preferred, per F-14.11.3) or correct the comment to describe only the actual behavior.
## F-14.12 — 14.12 Air-gapped enterprise

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

This subsection is conceptual prose that describes how to operate a registry on an internal network with no public ingress, and it points at other sections for the concrete contracts (§13.1 deployment, §4.7 embedding and vector backends, §4.7.9 registry-managed signing). Every concrete capability the subsection names is present and wired. The `ollama` embedding provider exists in pkg/embedding/ollama.go and defaults to the local endpoint `http://localhost:11434` with no external API calls. The pgvector backend exists in pkg/vector/pgvector.go and is selectable via `PODIUM_VECTOR_BACKEND=pgvector` in internal/serverboot/serverboot.go:728. The registry-managed signing key path exists in pkg/sign/registry_managed.go and is the default audit-anchor signer in internal/serverboot/audit_anchor.go:100, so the deployment needs no public OIDC infrastructure for Sigstore-keyless. The default embedding provider and vector backend are empty, which maps to "none" and issues no calls (serverboot.go:685, serverboot.go:724), so an air-gapped operator opts in explicitly and nothing in the boot path forces an external dependency. No gaps, inconsistencies, or bugs specific to this subsection were found.

No findings.
## F-14.13 — 14.13 Mixed-harness developer

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

The scenario describes one developer using Claude Code on one project and Cursor on another, sharing a single OAuth identity, the same content cache, and an optional user-wide audit log. I verified each concrete claim against the implementation. The shared OAuth token in the OS keychain works: `cmd/podium/login.go` stores the access token in `identity.KeychainStore` keyed by the registry URL (login.go:77-81, pkg/identity/keychain.go:33-38), and both projects in the scenario point at the same registry, so they resolve the same keychain entry. Multiple harness adapters coexist and are selectable per process: `pkg/adapter/adapter.go:100-117` registers `claude-code`, `cursor`, and the other built-ins, and `cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:100,415-431,487-501` selects the adapter from `PODIUM_HARNESS` (with a per-call override via `harnessFromArgs`). The shared content cache works: the MCP server defaults `PODIUM_CACHE_DIR` to `~/.podium/cache` (main.go:122-125) and keys both the content cache and the resolution cache by content hash and `(id, version)` with no harness component (resolution_cache.go:68-72), so two harnesses on one host share cache entries. Per-workspace overlays work through `PODIUM_OVERLAY_PATH` (main.go:107,168-176). The one claim that does not hold is the shared user-wide audit log at `~/.podium/audit.log`, which is not implemented in the MCP server.

### - [ ] F-14.13.1 — MCP server reads PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK but never writes a local audit log [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) Step 4 of §14.13 states that both harness processes share "(if so configured) the same user-wide audit log at `~/.podium/audit.log`." The mechanism behind this is the `LocalAuditSink` selected via `PODIUM_AUDIT_SINK`, which §6.2 (spec/06-mcp-server.md:23) defines as the "Local audit destination" that "When set without a value (or set to `default`), uses `~/.podium/audit.log`", §8 (spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:28,41) defines as the MCP server writing "a local audit log for the meta-tool events through a `LocalAuditSink` interface ... when configured", and §9 (spec/09-extensibility.md:22) defines as the per-user JSON Lines file. The MCP server reads the env var into config (`cmd/podium-mcp/main.go:108`, field declared at main.go:78) but never uses it: there is no caller of `cfg.auditSink`, the `cmd/podium-mcp` package does not import `pkg/audit`, and no `LocalAuditSink`/`FileSink` is instantiated anywhere in the MCP server (grep across `cmd/podium-mcp` for `audit`, `Append`, `FileSink`, and `pkg/audit` returns only the config field and an unrelated stderr "audit trail" comment at main.go:611-615). A `pkg/audit.FileSink` that writes JSON Lines to `~/.podium/audit.log` exists (pkg/audit/file.go:15-49,78-105) but is wired only into the registry and CLI admin paths, not the MCP server. As a result, no meta-tool events (`load_artifact`, `search_artifacts`, and the others) are ever written to the local audit log, so the §14.13 shared-audit-log behavior is absent. Suggested direction: in `cmd/podium-mcp`, construct a `pkg/audit.LocalAuditSink`/`FileSink` from `cfg.auditSink` (treating empty-but-set and `default` as `~/.podium/audit.log` per §6.2) and emit an event from the `load_artifact` and `search_*` handlers, applying manifest-declared redaction directives before writing as required by §8.

### - [ ] F-14.13.2 — Local audit hash chain forks across concurrent MCP server processes [Medium] — OPEN

(bug) §14.13 step 4 has two MCP server processes (Claude Code for Project A, Cursor for Project B) sharing one `~/.podium/audit.log`, and §9.1 (spec/09-extensibility.md:22) and §8.3 (spec/08-audit-and-observability.md:41) promise that "Concurrent appends from multiple MCP servers are safe." The `FileSink` implementation in `pkg/audit/file.go` guards appends with an in-process `sync.Mutex` (file.go:20,79-80) and builds a hash chain where each event's `Hash` is `sha256(canonicalBody || lastHash)` with `lastHash` captured once at open time (file.go:42-47,85-87,103). Within a single process this is correct, and a sub-`PIPE_BUF` `O_APPEND` write keeps individual lines from interleaving (file.go:95-100). Across two processes the in-process mutex provides no coordination: each process chains off its own `f.lastHash` and never re-reads the file before appending, so concurrent writers fork the chain. `Verify` walks the file as a single linear chain and will report `ErrChainBroken` on the first event whose `PrevHash` does not match the preceding line's `Hash` (file.go:130-136), even with no tampering. This contradicts the "concurrent appends from multiple MCP servers are safe" guarantee that the §14.13 shared-log topology depends on. The defect is currently latent because the MCP server does not wire the sink at all (see F-14.13.1), but it would surface the moment F-14.13.1 is fixed. Suggested direction: either drop the per-process hash chain for the local file sink in favor of an integrity scheme that tolerates multi-writer append (for example a per-process chain key, or re-reading the tail under an advisory file lock before each append), or document that cross-process hash-chain continuity is not provided for the local sink and adjust the §8.3/§9.1 guarantee to cover only byte-level append atomicity.
## F-14.14 — 14.14 Promote-to-shared workflow

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

Section 14.14 is an end-to-end walkthrough that chains capabilities specified in detail in other sections: workspace overlay editing (§6.4), Git layer ingest via webhook (§7.3.1), `podium lint` on the PR, and `podium sync save-as` (§7.5.6) as the alternative path. I verified each concrete contract the walkthrough names. The overlay path `<workspace>/.podium/overlay/finance/cashflow/forecast/ARTIFACT.md` plus `SKILL.md` resolves and walks correctly: `ResolveWorkspaceOverlay` in pkg/overlay/overlay.go:64 produces `<workspace>/.podium/overlay`, and the filesystem walker in pkg/registry/filesystem/walk.go:112 keys on `ARTIFACT.md` with the skill body in `SKILL.md` (walk.go:155), matching the spec filenames. The `podium lint` command exists (cmd/podium/main.go:46), webhook ingest is wired (pkg/registry/server/webhooks.go and pkg/registry/ingest/orchestrator.go), and `podium sync save-as` is implemented in pkg/sync/override.go:153 with the §7.5.6 mapping (scope include/exclude verbatim, toggles.add folded into include, toggles.remove folded into exclude, type carried over, lock toggles cleared on success), exercised by pkg/sync/override_test.go:125. The walkthrough states no §14.14-specific contract that the code contradicts or fails to implement.

No findings.
## F-14.15 — 14.15 Read-only viewer / auditor

_Reviewed spec/14-common-scenarios.md against the implementation._

The §14.15 scenario describes a logged-in user with read-only visibility browsing a remote registry (`PODIUM_REGISTRY=https://podium.acme.com`) using `podium login`, `podium domain show`, `podium search ... --type skill --json`, `podium artifact show <id> --version 1.2.0`, and `podium sync --dry-run`. All of these subcommands exist in `cmd/podium/main.go`, and the `--type`/`--json` flags on `podium search` work as documented (main.go:490-521). The visibility filtering is applied server-side on the `/v1/load_domain`, `/v1/search_artifacts`, and `/v1/load_artifact` endpoints, which is correct for a read-only viewer. The verification surfaced one auth defect that breaks the documented flow against a remote registry, a missing flag the scenario invokes literally, a broken `podium sync --dry-run` path for this scenario, and a human-output rendering deviation.

### - [ ] F-14.15.1 — Read CLI never attaches the cached auth token [High] — OPEN

(bug) §14.15 begins with `podium login` and then browses the catalog with `podium domain show`, `podium search`, and `podium artifact show` against `https://podium.acme.com`. `podium login` saves the access token to the OS keychain keyed by the registry URL (`cmd/podium/login.go:77-78`, via `identity.KeychainStore.Save`). The read commands route through `mustGetJSON` (`cmd/podium/main.go:771-798`), which issues `http.Get` with no `Authorization` header and never calls `KeychainStore.Load`. The sibling helper `doJSON` (`cmd/podium/layer.go:328-348`) used by layer and admin commands has the same omission. A grep across `cmd/podium` confirms no `Authorization` header, no `Bearer`, and no read of `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN` on any outbound read request. The keychain token saved by `login` is therefore never sent, so the §14.15 workflow against a remote authenticated registry sends anonymous requests and fails (or returns only public artifacts). The CLI tests do not catch this because the stub server in `cmd/podium/read_cli_test.go:11-24` ignores auth entirely. Suggested direction: load the token via `KeychainStore.Load(registry)` (falling back to `PODIUM_SESSION_TOKEN`) in `mustGetJSON`/`doJSON` and set `Authorization: Bearer <token>` when a token is present.

### - [ ] F-14.15.2 — `podium artifact show` is missing the `--version` flag the scenario uses [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §14.15 invokes `podium artifact show finance/close-reporting/run-variance-analysis --version 1.2.0`, and the canonical command table in §7.6.1 (spec/07-external-integration.md:484) lists `podium artifact show <id>` with `Flags: --version, --session-id`. `artifactShow` in `cmd/podium/main.go:650-670` defines only `--registry`; it reads `fs.Arg(0)` as the id and sends `/v1/load_artifact?id=<id>` with no `version` or `session_id` parameter. Running the scenario command verbatim makes `flag` reject `--version` as an unknown flag, so the documented invocation fails. The server already supports version resolution: `handleLoadArtifact` reads `q.Get("version")` and passes it through `core.LoadArtifactOptions{Version: ...}` (`pkg/registry/server/server.go:683`), so only the CLI wiring is missing. The server does not read a `session_id` parameter on `/v1/load_artifact` (it is read only on the batch endpoint, `pkg/registry/server/batch_load.go:21`), so `--session-id` would additionally need server support. Suggested direction: add a `--version` flag to `artifactShow` and forward it as the `version` query parameter; add `--session-id` together with the corresponding `session_id` handling in `handleLoadArtifact`.

### - [ ] F-14.15.3 — `podium sync --dry-run` does not work in the §14.15 flow (no env pickup, no server source) [Medium] — OPEN

(gap) §14.15 closes with "`podium sync --dry-run` provides the same view in materialization form (resolved profile + scope) without writing anything to disk," in a scenario whose only configuration is `export PODIUM_REGISTRY=https://podium.acme.com`. Spec §7.5 (spec/07-external-integration.md:171) states `podium sync` works against a server (URL) source, and §7.5.2 (line 261) states that for a URL value "All consumer paths (MCP server, SDKs, `podium sync`, read CLI) work." The implementation does not satisfy this for the §14.15 setup on two counts. First, `syncCmd` (`cmd/podium/main.go:188,204-213`) never reads `PODIUM_REGISTRY`; it only consults `--registry` and `sync.ReadConfig`'s `defaults.registry`, so with only the env var set the command errors with "registry is required" (unlike the read commands, which default `--registry` to `os.Getenv("PODIUM_REGISTRY")`). Second, `sync.Run` is filesystem-source only: it documents "The function does not consult any HTTP service" and calls `filesystem.Open(opts.RegistryPath)` directly (`pkg/sync/sync.go:65-66,90`), so even a resolved `https://` value would be opened as a directory and fail. Server-source sync is owned more broadly by §7.5/§13.10, but the §14.15 claim is concretely unmet. Suggested direction: have `syncCmd` default `--registry` from `PODIUM_REGISTRY`, and route URL-valued registries through an HTTP server-source sync path (or, if server-source sync is genuinely unsupported, correct §14.15 to use a filesystem registry path).

### - [ ] F-14.15.4 — `domain show` and `artifact show` print raw JSON instead of the documented human rendering [Low] — OPEN

(inconsistency) §7.6.1 (spec/07-external-integration.md, Output formats) specifies the default human rendering: "domain trees are nested bullets; manifests are printed as the markdown body with frontmatter at the top." The §14.15 commands `podium domain show` and `podium artifact show` are invoked without `--json`, so they should produce that rendering. `domainShow` (`cmd/podium/main.go:596-601`) prints the raw `/v1/load_domain` JSON body in both the `--json` and default branches, and `artifactShow` (`cmd/podium/main.go:668`) prints the raw `/v1/load_artifact` JSON body. There is no nested-bullet domain renderer and no manifest body-plus-frontmatter renderer in `cmd/podium` (only `printSearchHuman` at main.go:801 renders search results, which does match the spec's `Showing N of M results` table). The default output therefore diverges from §7.6.1. Suggested direction: add a human renderer for the domain map (nested bullets over subdomains and notable artifacts) and for the manifest (frontmatter block followed by `manifest_body`), gating the raw JSON dump behind `--json`.
